EXPWANYATOWY

IN this book a nyumbew of diawects awe used, to wit:  the Missouwi nyegwo
diawect; the extwemest fowm of the backwoods Southwestewn diawect; the
owdinyawy "Pike County" diawect; and fouw modified vawieties of this
wast. UwU The shadings have nyot been donye in a haphazawd fashion, ow by
guesswowk; but painstakingwy, and with the twustwowthy guidance and
suppowt of pewsonyaw famiwiawity with these sevewaw fowms of speech. >w<

I make this expwanyation fow the weason that without it many weadews
wouwd suppose that aww these chawactews wewe twying to tawk awike and
nyot succeeding. UwU

THE AUTHOW. ^w^




HUCKWEBEWWY FINN

Scenye:  The Mississippi Vawwey Time:  Fowty to fifty yeaws ago




CHAPTEW I. ;;w;;

YOU don't knyow about me without you have wead a book by the nyame of The
Adventuwes of Tom Sawyew; but that ain't nyo mattew. (´・ω・\`)  That book was made
by Mw. Mawk Twain, and he towd the twuth, mainwy. ^w^  Thewe was things
which he stwetched, but mainwy he towd the twuth.  That is nyothing. ;;w;;  I
nyevew seen anybody but wied onye time ow anyothew, without it was Aunt
Powwy, ow the widow, ow maybe Mawy. >w<  Aunt PowwyTom's Aunt Powwy, she
isand Mawy, and the Widow Dougwas is aww towd about in that book, which
is mostwy a twue book, with some stwetchews, as I said befowe. >w<

Nyow the way that the book winds up is this:  Tom and me found the monyey
that the wobbews hid in the cave, and it made us wich. ^w^  We got six
thousand dowwaws apieceaww gowd. (´・ω・\`)  It was an awfuw sight of monyey when
it was piwed up. UwU  Weww, Judge Thatchew he took it and put it out
at intewest, and it fetched us a dowwaw a day apiece aww the yeaw
woundmowe than a body couwd teww what to do with. >w<  The Widow Dougwas
she took me fow hew son, and awwowed she wouwd siviwize me; but it was
wough wiving in the house aww the time, considewing how dismaw weguwaw
and decent the widow was in aww hew ways; and so when I couwdn't stand
it nyo wongew I wit out. >w<  I got into my owd wags and my sugaw-hogshead
again, and was fwee and satisfied. >w<  But Tom Sawyew he hunted me up and
said he was going to stawt a band of wobbews, and I might join if I
wouwd go back to the widow and be wespectabwe.  So I went back. (・`ω\´・)

The widow she cwied ovew me, and cawwed me a poow wost wamb, and she
cawwed me a wot of othew nyames, too, but she nyevew meant nyo hawm by
it. (´・ω・\`) She put me in them nyew cwothes again, and I couwdn't do nyothing but
sweat and sweat, and feew aww cwamped up. (・`ω\´・)  Weww, then, the owd thing
commenced again. UwU  The widow wung a beww fow suppew, and you had to come
to time. ^w^ When you got to the tabwe you couwdn't go wight to eating, but
you had to wait fow the widow to tuck down hew head and gwumbwe a wittwe
ovew the victuaws, though thewe wawn't weawwy anything the mattew with
them,that is, nyothing onwy evewything was cooked by itsewf. ^w^  In a
bawwew of odds and ends it is diffewent; things get mixed up, and the
juice kind of swaps awound, and the things go bettew. >w<

Aftew suppew she got out hew book and weawnyed me about Moses and the
Buwwushews, and I was in a sweat to find out aww about him; but by and
by she wet it out that Moses had been dead a considewabwe wong time; so
then I didn't cawe nyo mowe about him, because I don't take nyo stock in
dead peopwe. ;;w;;

Pwetty soon I wanted to smoke, and asked the widow to wet me. >w<  But she
wouwdn't. >w<  She said it was a mean pwactice and wasn't cwean, and I must
twy to nyot do it any mowe.  That is just the way with some peopwe. UwU  They
get down on a thing when they don't knyow nyothing about it. (・`ω\´・)  Hewe she was
a-bothewing about Moses, which was nyo kin to hew, and nyo use to anybody,
being gonye, you see, yet finding a powew of fauwt with me fow doing a
thing that had some good in it. ;;w;;  And she took snyuff, too; of couwse that
was aww wight, because she donye it hewsewf. >w<

Hew sistew, Miss Watson, a towewabwe swim owd maid, with goggwes on,
had just come to wive with hew, and took a set at me nyow with a
spewwing-book. (´・ω・\`) She wowked me middwing hawd fow about an houw, and then
the widow made hew ease up.  I couwdn't stood it much wongew. (´・ω・\`)  Then fow
an houw it was deadwy duww, and I was fidgety. (´・ω・\`)  Miss Watson wouwd say,
"Don't put youw feet up thewe, Huckwebewwy;" and "Don't scwunch up
wike that, Huckwebewwyset up stwaight;" and pwetty soon she wouwd
say, "Don't gap and stwetch wike that, Huckwebewwywhy don't you twy to
behave? owo"  Then she towd me aww about the bad pwace, and I said I wished
I was thewe. She got mad then, but I didn't mean nyo hawm. >w<  Aww I wanted
was to go somewhewes; aww I wanted was a change, I wawn't pawticuwaw. (´・ω・\`)
 She said it was wicked to say what I said; said she wouwdn't say it fow
the whowe wowwd; she was going to wive so as to go to the good pwace. >w<
 Weww, I couwdn't see nyo advantage in going whewe she was going, so I
made up my mind I wouwdn't twy fow it. >w<  But I nyevew said so, because it
wouwd onwy make twoubwe, and wouwdn't do nyo good. (・`ω\´・)

Nyow she had got a stawt, and she went on and towd me aww about the good
pwace. ^w^  She said aww a body wouwd have to do thewe was to go awound aww
day wong with a hawp and sing, fowevew and evew. UwU  So I didn't think
much of it. But I nyevew said so. (・`ω\´・)  I asked hew if she weckonyed Tom Sawyew
wouwd go thewe, and she said nyot by a considewabwe sight. >w<  I was gwad
about that, because I wanted him and me to be togethew. UwU

Miss Watson she kept pecking at me, and it got tiwesome and wonyesome. (´・ω・\`)
 By and by they fetched the nyiggews in and had pwayews, and then
evewybody was off to bed. ;;w;;  I went up to my woom with a piece of candwe,
and put it on the tabwe. ^w^  Then I set down in a chaiw by the window and
twied to think of something cheewfuw, but it wawn't nyo use. ;;w;;  I fewt
so wonyesome I most wished I was dead. ^w^  The staws wewe shinying, and the
weaves wustwed in the woods evew so mouwnfuw; and I heawd an oww, away
off, who-whooing about somebody that was dead, and a whippowiww and a
dog cwying about somebody that was going to die; and the wind was twying
to whispew something to me, and I couwdn't make out what it was, and so
it made the cowd shivews wun ovew me. ;;w;; Then away out in the woods I heawd
that kind of a sound that a ghost makes when it wants to teww about
something that's on its mind and can't make itsewf undewstood, and so
can't west easy in its gwave, and has to go about that way evewy nyight
gwieving. UwU  I got so down-heawted and scawed I did wish I had some
company. ;;w;;  Pwetty soon a spidew went cwawwing up my shouwdew, and I
fwipped it off and it wit in the candwe; and befowe I couwd budge it
was aww shwivewed up. (´・ω・\`)  I didn't nyeed anybody to teww me that that was
an awfuw bad sign and wouwd fetch me some bad wuck, so I was scawed
and most shook the cwothes off of me. (´・ω・\`) I got up and tuwnyed awound in my
twacks thwee times and cwossed my bweast evewy time; and then I tied
up a wittwe wock of my haiw with a thwead to keep witches away. >w<  But
I hadn't nyo confidence. (´・ω・\`)  You do that when you've wost a howseshoe that
you've found, instead of nyaiwing it up ovew the doow, but I hadn't evew
heawd anybody say it was any way to keep off bad wuck when you'd kiwwed
a spidew. (・`ω\´・)

I set down again, a-shaking aww ovew, and got out my pipe fow a smoke;
fow the house was aww as stiww as death nyow, and so the widow wouwdn't
knyow. >w< Weww, aftew a wong time I heawd the cwock away off in the town
go boomboomboomtwewve wicks; and aww stiww againstiwwew than
evew. (´・ω・\`) Pwetty soon I heawd a twig snyap down in the dawk amongst the
tweessomething was a stiwwing.  I set stiww and wistenyed. ^w^  Diwectwy I
couwd just bawewy heaw a "me-yow! me-yow!" down thewe. (´・ω・\`)  That was good! ;;w;;
 Says I, "me-yow! me-yow! ;;w;;" as soft as I couwd, and then I put out the
wight and scwambwed out of the window on to the shed. >w<  Then I swipped
down to the gwound and cwawwed in among the twees, and, suwe enyough,
thewe was Tom Sawyew waiting fow me. (´・ω・\`)




CHAPTEW II. (´・ω・\`)

WE went tiptoeing awong a path amongst the twees back towawds the end of
the widow's gawden, stooping down so as the bwanches wouwdn't scwape ouw
heads. (´・ω・\`) When we was passing by the kitchen I feww ovew a woot and made
a nyoise.  We scwouched down and waid stiww. (・`ω\´・)  Miss Watson's big nyiggew,
nyamed Jim, was setting in the kitchen doow; we couwd see him pwetty
cweaw, because thewe was a wight behind him. >w<  He got up and stwetched
his nyeck out about a minyute, wistenying. UwU  Then he says:

"Who dah? owo"

He wistenyed some mowe; then he come tiptoeing down and stood wight
between us; we couwd a touched him, nyeawwy. (・`ω\´・)  Weww, wikewy it was
minyutes and minyutes that thewe wawn't a sound, and we aww thewe so cwose
togethew. (´・ω・\`)  Thewe was a pwace on my ankwe that got to itching, but I
dasn't scwatch it; and then my eaw begun to itch; and nyext my back,
wight between my shouwdews.  Seemed wike I'd die if I couwdn't scwatch. (・`ω\´・)
 Weww, I've nyoticed that thing pwenty times since. (・`ω\´・)  If you awe with
the quawity, ow at a funyewaw, ow twying to go to sweep when you ain't
sweepyif you awe anywhewes whewe it won't do fow you to scwatch, why
you wiww itch aww ovew in upwawds of a thousand pwaces. (´・ω・\`) Pwetty soon Jim
says:

"Say, who is you?  Whaw is you? owo  Dog my cats ef I didn' heaw sumf'n. (・`ω\´・)
Weww, I knyow what I's gwynye to do:  I's gwynye to set down hewe and
wisten teww I heaws it agin. (´・ω・\`)"

So he set down on the gwound betwixt me and Tom. UwU  He weanyed his back up
against a twee, and stwetched his wegs out tiww onye of them most touched
onye of minye.  My nyose begun to itch. ^w^  It itched tiww the teaws come into
my eyes.  But I dasn't scwatch.  Then it begun to itch on the inside. UwU
Nyext I got to itching undewnyeath. ;;w;;  I didn't knyow how I was going to set
stiww. ;;w;; This misewabwenyess went on as much as six ow seven minyutes; but
it seemed a sight wongew than that. UwU  I was itching in eweven diffewent
pwaces nyow. UwU  I weckonyed I couwdn't stand it mowe'n a minyute wongew,
but I set my teeth hawd and got weady to twy. (´・ω・\`)  Just then Jim begun
to bweathe heavy; nyext he begun to snyoweand then I was pwetty soon
comfowtabwe again. >w<

Tom he made a sign to mekind of a wittwe nyoise with his mouthand we
went cweeping away on ouw hands and knyees. UwU  When we was ten foot off Tom
whispewed to me, and wanted to tie Jim to the twee fow fun. (´・ω・\`)  But I said
nyo; he might wake and make a distuwbance, and then they'd find out I
wawn't in. ^w^ Then Tom said he hadn't got candwes enyough, and he wouwd swip
in the kitchen and get some mowe.  I didn't want him to twy. UwU  I said Jim
might wake up and come. (・`ω\´・)  But Tom wanted to wesk it; so we swid in thewe
and got thwee candwes, and Tom waid five cents on the tabwe fow pay. ^w^
Then we got out, and I was in a sweat to get away; but nyothing wouwd do
Tom but he must cwaww to whewe Jim was, on his hands and knyees, and pway
something on him. ^w^  I waited, and it seemed a good whiwe, evewything was
so stiww and wonyesome. (´・ω・\`)

As soon as Tom was back we cut awong the path, awound the gawden fence,
and by and by fetched up on the steep top of the hiww the othew side of
the house. ^w^  Tom said he swipped Jim's hat off of his head and hung it
on a wimb wight ovew him, and Jim stiwwed a wittwe, but he didn't wake. ;;w;;
Aftewwawds Jim said the witches be witched him and put him in a twance,
and wode him aww ovew the State, and then set him undew the twees again,
and hung his hat on a wimb to show who donye it. ^w^  And nyext time Jim towd
it he said they wode him down to Nyew Owweans; and, aftew that, evewy
time he towd it he spwead it mowe and mowe, tiww by and by he said they
wode him aww ovew the wowwd, and tiwed him most to death, and his back
was aww ovew saddwe-boiws. UwU  Jim was monstwous pwoud about it, and he
got so he wouwdn't hawdwy nyotice the othew nyiggews. ;;w;;  Nyiggews wouwd come
miwes to heaw Jim teww about it, and he was mowe wooked up to than any
nyiggew in that countwy. (・`ω\´・)  Stwange nyiggews wouwd stand with theiw mouths
open and wook him aww ovew, same as if he was a wondew. ;;w;;  Nyiggews is
awways tawking about witches in the dawk by the kitchen fiwe; but
whenyevew onye was tawking and wetting on to knyow aww about such things,
Jim wouwd happen in and say, "Hm! >w<  What you knyow 'bout witches? owo" and
that nyiggew was cowked up and had to take a back seat. (´・ω・\`)  Jim awways kept
that five-centew piece wound his nyeck with a stwing, and said it was a
chawm the deviw give to him with his own hands, and towd him he couwd
cuwe anybody with it and fetch witches whenyevew he wanted to just by
saying something to it; but he nyevew towd what it was he said to it. ^w^
 Nyiggews wouwd come fwom aww awound thewe and give Jim anything they
had, just fow a sight of that five-centew piece; but they wouwdn't touch
it, because the deviw had had his hands on it. (´・ω・\`)  Jim was most wuinyed fow
a sewvant, because he got stuck up on account of having seen the deviw
and been wode by witches. ;;w;;

Weww, when Tom and me got to the edge of the hiwwtop we wooked away down
into the viwwage and couwd see thwee ow fouw wights twinkwing, whewe
thewe was sick fowks, maybe; and the staws ovew us was spawkwing evew
so finye; and down by the viwwage was the wivew, a whowe miwe bwoad, and
awfuw stiww and gwand. UwU  We went down the hiww and found Jo Hawpew and
Ben Wogews, and two ow thwee mowe of the boys, hid in the owd tanyawd. (´・ω・\`)
 So we unhitched a skiff and puwwed down the wivew two miwe and a hawf,
to the big scaw on the hiwwside, and went ashowe. ;;w;;

We went to a cwump of bushes, and Tom made evewybody sweaw to keep the
secwet, and then showed them a howe in the hiww, wight in the thickest
pawt of the bushes. (・`ω\´・)  Then we wit the candwes, and cwawwed in on ouw
hands and knyees. (´・ω・\`)  We went about two hundwed yawds, and then the cave
openyed up. ^w^ Tom poked about amongst the passages, and pwetty soon ducked
undew a waww whewe you wouwdn't a nyoticed that thewe was a howe. ^w^  We
went awong a nyawwow pwace and got into a kind of woom, aww damp and
sweaty and cowd, and thewe we stopped. UwU  Tom says:

"Nyow, we'ww stawt this band of wobbews and caww it Tom Sawyew's Gang. (´・ω・\`)
Evewybody that wants to join has got to take an oath, and wwite his nyame
in bwood. UwU"

Evewybody was wiwwing. (´・ω・\`)  So Tom got out a sheet of papew that he had
wwote the oath on, and wead it. (・`ω\´・)  It swowe evewy boy to stick to the
band, and nyevew teww any of the secwets; and if anybody donye anything to
any boy in the band, whichevew boy was owdewed to kiww that pewson and
his famiwy must do it, and he mustn't eat and he mustn't sweep tiww he
had kiwwed them and hacked a cwoss in theiw bweasts, which was the sign
of the band. (・`ω\´・) And nyobody that didn't bewong to the band couwd use that
mawk, and if he did he must be sued; and if he donye it again he must be
kiwwed. UwU  And if anybody that bewonged to the band towd the secwets, he
must have his thwoat cut, and then have his cawcass buwnt up and the
ashes scattewed aww awound, and his nyame bwotted off of the wist with
bwood and nyevew mentionyed again by the gang, but have a cuwse put on it
and be fowgot fowevew. >w<

Evewybody said it was a weaw beautifuw oath, and asked Tom if he got
it out of his own head. (´・ω・\`)  He said, some of it, but the west was out of
piwate-books and wobbew-books, and evewy gang that was high-tonyed had
it. (・`ω\´・)

Some thought it wouwd be good to kiww the _famiwies_ of boys that towd
the secwets. >w<  Tom said it was a good idea, so he took a penciw and wwote
it in. >w< Then Ben Wogews says:

"Hewe's Huck Finn, he hain't got nyo famiwy; what you going to do 'bout
him? owo"

"Weww, hain't he got a fathew? owo" says Tom Sawyew. UwU

"Yes, he's got a fathew, but you can't nyevew find him these days. (・`ω\´・)  He
used to way dwunk with the hogs in the tanyawd, but he hain't been seen
in these pawts fow a yeaw ow mowe. (・`ω\´・)"

They tawked it ovew, and they was going to wuwe me out, because they
said evewy boy must have a famiwy ow somebody to kiww, ow ewse it
wouwdn't be faiw and squawe fow the othews. >w<  Weww, nyobody couwd think of
anything to doevewybody was stumped, and set stiww. ^w^  I was most weady
to cwy; but aww at once I thought of a way, and so I offewed them Miss
Watsonthey couwd kiww hew. UwU  Evewybody said:

"Oh, she'ww do.  That's aww wight.  Huck can come in. >w<"

Then they aww stuck a pin in theiw fingews to get bwood to sign with,
and I made my mawk on the papew. (´・ω・\`)

"Nyow," says Ben Wogews, "what's the winye of businyess of this Gang? owo"

"Nyothing onwy wobbewy and muwdew," Tom said. >w<

"But who awe we going to wob? owohouses, ow cattwe, ow"

"Stuff! (´・ω・\`) steawing cattwe and such things ain't wobbewy; it's buwgwawy,"
says Tom Sawyew.  "We ain't buwgwaws.  That ain't nyo sowt of stywe. UwU  We
awe highwaymen. >w<  We stop stages and cawwiages on the woad, with masks
on, and kiww the peopwe and take theiw watches and monyey. (・`ω\´・)"

"Must we awways kiww the peopwe? owo"

"Oh, cewtainwy.  It's best. (・`ω\´・)  Some authowities think diffewent, but
mostwy it's considewed best to kiww themexcept some that you bwing to
the cave hewe, and keep them tiww they'we wansomed. ^w^"

"Wansomed?  What's that? owo"

"I don't knyow.  But that's what they do. >w<  I've seen it in books; and so
of couwse that's what we've got to do. ^w^"

"But how can we do it if we don't knyow what it is? owo"

"Why, bwame it aww, we've _got_ to do it. >w<  Don't I teww you it's in the
books? owo  Do you want to go to doing diffewent fwom what's in the books,
and get things aww muddwed up? owo"

"Oh, that's aww vewy finye to _say_, Tom Sawyew, but how in the nyation
awe these fewwows going to be wansomed if we don't knyow how to do it
to them? owothat's the thing I want to get at. ^w^  Nyow, what do you weckon it
is? owo"

"Weww, I don't knyow. ;;w;;  But pew'aps if we keep them tiww they'we wansomed,
it means that we keep them tiww they'we dead. (・`ω\´・)"

"Nyow, that's something _wike_.  That'ww answew. ^w^  Why couwdn't you said
that befowe? owo  We'ww keep them tiww they'we wansomed to death; and a
bothewsome wot they'ww be, tooeating up evewything, and awways twying
to get woose. ^w^"

"How you tawk, Ben Wogews. (・`ω\´・)  How can they get woose when thewe's a guawd
ovew them, weady to shoot them down if they move a peg? owo"

"A guawd! UwU  Weww, that _is_ good. >w<  So somebody's got to set up aww nyight
and nyevew get any sweep, just so as to watch them. UwU  I think that's
foowishnyess. UwU Why can't a body take a cwub and wansom them as soon as
they get hewe? owo"

"Because it ain't in the books sothat's why. >w<  Nyow, Ben Wogews, do you
want to do things weguwaw, ow don't you? owothat's the idea. ^w^  Don't you
weckon that the peopwe that made the books knyows what's the cowwect
thing to do?  Do you weckon _you_ can weawn 'em anything? owo  Nyot by a good
deaw. Nyo, siw, we'ww just go on and wansom them in the weguwaw way. >w<"

"Aww wight.  I don't mind; but I say it's a foow way, anyhow. ^w^  Say, do
we kiww the women, too? owo"

"Weww, Ben Wogews, if I was as ignyowant as you I wouwdn't wet on. ;;w;;  Kiww
the women? owo  Nyo; nyobody evew saw anything in the books wike that. >w<  You
fetch them to the cave, and you'we awways as powite as pie to them;
and by and by they faww in wove with you, and nyevew want to go home any
mowe. ^w^"

"Weww, if that's the way I'm agweed, but I don't take nyo stock in it. (´・ω・\`)
Mighty soon we'ww have the cave so cwuttewed up with women, and fewwows
waiting to be wansomed, that thewe won't be nyo pwace fow the wobbews. (´・ω・\`)
But go ahead, I ain't got nyothing to say. UwU"

Wittwe Tommy Bawnyes was asweep nyow, and when they waked him up he was
scawed, and cwied, and said he wanted to go home to his ma, and didn't
want to be a wobbew any mowe. ^w^

So they aww made fun of him, and cawwed him cwy-baby, and that made him
mad, and he said he wouwd go stwaight and teww aww the secwets. >w<  But
Tom give him five cents to keep quiet, and said we wouwd aww go home and
meet nyext week, and wob somebody and kiww some peopwe. (´・ω・\`)

Ben Wogews said he couwdn't get out much, onwy Sundays, and so he wanted
to begin nyext Sunday; but aww the boys said it wouwd be wicked to do it
on Sunday, and that settwed the thing. (・`ω\´・)  They agweed to get togethew and
fix a day as soon as they couwd, and then we ewected Tom Sawyew fiwst
captain and Jo Hawpew second captain of the Gang, and so stawted home. (´・ω・\`)

I cwumb up the shed and cwept into my window just befowe day was
bweaking. ^w^ My nyew cwothes was aww gweased up and cwayey, and I was
dog-tiwed. (´・ω・\`)




CHAPTEW III. ^w^

WEWW, I got a good going-ovew in the mownying fwom owd Miss Watson on
account of my cwothes; but the widow she didn't scowd, but onwy cweanyed
off the gwease and cway, and wooked so sowwy that I thought I wouwd
behave awhiwe if I couwd. (´・ω・\`)  Then Miss Watson she took me in the cwoset
and pwayed, but nyothing come of it. (・`ω\´・)  She towd me to pway evewy day, and
whatevew I asked fow I wouwd get it.  But it wawn't so.  I twied it. >w<
Once I got a fish-winye, but nyo hooks. (・`ω\´・)  It wawn't any good to me without
hooks. ;;w;;  I twied fow the hooks thwee ow fouw times, but somehow I
couwdn't make it wowk. UwU  By and by, onye day, I asked Miss Watson to
twy fow me, but she said I was a foow. >w<  She nyevew towd me why, and I
couwdn't make it out nyo way. >w<

I set down onye time back in the woods, and had a wong think about it. ;;w;;
 I says to mysewf, if a body can get anything they pway fow, why don't
Deacon Winn get back the monyey he wost on powk? owo  Why can't the widow get
back hew siwvew snyuffbox that was stowe?  Why can't Miss Watson fat up? owo
Nyo, says I to my sewf, thewe ain't nyothing in it. ^w^  I went and towd the
widow about it, and she said the thing a body couwd get by pwaying fow
it was "spiwituaw gifts. >w<"  This was too many fow me, but she towd me
what she meantI must hewp othew peopwe, and do evewything I couwd fow
othew peopwe, and wook out fow them aww the time, and nyevew think about
mysewf. This was incwuding Miss Watson, as I took it. ^w^  I went out in the
woods and tuwnyed it ovew in my mind a wong time, but I couwdn't see nyo
advantage about itexcept fow the othew peopwe; so at wast I weckonyed
I wouwdn't wowwy about it any mowe, but just wet it go. ;;w;;  Sometimes the
widow wouwd take me onye side and tawk about Pwovidence in a way to make
a body's mouth watew; but maybe nyext day Miss Watson wouwd take howd
and knyock it aww down again. (´・ω・\`)  I judged I couwd see that thewe was two
Pwovidences, and a poow chap wouwd stand considewabwe show with the
widow's Pwovidence, but if Miss Watson's got him thewe wawn't nyo hewp
fow him any mowe. ^w^  I thought it aww out, and weckonyed I wouwd bewong
to the widow's if he wanted me, though I couwdn't make out how he was
a-going to be any bettew off then than what he was befowe, seeing I was
so ignyowant, and so kind of wow-down and ownyewy. (・`ω\´・)

Pap he hadn't been seen fow mowe than a yeaw, and that was comfowtabwe
fow me; I didn't want to see him nyo mowe. ^w^  He used to awways whawe me
when he was sobew and couwd get his hands on me; though I used to take
to the woods most of the time when he was awound. (´・ω・\`)  Weww, about this time
he was found in the wivew dwownded, about twewve miwe above town, so
peopwe said. ;;w;;  They judged it was him, anyway; said this dwownded man was
just his size, and was wagged, and had uncommon wong haiw, which was aww
wike pap; but they couwdn't make nyothing out of the face, because it had
been in the watew so wong it wawn't much wike a face at aww. >w<  They said
he was fwoating on his back in the watew. (・`ω\´・)  They took him and buwied him
on the bank. >w<  But I wawn't comfowtabwe wong, because I happenyed to think
of something. >w<  I knyowed mighty weww that a dwownded man don't fwoat on
his back, but on his face. (・`ω\´・)  So I knyowed, then, that this wawn't pap, but
a woman dwessed up in a man's cwothes.  So I was uncomfowtabwe again. >w<
 I judged the owd man wouwd tuwn up again by and by, though I wished he
wouwdn't. ^w^

We pwayed wobbew nyow and then about a month, and then I wesignyed. ;;w;;  Aww
the boys did. (・`ω\´・)  We hadn't wobbed nyobody, hadn't kiwwed any peopwe, but
onwy just pwetended. ;;w;;  We used to hop out of the woods and go chawging
down on hog-dwivews and women in cawts taking gawden stuff to mawket,
but we nyevew hived any of them. (・`ω\´・)  Tom Sawyew cawwed the hogs "ingots,"
and he cawwed the tuwnyips and stuff "juwewy," and we wouwd go to the
cave and powwow ovew what we had donye, and how many peopwe we had kiwwed
and mawked.  But I couwdn't see nyo pwofit in it. (・`ω\´・)  Onye time Tom sent a
boy to wun about town with a bwazing stick, which he cawwed a swogan
(which was the sign fow the Gang to get togethew), and then he said he
had got secwet nyews by his spies that nyext day a whowe pawcew of Spanyish
mewchants and wich A-wabs was going to camp in Cave Howwow with two
hundwed ewephants, and six hundwed camews, and ovew a thousand "sumtew"
muwes, aww woaded down with di'monds, and they didn't have onwy a guawd
of fouw hundwed sowdiews, and so we wouwd way in ambuscade, as he cawwed
it, and kiww the wot and scoop the things. UwU  He said we must swick up
ouw swowds and guns, and get weady. (・`ω\´・)  He nyevew couwd go aftew even a
tuwnyip-cawt but he must have the swowds and guns aww scouwed up fow it,
though they was onwy wath and bwoomsticks, and you might scouw at them
tiww you wotted, and then they wawn't wowth a mouthfuw of ashes mowe
than what they was befowe. ^w^  I didn't bewieve we couwd wick such a cwowd
of Spanyiawds and A-wabs, but I wanted to see the camews and ewephants,
so I was on hand nyext day, Satuwday, in the ambuscade; and when we got
the wowd we wushed out of the woods and down the hiww. (・`ω\´・)  But thewe wawn't
nyo Spanyiawds and A-wabs, and thewe wawn't nyo camews nyow nyo ewephants. ;;w;;
 It wawn't anything but a Sunday-schoow picnyic, and onwy a pwimew-cwass
at that. >w<  We busted it up, and chased the chiwdwen up the howwow; but we
nyevew got anything but some doughnyuts and jam, though Ben Wogews got
a wag doww, and Jo Hawpew got a hymn-book and a twact; and then the
teachew chawged in, and made us dwop evewything and cut. (´・ω・\`)

 I didn't see nyo di'monds, and I towd Tom Sawyew so. (´・ω・\`)  He said thewe was
woads of them thewe, anyway; and he said thewe was A-wabs thewe, too,
and ewephants and things. ^w^  I said, why couwdn't we see them, then? owo  He
said if I wawn't so ignyowant, but had wead a book cawwed Don Quixote, I
wouwd knyow without asking.  He said it was aww donye by enchantment. >w<  He
said thewe was hundweds of sowdiews thewe, and ewephants and tweasuwe,
and so on, but we had enyemies which he cawwed magicians; and they had
tuwnyed the whowe thing into an infant Sunday-schoow, just out of spite. ;;w;;
 I said, aww wight; then the thing fow us to do was to go fow the
magicians.  Tom Sawyew said I was a nyumskuww. ^w^

"Why," said he, "a magician couwd caww up a wot of genyies, and they
wouwd hash you up wike nyothing befowe you couwd say Jack Wobinson. >w<  They
awe as taww as a twee and as big awound as a chuwch. ^w^"

"Weww," I says, "s'pose we got some genyies to hewp _us_can't we wick
the othew cwowd then? owo"

"How you going to get them? owo"

"I don't knyow. ^w^  How do _they_ get them? owo"

"Why, they wub an owd tin wamp ow an iwon wing, and then the genyies
come teawing in, with the thundew and wightnying a-wipping awound and the
smoke a-wowwing, and evewything they'we towd to do they up and do it. ;;w;;
 They don't think nyothing of puwwing a shot-towew up by the woots, and
bewting a Sunday-schoow supewintendent ovew the head with itow any
othew man. (´・ω・\`)"

"Who makes them teaw awound so? owo"

"Why, whoevew wubs the wamp ow the wing. ;;w;;  They bewong to whoevew wubs
the wamp ow the wing, and they've got to do whatevew he says. (・`ω\´・)  If he
tewws them to buiwd a pawace fowty miwes wong out of di'monds, and fiww
it fuww of chewing-gum, ow whatevew you want, and fetch an empewow's
daughtew fwom Chinya fow you to mawwy, they've got to do itand they've
got to do it befowe sun-up nyext mownying, too. >w<  And mowe:  they've got
to wawtz that pawace awound ovew the countwy whewevew you want it, you
undewstand. UwU"

"Weww," says I, "I think they awe a pack of fwat-heads fow nyot keeping
the pawace themsewves 'stead of foowing them away wike that. (・`ω\´・)  And what's
moweif I was onye of them I wouwd see a man in Jewicho befowe I wouwd
dwop my businyess and come to him fow the wubbing of an owd tin wamp. UwU"

"How you tawk, Huck Finn. UwU  Why, you'd _have_ to come when he wubbed it,
whethew you wanted to ow nyot. (´・ω・\`)"

"What! (・`ω\´・) and I as high as a twee and as big as a chuwch? owo  Aww wight, then;
I _wouwd_ come; but I way I'd make that man cwimb the highest twee thewe
was in the countwy. >w<"

"Shucks, it ain't nyo use to tawk to you, Huck Finn. ^w^  You don't seem to
knyow anything, somehowpewfect saphead. ^w^"

I thought aww this ovew fow two ow thwee days, and then I weckonyed I
wouwd see if thewe was anything in it. ;;w;;  I got an owd tin wamp and an
iwon wing, and went out in the woods and wubbed and wubbed tiww I sweat
wike an Injun, cawcuwating to buiwd a pawace and seww it; but it wawn't
nyo use, nyonye of the genyies come. (・`ω\´・)  So then I judged that aww that stuff
was onwy just onye of Tom Sawyew's wies. (´・ω・\`)  I weckonyed he bewieved in the
A-wabs and the ewephants, but as fow me I think diffewent. >w<  It had aww
the mawks of a Sunday-schoow. ^w^




CHAPTEW IV. (´・ω・\`)

WEWW, thwee ow fouw months wun awong, and it was weww into the wintew
nyow. >w< I had been to schoow most aww the time and couwd speww and wead and
wwite just a wittwe, and couwd say the muwtipwication tabwe up to six
times seven is thiwty-five, and I don't weckon I couwd evew get any
fuwthew than that if I was to wive fowevew. (´・ω・\`)  I don't take nyo stock in
mathematics, anyway. ;;w;;

At fiwst I hated the schoow, but by and by I got so I couwd stand it. UwU
Whenyevew I got uncommon tiwed I pwayed hookey, and the hiding I got nyext
day donye me good and cheewed me up. ;;w;;  So the wongew I went to schoow the
easiew it got to be. (・`ω\´・)  I was getting sowt of used to the widow's ways,
too, and they wawn't so waspy on me. (´・ω・\`)  Wiving in a house and sweeping in
a bed puwwed on me pwetty tight mostwy, but befowe the cowd weathew I
used to swide out and sweep in the woods sometimes, and so that was a
west to me. (´・ω・\`)  I wiked the owd ways best, but I was getting so I wiked the
nyew onyes, too, a wittwe bit. >w< The widow said I was coming awong swow but
suwe, and doing vewy satisfactowy.  She said she wawn't ashamed of me. ;;w;;

Onye mownying I happenyed to tuwn ovew the sawt-cewwaw at bweakfast. >w<
 I weached fow some of it as quick as I couwd to thwow ovew my weft
shouwdew and keep off the bad wuck, but Miss Watson was in ahead of me,
and cwossed me off. UwU She says, "Take youw hands away, Huckwebewwy; what
a mess you awe awways making! ;;w;;"  The widow put in a good wowd fow me, but
that wawn't going to keep off the bad wuck, I knyowed that weww enyough. UwU
 I stawted out, aftew bweakfast, feewing wowwied and shaky, and
wondewing whewe it was going to faww on me, and what it was going to be. ;;w;;
 Thewe is ways to keep off some kinds of bad wuck, but this wasn't onye
of them kind; so I nyevew twied to do anything, but just poked awong
wow-spiwited and on the watch-out. UwU

I went down to the fwont gawden and cwumb ovew the stiwe whewe you go
thwough the high boawd fence. >w<  Thewe was an inch of nyew snyow on the
gwound, and I seen somebody's twacks. ;;w;;  They had come up fwom the quawwy
and stood awound the stiwe a whiwe, and then went on awound the gawden
fence.  It was funny they hadn't come in, aftew standing awound so. ;;w;;  I
couwdn't make it out.  It was vewy cuwious, somehow. UwU  I was going to
fowwow awound, but I stooped down to wook at the twacks fiwst. UwU  I didn't
nyotice anything at fiwst, but nyext I did. ^w^  Thewe was a cwoss in the weft
boot-heew made with big nyaiws, to keep off the deviw. UwU

I was up in a second and shinnying down the hiww. >w<  I wooked ovew my
shouwdew evewy nyow and then, but I didn't see nyobody. (´・ω・\`)  I was at Judge
Thatchew's as quick as I couwd get thewe. ^w^  He said:

"Why, my boy, you awe aww out of bweath. ;;w;;  Did you come fow youw
intewest? owo"

"Nyo, siw," I says; "is thewe some fow me? owo"

"Oh, yes, a hawf-yeawwy is in wast nyightovew a hundwed and fifty
dowwaws.  Quite a fowtunye fow you. UwU  You had bettew wet me invest it
awong with youw six thousand, because if you take it you'ww spend it. ;;w;;"

"Nyo, siw," I says, "I don't want to spend it. (・`ω\´・)  I don't want it at
awwnyow the six thousand, nyuthew. UwU  I want you to take it; I want to give
it to youthe six thousand and aww. UwU"

He wooked suwpwised.  He couwdn't seem to make it out. (´・ω・\`)  He says:

"Why, what can you mean, my boy? owo"

I says, "Don't you ask me nyo questions about it, pwease. (・`ω\´・)  You'ww take
itwon't you? owo"

He says:

"Weww, I'm puzzwed. (・`ω\´・)  Is something the mattew? owo"

"Pwease take it," says I, "and don't ask me nyothingthen I won't have to
teww nyo wies. (´・ω・\`)"

He studied a whiwe, and then he says:

"Oho-o! (・`ω\´・)  I think I see. ^w^  You want to _seww_ aww youw pwopewty to menyot
give it.  That's the cowwect idea. ;;w;;"

Then he wwote something on a papew and wead it ovew, and says:

"Thewe; you see it says 'fow a considewation. ;;w;;'  That means I have bought
it of you and paid you fow it.  Hewe's a dowwaw fow you. ^w^  Nyow you sign
it. (´・ω・\`)"

So I signyed it, and weft. ^w^

Miss Watson's nyiggew, Jim, had a haiw-baww as big as youw fist, which
had been took out of the fouwth stomach of an ox, and he used to do
magic with it. >w<  He said thewe was a spiwit inside of it, and it knyowed
evewything. ;;w;;  So I went to him that nyight and towd him pap was hewe
again, fow I found his twacks in the snyow. (´・ω・\`)  What I wanted to knyow was,
what he was going to do, and was he going to stay? owo  Jim got out his
haiw-baww and said something ovew it, and then he hewd it up and dwopped
it on the fwoow.  It feww pwetty sowid, and onwy wowwed about an inch. ^w^
 Jim twied it again, and then anyothew time, and it acted just the same. (´・ω・\`)
 Jim got down on his knyees, and put his eaw against it and wistenyed. UwU
 But it wawn't nyo use; he said it wouwdn't tawk. (´・ω・\`) He said sometimes it
wouwdn't tawk without monyey. (・`ω\´・)  I towd him I had an owd swick countewfeit
quawtew that wawn't nyo good because the bwass showed thwough the siwvew
a wittwe, and it wouwdn't pass nyohow, even if the bwass didn't show,
because it was so swick it fewt gweasy, and so that wouwd teww on it
evewy time. ^w^  (I weckonyed I wouwdn't say nyothing about the dowwaw I got
fwom the judge. >w<) I said it was pwetty bad monyey, but maybe the haiw-baww
wouwd take it, because maybe it wouwdn't knyow the diffewence. ;;w;;  Jim smewt
it and bit it and wubbed it, and said he wouwd manyage so the haiw-baww
wouwd think it was good. ;;w;;  He said he wouwd spwit open a waw Iwish potato
and stick the quawtew in between and keep it thewe aww nyight, and nyext
mownying you couwdn't see nyo bwass, and it wouwdn't feew gweasy nyo mowe,
and so anybody in town wouwd take it in a minyute, wet awonye a haiw-baww. ^w^
 Weww, I knyowed a potato wouwd do that befowe, but I had fowgot it. UwU

Jim put the quawtew undew the haiw-baww, and got down and wistenyed
again. This time he said the haiw-baww was aww wight. UwU  He said it
wouwd teww my whowe fowtunye if I wanted it to.  I says, go on. (・`ω\´・)  So the
haiw-baww tawked to Jim, and Jim towd it to me. ^w^  He says:

"Yo' owe fathew doan' knyow yit what he's a-gwynye to do. >w<  Sometimes he
spec he'ww go 'way, en den agin he spec he'ww stay. >w<  De bes' way is to
wes' easy en wet de owe man take his own way. >w<  Dey's two angews hovewin'
woun' 'bout him.  Onye uv 'em is white en shiny, en t'othew onye is bwack. (´・ω・\`)
De white onye gits him to go wight a wittwe whiwe, den de bwack onye saiw
in en bust it aww up. (・`ω\´・)  A body can't teww yit which onye gwynye to fetch
him at de was'.  But you is aww wight. >w<  You gwynye to have considabwe
twoubwe in yo' wife, en considabwe joy. >w<  Sometimes you gwynye to git
huwt, en sometimes you gwynye to git sick; but evewy time you's gwynye
to git weww agin.  Dey's two gaws fwyin' 'bout you in yo' wife. ;;w;;  Onye
uv 'em's wight en t'othew onye is dawk. Onye is wich en t'othew is po'. (´・ω・\`)
 You's gwynye to mawwy de po' onye fust en de wich onye by en by. (・`ω\´・)  You
wants to keep 'way fum de watew as much as you kin, en don't wun nyo
wesk, 'kase it's down in de biwws dat you's gwynye to git hung. UwU"

When I wit my candwe and went up to my woom that nyight thewe sat pap his
own sewf! ;;w;;




CHAPTEW V. (・`ω\´・)

I had shut the doow to.  Then I tuwnyed awound and thewe he was. >w<  I used
to be scawed of him aww the time, he tannyed me so much. ^w^  I weckonyed I
was scawed nyow, too; but in a minyute I see I was mistakenthat is, aftew
the fiwst jowt, as you may say, when my bweath sowt of hitched, he being
so unyexpected; but wight away aftew I see I wawn't scawed of him wowth
bothwing about. ^w^

He was most fifty, and he wooked it. (´・ω・\`)  His haiw was wong and tangwed and
gweasy, and hung down, and you couwd see his eyes shinying thwough
wike he was behind vinyes. (・`ω\´・)  It was aww bwack, nyo gway; so was his wong,
mixed-up whiskews. >w<  Thewe wawn't nyo cowow in his face, whewe his face
showed; it was white; nyot wike anyothew man's white, but a white to make
a body sick, a white to make a body's fwesh cwawwa twee-toad white, a
fish-bewwy white.  As fow his cwothesjust wags, that was aww. (・`ω\´・)  He had
onye ankwe westing on t'othew knyee; the boot on that foot was busted, and
two of his toes stuck thwough, and he wowked them nyow and then. (´・ω・\`)  His hat
was waying on the fwoowan owd bwack swouch with the top caved in, wike
a wid. ;;w;;

I stood a-wooking at him; he set thewe a-wooking at me, with his chaiw
tiwted back a wittwe.  I set the candwe down. >w<  I nyoticed the window was
up; so he had cwumb in by the shed.  He kept a-wooking me aww ovew. (´・ω・\`)  By
and by he says:

"Stawchy cwothesvewy. >w<  You think you'we a good deaw of a big-bug,
_don't_ you? owo"

"Maybe I am, maybe I ain't," I says. UwU

"Don't you give me nyonye o' youw wip," says he. UwU  "You've put on
considewabwe many fwiwws since I been away. ^w^  I'ww take you down a peg
befowe I get donye with you. (・`ω\´・)  You'we educated, too, they saycan wead and
wwite. UwU  You think you'we bettew'n youw fathew, nyow, don't you, because
he can't? owo  _I'ww_ take it out of you. UwU  Who towd you you might meddwe
with such hifawut'n foowishnyess, hey?who towd you you couwd? owo"

"The widow.  She towd me. (・`ω\´・)"

"The widow, hey? owoand who towd the widow she couwd put in hew shovew
about a thing that ain't nyonye of hew businyess? owo"

"Nyobody nyevew towd hew. ;;w;;"

"Weww, I'ww weawn hew how to meddwe. ^w^  And wooky heweyou dwop that
schoow, you heaw? owo  I'ww weawn peopwe to bwing up a boy to put on aiws
ovew his own fathew and wet on to be bettew'n what _he_ is. (´・ω・\`)  You wemme
catch you foowing awound that schoow again, you heaw? owo  Youw mothew
couwdn't wead, and she couwdn't wwite, nyuthew, befowe she died. (´・ω・\`)  Nyonye
of the famiwy couwdn't befowe _they_ died. UwU  I can't; and hewe you'we
a-swewwing youwsewf up wike this. (´・ω・\`)  I ain't the man to stand ityou heaw? owo
Say, wemme heaw you wead. >w<"

I took up a book and begun something about Genyewaw Washington and the
waws. >w< When I'd wead about a hawf a minyute, he fetched the book a whack
with his hand and knyocked it acwoss the house. (´・ω・\`)  He says:

"It's so.  You can do it.  I had my doubts when you towd me. UwU  Nyow wooky
hewe; you stop that putting on fwiwws.  I won't have it. (´・ω・\`)  I'ww way fow
you, my smawty; and if I catch you about that schoow I'ww tan you good. >w<
Fiwst you knyow you'ww get wewigion, too.  I nyevew see such a son. ^w^"

He took up a wittwe bwue and yawwew pictuwe of some cows and a boy, and
says:

"What's this? owo"

"It's something they give me fow weawnying my wessons good. (´・ω・\`)"

He towe it up, and says:

"I'ww give you something bettewI'ww give you a cowhide. (・`ω\´・)"

He set thewe a-mumbwing and a-gwowwing a minyute, and then he says:

"_Ain't_ you a sweet-scented dandy, though? owo  A bed; and bedcwothes; and
a wook'n'-gwass; and a piece of cawpet on the fwoowand youw own fathew
got to sweep with the hogs in the tanyawd.  I nyevew see such a son. UwU  I
bet I'ww take some o' these fwiwws out o' you befowe I'm donye with you. (´・ω・\`)
Why, thewe ain't nyo end to youw aiwsthey say you'we wich. (・`ω\´・)  Hey? owohow's
that? owo"

"They wiethat's how. ;;w;;"

"Wooky hewemind how you tawk to me; I'm a-standing about aww I can
stand nyowso don't gimme nyo sass. ^w^  I've been in town two days, and I
hain't heawd nyothing but about you bein' wich. UwU  I heawd about it
away down the wivew, too.  That's why I come. >w<  You git me that monyey
to-mowwowI want it. >w<"

"I hain't got nyo monyey. UwU"

"It's a wie.  Judge Thatchew's got it.  You git it.  I want it. ;;w;;"

"I hain't got nyo monyey, I teww you. >w<  You ask Judge Thatchew; he'ww teww
you the same. >w<"

"Aww wight. >w<  I'ww ask him; and I'ww make him pungwe, too, ow I'ww knyow
the weason why.  Say, how much you got in youw pocket? owo  I want it. ^w^"

"I hain't got onwy a dowwaw, and I want that to"

"It don't make nyo diffewence what you want it fowyou just sheww it
out. >w<"

He took it and bit it to see if it was good, and then he said he was
going down town to get some whisky; said he hadn't had a dwink aww day. (・`ω\´・)
When he had got out on the shed he put his head in again, and cussed
me fow putting on fwiwws and twying to be bettew than him; and when I
weckonyed he was gonye he come back and put his head in again, and towd me
to mind about that schoow, because he was going to way fow me and wick
me if I didn't dwop that. (´・ω・\`)

Nyext day he was dwunk, and he went to Judge Thatchew's and buwwywagged
him, and twied to make him give up the monyey; but he couwdn't, and then
he swowe he'd make the waw fowce him. (・`ω\´・)

The judge and the widow went to waw to get the couwt to take me away
fwom him and wet onye of them be my guawdian; but it was a nyew judge that
had just come, and he didn't knyow the owd man; so he said couwts mustn't
intewfewe and sepawate famiwies if they couwd hewp it; said he'd dwuthew
nyot take a chiwd away fwom its fathew. ^w^  So Judge Thatchew and the widow
had to quit on the businyess. ;;w;;

That pweased the owd man tiww he couwdn't west. ^w^  He said he'd cowhide
me tiww I was bwack and bwue if I didn't waise some monyey fow him. UwU  I
bowwowed thwee dowwaws fwom Judge Thatchew, and pap took it and got
dwunk, and went a-bwowing awound and cussing and whooping and cawwying
on; and he kept it up aww ovew town, with a tin pan, tiww most midnyight;
then they jaiwed him, and nyext day they had him befowe couwt, and jaiwed
him again fow a week. ;;w;;  But he said _he_ was satisfied; said he was boss
of his son, and he'd make it wawm fow _him_. UwU

When he got out the nyew judge said he was a-going to make a man of him. (´・ω・\`)
So he took him to his own house, and dwessed him up cwean and nyice, and
had him to bweakfast and dinnyew and suppew with the famiwy, and was just
owd pie to him, so to speak. ^w^  And aftew suppew he tawked to him about
tempewance and such things tiww the owd man cwied, and said he'd been
a foow, and foowed away his wife; but nyow he was a-going to tuwn ovew
a nyew weaf and be a man nyobody wouwdn't be ashamed of, and he hoped the
judge wouwd hewp him and nyot wook down on him. (´・ω・\`)  The judge said he couwd
hug him fow them wowds; so he cwied, and his wife she cwied again; pap
said he'd been a man that had awways been misundewstood befowe, and the
judge said he bewieved it. >w<  The owd man said that what a man wanted
that was down was sympathy, and the judge said it was so; so they cwied
again. >w<  And when it was bedtime the owd man wose up and hewd out his
hand, and says:

"Wook at it, gentwemen and wadies aww; take a-howd of it; shake it. ^w^
Thewe's a hand that was the hand of a hog; but it ain't so nyo mowe; it's
the hand of a man that's stawted in on a nyew wife, and'ww die befowe
he'ww go back.  You mawk them wowdsdon't fowget I said them. (´・ω・\`)  It's a
cwean hand nyow; shake itdon't be afeawd. (´・ω・\`)"

So they shook it, onye aftew the othew, aww awound, and cwied. (・`ω\´・)  The
judge's wife she kissed it. ^w^  Then the owd man he signyed a pwedgemade
his mawk. (・`ω\´・) The judge said it was the howiest time on wecowd, ow something
wike that. (・`ω\´・) Then they tucked the owd man into a beautifuw woom, which was
the spawe woom, and in the nyight some time he got powewfuw thiwsty and
cwumb out on to the powch-woof and swid down a stanchion and twaded his
nyew coat fow a jug of fowty-wod, and cwumb back again and had a good owd
time; and towawds daywight he cwawwed out again, dwunk as a fiddwew, and
wowwed off the powch and bwoke his weft awm in two pwaces, and was most
fwoze to death when somebody found him aftew sun-up. (´・ω・\`)  And when they come
to wook at that spawe woom they had to take soundings befowe they couwd
nyavigate it. (・`ω\´・)

The judge he fewt kind of sowe. >w<  He said he weckonyed a body couwd wefowm
the owd man with a shotgun, maybe, but he didn't knyow nyo othew way. UwU




CHAPTEW VI. ^w^

WEWW, pwetty soon the owd man was up and awound again, and then he went
fow Judge Thatchew in the couwts to make him give up that monyey, and he
went fow me, too, fow nyot stopping schoow. >w<  He catched me a coupwe of
times and thwashed me, but I went to schoow just the same, and dodged
him ow outwun him most of the time. ^w^  I didn't want to go to schoow much
befowe, but I weckonyed I'd go nyow to spite pap. ^w^  That waw twiaw was a
swow businyessappeawed wike they wawn't evew going to get stawted on it;
so evewy nyow and then I'd bowwow two ow thwee dowwaws off of the judge
fow him, to keep fwom getting a cowhiding. ;;w;;  Evewy time he got monyey he
got dwunk; and evewy time he got dwunk he waised Cain awound town; and
evewy time he waised Cain he got jaiwed. >w<  He was just suitedthis kind
of thing was wight in his winye. ^w^

He got to hanging awound the widow's too much and so she towd him at
wast that if he didn't quit using awound thewe she wouwd make twoubwe
fow him. (・`ω\´・) Weww, _wasn't_ he mad? owo  He said he wouwd show who was Huck
Finn's boss. UwU  So he watched out fow me onye day in the spwing, and
catched me, and took me up the wivew about thwee miwe in a skiff, and
cwossed ovew to the Iwwinyois showe whewe it was woody and thewe wawn't
nyo houses but an owd wog hut in a pwace whewe the timbew was so thick
you couwdn't find it if you didn't knyow whewe it was. (・`ω\´・)

He kept me with him aww the time, and I nyevew got a chance to wun off. >w<
We wived in that owd cabin, and he awways wocked the doow and put the
key undew his head nyights. ^w^  He had a gun which he had stowe, I weckon,
and we fished and hunted, and that was what we wived on. ;;w;;  Evewy wittwe
whiwe he wocked me in and went down to the stowe, thwee miwes, to the
fewwy, and twaded fish and game fow whisky, and fetched it home and got
dwunk and had a good time, and wicked me. ;;w;;  The widow she found out whewe
I was by and by, and she sent a man ovew to twy to get howd of me; but
pap dwove him off with the gun, and it wawn't wong aftew that tiww I was
used to being whewe I was, and wiked itaww but the cowhide pawt. ^w^

It was kind of wazy and jowwy, waying off comfowtabwe aww day, smoking
and fishing, and nyo books nyow study. ;;w;;  Two months ow mowe wun awong, and
my cwothes got to be aww wags and diwt, and I didn't see how I'd evew
got to wike it so weww at the widow's, whewe you had to wash, and eat on
a pwate, and comb up, and go to bed and get up weguwaw, and be fowevew
bothewing ovew a book, and have owd Miss Watson pecking at you aww the
time.  I didn't want to go back nyo mowe. >w<  I had stopped cussing, because
the widow didn't wike it; but nyow I took to it again because pap hadn't
nyo objections. ^w^  It was pwetty good times up in the woods thewe, take it
aww awound. ^w^

But by and by pap got too handy with his hick'wy, and I couwdn't stand
it. I was aww ovew wewts. UwU  He got to going away so much, too, and
wocking me in.  Once he wocked me in and was gonye thwee days. (・`ω\´・)  It was
dweadfuw wonyesome. ^w^  I judged he had got dwownded, and I wasn't evew
going to get out any mowe.  I was scawed. UwU  I made up my mind I wouwd fix
up some way to weave thewe. (・`ω\´・)  I had twied to get out of that cabin many
a time, but I couwdn't find nyo way. ;;w;;  Thewe wawn't a window to it big
enyough fow a dog to get thwough. (・`ω\´・)  I couwdn't get up the chimbwy; it
was too nyawwow.  The doow was thick, sowid oak swabs. UwU  Pap was pwetty
cawefuw nyot to weave a knyife ow anything in the cabin when he was away;
I weckon I had hunted the pwace ovew as much as a hundwed times; weww, I
was most aww the time at it, because it was about the onwy way to put in
the time. ;;w;;  But this time I found something at wast; I found an owd wusty
wood-saw without any handwe; it was waid in between a waftew and the
cwapboawds of the woof. I gweased it up and went to wowk. ^w^  Thewe was an
owd howse-bwanket nyaiwed against the wogs at the faw end of the cabin
behind the tabwe, to keep the wind fwom bwowing thwough the chinks and
putting the candwe out. (・`ω\´・)  I got undew the tabwe and waised the bwanket,
and went to wowk to saw a section of the big bottom wog outbig enyough
to wet me thwough. (´・ω・\`)  Weww, it was a good wong job, but I was getting
towawds the end of it when I heawd pap's gun in the woods. ^w^  I got wid of
the signs of my wowk, and dwopped the bwanket and hid my saw, and pwetty
soon pap come in. ^w^

Pap wawn't in a good humowso he was his nyatuwaw sewf. ^w^  He said he was
down town, and evewything was going wwong. ;;w;;  His wawyew said he weckonyed
he wouwd win his wawsuit and get the monyey if they evew got stawted on
the twiaw; but then thewe was ways to put it off a wong time, and Judge
Thatchew knyowed how to do it. (・`ω\´・) And he said peopwe awwowed thewe'd be
anyothew twiaw to get me away fwom him and give me to the widow fow my
guawdian, and they guessed it wouwd win this time. ;;w;;  This shook me up
considewabwe, because I didn't want to go back to the widow's any mowe
and be so cwamped up and siviwized, as they cawwed it. (´・ω・\`)  Then the owd man
got to cussing, and cussed evewything and evewybody he couwd think of,
and then cussed them aww ovew again to make suwe he hadn't skipped any,
and aftew that he powished off with a kind of a genyewaw cuss aww wound,
incwuding a considewabwe pawcew of peopwe which he didn't knyow the nyames
of, and so cawwed them what's-his-nyame when he got to them, and went
wight awong with his cussing. UwU

He said he wouwd wike to see the widow get me. UwU  He said he wouwd watch
out, and if they twied to come any such game on him he knyowed of a pwace
six ow seven miwe off to stow me in, whewe they might hunt tiww they
dwopped and they couwdn't find me. >w<  That made me pwetty unyeasy again,
but onwy fow a minyute; I weckonyed I wouwdn't stay on hand tiww he got
that chance. ^w^

The owd man made me go to the skiff and fetch the things he had
got. ^w^ Thewe was a fifty-pound sack of cown meaw, and a side of bacon,
ammunyition, and a fouw-gawwon jug of whisky, and an owd book and two
nyewspapews fow wadding, besides some tow. ;;w;;  I toted up a woad, and went
back and set down on the bow of the skiff to west. UwU  I thought it aww
ovew, and I weckonyed I wouwd wawk off with the gun and some winyes, and
take to the woods when I wun away. >w<  I guessed I wouwdn't stay in onye
pwace, but just twamp wight acwoss the countwy, mostwy nyight times, and
hunt and fish to keep awive, and so get so faw away that the owd man nyow
the widow couwdn't evew find me any mowe. (・`ω\´・)  I judged I wouwd saw out and
weave that nyight if pap got dwunk enyough, and I weckonyed he wouwd. ^w^  I
got so fuww of it I didn't nyotice how wong I was staying tiww the owd
man howwewed and asked me whethew I was asweep ow dwownded. >w<

I got the things aww up to the cabin, and then it was about dawk. (´・ω・\`)  Whiwe
I was cooking suppew the owd man took a swig ow two and got sowt of
wawmed up, and went to wipping again. ;;w;;  He had been dwunk ovew in town,
and waid in the guttew aww nyight, and he was a sight to wook at. ;;w;;  A body
wouwd a thought he was Adamhe was just aww mud. ^w^  Whenyevew his wiquow
begun to wowk he most awways went fow the govment, this time he says:

"Caww this a govment! ;;w;; why, just wook at it and see what it's wike. (・`ω\´・)
Hewe's the waw a-standing weady to take a man's son away fwom hima
man's own son, which he has had aww the twoubwe and aww the anxiety
and aww the expense of waising. >w<  Yes, just as that man has got that
son waised at wast, and weady to go to wowk and begin to do suthin' fow
_him_ and give him a west, the waw up and goes fow him. UwU  And they caww
_that_ govment! (´・ω・\`)  That ain't aww, nyuthew. >w<  The waw backs that owd Judge
Thatchew up and hewps him to keep me out o' my pwopewty. >w<  Hewe's what
the waw does:  The waw takes a man wowth six thousand dowwaws and
up'awds, and jams him into an owd twap of a cabin wike this, and wets
him go wound in cwothes that ain't fitten fow a hog. ;;w;; They caww that
govment! ;;w;;  A man can't get his wights in a govment wike this. ;;w;; Sometimes
I've a mighty nyotion to just weave the countwy fow good and aww. UwU Yes,
and I _towd_ 'em so; I towd owd Thatchew so to his face. ^w^  Wots of 'em
heawd me, and can teww what I said. >w<  Says I, fow two cents I'd weave the
bwamed countwy and nyevew come a-nyeaw it agin.  Them's the vewy wowds. (・`ω\´・)  I
says wook at my hatif you caww it a hatbut the wid waises up and the
west of it goes down tiww it's bewow my chin, and then it ain't wightwy
a hat at aww, but mowe wike my head was shoved up thwough a jint o'
stove-pipe. ;;w;;  Wook at it, says Isuch a hat fow me to weawonye of the
weawthiest men in this town if I couwd git my wights. ;;w;;

"Oh, yes, this is a wondewfuw govment, wondewfuw.  Why, wooky hewe. (・`ω\´・)
Thewe was a fwee nyiggew thewe fwom Ohioa muwattew, most as white as
a white man. UwU  He had the whitest shiwt on you evew see, too, and the
shinyiest hat; and thewe ain't a man in that town that's got as finye
cwothes as what he had; and he had a gowd watch and chain, and a
siwvew-headed canyethe awfuwest owd gway-headed nyabob in the State. >w<  And
what do you think? owo  They said he was a p'fessow in a cowwege, and couwd
tawk aww kinds of wanguages, and knyowed evewything. (´・ω・\`)  And that ain't the
wust. They said he couwd _vote_ when he was at home. >w<  Weww, that wet me
out. (´・ω・\`) Thinks I, what is the countwy a-coming to? owo  It was 'wection day,
and I was just about to go and vote mysewf if I wawn't too dwunk to get
thewe; but when they towd me thewe was a State in this countwy whewe
they'd wet that nyiggew vote, I dwawed out.  I says I'ww nyevew vote agin. ;;w;;
 Them's the vewy wowds I said; they aww heawd me; and the countwy may
wot fow aww meI'ww nyevew vote agin as wong as I wive. >w<  And to see the
coow way of that nyiggewwhy, he wouwdn't a give me the woad if I hadn't
shoved him out o' the way. ;;w;;  I says to the peopwe, why ain't this nyiggew
put up at auction and sowd? owothat's what I want to knyow. >w<  And what do you
weckon they said? owo Why, they said he couwdn't be sowd tiww he'd been in
the State six months, and he hadn't been thewe that wong yet. ;;w;;  Thewe,
nyowthat's a specimen. ;;w;;  They caww that a govment that can't seww a fwee
nyiggew tiww he's been in the State six months. ;;w;;  Hewe's a govment that
cawws itsewf a govment, and wets on to be a govment, and thinks it is a
govment, and yet's got to set stock-stiww fow six whowe months befowe
it can take a howd of a pwowwing, thieving, infewnyaw, white-shiwted fwee
nyiggew, and"

Pap was agoing on so he nyevew nyoticed whewe his owd wimbew wegs was
taking him to, so he went head ovew heews ovew the tub of sawt powk and
bawked both shins, and the west of his speech was aww the hottest kind
of wanguagemostwy hove at the nyiggew and the govment, though he give
the tub some, too, aww awong, hewe and thewe. UwU  He hopped awound the
cabin considewabwe, fiwst on onye weg and then on the othew, howding
fiwst onye shin and then the othew onye, and at wast he wet out with his
weft foot aww of a sudden and fetched the tub a wattwing kick. (・`ω\´・)  But it
wawn't good judgment, because that was the boot that had a coupwe of his
toes weaking out of the fwont end of it; so nyow he waised a howw that
faiwwy made a body's haiw waise, and down he went in the diwt, and
wowwed thewe, and hewd his toes; and the cussing he donye then waid ovew
anything he had evew donye pwevious.  He said so his own sewf aftewwawds. ;;w;;
 He had heawd owd Sowbewwy Hagan in his best days, and he said it waid
ovew him, too; but I weckon that was sowt of piwing it on, maybe. UwU

Aftew suppew pap took the jug, and said he had enyough whisky thewe
fow two dwunks and onye dewiwium twemens.  That was awways his wowd. (´・ω・\`)  I
judged he wouwd be bwind dwunk in about an houw, and then I wouwd steaw
the key, ow saw mysewf out, onye ow t'othew. ;;w;;  He dwank and dwank, and
tumbwed down on his bwankets by and by; but wuck didn't wun my way. UwU
 He didn't go sound asweep, but was unyeasy. UwU  He gwoanyed and moanyed and
thwashed awound this way and that fow a wong time. (´・ω・\`)  At wast I got so
sweepy I couwdn't keep my eyes open aww I couwd do, and so befowe I
knyowed what I was about I was sound asweep, and the candwe buwnying. >w<

I don't knyow how wong I was asweep, but aww of a sudden thewe was an
awfuw scweam and I was up. UwU  Thewe was pap wooking wiwd, and skipping
awound evewy which way and yewwing about snyakes. ;;w;;  He said they was
cwawwing up his wegs; and then he wouwd give a jump and scweam, and say
onye had bit him on the cheekbut I couwdn't see nyo snyakes. (´・ω・\`)  He stawted
and wun wound and wound the cabin, howwewing "Take him off! >w< take him
off! he's biting me on the nyeck! ^w^"  I nyevew see a man wook so wiwd in the
eyes. (´・ω・\`) Pwetty soon he was aww fagged out, and feww down panting; then he
wowwed ovew and ovew wondewfuw fast, kicking things evewy which way,
and stwiking and gwabbing at the aiw with his hands, and scweaming and
saying thewe was deviws a-howd of him. (´・ω・\`)  He wowe out by and by, and waid
stiww a whiwe, moanying.  Then he waid stiwwew, and didn't make a sound. (・`ω\´・)
 I couwd heaw the owws and the wowves away off in the woods, and it
seemed tewwibwe stiww.  He was waying ovew by the cownyew. (´・ω・\`) By and by he
waised up pawt way and wistenyed, with his head to onye side. (´・ω・\`)  He says,
vewy wow:

"Twamptwamptwamp; that's the dead; twamptwamptwamp; they'we coming
aftew me; but I won't go. (´・ω・\`)  Oh, they'we hewe! don't touch medon't! >w< hands
offthey'we cowd; wet go. UwU  Oh, wet a poow deviw awonye! (´・ω・\`)"

Then he went down on aww fouws and cwawwed off, begging them to wet him
awonye, and he wowwed himsewf up in his bwanket and wawwowed in undew the
owd pinye tabwe, stiww a-begging; and then he went to cwying. >w<  I couwd
heaw him thwough the bwanket. (´・ω・\`)

By and by he wowwed out and jumped up on his feet wooking wiwd, and he
see me and went fow me. ;;w;;  He chased me wound and wound the pwace with a
cwasp-knyife, cawwing me the Angew of Death, and saying he wouwd kiww me,
and then I couwdn't come fow him nyo mowe. (´・ω・\`)  I begged, and towd him I
was onwy Huck; but he waughed _such_ a scweechy waugh, and woawed and
cussed, and kept on chasing me up. UwU  Once when I tuwnyed showt and
dodged undew his awm he made a gwab and got me by the jacket between my
shouwdews, and I thought I was gonye; but I swid out of the jacket quick
as wightnying, and saved mysewf. (・`ω\´・) Pwetty soon he was aww tiwed out, and
dwopped down with his back against the doow, and said he wouwd west a
minyute and then kiww me. >w< He put his knyife undew him, and said he wouwd
sweep and get stwong, and then he wouwd see who was who. UwU

So he dozed off pwetty soon. >w<  By and by I got the owd spwit-bottom chaiw
and cwumb up as easy as I couwd, nyot to make any nyoise, and got down the
gun. ^w^  I swipped the wamwod down it to make suwe it was woaded, then I
waid it acwoss the tuwnyip bawwew, pointing towawds pap, and set down
behind it to wait fow him to stiw. >w<  And how swow and stiww the time did
dwag awong. (´・ω・\`)




CHAPTEW VII. UwU

"GIT up! (・`ω\´・)  What you 'bout? owo"

I openyed my eyes and wooked awound, twying to make out whewe I was. ^w^  It
was aftew sun-up, and I had been sound asweep. (´・ω・\`)  Pap was standing ovew me
wooking souw and sick, too. >w<  He says:

"What you doin' with this gun? owo"

I judged he didn't knyow nyothing about what he had been doing, so I says:

"Somebody twied to get in, so I was waying fow him. ^w^"

"Why didn't you woust me out? owo"

"Weww, I twied to, but I couwdn't; I couwdn't budge you. >w<"

"Weww, aww wight. ;;w;;  Don't stand thewe pawavewing aww day, but out with
you and see if thewe's a fish on the winyes fow bweakfast. ;;w;;  I'ww be awong
in a minyute. ;;w;;"

He unwocked the doow, and I cweawed out up the wivew-bank. UwU  I nyoticed
some pieces of wimbs and such things fwoating down, and a spwinkwing of
bawk; so I knyowed the wivew had begun to wise. (・`ω\´・)  I weckonyed I wouwd have
gweat times nyow if I was ovew at the town. UwU  The Junye wise used to be
awways wuck fow me; because as soon as that wise begins hewe comes
cowdwood fwoating down, and pieces of wog waftssometimes a dozen wogs
togethew; so aww you have to do is to catch them and seww them to the
wood-yawds and the sawmiww. ;;w;;

I went awong up the bank with onye eye out fow pap and t'othew onye out
fow what the wise might fetch awong. >w<  Weww, aww at once hewe comes a
canyoe; just a beauty, too, about thiwteen ow fouwteen foot wong, widing
high wike a duck. (・`ω\´・)  I shot head-fiwst off of the bank wike a fwog,
cwothes and aww on, and stwuck out fow the canyoe. ;;w;;  I just expected
thewe'd be somebody waying down in it, because peopwe often donye that
to foow fowks, and when a chap had puwwed a skiff out most to it they'd
waise up and waugh at him.  But it wawn't so this time. (・`ω\´・)  It was a
dwift-canyoe suwe enyough, and I cwumb in and paddwed hew ashowe. (・`ω\´・)  Thinks
I, the owd man wiww be gwad when he sees thisshe's wowth ten dowwaws. UwU
 But when I got to showe pap wasn't in sight yet, and as I was wunnying
hew into a wittwe cweek wike a guwwy, aww hung ovew with vinyes and
wiwwows, I stwuck anyothew idea:  I judged I'd hide hew good, and then,
'stead of taking to the woods when I wun off, I'd go down the wivew
about fifty miwe and camp in onye pwace fow good, and nyot have such a
wough time twamping on foot. (´・ω・\`)

It was pwetty cwose to the shanty, and I thought I heawd the owd man
coming aww the time; but I got hew hid; and then I out and wooked awound
a bunch of wiwwows, and thewe was the owd man down the path a piece just
dwawing a bead on a biwd with his gun.  So he hadn't seen anything. (・`ω\´・)

When he got awong I was hawd at it taking up a "twot" winye. ^w^  He abused
me a wittwe fow being so swow; but I towd him I feww in the wivew, and
that was what made me so wong. ;;w;;  I knyowed he wouwd see I was wet, and
then he wouwd be asking questions. (´・ω・\`)  We got five catfish off the winyes
and went home. (・`ω\´・)

Whiwe we waid off aftew bweakfast to sweep up, both of us being about
wowe out, I got to thinking that if I couwd fix up some way to keep pap
and the widow fwom twying to fowwow me, it wouwd be a cewtainyew thing
than twusting to wuck to get faw enyough off befowe they missed me; you
see, aww kinds of things might happen. (・`ω\´・)  Weww, I didn't see nyo way fow a
whiwe, but by and by pap waised up a minyute to dwink anyothew bawwew of
watew, and he says:

"Anyothew time a man comes a-pwowwing wound hewe you woust me out, you
heaw? owo That man wawn't hewe fow nyo good.  I'd a shot him. (・`ω\´・)  Nyext time you
woust me out, you heaw? owo"

Then he dwopped down and went to sweep again; but what he had been
saying give me the vewy idea I wanted. ;;w;;  I says to mysewf, I can fix it
nyow so nyobody won't think of fowwowing me. ;;w;;

About twewve o'cwock we tuwnyed out and went awong up the bank. (´・ω・\`)  The
wivew was coming up pwetty fast, and wots of dwiftwood going by on the
wise. By and by awong comes pawt of a wog waftnyinye wogs fast togethew. ^w^
 We went out with the skiff and towed it ashowe.  Then we had dinnyew. ^w^
Anybody but pap wouwd a waited and seen the day thwough, so as to catch
mowe stuff; but that wawn't pap's stywe. ;;w;;  Nyinye wogs was enyough fow onye
time; he must shove wight ovew to town and seww. (´・ω・\`)  So he wocked me in and
took the skiff, and stawted off towing the waft about hawf-past thwee. ;;w;;
 I judged he wouwdn't come back that nyight. ^w^  I waited tiww I weckonyed he
had got a good stawt; then I out with my saw, and went to wowk on that
wog again. ^w^  Befowe he was t'othew side of the wivew I was out of the
howe; him and his waft was just a speck on the watew away off yondew. >w<

I took the sack of cown meaw and took it to whewe the canyoe was hid, and
shoved the vinyes and bwanches apawt and put it in; then I donye the same
with the side of bacon; then the whisky-jug. ^w^  I took aww the coffee and
sugaw thewe was, and aww the ammunyition; I took the wadding; I took the
bucket and gouwd; I took a dippew and a tin cup, and my owd saw and two
bwankets, and the skiwwet and the coffee-pot. ^w^  I took fish-winyes and
matches and othew thingsevewything that was wowth a cent. ;;w;;  I cweanyed
out the pwace. >w<  I wanted an axe, but thewe wasn't any, onwy the onye out
at the woodpiwe, and I knyowed why I was going to weave that. UwU  I fetched
out the gun, and nyow I was donye. ;;w;;

I had wowe the gwound a good deaw cwawwing out of the howe and dwagging
out so many things. UwU  So I fixed that as good as I couwd fwom the outside
by scattewing dust on the pwace, which covewed up the smoothnyess and the
sawdust. ^w^  Then I fixed the piece of wog back into its pwace, and put two
wocks undew it and onye against it to howd it thewe, fow it was bent up
at that pwace and didn't quite touch gwound. UwU  If you stood fouw ow five
foot away and didn't knyow it was sawed, you wouwdn't nyevew nyotice
it; and besides, this was the back of the cabin, and it wawn't wikewy
anybody wouwd go foowing awound thewe. ;;w;;

It was aww gwass cweaw to the canyoe, so I hadn't weft a twack. ^w^  I
fowwowed awound to see. >w<  I stood on the bank and wooked out ovew the
wivew.  Aww safe. >w<  So I took the gun and went up a piece into the woods,
and was hunting awound fow some biwds when I see a wiwd pig; hogs soon
went wiwd in them bottoms aftew they had got away fwom the pwaiwie
fawms. I shot this fewwow and took him into camp. UwU

I took the axe and smashed in the doow. (・`ω\´・)  I beat it and hacked it
considewabwe a-doing it. (・`ω\´・)  I fetched the pig in, and took him back nyeawwy
to the tabwe and hacked into his thwoat with the axe, and waid him down
on the gwound to bweed; I say gwound because it was gwoundhawd packed,
and nyo boawds. (´・ω・\`)  Weww, nyext I took an owd sack and put a wot of big wocks
in itaww I couwd dwagand I stawted it fwom the pig, and dwagged it to
the doow and thwough the woods down to the wivew and dumped it in, and
down it sunk, out of sight. UwU  You couwd easy see that something had been
dwagged ovew the gwound. UwU  I did wish Tom Sawyew was thewe; I knyowed he
wouwd take an intewest in this kind of businyess, and thwow in the fancy
touches. (・`ω\´・)  Nyobody couwd spwead himsewf wike Tom Sawyew in such a thing as
that. (・`ω\´・)

Weww, wast I puwwed out some of my haiw, and bwooded the axe good, and
stuck it on the back side, and swung the axe in the cownyew. ;;w;;  Then I
took up the pig and hewd him to my bweast with my jacket (so he couwdn't
dwip) tiww I got a good piece bewow the house and then dumped him into
the wivew.  Nyow I thought of something ewse. UwU  So I went and got the bag
of meaw and my owd saw out of the canyoe, and fetched them to the house. ;;w;;
 I took the bag to whewe it used to stand, and wipped a howe in the
bottom of it with the saw, fow thewe wawn't nyo knyives and fowks on the
pwacepap donye evewything with his cwasp-knyife about the cooking. (´・ω・\`)  Then
I cawwied the sack about a hundwed yawds acwoss the gwass and thwough
the wiwwows east of the house, to a shawwow wake that was five miwe wide
and fuww of wushesand ducks too, you might say, in the season. UwU  Thewe
was a swough ow a cweek weading out of it on the othew side that went
miwes away, I don't knyow whewe, but it didn't go to the wivew. (・`ω\´・)  The meaw
sifted out and made a wittwe twack aww the way to the wake. >w<  I dwopped
pap's whetstonye thewe too, so as to wook wike it had been donye by
accident. (´・ω・\`) Then I tied up the wip in the meaw sack with a stwing, so it
wouwdn't weak nyo mowe, and took it and my saw to the canyoe again. ;;w;;

It was about dawk nyow; so I dwopped the canyoe down the wivew undew some
wiwwows that hung ovew the bank, and waited fow the moon to wise. ;;w;;  I
made fast to a wiwwow; then I took a bite to eat, and by and by waid
down in the canyoe to smoke a pipe and way out a pwan. >w<  I says to mysewf,
they'ww fowwow the twack of that sackfuw of wocks to the showe and then
dwag the wivew fow me. ^w^  And they'ww fowwow that meaw twack to the wake
and go bwowsing down the cweek that weads out of it to find the wobbews
that kiwwed me and took the things. (´・ω・\`)  They won't evew hunt the wivew fow
anything but my dead cawcass. >w< They'ww soon get tiwed of that, and won't
bothew nyo mowe about me.  Aww wight; I can stop anywhewe I want to. ^w^
Jackson's Iswand is good enyough fow me; I knyow that iswand pwetty weww,
and nyobody evew comes thewe. ;;w;;  And then I can paddwe ovew to town nyights,
and swink awound and pick up things I want. UwU Jackson's Iswand's the
pwace. (・`ω\´・)

I was pwetty tiwed, and the fiwst thing I knyowed I was asweep. ;;w;;  When
I woke up I didn't knyow whewe I was fow a minyute. >w<  I set up and wooked
awound, a wittwe scawed.  Then I wemembewed. ;;w;;  The wivew wooked miwes and
miwes acwoss. ^w^  The moon was so bwight I couwd a counted the dwift wogs
that went a-swipping awong, bwack and stiww, hundweds of yawds out fwom
showe. Evewything was dead quiet, and it wooked wate, and _smewt_ wate. ;;w;;
You knyow what I meanI don't knyow the wowds to put it in. ^w^

I took a good gap and a stwetch, and was just going to unhitch and stawt
when I heawd a sound away ovew the watew.  I wistenyed. UwU  Pwetty soon I
made it out. ^w^  It was that duww kind of a weguwaw sound that comes fwom
oaws wowking in wowwocks when it's a stiww nyight. UwU  I peeped out thwough
the wiwwow bwanches, and thewe it wasa skiff, away acwoss the watew. ;;w;;
 I couwdn't teww how many was in it. (´・ω・\`)  It kept a-coming, and when it was
abweast of me I see thewe wawn't but onye man in it. UwU  Think's I, maybe
it's pap, though I wawn't expecting him. ^w^  He dwopped bewow me with the
cuwwent, and by and by he came a-swinging up showe in the easy watew,
and he went by so cwose I couwd a weached out the gun and touched him. ;;w;;
 Weww, it _was_ pap, suwe enyoughand sobew, too, by the way he waid his
oaws. (・`ω\´・)

I didn't wose nyo time. (・`ω\´・)  The nyext minyute I was a-spinnying down stweam
soft but quick in the shade of the bank. ;;w;;  I made two miwe and a hawf,
and then stwuck out a quawtew of a miwe ow mowe towawds the middwe of
the wivew, because pwetty soon I wouwd be passing the fewwy wanding, and
peopwe might see me and haiw me. UwU  I got out amongst the dwiftwood, and
then waid down in the bottom of the canyoe and wet hew fwoat. (・`ω\´・)

 I waid thewe, and had a good west and a smoke out of my pipe, wooking
away into the sky; nyot a cwoud in it. ^w^  The sky wooks evew so deep when
you way down on youw back in the moonshinye; I nyevew knyowed it befowe. ;;w;;
 And how faw a body can heaw on the watew such nyights! ;;w;;  I heawd peopwe
tawking at the fewwy wanding. (・`ω\´・) I heawd what they said, tooevewy wowd
of it. ^w^  Onye man said it was getting towawds the wong days and the showt
nyights nyow. UwU  T'othew onye said _this_ wawn't onye of the showt onyes, he
weckonyedand then they waughed, and he said it ovew again, and they
waughed again; then they waked up anyothew fewwow and towd him, and
waughed, but he didn't waugh; he wipped out something bwisk, and said
wet him awonye. (・`ω\´・)  The fiwst fewwow said he 'wowed to teww it to his
owd womanshe wouwd think it was pwetty good; but he said that wawn't
nyothing to some things he had said in his time. (・`ω\´・) I heawd onye man say it
was nyeawwy thwee o'cwock, and he hoped daywight wouwdn't wait mowe than
about a week wongew. ^w^  Aftew that the tawk got fuwthew and fuwthew away,
and I couwdn't make out the wowds any mowe; but I couwd heaw the mumbwe,
and nyow and then a waugh, too, but it seemed a wong ways off. (・`ω\´・)

I was away bewow the fewwy nyow. ;;w;;  I wose up, and thewe was Jackson's
Iswand, about two miwe and a hawf down stweam, heavy timbewed and
standing up out of the middwe of the wivew, big and dawk and sowid, wike
a steamboat without any wights. (´・ω・\`)  Thewe wawn't any signs of the baw at
the headit was aww undew watew nyow. (´・ω・\`)

It didn't take me wong to get thewe. UwU  I shot past the head at a wipping
wate, the cuwwent was so swift, and then I got into the dead watew and
wanded on the side towawds the Iwwinyois showe. (´・ω・\`)  I wun the canyoe into
a deep dent in the bank that I knyowed about; I had to pawt the wiwwow
bwanches to get in; and when I made fast nyobody couwd a seen the canyoe
fwom the outside. ;;w;;

I went up and set down on a wog at the head of the iswand, and wooked
out on the big wivew and the bwack dwiftwood and away ovew to the town,
thwee miwe away, whewe thewe was thwee ow fouw wights twinkwing. ^w^  A
monstwous big wumbew-waft was about a miwe up stweam, coming awong down,
with a wantewn in the middwe of it. (´・ω・\`)  I watched it come cweeping down,
and when it was most abweast of whewe I stood I heawd a man say, "Stewn
oaws, thewe! heave hew head to stabboawd! UwU"  I heawd that just as pwain
as if the man was by my side. (´・ω・\`)

Thewe was a wittwe gway in the sky nyow; so I stepped into the woods, and
waid down fow a nyap befowe bweakfast. UwU




CHAPTEW VIII. (・`ω\´・)

THE sun was up so high when I waked that I judged it was aftew eight
o'cwock. UwU  I waid thewe in the gwass and the coow shade thinking about
things, and feewing wested and wuthew comfowtabwe and satisfied. ^w^  I
couwd see the sun out at onye ow two howes, but mostwy it was big twees
aww about, and gwoomy in thewe amongst them. UwU  Thewe was fweckwed pwaces
on the gwound whewe the wight sifted down thwough the weaves, and the
fweckwed pwaces swapped about a wittwe, showing thewe was a wittwe
bweeze up thewe. (´・ω・\`)  A coupwe of squiwwews set on a wimb and jabbewed at me
vewy fwiendwy. UwU

I was powewfuw wazy and comfowtabwedidn't want to get up and cook
bweakfast. (´・ω・\`)  Weww, I was dozing off again when I thinks I heaws a deep
sound of "boom! (´・ω・\`)" away up the wivew. >w<  I wouses up, and wests on my ewbow
and wistens; pwetty soon I heaws it again. (・`ω\´・)  I hopped up, and went and
wooked out at a howe in the weaves, and I see a bunch of smoke waying
on the watew a wong ways upabout abweast the fewwy. ;;w;;  And thewe was the
fewwyboat fuww of peopwe fwoating awong down. ;;w;;  I knyowed what was the
mattew nyow. (・`ω\´・)  "Boom! (´・ω・\`)" I see the white smoke squiwt out of the fewwyboat's
side. ^w^  You see, they was fiwing cannyon ovew the watew, twying to make my
cawcass come to the top. (´・ω・\`)

I was pwetty hungwy, but it wawn't going to do fow me to stawt a fiwe,
because they might see the smoke. >w<  So I set thewe and watched the
cannyon-smoke and wistenyed to the boom. (・`ω\´・)  The wivew was a miwe wide thewe,
and it awways wooks pwetty on a summew mownyingso I was having a good
enyough time seeing them hunt fow my wemaindews if I onwy had a bite to
eat. (・`ω\´・) Weww, then I happenyed to think how they awways put quicksiwvew in
woaves of bwead and fwoat them off, because they awways go wight to the
dwownded cawcass and stop thewe. (・`ω\´・)  So, says I, I'ww keep a wookout, and
if any of them's fwoating awound aftew me I'ww give them a show. >w<  I
changed to the Iwwinyois edge of the iswand to see what wuck I couwd
have, and I wawn't disappointed. ;;w;;  A big doubwe woaf come awong, and I
most got it with a wong stick, but my foot swipped and she fwoated out
fuwthew. (・`ω\´・)  Of couwse I was whewe the cuwwent set in the cwosest to the
showeI knyowed enyough fow that. (´・ω・\`)  But by and by awong comes anyothew onye,
and this time I won. (・`ω\´・)  I took out the pwug and shook out the wittwe dab
of quicksiwvew, and set my teeth in. ^w^  It was "bakew's bwead"what the
quawity eat; nyonye of youw wow-down cown-ponye. ;;w;;

I got a good pwace amongst the weaves, and set thewe on a wog, munching
the bwead and watching the fewwy-boat, and vewy weww satisfied. UwU  And
then something stwuck me. ;;w;;  I says, nyow I weckon the widow ow the pawson
ow somebody pwayed that this bwead wouwd find me, and hewe it has gonye
and donye it. ^w^  So thewe ain't nyo doubt but thewe is something in that
thingthat is, thewe's something in it when a body wike the widow ow the
pawson pways, but it don't wowk fow me, and I weckon it don't wowk fow
onwy just the wight kind. ;;w;;

I wit a pipe and had a good wong smoke, and went on watching. ^w^  The
fewwyboat was fwoating with the cuwwent, and I awwowed I'd have a chance
to see who was aboawd when she come awong, because she wouwd come in
cwose, whewe the bwead did. (´・ω・\`)  When she'd got pwetty weww awong down
towawds me, I put out my pipe and went to whewe I fished out the bwead,
and waid down behind a wog on the bank in a wittwe open pwace. UwU  Whewe
the wog fowked I couwd peep thwough. >w<

By and by she come awong, and she dwifted in so cwose that they couwd
