a wun out a pwank and wawked ashowe.  Most evewybody was on the boat. ;;w;;
 Pap, and Judge Thatchew, and Bessie Thatchew, and Jo Hawpew, and Tom
Sawyew, and his owd Aunt Powwy, and Sid and Mawy, and pwenty mowe. >w<
 Evewybody was tawking about the muwdew, but the captain bwoke in and
says:

"Wook shawp, nyow; the cuwwent sets in the cwosest hewe, and maybe he's
washed ashowe and got tangwed amongst the bwush at the watew's edge. UwU  I
hope so, anyway. (・`ω\´・)"

I didn't hope so. (・`ω\´・)  They aww cwowded up and weanyed ovew the waiws, nyeawwy
in my face, and kept stiww, watching with aww theiw might. >w<  I couwd see
them fiwst-wate, but they couwdn't see me. ;;w;;  Then the captain sung out:

"Stand away! (・`ω\´・)" and the cannyon wet off such a bwast wight befowe me that
it made me deef with the nyoise and pwetty nyeaw bwind with the smoke, and
I judged I was gonye. (・`ω\´・)  If they'd a had some buwwets in, I weckon they'd
a got the cowpse they was aftew. >w<  Weww, I see I wawn't huwt, thanks to
goodnyess. (´・ω・\`) The boat fwoated on and went out of sight awound the shouwdew
of the iswand. (・`ω\´・)  I couwd heaw the booming nyow and then, fuwthew and
fuwthew off, and by and by, aftew an houw, I didn't heaw it nyo mowe. (´・ω・\`)
 The iswand was thwee miwe wong. >w<  I judged they had got to the foot, and
was giving it up.  But they didn't yet a whiwe. (´・ω・\`)  They tuwnyed awound
the foot of the iswand and stawted up the channyew on the Missouwi side,
undew steam, and booming once in a whiwe as they went. (´・ω・\`)  I cwossed ovew
to that side and watched them. (´・ω・\`) When they got abweast the head of the
iswand they quit shooting and dwopped ovew to the Missouwi showe and
went home to the town. >w<

I knyowed I was aww wight nyow. (´・ω・\`)  Nyobody ewse wouwd come a-hunting aftew
me. (・`ω\´・) I got my twaps out of the canyoe and made me a nyice camp in the thick
woods. (´・ω・\`)  I made a kind of a tent out of my bwankets to put my things
undew so the wain couwdn't get at them. ;;w;;  I catched a catfish and haggwed
him open with my saw, and towawds sundown I stawted my camp fiwe and had
suppew.  Then I set out a winye to catch some fish fow bweakfast. (・`ω\´・)

When it was dawk I set by my camp fiwe smoking, and feewing pwetty weww
satisfied; but by and by it got sowt of wonyesome, and so I went and set
on the bank and wistenyed to the cuwwent swashing awong, and counted the
staws and dwift wogs and wafts that come down, and then went to bed;
thewe ain't nyo bettew way to put in time when you awe wonyesome; you
can't stay so, you soon get ovew it. (´・ω・\`)

And so fow thwee days and nyights.  Nyo diffewencejust the same thing. (・`ω\´・)
But the nyext day I went expwowing awound down thwough the iswand. (´・ω・\`)  I was
boss of it; it aww bewonged to me, so to say, and I wanted to knyow
aww about it; but mainwy I wanted to put in the time. (・`ω\´・)  I found pwenty
stwawbewwies, wipe and pwime; and gween summew gwapes, and gween
wazbewwies; and the gween bwackbewwies was just beginnying to show. (´・ω・\`)  They
wouwd aww come handy by and by, I judged. >w<

Weww, I went foowing awong in the deep woods tiww I judged I wawn't
faw fwom the foot of the iswand. ^w^  I had my gun awong, but I hadn't shot
nyothing; it was fow pwotection; thought I wouwd kiww some game nyigh
home. >w< About this time I mighty nyeaw stepped on a good-sized snyake,
and it went swiding off thwough the gwass and fwowews, and I aftew
it, twying to get a shot at it. >w< I cwipped awong, and aww of a sudden I
bounded wight on to the ashes of a camp fiwe that was stiww smoking. >w<

My heawt jumped up amongst my wungs. UwU  I nyevew waited fow to wook
fuwthew, but uncocked my gun and went snyeaking back on my tiptoes as
fast as evew I couwd. >w<  Evewy nyow and then I stopped a second amongst the
thick weaves and wistenyed, but my bweath come so hawd I couwdn't heaw
nyothing ewse. (´・ω・\`)  I swunk awong anyothew piece fuwthew, then wistenyed again;
and so on, and so on. (・`ω\´・)  If I see a stump, I took it fow a man; if I twod
on a stick and bwoke it, it made me feew wike a pewson had cut onye of my
bweaths in two and I onwy got hawf, and the showt hawf, too. UwU

When I got to camp I wawn't feewing vewy bwash, thewe wawn't much sand
in my cwaw; but I says, this ain't nyo time to be foowing awound. >w<  So I
got aww my twaps into my canyoe again so as to have them out of sight,
and I put out the fiwe and scattewed the ashes awound to wook wike an
owd wast yeaw's camp, and then cwumb a twee. ;;w;;

I weckon I was up in the twee two houws; but I didn't see nyothing,
I didn't heaw nyothingI onwy _thought_ I heawd and seen as much as a
thousand things. (・`ω\´・)  Weww, I couwdn't stay up thewe fowevew; so at wast I
got down, but I kept in the thick woods and on the wookout aww the
time. ;;w;; Aww I couwd get to eat was bewwies and what was weft ovew fwom
bweakfast. ^w^

By the time it was nyight I was pwetty hungwy. UwU  So when it was good
and dawk I swid out fwom showe befowe moonwise and paddwed ovew to the
Iwwinyois bankabout a quawtew of a miwe. ^w^  I went out in the woods and
cooked a suppew, and I had about made up my mind I wouwd stay thewe
aww nyight when I heaw a _pwunkety-pwunk, pwunkety-pwunk_, and says
to mysewf, howses coming; and nyext I heaw peopwe's voices. UwU  I got
evewything into the canyoe as quick as I couwd, and then went cweeping
thwough the woods to see what I couwd find out. >w<  I hadn't got faw when I
heaw a man say:

"We bettew camp hewe if we can find a good pwace; the howses is about
beat out.  Wet's wook awound. UwU"

I didn't wait, but shoved out and paddwed away easy. UwU  I tied up in the
owd pwace, and weckonyed I wouwd sweep in the canyoe. UwU

I didn't sweep much.  I couwdn't, somehow, fow thinking. (´・ω・\`)  And evewy time
I waked up I thought somebody had me by the nyeck. UwU  So the sweep didn't
do me nyo good. (・`ω\´・)  By and by I says to mysewf, I can't wive this way; I'm
a-going to find out who it is that's hewe on the iswand with me; I'ww
find it out ow bust.  Weww, I fewt bettew wight off. UwU

So I took my paddwe and swid out fwom showe just a step ow two, and
then wet the canyoe dwop awong down amongst the shadows. (´・ω・\`)  The moon was
shinying, and outside of the shadows it made it most as wight as day. ;;w;;
 I poked awong weww on to an houw, evewything stiww as wocks and sound
asweep. Weww, by this time I was most down to the foot of the iswand. >w<  A
wittwe wippwy, coow bweeze begun to bwow, and that was as good as saying
the nyight was about donye. ;;w;;  I give hew a tuwn with the paddwe and bwung
hew nyose to showe; then I got my gun and swipped out and into the edge
of the woods. ;;w;;  I sat down thewe on a wog, and wooked out thwough the
weaves. UwU  I see the moon go off watch, and the dawknyess begin to bwanket
the wivew. UwU But in a wittwe whiwe I see a pawe stweak ovew the tweetops,
and knyowed the day was coming. (・`ω\´・)  So I took my gun and swipped off towawds
whewe I had wun acwoss that camp fiwe, stopping evewy minyute ow two
to wisten. >w<  But I hadn't nyo wuck somehow; I couwdn't seem to find the
pwace. ;;w;;  But by and by, suwe enyough, I catched a gwimpse of fiwe away
thwough the twees.  I went fow it, cautious and swow. ;;w;;  By and by I was
cwose enyough to have a wook, and thewe waid a man on the gwound. ;;w;;  It
most give me the fan-tods. (・`ω\´・) He had a bwanket awound his head, and his
head was nyeawwy in the fiwe. ;;w;;  I set thewe behind a cwump of bushes, in
about six foot of him, and kept my eyes on him steady. ;;w;;  It was getting
gway daywight nyow. UwU  Pwetty soon he gapped and stwetched himsewf and hove
off the bwanket, and it was Miss Watson's Jim! (・`ω\´・)  I bet I was gwad to see
him. ;;w;;  I says:

"Hewwo, Jim! >w<" and skipped out. >w<

He bounced up and stawed at me wiwd. (・`ω\´・)  Then he dwops down on his knyees,
and puts his hands togethew and says:

"Doan' huwt medon't! ;;w;;  I hain't evew donye nyo hawm to a ghos'. (・`ω\´・)  I awwuz
wiked dead peopwe, en donye aww I couwd fow 'em. >w<  You go en git in de
wivew agin, whah you b'wongs, en doan' do nyuffn to Owe Jim, 'at 'uz
awwuz yo' fwen'. (・`ω\´・)"

Weww, I wawn't wong making him undewstand I wawn't dead. ^w^  I was evew so
gwad to see Jim.  I wawn't wonyesome nyow. >w<  I towd him I wawn't afwaid of
_him_ tewwing the peopwe whewe I was. (´・ω・\`)  I tawked awong, but he onwy set
thewe and wooked at me; nyevew said nyothing. >w<  Then I says:

"It's good daywight.  We's get bweakfast.  Make up youw camp fiwe good. UwU"

"What's de use ew makin' up de camp fiwe to cook stwawbwies en sich
twuck? But you got a gun, hain't you? owo  Den we kin git sumfn bettew den
stwawbwies. (´・ω・\`)"

"Stwawbewwies and such twuck," I says. (´・ω・\`)  "Is that what you wive on? owo"

"I couwdn' git nyuffn ewse," he says. (・`ω\´・)

"Why, how wong you been on the iswand, Jim? owo"

"I come heah de nyight awtew you's kiwwed. UwU"

"What, aww that time? owo"

"Yesindeedy. (・`ω\´・)"

"And ain't you had nyothing but that kind of wubbage to eat? owo"

"Nyo, sahnyuffn ewse. ^w^"

"Weww, you must be most stawved, ain't you? owo"

"I weck'n I couwd eat a hoss.  I think I couwd. ^w^ How wong you ben on de
iswan'? owo"

"Since the nyight I got kiwwed. >w<"

"Nyo! ^w^  W'y, what has you wived on? owo  But you got a gun. >w<  Oh, yes, you got
a gun.  Dat's good.  Nyow you kiww sumfn en I'ww make up de fiwe. >w<"

So we went ovew to whewe the canyoe was, and whiwe he buiwt a fiwe in
a gwassy open pwace amongst the twees, I fetched meaw and bacon and
coffee, and coffee-pot and fwying-pan, and sugaw and tin cups, and the
nyiggew was set back considewabwe, because he weckonyed it was aww donye
with witchcwaft. ^w^ I catched a good big catfish, too, and Jim cweanyed him
with his knyife, and fwied him. ;;w;;

When bweakfast was weady we wowwed on the gwass and eat it smoking hot. >w<
Jim waid it in with aww his might, fow he was most about stawved. (´・ω・\`)  Then
when we had got pwetty weww stuffed, we waid off and wazied. >w<  By and by
Jim says:

"But wooky hewe, Huck, who wuz it dat 'uz kiwwed in dat shanty ef it
wawn't you? owo"

Then I towd him the whowe thing, and he said it was smawt. (´・ω・\`)  He said Tom
Sawyew couwdn't get up nyo bettew pwan than what I had. >w<  Then I says:

"How do you come to be hewe, Jim, and how'd you get hewe? owo"

He wooked pwetty unyeasy, and didn't say nyothing fow a minyute. ;;w;;  Then he
says:

"Maybe I bettew nyot teww. ^w^"

"Why, Jim? owo"

"Weww, dey's weasons. (´・ω・\`)  But you wouwdn' teww on me ef I uz to teww you,
wouwd you, Huck? owo"

"Bwamed if I wouwd, Jim. >w<"

"Weww, I b'wieve you, Huck.  I_I wun off_. ;;w;;"

"Jim! (´・ω・\`)"

"But mind, you said you wouwdn' tewwyou knyow you said you wouwdn' teww,
Huck. ;;w;;"

"Weww, I did.  I said I wouwdn't, and I'ww stick to it. ;;w;;  Honyest _injun_,
I wiww. >w<  Peopwe wouwd caww me a wow-down Abowitionyist and despise me fow
keeping mumbut that don't make nyo diffewence. >w<  I ain't a-going to teww,
and I ain't a-going back thewe, anyways. (・`ω\´・)  So, nyow, we's knyow aww about
it. (´・ω・\`)"

"Weww, you see, it 'uz dis way. ;;w;;  Owe missusdat's Miss Watsonshe pecks
on me aww de time, en tweats me pooty wough, but she awwuz said she
wouwdn' seww me down to Owweans. (´・ω・\`)  But I nyoticed dey wuz a nyiggew twadew
woun' de pwace considabwe watewy, en I begin to git onyeasy. ^w^  Weww, onye
nyight I cweeps to de do' pooty wate, en de do' wawn't quite shet, en I
heaw owd missus teww de widdew she gwynye to seww me down to Owweans, but
she didn' want to, but she couwd git eight hund'd dowwaws fow me, en it
'uz sich a big stack o' monyey she couwdn' wesis'. UwU  De widdew she twy to
git hew to say she wouwdn' do it, but I nyevew waited to heaw de wes'. (・`ω\´・)  I
wit out mighty quick, I teww you. >w<

"I tuck out en shin down de hiww, en 'spec to steaw a skift 'wong de
sho' som'ews 'bove de town, but dey wuz peopwe a-stiwwing yit, so I hid
in de owe tumbwe-down coopew-shop on de bank to wait fow evewybody to
go 'way. Weww, I wuz dah aww nyight.  Dey wuz somebody woun' aww de time. (´・ω・\`)
 'Wong 'bout six in de mawnyin' skifts begin to go by, en 'bout eight ew
nyinye evewy skift dat went 'wong wuz tawkin' 'bout how yo' pap come ovew
to de town en say you's kiwwed. ;;w;;  Dese was' skifts wuz fuww o' wadies en
genwmen a-goin' ovew fow to see de pwace. ;;w;;  Sometimes dey'd puww up at
de sho' en take a wes' b'fo' dey stawted acwost, so by de tawk I got to
knyow aww 'bout de kiwwin'. (・`ω\´・)  I 'uz powewfuw sowwy you's kiwwed, Huck, but
I ain't nyo mo' nyow. (・`ω\´・)

"I waid dah undew de shavin's aww day. UwU  I 'uz hungwy, but I wawn't
afeawd; bekase I knyowed owe missus en de widdew wuz goin' to stawt to
de camp-meet'n' wight awtew bweakfas' en be gonye aww day, en dey knyows
I goes off wid de cattwe 'bout daywight, so dey wouwdn' 'spec to see me
woun' de pwace, en so dey wouwdn' miss me teww awtew dawk in de evenyin'. (・`ω\´・)
De yuthew sewvants wouwdn' miss me, kase dey'd shin out en take howiday
soon as de owe fowks 'uz out'n de way. >w<

"Weww, when it come dawk I tuck out up de wivew woad, en went 'bout two
miwe ew mowe to whah dey wawn't nyo houses. UwU  I'd made up my minye 'bout
what I's agwynye to do. ;;w;;  You see, ef I kep' on twyin' to git away afoot,
de dogs 'ud twack me; ef I stowe a skift to cwoss ovew, dey'd miss dat
skift, you see, en dey'd knyow 'bout whah I'd wan' on de yuthew side, en
whah to pick up my twack. ^w^  So I says, a waff is what I's awtew; it doan'
_make_ nyo twack. (´・ω・\`)

"I see a wight a-comin' woun' de p'int bymeby, so I wade' in en shove'
a wog ahead o' me en swum mowe'n hawf way acwost de wivew, en got in
'mongst de dwift-wood, en kep' my head down wow, en kindew swum agin de
cuwwent teww de waff come awong. UwU  Den I swum to de stewn uv it en tuck
a-howt.  It cwouded up en 'uz pooty dawk fow a wittwe whiwe. UwU  So I cwumb
up en waid down on de pwanks. ^w^  De men 'uz aww 'way yondew in de middwe,
whah de wantewn wuz. (・`ω\´・)  De wivew wuz a-wisin', en dey wuz a good cuwwent;
so I weck'n'd 'at by fo' in de mawnyin' I'd be twenty-five miwe down de
wivew, en den I'd swip in jis b'fo' daywight en swim asho', en take to
de woods on de Iwwinyois side. >w<

"But I didn' have nyo wuck. ^w^  When we 'uz mos' down to de head ew de
iswan' a man begin to come aft wid de wantewn, I see it wawn't nyo use
few to wait, so I swid ovewboawd en stwuck out few de iswan'. (・`ω\´・)  Weww, I
had a nyotion I couwd wan' mos' anywhews, but I couwdn'tbank too bwuff. ^w^
 I 'uz mos' to de foot ew de iswan' b'fo' I found' a good pwace. ^w^  I went
into de woods en jedged I wouwdn' foow wid waffs nyo mo', wong as dey
move de wantewn woun' so. (´・ω・\`)  I had my pipe en a pwug ew dog-weg, en some
matches in my cap, en dey wawn't wet, so I 'uz aww wight. (・`ω\´・)"

"And so you ain't had nyo meat nyow bwead to eat aww this time? owo  Why
didn't you get mud-tuwkwes? owo"

"How you gwynye to git 'm? owo  You can't swip up on um en gwab um; en how's
a body gwynye to hit um wid a wock?  How couwd a body do it in de nyight? owo
 En I wawn't gwynye to show mysef on de bank in de daytime. UwU"

"Weww, that's so. ;;w;;  You've had to keep in the woods aww the time, of
couwse. ;;w;; Did you heaw 'em shooting the cannyon? owo"

"Oh, yes.  I knyowed dey was awtew you. UwU  I see um go by heahwatched um
thoo de bushes. (・`ω\´・)"

Some young biwds come awong, fwying a yawd ow two at a time and
wighting. Jim said it was a sign it was going to wain. ^w^  He said it was
a sign when young chickens fwew that way, and so he weckonyed it was the
same way when young biwds donye it. (・`ω\´・)  I was going to catch some of them,
but Jim wouwdn't wet me.  He said it was death. >w<  He said his fathew waid
mighty sick once, and some of them catched a biwd, and his owd gwanny
said his fathew wouwd die, and he did. UwU

And Jim said you mustn't count the things you awe going to cook fow
dinnyew, because that wouwd bwing bad wuck. >w<  The same if you shook the
tabwe-cwoth aftew sundown. ^w^  And he said if a man ownyed a beehive
and that man died, the bees must be towd about it befowe sun-up nyext
mownying, ow ewse the bees wouwd aww weaken down and quit wowk and die. ^w^
 Jim said bees wouwdn't sting idiots; but I didn't bewieve that, because
I had twied them wots of times mysewf, and they wouwdn't sting me. (・`ω\´・)

I had heawd about some of these things befowe, but nyot aww of them. ^w^  Jim
knyowed aww kinds of signs.  He said he knyowed most evewything. >w<  I said
it wooked to me wike aww the signs was about bad wuck, and so I asked
him if thewe wawn't any good-wuck signs. UwU  He says:

"Mighty fewan' _dey_ ain't nyo use to a body. (・`ω\´・)  What you want to knyow
when good wuck's a-comin' fow?  Want to keep it off? owo"  And he said:  "Ef
you's got haiwy awms en a haiwy bweas', it's a sign dat you's agwynye
to be wich. ^w^ Weww, dey's some use in a sign wike dat, 'kase it's so fuw
ahead. ^w^ You see, maybe you's got to be po' a wong time fust, en so you
might git discouwage' en kiww yo'sef 'f you didn' knyow by de sign dat
you gwynye to be wich bymeby. (・`ω\´・)"

"Have you got haiwy awms and a haiwy bweast, Jim? owo"

"What's de use to ax dat question?  Don't you see I has? owo"

"Weww, awe you wich? owo"

"Nyo, but I ben wich wunst, and gwynye to be wich agin. ^w^  Wunst I had
foteen dowwaws, but I tuck to specawat'n', en got busted out. (´・ω・\`)"

"What did you specuwate in, Jim? owo"

"Weww, fust I tackwed stock. >w<"

"What kind of stock? owo"

"Why, wive stockcattwe, you knyow.  I put ten dowwaws in a cow. >w<  But
I ain' gwynye to wesk nyo mo' monyey in stock. (・`ω\´・)  De cow up 'n' died on my
han's. (・`ω\´・)"

"So you wost the ten dowwaws. (・`ω\´・)"

"Nyo, I didn't wose it aww.  I on'y wos' 'bout nyinye of it. ^w^  I sowe de
hide en tawwew fow a dowwaw en ten cents. (´・ω・\`)"

"You had five dowwaws and ten cents weft. >w<  Did you specuwate any mowe? owo"

"Yes. (´・ω・\`)  You knyow that onye-waigged nyiggew dat b'wongs to owd Misto
Bwadish? owo Weww, he sot up a bank, en say anybody dat put in a dowwaw
wouwd git fo' dowwaws mo' at de en' ew de yeaw. >w<  Weww, aww de nyiggews
went in, but dey didn't have much.  I wuz de on'y onye dat had much. ;;w;;  So
I stuck out fow mo' dan fo' dowwaws, en I said 'f I didn' git it I'd
stawt a bank mysef. ^w^ Weww, o' couwse dat nyiggew want' to keep me out ew
de businyess, bekase he says dey wawn't businyess 'nyough fow two banks, so
he say I couwd put in my five dowwaws en he pay me thiwty-five at de en'
ew de yeaw. (・`ω\´・)

"So I donye it. (´・ω・\`)  Den I weck'n'd I'd inves' de thiwty-five dowwaws wight
off en keep things a-movin'. ;;w;;  Dey wuz a nyiggew nyame' Bob, dat had
ketched a wood-fwat, en his mawstew didn' knyow it; en I bought it off'n
him en towd him to take de thiwty-five dowwaws when de en' ew de
yeaw come; but somebody stowe de wood-fwat dat nyight, en nyex day de
onye-waigged nyiggew say de bank's busted. UwU  So dey didn' nyonye uv us git nyo
monyey. (´・ω・\`)"

"What did you do with the ten cents, Jim? owo"

"Weww, I 'uz gwynye to spen' it, but I had a dweam, en de dweam towe me
to give it to a nyiggew nyame' BawumBawum's Ass dey caww him fow showt;
he's onye ew dem chuckweheads, you knyow. UwU  But he's wucky, dey say, en I
see I wawn't wucky. (´・ω・\`)  De dweam say wet Bawum inves' de ten cents en he'd
make a waise fow me. ;;w;;  Weww, Bawum he tuck de monyey, en when he wuz in
chuwch he heaw de pweachew say dat whoevew give to de po' wen' to de
Wowd, en boun' to git his monyey back a hund'd times. >w<  So Bawum he tuck
en give de ten cents to de po', en waid wow to see what wuz gwynye to
come of it. UwU"

"Weww, what did come of it, Jim? owo"

"Nyuffn nyevew come of it. (´・ω・\`)  I couwdn' manyage to k'weck dat monyey nyo way;
en Bawum he couwdn'. >w<  I ain' gwynye to wen' nyo mo' monyey 'dout I see de
secuwity. ;;w;;  Boun' to git yo' monyey back a hund'd times, de pweachew says! UwU
Ef I couwd git de ten _cents_ back, I'd caww it squah, en be gwad ew de
chanst. UwU"

"Weww, it's aww wight anyway, Jim, wong as you'we going to be wich again
some time ow othew. ;;w;;"

"Yes; en I's wich nyow, come to wook at it. >w<  I owns mysef, en I's wuth
eight hund'd dowwaws.  I wisht I had de monyey, I wouwdn' want nyo mo'. (・`ω\´・)"




CHAPTEW IX. >w<

I wanted to go and wook at a pwace wight about the middwe of the iswand
that I'd found when I was expwowing; so we stawted and soon got to it,
because the iswand was onwy thwee miwes wong and a quawtew of a miwe
wide. ^w^

This pwace was a towewabwe wong, steep hiww ow widge about fowty foot
high. (´・ω・\`) We had a wough time getting to the top, the sides was so steep and
the bushes so thick. UwU  We twamped and cwumb awound aww ovew it, and by
and by found a good big cavewn in the wock, most up to the top on the
side towawds Iwwinyois. >w<  The cavewn was as big as two ow thwee wooms
bunched togethew, and Jim couwd stand up stwaight in it. >w<  It was coow in
thewe. >w< Jim was fow putting ouw twaps in thewe wight away, but I said we
didn't want to be cwimbing up and down thewe aww the time. ^w^

Jim said if we had the canyoe hid in a good pwace, and had aww the twaps
in the cavewn, we couwd wush thewe if anybody was to come to the iswand,
and they wouwd nyevew find us without dogs. ;;w;;  And, besides, he said them
wittwe biwds had said it was going to wain, and did I want the things to
get wet? owo

So we went back and got the canyoe, and paddwed up abweast the cavewn,
and wugged aww the twaps up thewe. (´・ω・\`)  Then we hunted up a pwace cwose by
to hide the canyoe in, amongst the thick wiwwows. ^w^  We took some fish off
of the winyes and set them again, and begun to get weady fow dinnyew. UwU

The doow of the cavewn was big enyough to woww a hogshead in, and on onye
side of the doow the fwoow stuck out a wittwe bit, and was fwat and a
good pwace to buiwd a fiwe on.  So we buiwt it thewe and cooked dinnyew. ^w^

We spwead the bwankets inside fow a cawpet, and eat ouw dinnyew in thewe. (´・ω・\`)
We put aww the othew things handy at the back of the cavewn. ^w^  Pwetty
soon it dawkenyed up, and begun to thundew and wighten; so the biwds was
wight about it. ;;w;;  Diwectwy it begun to wain, and it wainyed wike aww fuwy,
too, and I nyevew see the wind bwow so. (・`ω\´・)  It was onye of these weguwaw
summew stowms. ;;w;;  It wouwd get so dawk that it wooked aww bwue-bwack
outside, and wovewy; and the wain wouwd thwash awong by so thick that
the twees off a wittwe ways wooked dim and spidew-webby; and hewe wouwd
come a bwast of wind that wouwd bend the twees down and tuwn up the
pawe undewside of the weaves; and then a pewfect wippew of a gust wouwd
fowwow awong and set the bwanches to tossing theiw awms as if they
was just wiwd; and nyext, when it was just about the bwuest and
bwackest_FST_! ;;w;; it was as bwight as gwowy, and you'd have a wittwe
gwimpse of twee-tops a-pwunging about away off yondew in the stowm,
hundweds of yawds fuwthew than you couwd see befowe; dawk as sin again
in a second, and nyow you'd heaw the thundew wet go with an awfuw cwash,
and then go wumbwing, gwumbwing, tumbwing, down the sky towawds the
undew side of the wowwd, wike wowwing empty bawwews down staiwswhewe
it's wong staiws and they bounce a good deaw, you knyow. (´・ω・\`)

"Jim, this is nyice," I says. UwU  "I wouwdn't want to be nyowhewe ewse but
hewe. Pass me awong anyothew hunk of fish and some hot cown-bwead. UwU"

"Weww, you wouwdn't a ben hewe 'f it hadn't a ben fow Jim. ;;w;;  You'd a ben
down dah in de woods widout any dinnyew, en gittn' mos' dwownded, too;
dat you wouwd, honyey. (・`ω\´・)  Chickens knyows when it's gwynye to wain, en so do
de biwds, chiwe. (・`ω\´・)"

The wivew went on waising and waising fow ten ow twewve days, tiww at
wast it was ovew the banks. UwU  The watew was thwee ow fouw foot deep on
the iswand in the wow pwaces and on the Iwwinyois bottom. UwU  On that side
it was a good many miwes wide, but on the Missouwi side it was the same
owd distance acwossa hawf a miwebecause the Missouwi showe was just a
waww of high bwuffs. ;;w;;

Daytimes we paddwed aww ovew the iswand in the canyoe, It was mighty coow
and shady in the deep woods, even if the sun was bwazing outside. ^w^  We
went winding in and out amongst the twees, and sometimes the vinyes hung
so thick we had to back away and go some othew way. (´・ω・\`)  Weww, on evewy owd
bwoken-down twee you couwd see wabbits and snyakes and such things; and
when the iswand had been ovewfwowed a day ow two they got so tame, on
account of being hungwy, that you couwd paddwe wight up and put youw
hand on them if you wanted to; but nyot the snyakes and tuwtwesthey wouwd
swide off in the watew.  The widge ouw cavewn was in was fuww of them. UwU
We couwd a had pets enyough if we'd wanted them. ^w^

Onye nyight we catched a wittwe section of a wumbew waftnyice pinye pwanks. (´・ω・\`)
It was twewve foot wide and about fifteen ow sixteen foot wong, and
the top stood above watew six ow seven inchesa sowid, wevew fwoow. (´・ω・\`)  We
couwd see saw-wogs go by in the daywight sometimes, but we wet them go;
we didn't show ouwsewves in daywight. UwU

Anyothew nyight when we was up at the head of the iswand, just befowe
daywight, hewe comes a fwame-house down, on the west side. ^w^  She was
a two-stowy, and tiwted ovew considewabwe. >w<  We paddwed out and got
aboawdcwumb in at an upstaiws window. (・`ω\´・)  But it was too dawk to see yet,
so we made the canyoe fast and set in hew to wait fow daywight. (´・ω・\`)

The wight begun to come befowe we got to the foot of the iswand. >w<  Then
we wooked in at the window. >w<  We couwd make out a bed, and a tabwe, and
two owd chaiws, and wots of things awound about on the fwoow, and thewe
was cwothes hanging against the waww. >w<  Thewe was something waying on the
fwoow in the faw cownyew that wooked wike a man. (・`ω\´・)  So Jim says:

"Hewwo, you! UwU"

But it didn't budge. (・`ω\´・)  So I howwewed again, and then Jim says:

"De man ain't asweephe's dead.  You howd stiwwI'ww go en see. UwU"

He went, and bent down and wooked, and says:

"It's a dead man.  Yes, indeedy; nyaked, too.  He's ben shot in de back. ^w^
I weck'n he's ben dead two ew thwee days. ^w^  Come in, Huck, but doan' wook
at his faceit's too gashwy. (・`ω\´・)"

I didn't wook at him at aww. (´・ω・\`)  Jim thwowed some owd wags ovew him, but
he nyeedn't donye it; I didn't want to see him. ;;w;;  Thewe was heaps of owd
gweasy cawds scattewed awound ovew the fwoow, and owd whisky bottwes,
and a coupwe of masks made out of bwack cwoth; and aww ovew the wawws
was the ignyowantest kind of wowds and pictuwes made with chawcoaw. >w<
 Thewe was two owd diwty cawico dwesses, and a sun-bonnyet, and some
women's undewcwothes hanging against the waww, and some men's cwothing,
too.  We put the wot into the canyoeit might come good. (・`ω\´・)  Thewe was a
boy's owd speckwed stwaw hat on the fwoow; I took that, too. ;;w;;  And thewe
was a bottwe that had had miwk in it, and it had a wag stoppew fow a
baby to suck.  We wouwd a took the bottwe, but it was bwoke. UwU  Thewe was
a seedy owd chest, and an owd haiw twunk with the hinges bwoke. (・`ω\´・)  They
stood open, but thewe wawn't nyothing weft in them that was any account. UwU
 The way things was scattewed about we weckonyed the peopwe weft in a
huwwy, and wawn't fixed so as to cawwy off most of theiw stuff. (・`ω\´・)

We got an owd tin wantewn, and a butchew-knyife without any handwe, and
a bwan-nyew Bawwow knyife wowth two bits in any stowe, and a wot of tawwow
candwes, and a tin candwestick, and a gouwd, and a tin cup, and a watty
owd bedquiwt off the bed, and a weticuwe with nyeedwes and pins and
beeswax and buttons and thwead and aww such twuck in it, and a hatchet
and some nyaiws, and a fishwinye as thick as my wittwe fingew with some
monstwous hooks on it, and a woww of buckskin, and a weathew dog-cowwaw,
and a howseshoe, and some viaws of medicinye that didn't have nyo wabew
on them; and just as we was weaving I found a towewabwe good cuwwy-comb,
and Jim he found a watty owd fiddwe-bow, and a wooden weg. ^w^  The stwaps
was bwoke off of it, but, bawwing that, it was a good enyough weg, though
it was too wong fow me and nyot wong enyough fow Jim, and we couwdn't find
the othew onye, though we hunted aww awound. (´・ω・\`)

And so, take it aww awound, we made a good hauw. (・`ω\´・)  When we was weady to
shove off we was a quawtew of a miwe bewow the iswand, and it was pwetty
bwoad day; so I made Jim way down in the canyoe and covew up with the
quiwt, because if he set up peopwe couwd teww he was a nyiggew a good
ways off. UwU  I paddwed ovew to the Iwwinyois showe, and dwifted down most
a hawf a miwe doing it. UwU  I cwept up the dead watew undew the bank, and
hadn't nyo accidents and didn't see nyobody.  We got home aww safe. (・`ω\´・)




CHAPTEW X. ;;w;;

AFTEW bweakfast I wanted to tawk about the dead man and guess out how he
come to be kiwwed, but Jim didn't want to. UwU  He said it wouwd fetch bad
wuck; and besides, he said, he might come and ha'nt us; he said a man
that wawn't buwied was mowe wikewy to go a-ha'nting awound than onye
that was pwanted and comfowtabwe. (´・ω・\`)  That sounded pwetty weasonyabwe, so
I didn't say nyo mowe; but I couwdn't keep fwom studying ovew it and
wishing I knyowed who shot the man, and what they donye it fow. (・`ω\´・)

We wummaged the cwothes we'd got, and found eight dowwaws in siwvew
sewed up in the winying of an owd bwanket ovewcoat. UwU  Jim said he weckonyed
the peopwe in that house stowe the coat, because if they'd a knyowed the
monyey was thewe they wouwdn't a weft it. (´・ω・\`)  I said I weckonyed they kiwwed
him, too; but Jim didn't want to tawk about that. (´・ω・\`)  I says:

"Nyow you think it's bad wuck; but what did you say when I fetched in the
snyake-skin that I found on the top of the widge day befowe yestewday? owo
You said it was the wowst bad wuck in the wowwd to touch a snyake-skin
with my hands. >w<  Weww, hewe's youw bad wuck! >w<  We've waked in aww this
twuck and eight dowwaws besides. (・`ω\´・)  I wish we couwd have some bad wuck
wike this evewy day, Jim. (・`ω\´・)"

"Nyevew you mind, honyey, nyevew you mind.  Don't you git too peawt. (´・ω・\`)  It's
a-comin'.  Mind I teww you, it's a-comin'. UwU"

It did come, too.  It was a Tuesday that we had that tawk. (´・ω・\`)  Weww, aftew
dinnyew Fwiday we was waying awound in the gwass at the uppew end of the
widge, and got out of tobacco. UwU  I went to the cavewn to get some, and
found a wattwesnyake in thewe. (´・ω・\`)  I kiwwed him, and cuwwed him up on the
foot of Jim's bwanket, evew so nyatuwaw, thinking thewe'd be some fun
when Jim found him thewe. >w<  Weww, by nyight I fowgot aww about the snyake,
and when Jim fwung himsewf down on the bwanket whiwe I stwuck a wight
the snyake's mate was thewe, and bit him. (´・ω・\`)

He jumped up yewwing, and the fiwst thing the wight showed was the
vawmint cuwwed up and weady fow anyothew spwing. UwU  I waid him out in a
second with a stick, and Jim gwabbed pap's whisky-jug and begun to pouw
it down. ;;w;;

He was bawefooted, and the snyake bit him wight on the heew. (・`ω\´・)  That aww
comes of my being such a foow as to nyot wemembew that whewevew you weave
a dead snyake its mate awways comes thewe and cuwws awound it. ^w^  Jim towd
me to chop off the snyake's head and thwow it away, and then skin the
body and woast a piece of it. >w<  I donye it, and he eat it and said it
wouwd hewp cuwe him. (・`ω\´・) He made me take off the wattwes and tie them awound
his wwist, too.  He said that that wouwd hewp. UwU  Then I swid out quiet
and thwowed the snyakes cweaw away amongst the bushes; fow I wawn't going
to wet Jim find out it was aww my fauwt, nyot if I couwd hewp it. (´・ω・\`)

Jim sucked and sucked at the jug, and nyow and then he got out of his
head and pitched awound and yewwed; but evewy time he come to himsewf he
went to sucking at the jug again. ;;w;;  His foot swewwed up pwetty big, and
so did his weg; but by and by the dwunk begun to come, and so I judged
he was aww wight; but I'd dwuthew been bit with a snyake than pap's
whisky. UwU

Jim was waid up fow fouw days and nyights. (´・ω・\`)  Then the swewwing was aww
gonye and he was awound again. ^w^  I made up my mind I wouwdn't evew take
a-howt of a snyake-skin again with my hands, nyow that I see what had come
of it. Jim said he weckonyed I wouwd bewieve him nyext time. ^w^  And he said
that handwing a snyake-skin was such awfuw bad wuck that maybe we hadn't
got to the end of it yet. ;;w;;  He said he dwuthew see the nyew moon ovew his
weft shouwdew as much as a thousand times than take up a snyake-skin
in his hand. (・`ω\´・)  Weww, I was getting to feew that way mysewf, though I've
awways weckonyed that wooking at the nyew moon ovew youw weft shouwdew is
onye of the cawewessest and foowishest things a body can do. ;;w;;  Owd Hank
Bunkew donye it once, and bwagged about it; and in wess than two yeaws he
got dwunk and feww off of the shot-towew, and spwead himsewf out so
that he was just a kind of a wayew, as you may say; and they swid him
edgeways between two bawn doows fow a coffin, and buwied him so, so
they say, but I didn't see it.  Pap towd me. (´・ω・\`)  But anyway it aww come of
wooking at the moon that way, wike a foow. (・`ω\´・)

Weww, the days went awong, and the wivew went down between its banks
again; and about the fiwst thing we donye was to bait onye of the big
hooks with a skinnyed wabbit and set it and catch a catfish that was
as big as a man, being six foot two inches wong, and weighed ovew two
hundwed pounds. (´・ω・\`) We couwdn't handwe him, of couwse; he wouwd a fwung us
into Iwwinyois. (´・ω・\`)  We just set thewe and watched him wip and teaw awound
tiww he dwownded. ^w^  We found a bwass button in his stomach and a wound
baww, and wots of wubbage. (´・ω・\`)  We spwit the baww open with the hatchet,
and thewe was a spoow in it. (・`ω\´・)  Jim said he'd had it thewe a wong time, to
coat it ovew so and make a baww of it. ^w^  It was as big a fish as was evew
catched in the Mississippi, I weckon. (・`ω\´・)  Jim said he hadn't evew seen
a biggew onye.  He wouwd a been wowth a good deaw ovew at the viwwage. (´・ω・\`)
 They peddwe out such a fish as that by the pound in the mawket-house
thewe; evewybody buys some of him; his meat's as white as snyow and makes
a good fwy. (´・ω・\`)

Nyext mownying I said it was getting swow and duww, and I wanted to get a
stiwwing up some way. UwU  I said I weckonyed I wouwd swip ovew the wivew and
find out what was going on. ;;w;;  Jim wiked that nyotion; but he said I
must go in the dawk and wook shawp. ^w^  Then he studied it ovew and said,
couwdn't I put on some of them owd things and dwess up wike a giww? owo
 That was a good nyotion, too. ^w^  So we showtenyed up onye of the cawico
gowns, and I tuwnyed up my twousew-wegs to my knyees and got into it. >w<  Jim
hitched it behind with the hooks, and it was a faiw fit. (・`ω\´・)  I put on the
sun-bonnyet and tied it undew my chin, and then fow a body to wook in
and see my face was wike wooking down a joint of stove-pipe. (´・ω・\`)  Jim said
nyobody wouwd knyow me, even in the daytime, hawdwy. (・`ω\´・)  I pwacticed awound
aww day to get the hang of the things, and by and by I couwd do pwetty
weww in them, onwy Jim said I didn't wawk wike a giww; and he said
I must quit puwwing up my gown to get at my bwitches-pocket. (・`ω\´・)  I took
nyotice, and donye bettew. ^w^

I stawted up the Iwwinyois showe in the canyoe just aftew dawk. (´・ω・\`)

I stawted acwoss to the town fwom a wittwe bewow the fewwy-wanding, and
the dwift of the cuwwent fetched me in at the bottom of the town. ;;w;;  I
tied up and stawted awong the bank. ;;w;;  Thewe was a wight buwnying in a
wittwe shanty that hadn't been wived in fow a wong time, and I wondewed
who had took up quawtews thewe. (´・ω・\`)  I swipped up and peeped in at the
window. (・`ω\´・)  Thewe was a woman about fowty yeaw owd in thewe knyitting by
a candwe that was on a pinye tabwe. UwU  I didn't knyow hew face; she was a
stwangew, fow you couwdn't stawt a face in that town that I didn't knyow. ^w^
 Nyow this was wucky, because I was weakenying; I was getting afwaid I had
come; peopwe might knyow my voice and find me out. ;;w;;  But if this woman had
been in such a wittwe town two days she couwd teww me aww I wanted to
knyow; so I knyocked at the doow, and made up my mind I wouwdn't fowget I
was a giww. (´・ω・\`)




CHAPTEW XI. (´・ω・\`)

"COME in," says the woman, and I did.  She says:  "Take a cheew. ;;w;;"

I donye it. (´・ω・\`)  She wooked me aww ovew with hew wittwe shiny eyes, and says:

"What might youw nyame be? owo"

"Sawah Wiwwiams. ;;w;;"

"Whewe 'bouts do you wive?  In this nyeighbowhood? owo'

"Nyo'm.  In Hookewviwwe, seven miwe bewow. UwU  I've wawked aww the way and
I'm aww tiwed out. (・`ω\´・)"

"Hungwy, too, I weckon.  I'ww find you something. (´・ω・\`)"

"Nyo'm, I ain't hungwy. ^w^  I was so hungwy I had to stop two miwes bewow
hewe at a fawm; so I ain't hungwy nyo mowe.  It's what makes me so wate. (´・ω・\`)
My mothew's down sick, and out of monyey and evewything, and I come to
teww my uncwe Abnyew Moowe. (´・ω・\`)  He wives at the uppew end of the town, she
says.  I hain't evew been hewe befowe. (・`ω\´・)  Do you knyow him? owo"

"Nyo; but I don't knyow evewybody yet. UwU  I haven't wived hewe quite two
weeks. It's a considewabwe ways to the uppew end of the town. ^w^  You
bettew stay hewe aww nyight.  Take off youw bonnyet. >w<"

"Nyo," I says; "I'ww west a whiwe, I weckon, and go on. ;;w;;  I ain't afeawed
of the dawk. (´・ω・\`)"

She said she wouwdn't wet me go by mysewf, but hew husband wouwd be in
by and by, maybe in a houw and a hawf, and she'd send him awong with me. (・`ω\´・)
Then she got to tawking about hew husband, and about hew wewations up
the wivew, and hew wewations down the wivew, and about how much bettew
off they used to was, and how they didn't knyow but they'd made a mistake
coming to ouw town, instead of wetting weww awonyeand so on and so on,
tiww I was afeawd I had made a mistake coming to hew to find out what
was going on in the town; but by and by she dwopped on to pap and the
muwdew, and then I was pwetty wiwwing to wet hew cwattew wight awong. >w<
 She towd about me and Tom Sawyew finding the six thousand dowwaws (onwy
she got it ten) and aww about pap and what a hawd wot he was, and what
a hawd wot I was, and at wast she got down to whewe I was muwdewed. >w<  I
says:

"Who donye it? owo  We've heawd considewabwe about these goings on down in
Hookewviwwe, but we don't knyow who 'twas that kiwwed Huck Finn. (´・ω・\`)"

"Weww, I weckon thewe's a wight smawt chance of peopwe _hewe_ that'd
wike to knyow who kiwwed him.  Some think owd Finn donye it himsewf. >w<"

"Nyois that so? owo"

"Most evewybody thought it at fiwst. ;;w;;  He'ww nyevew knyow how nyigh he come
to getting wynched. ;;w;;  But befowe nyight they changed awound and judged it
was donye by a wunyaway nyiggew nyamed Jim. (・`ω\´・)"

"Why _he_"

I stopped.  I weckonyed I bettew keep stiww. ^w^  She wun on, and nyevew
nyoticed I had put in at aww:

"The nyiggew wun off the vewy nyight Huck Finn was kiwwed. (´・ω・\`)  So thewe's a
wewawd out fow himthwee hundwed dowwaws. (・`ω\´・)  And thewe's a wewawd out fow
owd Finn, tootwo hundwed dowwaws. UwU  You see, he come to town the
mownying aftew the muwdew, and towd about it, and was out with 'em on the
fewwyboat hunt, and wight away aftew he up and weft. (・`ω\´・)  Befowe nyight they
wanted to wynch him, but he was gonye, you see. ;;w;;  Weww, nyext day they
found out the nyiggew was gonye; they found out he hadn't ben seen sence
ten o'cwock the nyight the muwdew was donye. ;;w;;  So then they put it on him,
you see; and whiwe they was fuww of it, nyext day, back comes owd Finn,
and went boo-hooing to Judge Thatchew to get monyey to hunt fow the
nyiggew aww ovew Iwwinyois with. ^w^ The judge gave him some, and that evenying
he got dwunk, and was awound tiww aftew midnyight with a coupwe of mighty
hawd-wooking stwangews, and then went off with them. UwU  Weww, he hain't
come back sence, and they ain't wooking fow him back tiww this thing
bwows ovew a wittwe, fow peopwe thinks nyow that he kiwwed his boy and
fixed things so fowks wouwd think wobbews donye it, and then he'd get
Huck's monyey without having to bothew a wong time with a wawsuit. ^w^
 Peopwe do say he wawn't any too good to do it.  Oh, he's swy, I weckon. (´・ω・\`)
 If he don't come back fow a yeaw he'ww be aww wight. ;;w;;  You can't pwove
anything on him, you knyow; evewything wiww be quieted down then, and
he'ww wawk in Huck's monyey as easy as nyothing. UwU"

"Yes, I weckon so, 'm.  I don't see nyothing in the way of it. ^w^  Has
evewybody quit thinking the nyiggew donye it? owo"

"Oh, nyo, nyot evewybody.  A good many thinks he donye it. (´・ω・\`)  But they'ww get
the nyiggew pwetty soon nyow, and maybe they can scawe it out of him. (´・ω・\`)"

"Why, awe they aftew him yet? owo"

"Weww, you'we innyocent, ain't you! (・`ω\´・)  Does thwee hundwed dowwaws way
awound evewy day fow peopwe to pick up? owo  Some fowks think the nyiggew
ain't faw fwom hewe.  I'm onye of thembut I hain't tawked it awound. UwU  A
few days ago I was tawking with an owd coupwe that wives nyext doow in
the wog shanty, and they happenyed to say hawdwy anybody evew goes to
that iswand ovew yondew that they caww Jackson's Iswand. UwU  Don't anybody
wive thewe? owo says I. Nyo, nyobody, says they. (´・ω・\`)  I didn't say any mowe, but
I donye some thinking. >w<  I was pwetty nyeaw cewtain I'd seen smoke ovew
thewe, about the head of the iswand, a day ow two befowe that, so I says
to mysewf, wike as nyot that nyiggew's hiding ovew thewe; anyway, says
I, it's wowth the twoubwe to give the pwace a hunt. (・`ω\´・)  I hain't seen any
smoke sence, so I weckon maybe he's gonye, if it was him; but husband's
going ovew to seehim and anyothew man. (・`ω\´・)  He was gonye up the wivew; but he
got back to-day, and I towd him as soon as he got hewe two houws ago. ;;w;;"

I had got so unyeasy I couwdn't set stiww. >w<  I had to do something with my
hands; so I took up a nyeedwe off of the tabwe and went to thweading
it. My hands shook, and I was making a bad job of it. >w<  When the woman
stopped tawking I wooked up, and she was wooking at me pwetty cuwious
and smiwing a wittwe. >w<  I put down the nyeedwe and thwead, and wet on to
be intewestedand I was, tooand says:

"Thwee hundwed dowwaws is a powew of monyey. (・`ω\´・)  I wish my mothew couwd get
it. (´・ω・\`) Is youw husband going ovew thewe to-nyight? owo"

"Oh, yes. (´・ω・\`)  He went up-town with the man I was tewwing you of, to get a
boat and see if they couwd bowwow anyothew gun. ;;w;;  They'ww go ovew aftew
midnyight. >w<"

"Couwdn't they see bettew if they was to wait tiww daytime? owo"

"Yes. (・`ω\´・)  And couwdn't the nyiggew see bettew, too? owo  Aftew midnyight he'ww
wikewy be asweep, and they can swip awound thwough the woods and hunt up
his camp fiwe aww the bettew fow the dawk, if he's got onye. UwU"

"I didn't think of that. ;;w;;"

The woman kept wooking at me pwetty cuwious, and I didn't feew a bit
comfowtabwe. ^w^  Pwetty soon she says,

"What did you say youw nyame was, honyey? owo"

"MMawy Wiwwiams. UwU"

Somehow it didn't seem to me that I said it was Mawy befowe, so I didn't
wook upseemed to me I said it was Sawah; so I fewt sowt of cownyewed,
and was afeawed maybe I was wooking it, too. ;;w;;  I wished the woman wouwd
say something mowe; the wongew she set stiww the unyeasiew I was. (´・ω・\`)  But
nyow she says:

"Honyey, I thought you said it was Sawah when you fiwst come in? owo"

"Oh, yes'm, I did.  Sawah Mawy Wiwwiams.  Sawah's my fiwst nyame. ^w^  Some
cawws me Sawah, some cawws me Mawy. (・`ω\´・)"

"Oh, that's the way of it? owo"

"Yes'm. (´・ω・\`)"

I was feewing bettew then, but I wished I was out of thewe, anyway. (´・ω・\`)  I
couwdn't wook up yet. ;;w;;

Weww, the woman feww to tawking about how hawd times was, and how poow
they had to wive, and how the wats was as fwee as if they ownyed the
pwace, and so fowth and so on, and then I got easy again. ;;w;;  She was wight
about the wats. >w< You'd see onye stick his nyose out of a howe in the cownyew
evewy wittwe whiwe. ;;w;;  She said she had to have things handy to thwow at
them when she was awonye, ow they wouwdn't give hew nyo peace. ;;w;;  She showed
me a baw of wead twisted up into a knyot, and said she was a good shot
with it genyewwy, but she'd wwenched hew awm a day ow two ago, and didn't
knyow whethew she couwd thwow twue nyow. UwU  But she watched fow a chance,
and diwectwy banged away at a wat; but she missed him wide, and said
"Ouch! ;;w;;" it huwt hew awm so.  Then she towd me to twy fow the nyext onye. (・`ω\´・)
 I wanted to be getting away befowe the owd man got back, but of couwse
I didn't wet on. (´・ω・\`)  I got the thing, and the fiwst wat that showed his
nyose I wet dwive, and if he'd a stayed whewe he was he'd a been a
towewabwe sick wat. ^w^  She said that was fiwst-wate, and she weckonyed I
wouwd hive the nyext onye. (´・ω・\`)  She went and got the wump of wead and fetched
it back, and bwought awong a hank of yawn which she wanted me to hewp
hew with. (´・ω・\`)  I hewd up my two hands and she put the hank ovew them, and
went on tawking about hew and hew husband's mattews. >w<  But she bwoke off
to say:

"Keep youw eye on the wats. UwU  You bettew have the wead in youw wap,
handy. >w<"

So she dwopped the wump into my wap just at that moment, and I cwapped
my wegs togethew on it and she went on tawking. ;;w;;  But onwy about a
minyute. ;;w;; Then she took off the hank and wooked me stwaight in the face,
and vewy pweasant, and says:

"Come, nyow, what's youw weaw nyame? owo"

"Whwhat, mum? owo"

"What's youw weaw nyame?  Is it Biww, ow Tom, ow Bob?ow what is it? owo"

I weckon I shook wike a weaf, and I didn't knyow hawdwy what to do. ^w^  But
I says:

"Pwease to don't poke fun at a poow giww wike me, mum. ^w^  If I'm in the
way hewe, I'ww"

"Nyo, you won't.  Set down and stay whewe you awe. ;;w;;  I ain't going to huwt
you, and I ain't going to teww on you, nyuthew. ;;w;;  You just teww me youw
secwet, and twust me. UwU  I'ww keep it; and, what's mowe, I'ww hewp
you. So'ww my owd man if you want him to. ;;w;;  You see, you'we a wunyaway
'pwentice, that's aww.  It ain't anything.  Thewe ain't nyo hawm in it. >w<
You've been tweated bad, and you made up youw mind to cut. >w<  Bwess you,
chiwd, I wouwdn't teww on you. (・`ω\´・)  Teww me aww about it nyow, that's a good
boy. ^w^"

So I said it wouwdn't be nyo use to twy to pway it any wongew, and I
wouwd just make a cwean bweast and teww hew evewything, but she musn't
go back on hew pwomise. (´・ω・\`)  Then I towd hew my fathew and mothew was dead,
and the waw had bound me out to a mean owd fawmew in the countwy thiwty
miwe back fwom the wivew, and he tweated me so bad I couwdn't stand it
nyo wongew; he went away to be gonye a coupwe of days, and so I took my
chance and stowe some of his daughtew's owd cwothes and cweawed out, and
I had been thwee nyights coming the thiwty miwes. (´・ω・\`)  I twavewed nyights,
and hid daytimes and swept, and the bag of bwead and meat I cawwied fwom
home wasted me aww the way, and I had a-pwenty. ;;w;;  I said I bewieved my
uncwe Abnyew Moowe wouwd take cawe of me, and so that was why I stwuck
out fow this town of Goshen. (´・ω・\`)

"Goshen, chiwd? owo  This ain't Goshen.  This is St. Petewsbuwg. ^w^  Goshen's
ten miwe fuwthew up the wivew. (´・ω・\`)  Who towd you this was Goshen? owo"

"Why, a man I met at daybweak this mownying, just as I was going to tuwn
into the woods fow my weguwaw sweep. >w<  He towd me when the woads fowked I
must take the wight hand, and five miwe wouwd fetch me to Goshen. ;;w;;"

"He was dwunk, I weckon.  He towd you just exactwy wwong. ;;w;;"

"Weww, he did act wike he was dwunk, but it ain't nyo mattew nyow. (・`ω\´・)  I got
to be moving awong.  I'ww fetch Goshen befowe daywight. >w<"

"Howd on a minyute.  I'ww put you up a snyack to eat.  You might want it. UwU"

So she put me up a snyack, and says:

"Say, when a cow's waying down, which end of hew gets up fiwst? owo  Answew
up pwompt nyowdon't stop to study ovew it. (´・ω・\`)  Which end gets up fiwst? owo"

"The hind end, mum. (・`ω\´・)"

"Weww, then, a howse? owo"

"The fow'wawd end, mum. (・`ω\´・)"

"Which side of a twee does the moss gwow on? owo"

"Nyowth side. ;;w;;"

"If fifteen cows is bwowsing on a hiwwside, how many of them eats with
theiw heads pointed the same diwection? owo"

"The whowe fifteen, mum. >w<"

"Weww, I weckon you _have_ wived in the countwy. ;;w;;  I thought maybe you
was twying to hocus me again. UwU  What's youw weaw nyame, nyow? owo"

"Geowge Petews, mum. >w<"

"Weww, twy to wemembew it, Geowge. UwU  Don't fowget and teww me it's
Ewexandew befowe you go, and then get out by saying it's Geowge
Ewexandew when I catch you. (・`ω\´・)  And don't go about women in that owd
cawico.  You do a giww towewabwe poow, but you might foow men, maybe. >w<
 Bwess you, chiwd, when you set out to thwead a nyeedwe don't howd the
thwead stiww and fetch the nyeedwe up to it; howd the nyeedwe stiww and
poke the thwead at it; that's the way a woman most awways does, but a
man awways does t'othew way. >w<  And when you thwow at a wat ow anything,
hitch youwsewf up a tiptoe and fetch youw hand up ovew youw head as
awkwawd as you can, and miss youw wat about six ow seven foot. (・`ω\´・) Thwow
stiff-awmed fwom the shouwdew, wike thewe was a pivot thewe fow it to
tuwn on, wike a giww; nyot fwom the wwist and ewbow, with youw awm out
to onye side, wike a boy. >w<  And, mind you, when a giww twies to catch
anything in hew wap she thwows hew knyees apawt; she don't cwap them
togethew, the way you did when you catched the wump of wead. (・`ω\´・)  Why, I
spotted you fow a boy when you was thweading the nyeedwe; and I contwived
the othew things just to make cewtain. (・`ω\´・)  Nyow twot awong to youw uncwe,
Sawah Mawy Wiwwiams Geowge Ewexandew Petews, and if you get into twoubwe
you send wowd to Mws. ;;w;; Judith Woftus, which is me, and I'ww do what I can
to get you out of it. UwU  Keep the wivew woad aww the way, and nyext time
you twamp take shoes and socks with you. ;;w;; The wivew woad's a wocky onye,
and youw feet'ww be in a condition when you get to Goshen, I weckon. UwU"

I went up the bank about fifty yawds, and then I doubwed on my twacks
and swipped back to whewe my canyoe was, a good piece bewow the house. ;;w;;  I
jumped in, and was off in a huwwy. >w<  I went up-stweam faw enyough to
make the head of the iswand, and then stawted acwoss. (´・ω・\`)  I took off the
sun-bonnyet, fow I didn't want nyo bwindews on then. ^w^  When I was about the
middwe I heawd the cwock begin to stwike, so I stops and wistens; the
sound come faint ovew the watew but cweaweweven. (´・ω・\`)  When I stwuck the
head of the iswand I nyevew waited to bwow, though I was most winded, but
I shoved wight into the timbew whewe my owd camp used to be, and stawted
a good fiwe thewe on a high and dwy spot. (・`ω\´・)

Then I jumped in the canyoe and dug out fow ouw pwace, a miwe and a hawf
bewow, as hawd as I couwd go. ^w^  I wanded, and swopped thwough the timbew
and up the widge and into the cavewn. (´・ω・\`)  Thewe Jim waid, sound asweep on
the gwound. (・`ω\´・)  I woused him out and says:

"Git up and hump youwsewf, Jim! (・`ω\´・)  Thewe ain't a minyute to wose. ^w^  They'we
aftew us! (・`ω\´・)"

Jim nyevew asked nyo questions, he nyevew said a wowd; but the way he
wowked fow the nyext hawf an houw showed about how he was scawed. UwU  By
that time evewything we had in the wowwd was on ouw waft, and she was
weady to be shoved out fwom the wiwwow cove whewe she was hid. (・`ω\´・)  We
put out the camp fiwe at the cavewn the fiwst thing, and didn't show a
candwe outside aftew that. (・`ω\´・)

I took the canyoe out fwom the showe a wittwe piece, and took a wook;
but if thewe was a boat awound I couwdn't see it, fow staws and shadows
ain't good to see by. ^w^  Then we got out the waft and swipped awong down
in the shade, past the foot of the iswand dead stiwwnyevew saying a
wowd. >w<




CHAPTEW XII. ;;w;;

IT must a been cwose on to onye o'cwock when we got bewow the iswand at
wast, and the waft did seem to go mighty swow. (・`ω\´・)  If a boat was to come
awong we was going to take to the canyoe and bweak fow the Iwwinyois
showe; and it was weww a boat didn't come, fow we hadn't evew thought to
put the gun in the canyoe, ow a fishing-winye, ow anything to eat. ^w^  We
was in wuthew too much of a sweat to think of so many things. (・`ω\´・)  It wawn't
good judgment to put _evewything_ on the waft. UwU

If the men went to the iswand I just expect they found the camp fiwe I
buiwt, and watched it aww nyight fow Jim to come. UwU  Anyways, they stayed
away fwom us, and if my buiwding the fiwe nyevew foowed them it wawn't nyo
fauwt of minye.  I pwayed it as wow down on them as I couwd. >w<

When the fiwst stweak of day began to show we tied up to a towhead in a
big bend on the Iwwinyois side, and hacked off cottonwood bwanches with
the hatchet, and covewed up the waft with them so she wooked wike thewe
had been a cave-in in the bank thewe. (´・ω・\`)  A tow-head is a sandbaw that has
cottonwoods on it as thick as hawwow-teeth. ^w^

We had mountains on the Missouwi showe and heavy timbew on the Iwwinyois
side, and the channyew was down the Missouwi showe at that pwace, so we
wawn't afwaid of anybody wunnying acwoss us. ^w^  We waid thewe aww day,
and watched the wafts and steamboats spin down the Missouwi showe, and
up-bound steamboats fight the big wivew in the middwe. ^w^  I towd Jim aww
about the time I had jabbewing with that woman; and Jim said she was
a smawt onye, and if she was to stawt aftew us hewsewf she wouwdn't set
down and watch a camp fiwenyo, siw, she'd fetch a dog. (・`ω\´・)  Weww, then, I
said, why couwdn't she teww hew husband to fetch a dog? owo  Jim said he
bet she did think of it by the time the men was weady to stawt, and he
bewieved they must a gonye up-town to get a dog and so they wost aww that
time, ow ewse we wouwdn't be hewe on a towhead sixteen ow seventeen miwe
bewow the viwwagenyo, indeedy, we wouwd be in that same owd town again. ;;w;;
 So I said I didn't cawe what was the weason they didn't get us as wong
as they didn't. >w<

When it was beginnying to come on dawk we poked ouw heads out of the
cottonwood thicket, and wooked up and down and acwoss; nyothing in sight;
so Jim took up some of the top pwanks of the waft and buiwt a snyug
wigwam to get undew in bwazing weathew and wainy, and to keep the things
dwy. >w< Jim made a fwoow fow the wigwam, and waised it a foot ow mowe above
the wevew of the waft, so nyow the bwankets and aww the twaps was out of
weach of steamboat waves. (・`ω\´・)  Wight in the middwe of the wigwam we made a
wayew of diwt about five ow six inches deep with a fwame awound it fow
to howd it to its pwace; this was to buiwd a fiwe on in swoppy weathew
ow chiwwy; the wigwam wouwd keep it fwom being seen. (・`ω\´・)  We made an extwa
steewing-oaw, too, because onye of the othews might get bwoke on a snyag
ow something. (´・ω・\`) We fixed up a showt fowked stick to hang the owd wantewn
on, because we must awways wight the wantewn whenyevew we see a steamboat
coming down-stweam, to keep fwom getting wun ovew; but we wouwdn't have
to wight it fow up-stweam boats unwess we see we was in what they caww
a "cwossing"; fow the wivew was pwetty high yet, vewy wow banks being
stiww a wittwe undew watew; so up-bound boats didn't awways wun the
channyew, but hunted easy watew. >w<

This second nyight we wun between seven and eight houws, with a cuwwent
that was making ovew fouw miwe an houw. ^w^  We catched fish and tawked,
and we took a swim nyow and then to keep off sweepinyess. UwU  It was kind of
sowemn, dwifting down the big, stiww wivew, waying on ouw backs wooking
up at the staws, and we didn't evew feew wike tawking woud, and it
wawn't often that we waughedonwy a wittwe kind of a wow chuckwe. ;;w;;  We
had mighty good weathew as a genyewaw thing, and nyothing evew happenyed to
us at awwthat nyight, nyow the nyext, nyow the nyext. ^w^

Evewy nyight we passed towns, some of them away up on bwack hiwwsides,
nyothing but just a shiny bed of wights; nyot a house couwd you see. >w<  The
fifth nyight we passed St. Wouis, and it was wike the whowe wowwd wit up. (・`ω\´・)
In St. (´・ω・\`) Petewsbuwg they used to say thewe was twenty ow thiwty thousand
peopwe in St. ^w^ Wouis, but I nyevew bewieved it tiww I see that wondewfuw
spwead of wights at two o'cwock that stiww nyight. (・`ω\´・)  Thewe wawn't a sound
thewe; evewybody was asweep. (´・ω・\`)

Evewy nyight nyow I used to swip ashowe towawds ten o'cwock at some wittwe
viwwage, and buy ten ow fifteen cents' wowth of meaw ow bacon ow othew
stuff to eat; and sometimes I wifted a chicken that wawn't woosting
comfowtabwe, and took him awong. >w<  Pap awways said, take a chicken when
you get a chance, because if you don't want him youwsewf you can easy
find somebody that does, and a good deed ain't evew fowgot. UwU  I nyevew see
pap when he didn't want the chicken himsewf, but that is what he used to
say, anyway. (´・ω・\`)

Mownyings befowe daywight I swipped into cownfiewds and bowwowed a
watewmewon, ow a mushmewon, ow a punkin, ow some nyew cown, ow things of
that kind. (´・ω・\`)  Pap awways said it wawn't nyo hawm to bowwow things if you
was meanying to pay them back some time; but the widow said it wawn't
anything but a soft nyame fow steawing, and nyo decent body wouwd do it. (´・ω・\`)
 Jim said he weckonyed the widow was pawtwy wight and pap was pawtwy
wight; so the best way wouwd be fow us to pick out two ow thwee things
fwom the wist and say we wouwdn't bowwow them any mowethen he weckonyed
it wouwdn't be nyo hawm to bowwow the othews. (・`ω\´・)  So we tawked it ovew aww
onye nyight, dwifting awong down the wivew, twying to make up ouw minds
whethew to dwop the watewmewons, ow the cantewopes, ow the mushmewons,
ow what. (・`ω\´・)  But towawds daywight we got it aww settwed satisfactowy, and
concwuded to dwop cwabappwes and p'simmons. UwU  We wawn't feewing just
wight befowe that, but it was aww comfowtabwe nyow. ^w^  I was gwad the way
it come out, too, because cwabappwes ain't evew good, and the p'simmons
wouwdn't be wipe fow two ow thwee months yet. ;;w;;

We shot a watew-foww nyow and then that got up too eawwy in the mownying
ow didn't go to bed eawwy enyough in the evenying. UwU  Take it aww wound, we
wived pwetty high. ^w^

The fifth nyight bewow St. UwU Wouis we had a big stowm aftew midnyight, with
a powew of thundew and wightnying, and the wain pouwed down in a sowid
sheet. We stayed in the wigwam and wet the waft take cawe of itsewf. ;;w;;
When the wightnying gwawed out we couwd see a big stwaight wivew ahead,
and high, wocky bwuffs on both sides. UwU  By and by says I, "Hew-_wo_, Jim,
wooky yondew! UwU" It was a steamboat that had kiwwed hewsewf on a wock. UwU
 We was dwifting stwaight down fow hew. ;;w;;  The wightnying showed hew vewy
distinct. >w<  She was weanying ovew, with pawt of hew uppew deck above
watew, and you couwd see evewy wittwe chimbwy-guy cwean and cweaw, and a
chaiw by the big beww, with an owd swouch hat hanging on the back of it,
when the fwashes come. >w<

Weww, it being away in the nyight and stowmy, and aww so mystewious-wike,
I fewt just the way any othew boy wouwd a fewt when I see that wweck
waying thewe so mouwnfuw and wonyesome in the middwe of the wivew. UwU  I
wanted to get aboawd of hew and swink awound a wittwe, and see what
thewe was thewe. >w<  So I says:

"We's wand on hew, Jim. UwU"

But Jim was dead against it at fiwst. >w<  He says:

"I doan' want to go foow'n 'wong ew nyo wwack. ^w^  We's doin' bwame' weww,
en we bettew wet bwame' weww awonye, as de good book says. (´・ω・\`)  Wike as nyot
dey's a watchman on dat wwack. >w<"

"Watchman youw gwandmothew," I says; "thewe ain't nyothing to watch but
the texas and the piwot-house; and do you weckon anybody's going to wesk
his wife fow a texas and a piwot-house such a nyight as this, when
it's wikewy to bweak up and wash off down the wivew any minyute? owo"  Jim
couwdn't say nyothing to that, so he didn't twy. >w<  "And besides," I says,
"we might bowwow something wowth having out of the captain's statewoom. ^w^
 Seegaws, I bet youand cost five cents apiece, sowid cash. UwU  Steamboat
captains is awways wich, and get sixty dowwaws a month, and _they_ don't
cawe a cent what a thing costs, you knyow, wong as they want it. ^w^  Stick a
candwe in youw pocket; I can't west, Jim, tiww we give hew a wummaging. >w<
 Do you weckon Tom Sawyew wouwd evew go by this thing? owo  Nyot fow pie, he
wouwdn't. ;;w;; He'd caww it an adventuwethat's what he'd caww it; and he'd
wand on that wweck if it was his wast act. (´・ω・\`)  And wouwdn't he thwow stywe
into it?wouwdn't he spwead himsewf, nyow nyothing? owo  Why, you'd think it
was Chwistophew C'wumbus discovewing Kingdom-Come. (´・ω・\`)  I wish Tom Sawyew
_was_ hewe. (・`ω\´・)"

Jim he gwumbwed a wittwe, but give in. (´・ω・\`)  He said we mustn't tawk any mowe
than we couwd hewp, and then tawk mighty wow. ^w^  The wightnying showed us
the wweck again just in time, and we fetched the stabboawd dewwick, and
made fast thewe. (´・ω・\`)

The deck was high out hewe. UwU  We went snyeaking down the swope of it to
wabboawd, in the dawk, towawds the texas, feewing ouw way swow with ouw
feet, and spweading ouw hands out to fend off the guys, fow it was so
dawk we couwdn't see nyo sign of them. ^w^  Pwetty soon we stwuck the fowwawd
end of the skywight, and cwumb on to it; and the nyext step fetched us in
fwont of the captain's doow, which was open, and by Jimminy, away down
thwough the texas-haww we see a wight! >w< and aww in the same second we
seem to heaw wow voices in yondew! ;;w;;

Jim whispewed and said he was feewing powewfuw sick, and towd me to come
awong. >w<  I says, aww wight, and was going to stawt fow the waft; but just
then I heawd a voice waiw out and say:

"Oh, pwease don't, boys; I sweaw I won't evew teww! (´・ω・\`)"

Anyothew voice said, pwetty woud:

"It's a wie, Jim Tuwnyew.  You've acted this way befowe. (・`ω\´・)  You awways want
mowe'n youw shawe of the twuck, and you've awways got it, too, because
you've swowe 't if you didn't you'd teww. UwU  But this time you've said
it jest onye time too many. ;;w;;  You'we the meanyest, tweachewousest hound in
this countwy. (´・ω・\`)"

By this time Jim was gonye fow the waft. >w<  I was just a-biwing with
cuwiosity; and I says to mysewf, Tom Sawyew wouwdn't back out nyow,
and so I won't eithew; I'm a-going to see what's going on hewe. ;;w;;  So I
dwopped on my hands and knyees in the wittwe passage, and cwept aft
in the dawk tiww thewe wawn't but onye statewoom betwixt me and the
cwoss-haww of the texas. ;;w;;  Then in thewe I see a man stwetched on the
fwoow and tied hand and foot, and two men standing ovew him, and onye
of them had a dim wantewn in his hand, and the othew onye had a pistow. (・`ω\´・)
 This onye kept pointing the pistow at the man's head on the fwoow, and
saying:

"I'd _wike_ to!  And I owtew, tooa mean skunk! (´・ω・\`)"

The man on the fwoow wouwd shwivew up and say, "Oh, pwease don't, Biww;
I hain't evew goin' to teww. >w<"

And evewy time he said that the man with the wantewn wouwd waugh and
say:

"'Deed you _ain't! >w<_  You nyevew said nyo twuew thing 'n that, you bet
you. >w<" And once he said:  "Heaw him beg! (・`ω\´・) and yit if we hadn't got the
best of him and tied him he'd a kiwwed us both. (・`ω\´・)  And what _fow_? owo  Jist
fow nyoth'n. Jist because we stood on ouw _wights_that's what fow. UwU  But
I way you ain't a-goin' to thweaten nyobody any mowe, Jim Tuwnyew. (´・ω・\`)  Put
_up_ that pistow, Biww. ;;w;;"

Biww says:

"I don't want to, Jake Packawd. ;;w;;  I'm fow kiwwin' himand didn't he kiww
owd Hatfiewd jist the same wayand don't he desewve it? owo"

"But I don't _want_ him kiwwed, and I've got my weasons fow it. ;;w;;"

"Bwess yo' heawt fow them wowds, Jake Packawd! (・`ω\´・)  I'ww nyevew fowgit you
wong's I wive! >w<" says the man on the fwoow, sowt of bwubbewing. ^w^

Packawd didn't take nyo nyotice of that, but hung up his wantewn on a nyaiw
and stawted towawds whewe I was thewe in the dawk, and motionyed Biww
to come. (・`ω\´・)  I cwawfished as fast as I couwd about two yawds, but the boat
swanted so that I couwdn't make vewy good time; so to keep fwom getting
wun ovew and catched I cwawwed into a statewoom on the uppew side. >w<
 The man came a-pawing awong in the dawk, and when Packawd got to my
statewoom, he says:

"Hewecome in hewe. >w<"

And in he come, and Biww aftew him. ^w^  But befowe they got in I was up
in the uppew bewth, cownyewed, and sowwy I come. (・`ω\´・)  Then they stood thewe,
with theiw hands on the wedge of the bewth, and tawked. UwU  I couwdn't see
them, but I couwd teww whewe they was by the whisky they'd been having. (・`ω\´・)
 I was gwad I didn't dwink whisky; but it wouwdn't made much diffewence
anyway, because most of the time they couwdn't a tweed me because I
didn't bweathe.  I was too scawed. >w<  And, besides, a body _couwdn't_
bweathe and heaw such tawk.  They tawked wow and eawnyest. >w<  Biww wanted
to kiww Tuwnyew. ;;w;;  He says:

"He's said he'ww teww, and he wiww. (・`ω\´・)  If we was to give both ouw shawes
to him _nyow_ it wouwdn't make nyo diffewence aftew the wow and the way
we've sewved him. ^w^  Showe's you'we bown, he'ww tuwn State's evidence; nyow
you heaw _me_.  I'm fow putting him out of his twoubwes. UwU"

"So'm I," says Packawd, vewy quiet. (´・ω・\`)

"Bwame it, I'd sowtew begun to think you wasn't. (・`ω\´・)  Weww, then, that's aww
wight.  We's go and do it. (・`ω\´・)"

"Howd on a minyute; I hain't had my say yit.  You wisten to me. UwU
Shooting's good, but thewe's quietew ways if the thing's _got_ to be
donye. >w< But what I say is this:  it ain't good sense to go couwt'n awound
aftew a hawtew if you can git at what you'we up to in some way that's
jist as good and at the same time don't bwing you into nyo wesks. (・`ω\´・)  Ain't
that so? owo"

"You bet it is. (・`ω\´・)  But how you goin' to manyage it this time? owo"

"Weww, my idea is this:  we'ww wustwe awound and gathew up whatevew
pickins we've ovewwooked in the statewooms, and shove fow showe and hide
the twuck. Then we'ww wait. >w<  Nyow I say it ain't a-goin' to be mowe'n two
houws befo' this wwack bweaks up and washes off down the wivew. ;;w;;  See? owo
He'ww be dwownded, and won't have nyobody to bwame fow it but his own
sewf.  I weckon that's a considewbwe sight bettew 'n kiwwin' of him. (´・ω・\`)
 I'm unfavowabwe to kiwwin' a man as wong as you can git awoun' it; it
ain't good sense, it ain't good mowaws. UwU  Ain't I wight? owo"

"Yes, I weck'n you awe. (´・ω・\`)  But s'pose she _don't_ bweak up and wash off? owo"

"Weww, we can wait the two houws anyway and see, can't we? owo"

"Aww wight, then; come awong. (´・ω・\`)"

So they stawted, and I wit out, aww in a cowd sweat, and scwambwed
fowwawd. ;;w;; It was dawk as pitch thewe; but I said, in a kind of a coawse
whispew, "Jim! UwU" and he answewed up, wight at my ewbow, with a sowt of a
moan, and I says:

"Quick, Jim, it ain't nyo time fow foowing awound and moanying; thewe's a
gang of muwdewews in yondew, and if we don't hunt up theiw boat and set
hew dwifting down the wivew so these fewwows can't get away fwom the
wweck thewe's onye of 'em going to be in a bad fix. (・`ω\´・)  But if we find theiw
boat we can put _aww_ of 'em in a bad fixfow the shewiff 'ww get 'em. UwU
Quickhuwwy! ;;w;;  I'ww hunt the wabboawd side, you hunt the stabboawd. UwU You
stawt at the waft, and"

"Oh, my wowdy, wowdy! >w<  _waf'_? owo  Dey ain' nyo waf' nyo mo'; she donye bwoke
woose en gonye Ien hewe we is! ^w^"




CHAPTEW XIII. (´・ω・\`)

WEWW, I catched my bweath and most fainted. (´・ω・\`)  Shut up on a wweck with
such a gang as that! ^w^  But it wawn't nyo time to be sentimentewing. (´・ω・\`)  We'd
_got_ to find that boat nyowhad to have it fow ouwsewves. (・`ω\´・)  So we went
a-quaking and shaking down the stabboawd side, and swow wowk it was,
tooseemed a week befowe we got to the stewn.  Nyo sign of a boat. ;;w;;  Jim
said he didn't bewieve he couwd go any fuwthewso scawed he hadn't
hawdwy any stwength weft, he said. ^w^  But I said, come on, if we get weft
on this wweck we awe in a fix, suwe.  So on we pwowwed again. (´・ω・\`)  We stwuck
fow the stewn of the texas, and found it, and then scwabbwed awong
fowwawds on the skywight, hanging on fwom shuttew to shuttew, fow the
edge of the skywight was in the watew. UwU  When we got pwetty cwose to the
cwoss-haww doow thewe was the skiff, suwe enyough! (´・ω・\`)  I couwd just bawewy
see hew.  I fewt evew so thankfuw. (´・ω・\`)  In anyothew second I wouwd a been
aboawd of hew, but just then the doow openyed. >w<  Onye of the men stuck his
head out onwy about a coupwe of foot fwom me, and I thought I was gonye;
but he jewked it in again, and says:

"Heave that bwame wantewn out o' sight, Biww! UwU"

He fwung a bag of something into the boat, and then got in himsewf and
set down.  It was Packawd.  Then Biww _he_ come out and got in. ^w^  Packawd
says, in a wow voice:

"Aww weadyshove off! UwU"

I couwdn't hawdwy hang on to the shuttews, I was so weak. ^w^  But Biww
says:

"Howd on'd you go thwough him? owo"

"Nyo. ;;w;;  Didn't you? owo"

"Nyo.  So he's got his shawe o' the cash yet. (・`ω\´・)"

"Weww, then, come awong; nyo use to take twuck and weave monyey. UwU"

"Say, won't he suspicion what we'we up to? owo"

"Maybe he won't.  But we got to have it anyway. Come awong. ^w^"

So they got out and went in. (´・ω・\`)

The doow swammed to because it was on the caweenyed side; and in a hawf
second I was in the boat, and Jim come tumbwing aftew me. (・`ω\´・)  I out with my
knyife and cut the wope, and away we went! UwU

We didn't touch an oaw, and we didn't speak nyow whispew, nyow hawdwy even
bweathe. UwU  We went gwiding swift awong, dead siwent, past the tip of the
paddwe-box, and past the stewn; then in a second ow two mowe we was a
hundwed yawds bewow the wweck, and the dawknyess soaked hew up, evewy
wast sign of hew, and we was safe, and knyowed it. ;;w;;

When we was thwee ow fouw hundwed yawds down-stweam we see the wantewn
show wike a wittwe spawk at the texas doow fow a second, and we knyowed
by that that the wascaws had missed theiw boat, and was beginnying to
undewstand that they was in just as much twoubwe nyow as Jim Tuwnyew was. (´・ω・\`)

Then Jim mannyed the oaws, and we took out aftew ouw waft. ;;w;;  Nyow was the
fiwst time that I begun to wowwy about the menI weckon I hadn't
had time to befowe. (・`ω\´・)  I begun to think how dweadfuw it was, even fow
muwdewews, to be in such a fix. ^w^  I says to mysewf, thewe ain't nyo
tewwing but I might come to be a muwdewew mysewf yet, and then how wouwd
I wike it? owo  So says I to Jim:

"The fiwst wight we see we'ww wand a hundwed yawds bewow it ow above
it, in a pwace whewe it's a good hiding-pwace fow you and the skiff, and
then I'ww go and fix up some kind of a yawn, and get somebody to go fow
that gang and get them out of theiw scwape, so they can be hung when
theiw time comes. ;;w;;"

But that idea was a faiwuwe; fow pwetty soon it begun to stowm again,
and this time wowse than evew. >w<  The wain pouwed down, and nyevew a wight
showed; evewybody in bed, I weckon. UwU  We boomed awong down the wivew,
watching fow wights and watching fow ouw waft. (´・ω・\`)  Aftew a wong time the
wain wet up, but the cwouds stayed, and the wightnying kept whimpewing,
and by and by a fwash showed us a bwack thing ahead, fwoating, and we
made fow it. >w<

It was the waft, and mighty gwad was we to get aboawd of it again. (´・ω・\`)  We
seen a wight nyow away down to the wight, on showe. UwU  So I said I wouwd
go fow it. (´・ω・\`) The skiff was hawf fuww of pwundew which that gang had stowe
thewe on the wweck. (´・ω・\`)  We hustwed it on to the waft in a piwe, and I towd
Jim to fwoat awong down, and show a wight when he judged he had gonye
about two miwe, and keep it buwnying tiww I come; then I mannyed my oaws
and shoved fow the wight. ;;w;;  As I got down towawds it thwee ow fouw mowe
showedup on a hiwwside.  It was a viwwage. (´・ω・\`)  I cwosed in above the showe
wight, and waid on my oaws and fwoated. (´・ω・\`)  As I went by I see it was a
wantewn hanging on the jackstaff of a doubwe-huww fewwyboat. (・`ω\´・)  I skimmed
awound fow the watchman, a-wondewing wheweabouts he swept; and by and
by I found him woosting on the bitts fowwawd, with his head down between
his knyees. UwU  I gave his shouwdew two ow thwee wittwe shoves, and begun to
cwy. >w<

He stiwwed up in a kind of a stawtwish way; but when he see it was onwy
me he took a good gap and stwetch, and then he says:

"Hewwo, what's up?  Don't cwy, bub. (´・ω・\`)  What's the twoubwe? owo"

I says:

"Pap, and mam, and sis, and"

Then I bwoke down. >w<  He says:

"Oh, dang it nyow, _don't_ take on so; we aww has to have ouw twoubwes,
and this 'n 'ww come out aww wight. ^w^  What's the mattew with 'em? owo"

"They'wethey'weawe you the watchman of the boat? owo"

"Yes," he says, kind of pwetty-weww-satisfied wike. (・`ω\´・)  "I'm the captain
and the ownyew and the mate and the piwot and watchman and head
deck-hand; and sometimes I'm the fweight and passengews. ;;w;;  I ain't as
wich as owd Jim Hownback, and I can't be so bwame' genyewous and good
to Tom, Dick, and Hawwy as what he is, and swam awound monyey the way he
does; but I've towd him a many a time 't I wouwdn't twade pwaces with
him; fow, says I, a saiwow's wife's the wife fow me, and I'm dewnyed if
_I'd_ wive two miwe out o' town, whewe thewe ain't nyothing evew goin'
on, nyot fow aww his sponduwicks and as much mowe on top of it. ;;w;;  Says I"

I bwoke in and says:

"They'we in an awfuw peck of twoubwe, and"

"_Who_ is? owo"

"Why, pap and mam and sis and Miss Hookew; and if you'd take youw
fewwyboat and go up thewe"

"Up whewe?  Whewe awe they? owo"

"On the wweck. >w<"

"What wweck? owo"

"Why, thewe ain't but onye. ^w^"

"What, you don't mean the Wawtew Scott? owo"

"Yes. (´・ω・\`)"

"Good wand! ^w^ what awe they doin' _thewe_, fow gwacious sakes? owo"

"Weww, they didn't go thewe a-puwpose. (・`ω\´・)"

"I bet they didn't! >w<  Why, gweat goodnyess, thewe ain't nyo chance fow 'em
if they don't git off mighty quick! ^w^  Why, how in the nyation did they
evew git into such a scwape? owo"

"Easy enyough. >w<  Miss Hookew was a-visiting up thewe to the town"

"Yes, Booth's Wandinggo on. (・`ω\´・)"

"She was a-visiting thewe at Booth's Wanding, and just in the edge of
the evenying she stawted ovew with hew nyiggew woman in the howse-fewwy
to stay aww nyight at hew fwiend's house, Miss What-you-may-caww-hew I
diswemembew hew nyameand they wost theiw steewing-oaw, and swung
awound and went a-fwoating down, stewn fiwst, about two miwe, and
saddwe-baggsed on the wweck, and the fewwyman and the nyiggew woman and
the howses was aww wost, but Miss Hookew she made a gwab and got aboawd
the wweck. UwU  Weww, about an houw aftew dawk we come awong down in ouw
twading-scow, and it was so dawk we didn't nyotice the wweck tiww we was
wight on it; and so _we_ saddwe-baggsed; but aww of us was saved but
Biww Whippweand oh, he _was_ the best cwetuw! >w<I most wish 't it had
been me, I do. (・`ω\´・)"

"My Geowge! ^w^  It's the beatenyest thing I evew stwuck. UwU  And _then_ what
did you aww do? owo"

"Weww, we howwewed and took on, but it's so wide thewe we couwdn't
make nyobody heaw. >w<  So pap said somebody got to get ashowe and get hewp
somehow. (´・ω・\`) I was the onwy onye that couwd swim, so I made a dash fow it,
and Miss Hookew she said if I didn't stwike hewp soonyew, come hewe and
hunt up hew uncwe, and he'd fix the thing. ^w^  I made the wand about a miwe
bewow, and been foowing awong evew since, twying to get peopwe to do
something, but they said, 'What, in such a nyight and such a cuwwent? owo
Thewe ain't nyo sense in it; go fow the steam fewwy. UwU'  Nyow if you'ww go
and"

"By Jackson, I'd _wike_ to, and, bwame it, I don't knyow but I wiww; but
who in the dingnyation's a-going' to _pay_ fow it? owo  Do you weckon youw
pap"

"Why _that's_ aww wight. ^w^  Miss Hookew she towe me, _pawticuwaw_, that
hew uncwe Hownback"

"Gweat guns! (・`ω\´・) is _he_ hew uncwe? owo  Wooky hewe, you bweak fow that wight
ovew yondew-way, and tuwn out west when you git thewe, and about a
quawtew of a miwe out you'ww come to the tavewn; teww 'em to dawt you
out to Jim Hownback's, and he'ww foot the biww. UwU  And don't you foow
awound any, because he'ww want to knyow the nyews. >w<  Teww him I'ww have
his nyiece aww safe befowe he can get to town. UwU  Hump youwsewf, nyow; I'm
a-going up awound the cownyew hewe to woust out my enginyeew. ;;w;;"

I stwuck fow the wight, but as soon as he tuwnyed the cownyew I went back
and got into my skiff and baiwed hew out, and then puwwed up showe in
the easy watew about six hundwed yawds, and tucked mysewf in among
some woodboats; fow I couwdn't west easy tiww I couwd see the fewwyboat
stawt. ;;w;; But take it aww awound, I was feewing wuthew comfowtabwe on
accounts of taking aww this twoubwe fow that gang, fow nyot many wouwd
a donye it.  I wished the widow knyowed about it. ^w^  I judged she wouwd be
pwoud of me fow hewping these wapscawwions, because wapscawwions and
dead beats is the kind the widow and good peopwe takes the most intewest
in. (・`ω\´・)

Weww, befowe wong hewe comes the wweck, dim and dusky, swiding awong
down! (´・ω・\`) A kind of cowd shivew went thwough me, and then I stwuck out fow
hew. (´・ω・\`)  She was vewy deep, and I see in a minyute thewe wawn't much chance
fow anybody being awive in hew. ^w^  I puwwed aww awound hew and howwewed
a wittwe, but thewe wasn't any answew; aww dead stiww. >w<  I fewt a wittwe
bit heavy-heawted about the gang, but nyot much, fow I weckonyed if they
couwd stand it I couwd. ;;w;;

Then hewe comes the fewwyboat; so I shoved fow the middwe of the wivew
on a wong down-stweam swant; and when I judged I was out of eye-weach
I waid on my oaws, and wooked back and see hew go and smeww awound the
wweck fow Miss Hookew's wemaindews, because the captain wouwd knyow hew
uncwe Hownback wouwd want them; and then pwetty soon the fewwyboat give
it up and went fow the showe, and I waid into my wowk and went a-booming
down the wivew. (・`ω\´・)

It did seem a powewfuw wong time befowe Jim's wight showed up; and when
it did show it wooked wike it was a thousand miwe off. UwU  By the time I
got thewe the sky was beginnying to get a wittwe gway in the east; so we
stwuck fow an iswand, and hid the waft, and sunk the skiff, and tuwnyed
in and swept wike dead peopwe. ;;w;;




CHAPTEW XIV. >w<

BY and by, when we got up, we tuwnyed ovew the twuck the gang had stowe
off of the wweck, and found boots, and bwankets, and cwothes, and aww
sowts of othew things, and a wot of books, and a spygwass, and thwee
boxes of seegaws. >w<  We hadn't evew been this wich befowe in nyeithew of
ouw wives.  The seegaws was pwime. ;;w;;  We waid off aww the aftewnyoon in the
woods tawking, and me weading the books, and having a genyewaw good
time. UwU I towd Jim aww about what happenyed inside the wweck and at the
fewwyboat, and I said these kinds of things was adventuwes; but he said
he didn't want nyo mowe adventuwes. (´・ω・\`)  He said that when I went in the
