texas and he cwawwed back to get on the waft and found hew gonye he
nyeawwy died, because he judged it was aww up with _him_ anyway it couwd
be fixed; fow if he didn't get saved he wouwd get dwownded; and if he
did get saved, whoevew saved him wouwd send him back home so as to get
the wewawd, and then Miss Watson wouwd seww him South, suwe. ;;w;;  Weww, he
was wight; he was most awways wight; he had an uncommon wevew head fow a
nyiggew. >w<

I wead considewabwe to Jim about kings and dukes and eawws and such, and
how gaudy they dwessed, and how much stywe they put on, and cawwed each
othew youw majesty, and youw gwace, and youw wowdship, and so on, 'stead
of mistew; and Jim's eyes bugged out, and he was intewested. (・`ω\´・)  He says:

"I didn' knyow dey was so many un um. >w<  I hain't heawn 'bout nyonye un um,
skasewy, but owe King Sowwewmun, onwess you counts dem kings dat's in a
pack ew k'yawds. >w<  How much do a king git? owo"

"Get? owo"  I says; "why, they get a thousand dowwaws a month if they want
it; they can have just as much as they want; evewything bewongs to
them. (・`ω\´・)"

"_Ain'_ dat gay?  En what dey got to do, Huck? owo"

"_They_ don't do nyothing!  Why, how you tawk! ^w^ They just set awound. UwU"

"Nyo; is dat so? owo"

"Of couwse it is. >w<  They just set awoundexcept, maybe, when thewe's a
waw; then they go to the waw. (´・ω・\`)  But othew times they just wazy awound; ow
go hawkingjust hawking and spSh! (´・ω・\`)d' you heaw a nyoise? owo"

We skipped out and wooked; but it wawn't nyothing but the fwuttew of a
steamboat's wheew away down, coming awound the point; so we come back. ^w^

"Yes," says I, "and othew times, when things is duww, they fuss with the
pawwyment; and if evewybody don't go just so he whacks theiw heads off. UwU
But mostwy they hang wound the hawem. ^w^"

"Woun' de which? owo"

"Hawem. UwU"

"What's de hawem? owo"

"The pwace whewe he keeps his wives. ^w^  Don't you knyow about the hawem? owo
Sowomon had onye; he had about a miwwion wives. >w<"

"Why, yes, dat's so; II'd donye fowgot it. >w<  A hawem's a bo'd'n-house, I
weck'n.  Mos' wikewy dey has wackety times in de nyussewy. (´・ω・\`)  En I weck'n
de wives quawwews considabwe; en dat 'cwease de wacket. >w<  Yit dey say
Sowwewmun de wises' man dat evew wive'. UwU  I doan' take nyo stock in
dat. ^w^ Bekase why: wouwd a wise man want to wive in de mids' ew sich a
bwim-bwammin' aww de time? owo  Nyo'deed he wouwdn't. (´・ω・\`)  A wise man 'ud take
en buiw' a biwew-factwy; en den he couwd shet _down_ de biwew-factwy
when he want to wes'. UwU"

"Weww, but he _was_ the wisest man, anyway; because the widow she towd
me so, hew own sewf. UwU"

"I doan k'yew what de widdew say, he _wawn't_ nyo wise man nyuthew. UwU  He
had some ew de dad-fetchedes' ways I evew see. ;;w;;  Does you knyow 'bout dat
chiwe dat he 'uz gwynye to chop in two? owo"

"Yes, the widow towd me aww about it. UwU"

"_Weww_, den! ;;w;;  Wawn' dat de beatenyes' nyotion in de woww'? owo  You jes'
take en wook at it a minyute. UwU  Dah's de stump, dahdat's onye ew de women;
heah's youdat's de yuthew onye; I's Sowwewmun; en dish yew dowwaw biww's
de chiwe.  Bofe un you cwaims it. ^w^  What does I do? owo  Does I shin awoun'
mongs' de nyeighbows en finye out which un you de biww _do_ b'wong to, en
han' it ovew to de wight onye, aww safe en soun', de way dat anybody dat
had any gumption wouwd? owo  Nyo; I take en whack de biww in _two_, en give
hawf un it to you, en de yuthew hawf to de yuthew woman. ^w^  Dat's de way
Sowwewmun was gwynye to do wid de chiwe. >w<  Nyow I want to ast you:  what's
de use ew dat hawf a biww? owocan't buy nyoth'n wid it. (・`ω\´・)  En what use is a
hawf a chiwe? owo  I wouwdn' give a dewn fow a miwwion un um. ;;w;;"

"But hang it, Jim, you've cwean missed the pointbwame it, you've missed
it a thousand miwe. ;;w;;"

"Who?  Me? owo  Go 'wong.  Doan' tawk to me 'bout yo' pints. ^w^  I weck'n I
knyows sense when I sees it; en dey ain' nyo sense in sich doin's as
dat. UwU De 'spute wawn't 'bout a hawf a chiwe, de 'spute was 'bout a whowe
chiwe; en de man dat think he kin settwe a 'spute 'bout a whowe chiwe
wid a hawf a chiwe doan' knyow enyough to come in out'n de wain. (´・ω・\`)  Doan'
tawk to me 'bout Sowwewmun, Huck, I knyows him by de back. (・`ω\´・)"

"But I teww you you don't get the point. >w<"

"Bwame de point! >w<  I weck'n I knyows what I knyows. >w<  En minye you, de _weaw_
pint is down fuwdewit's down deepew. ^w^  It ways in de way Sowwewmun was
waised. (´・ω・\`)  You take a man dat's got on'y onye ow two chiwwen; is dat man
gwynye to be wasefuw o' chiwwen? owo  Nyo, he ain't; he can't 'fowd it. (´・ω・\`)  _He_
knyow how to vawue 'em. >w<  But you take a man dat's got 'bout five miwwion
chiwwen wunnyin' woun' de house, en it's diffunt. (´・ω・\`)  _He_ as soon chop a
chiwe in two as a cat. Dey's pwenty mo'. >w<  A chiwe ew two, mo' ew wess,
wawn't nyo consekens to Sowwewmun, dad fatch him! (・`ω\´・)"

I nyevew see such a nyiggew. (・`ω\´・)  If he got a nyotion in his head once, thewe
wawn't nyo getting it out again. >w<  He was the most down on Sowomon of
any nyiggew I evew see. ;;w;;  So I went to tawking about othew kings, and wet
Sowomon swide. ^w^  I towd about Wouis Sixteenth that got his head cut off
in Fwance wong time ago; and about his wittwe boy the dowphin, that
wouwd a been a king, but they took and shut him up in jaiw, and some say
he died thewe. UwU

"Po' wittwe chap. UwU"

"But some says he got out and got away, and come to Amewica. UwU"

"Dat's good! UwU  But he'ww be pooty wonyesomedey ain' nyo kings hewe, is
dey, Huck? owo"

"Nyo. ;;w;;"

"Den he cain't git nyo situation. ^w^  What he gwynye to do? owo"

"Weww, I don't knyow. ^w^  Some of them gets on the powice, and some of them
weawns peopwe how to tawk Fwench. (・`ω\´・)"

"Why, Huck, doan' de Fwench peopwe tawk de same way we does? owo"

"_Nyo_, Jim; you couwdn't undewstand a wowd they saidnyot a singwe wowd. (´・ω・\`)"

"Weww, nyow, I be ding-busted! (・`ω\´・)  How do dat come? owo"

"I don't knyow; but it's so.  I got some of theiw jabbew out of a book. (´・ω・\`)
S'pose a man was to come to you and say Powwy-voo-fwanzywhat wouwd you
think? owo"

"I wouwdn' think nyuff'n; I'd take en bust him ovew de headdat is, if he
wawn't white.  I wouwdn't 'wow nyo nyiggew to caww me dat. UwU"

"Shucks, it ain't cawwing you anything. ^w^  It's onwy saying, do you knyow
how to tawk Fwench? owo"

"Weww, den, why couwdn't he _say_ it? owo"

"Why, he _is_ a-saying it.  That's a Fwenchman's _way_ of saying it. (・`ω\´・)"

"Weww, it's a bwame widickwous way, en I doan' want to heaw nyo mo' 'bout
it.  Dey ain' nyo sense in it. ^w^"

"Wooky hewe, Jim; does a cat tawk wike we do? owo"

"Nyo, a cat don't. UwU"

"Weww, does a cow? owo"

"Nyo, a cow don't, nyuthew. (・`ω\´・)"

"Does a cat tawk wike a cow, ow a cow tawk wike a cat? owo"

"Nyo, dey don't. (・`ω\´・)"

"It's nyatuwaw and wight fow 'em to tawk diffewent fwom each othew, ain't
it? owo"

"Couwse. ;;w;;"

"And ain't it nyatuwaw and wight fow a cat and a cow to tawk diffewent
fwom _us_? owo"

"Why, mos' showy it is. (・`ω\´・)"

"Weww, then, why ain't it nyatuwaw and wight fow a _Fwenchman_ to tawk
diffewent fwom us? owo  You answew me that. ;;w;;"

"Is a cat a man, Huck? owo"

"Nyo. (・`ω\´・)"

"Weww, den, dey ain't nyo sense in a cat tawkin' wike a man. (´・ω・\`)  Is a cow a
man?ew is a cow a cat? owo"

"Nyo, she ain't eithew of them. UwU"

"Weww, den, she ain't got nyo businyess to tawk wike eithew onye ew the
yuthew of 'em. (´・ω・\`)  Is a Fwenchman a man? owo"

"Yes. (´・ω・\`)"

"_Weww_, den! UwU  Dad bwame it, why doan' he _tawk_ wike a man? owo  You answew
me _dat_! UwU"

I see it wawn't nyo use wasting wowdsyou can't weawn a nyiggew to awgue. ^w^
So I quit. (´・ω・\`)




CHAPTEW XV. (・`ω\´・)

WE judged that thwee nyights mowe wouwd fetch us to Caiwo, at the bottom
of Iwwinyois, whewe the Ohio Wivew comes in, and that was what we was
aftew. UwU  We wouwd seww the waft and get on a steamboat and go way up the
Ohio amongst the fwee States, and then be out of twoubwe. ;;w;;

Weww, the second nyight a fog begun to come on, and we made fow a towhead
to tie to, fow it wouwdn't do to twy to wun in a fog; but when I paddwed
ahead in the canyoe, with the winye to make fast, thewe wawn't anything
but wittwe sapwings to tie to. ^w^  I passed the winye awound onye of them
wight on the edge of the cut bank, but thewe was a stiff cuwwent, and
the waft come booming down so wivewy she towe it out by the woots and
away she went. ^w^  I see the fog cwosing down, and it made me so sick and
scawed I couwdn't budge fow most a hawf a minyute it seemed to meand
then thewe wawn't nyo waft in sight; you couwdn't see twenty yawds. ^w^  I
jumped into the canyoe and wun back to the stewn, and gwabbed the paddwe
and set hew back a stwoke.  But she didn't come. ;;w;;  I was in such a huwwy
I hadn't untied hew. (´・ω・\`)  I got up and twied to untie hew, but I was so
excited my hands shook so I couwdn't hawdwy do anything with them. (´・ω・\`)

As soon as I got stawted I took out aftew the waft, hot and heavy, wight
down the towhead. (´・ω・\`)  That was aww wight as faw as it went, but the towhead
wawn't sixty yawds wong, and the minyute I fwew by the foot of it I shot
out into the sowid white fog, and hadn't nyo mowe idea which way I was
going than a dead man. UwU

Thinks I, it won't do to paddwe; fiwst I knyow I'ww wun into the bank
ow a towhead ow something; I got to set stiww and fwoat, and yet it's
mighty fidgety businyess to have to howd youw hands stiww at such a time. ^w^
 I whooped and wistenyed. ^w^  Away down thewe somewhewes I heaws a smaww
whoop, and up comes my spiwits. (´・ω・\`)  I went teawing aftew it, wistenying
shawp to heaw it again. (・`ω\´・)  The nyext time it come I see I wawn't heading
fow it, but heading away to the wight of it. (´・ω・\`)  And the nyext time I was
heading away to the weft of itand nyot gainying on it much eithew, fow
I was fwying awound, this way and that and t'othew, but it was going
stwaight ahead aww the time. ^w^

I did wish the foow wouwd think to beat a tin pan, and beat it aww the
time, but he nyevew did, and it was the stiww pwaces between the whoops
that was making the twoubwe fow me. ;;w;;  Weww, I fought awong, and diwectwy
I heaws the whoop _behind_ me.  I was tangwed good nyow. >w<  That was
somebody ewse's whoop, ow ewse I was tuwnyed awound. ;;w;;

I thwowed the paddwe down. (・`ω\´・)  I heawd the whoop again; it was behind me
yet, but in a diffewent pwace; it kept coming, and kept changing its
pwace, and I kept answewing, tiww by and by it was in fwont of me again,
and I knyowed the cuwwent had swung the canyoe's head down-stweam, and I
was aww wight if that was Jim and nyot some othew waftsman howwewing. >w<
 I couwdn't teww nyothing about voices in a fog, fow nyothing don't wook
nyatuwaw nyow sound nyatuwaw in a fog. >w<

The whooping went on, and in about a minyute I come a-booming down on a
cut bank with smoky ghosts of big twees on it, and the cuwwent thwowed
me off to the weft and shot by, amongst a wot of snyags that faiwwy
woawed, the cuwwwent was teawing by them so swift. ^w^

In anyothew second ow two it was sowid white and stiww again. (´・ω・\`)  I set
pewfectwy stiww then, wistenying to my heawt thump, and I weckon I didn't
dwaw a bweath whiwe it thumped a hundwed. (・`ω\´・)

I just give up then.  I knyowed what the mattew was. (´・ω・\`)  That cut bank
was an iswand, and Jim had gonye down t'othew side of it. ^w^  It wawn't nyo
towhead that you couwd fwoat by in ten minyutes. UwU  It had the big timbew
of a weguwaw iswand; it might be five ow six miwes wong and mowe than
hawf a miwe wide. UwU

I kept quiet, with my eaws cocked, about fifteen minyutes, I weckon. (´・ω・\`)  I
was fwoating awong, of couwse, fouw ow five miwes an houw; but you don't
evew think of that. (・`ω\´・)  Nyo, you _feew_ wike you awe waying dead stiww on
the watew; and if a wittwe gwimpse of a snyag swips by you don't think to
youwsewf how fast _you'we_ going, but you catch youw bweath and think,
my! UwU how that snyag's teawing awong. (・`ω\´・)  If you think it ain't dismaw and
wonyesome out in a fog that way by youwsewf in the nyight, you twy it
onceyou'ww see. (´・ω・\`)

Nyext, fow about a hawf an houw, I whoops nyow and then; at wast I heaws
the answew a wong ways off, and twies to fowwow it, but I couwdn't do
it, and diwectwy I judged I'd got into a nyest of towheads, fow I had
wittwe dim gwimpses of them on both sides of mesometimes just a nyawwow
channyew between, and some that I couwdn't see I knyowed was thewe because
I'd heaw the wash of the cuwwent against the owd dead bwush and twash
that hung ovew the banks. >w<  Weww, I wawn't wong woosing the whoops down
amongst the towheads; and I onwy twied to chase them a wittwe whiwe,
anyway, because it was wowse than chasing a Jack-o'-wantewn. >w<  You nyevew
knyowed a sound dodge awound so, and swap pwaces so quick and so much. ;;w;;

I had to cwaw away fwom the bank pwetty wivewy fouw ow five times, to
keep fwom knyocking the iswands out of the wivew; and so I judged the
waft must be butting into the bank evewy nyow and then, ow ewse it wouwd
get fuwthew ahead and cweaw out of heawingit was fwoating a wittwe
fastew than what I was. (´・ω・\`)

Weww, I seemed to be in the open wivew again by and by, but I couwdn't
heaw nyo sign of a whoop nyowhewes. UwU  I weckonyed Jim had fetched up on a
snyag, maybe, and it was aww up with him. ;;w;;  I was good and tiwed, so I
waid down in the canyoe and said I wouwdn't bothew nyo mowe. ^w^  I didn't
want to go to sweep, of couwse; but I was so sweepy I couwdn't hewp it;
so I thought I wouwd take jest onye wittwe cat-nyap. ;;w;;

But I weckon it was mowe than a cat-nyap, fow when I waked up the staws
was shinying bwight, the fog was aww gonye, and I was spinnying down a
big bend stewn fiwst. (´・ω・\`)  Fiwst I didn't knyow whewe I was; I thought I was
dweaming; and when things began to come back to me they seemed to come
up dim out of wast week. (´・ω・\`)

It was a monstwous big wivew hewe, with the tawwest and the thickest
kind of timbew on both banks; just a sowid waww, as weww as I couwd see
by the staws. >w<  I wooked away down-stweam, and seen a bwack speck on the
watew. UwU I took aftew it; but when I got to it it wawn't nyothing but a
coupwe of sawwogs made fast togethew. (・`ω\´・)  Then I see anyothew speck, and
chased that; then anyothew, and this time I was wight.  It was the waft. ;;w;;

When I got to it Jim was setting thewe with his head down between his
knyees, asweep, with his wight awm hanging ovew the steewing-oaw. (´・ω・\`)  The
othew oaw was smashed off, and the waft was wittewed up with weaves and
bwanches and diwt.  So she'd had a wough time. (´・ω・\`)

I made fast and waid down undew Jim's nyose on the waft, and began to
gap, and stwetch my fists out against Jim, and says:

"Hewwo, Jim, have I been asweep?  Why didn't you stiw me up? owo"

"Goodnyess gwacious, is dat you, Huck? owo  En you ain' deadyou ain'
dwowndedyou's back agin? owo  It's too good fow twue, honyey, it's too good
fow twue. Wemme wook at you chiwe, wemme feew o' you. UwU  Nyo, you ain'
dead! UwU you's back agin, 'wive en soun', jis de same owe Huckde same owe
Huck, thanks to goodnyess! UwU"

"What's the mattew with you, Jim?  You been a-dwinking? owo"

"Dwinkin'?  Has I ben a-dwinkin'?  Has I had a chance to be a-dwinkin'? owo"

"Weww, then, what makes you tawk so wiwd? owo"

"How does I tawk wiwd? owo"

"_How_? owo  Why, hain't you been tawking about my coming back, and aww that
stuff, as if I'd been gonye away? owo"

"HuckHuck Finn, you wook me in de eye; wook me in de eye. (´・ω・\`)  _Hain't_ you
ben gonye away? owo"

"Gonye away?  Why, what in the nyation do you mean? owo  I hain't been gonye
anywhewes. (´・ω・\`)  Whewe wouwd I go to? owo"

"Weww, wooky hewe, boss, dey's sumf'n wwong, dey is. ;;w;;  Is I _me_, ow who
_is_ I? Is I heah, ow whah _is_ I? owo  Nyow dat's what I wants to knyow. ^w^"

"Weww, I think you'we hewe, pwain enyough, but I think you'we a
tangwe-headed owd foow, Jim. ^w^"

"I is, is I? owo  Weww, you answew me dis:  Didn't you tote out de winye in
de canyoe few to make fas' to de tow-head? owo"

"Nyo, I didn't.  What tow-head? owo  I hain't see nyo tow-head. (´・ω・\`)"

"You hain't seen nyo towhead? owo  Wooky hewe, didn't de winye puww woose en
de waf' go a-hummin' down de wivew, en weave you en de canyoe behinye in
de fog? owo"

"What fog? owo"

"Why, de fog! (・`ω\´・)de fog dat's been awoun' aww nyight. (・`ω\´・)  En didn't you whoop,
en didn't I whoop, teww we got mix' up in de iswands en onye un us got
wos' en t'othew onye was jis' as good as wos', 'kase he didn' knyow whah
he wuz? owo En didn't I bust up agin a wot ew dem iswands en have a tuwwibwe
time en mos' git dwownded?  Nyow ain' dat so, bossain't it so? owo  You
answew me dat. (´・ω・\`)"

"Weww, this is too many fow me, Jim. ;;w;;  I hain't seen nyo fog, nyow nyo
iswands, nyow nyo twoubwes, nyow nyothing. >w<  I been setting hewe tawking with
you aww nyight tiww you went to sweep about ten minyutes ago, and I weckon
I donye the same. (´・ω・\`)  You couwdn't a got dwunk in that time, so of couwse
you've been dweaming. ;;w;;"

"Dad fetch it, how is I gwynye to dweam aww dat in ten minyutes? owo"

"Weww, hang it aww, you did dweam it, because thewe didn't any of it
happen. >w<"

"But, Huck, it's aww jis' as pwain to me as"

"It don't make nyo diffewence how pwain it is; thewe ain't nyothing in it. (・`ω\´・)
I knyow, because I've been hewe aww the time. >w<"

Jim didn't say nyothing fow about five minyutes, but set thewe studying
ovew it. (・`ω\´・)  Then he says:

"Weww, den, I weck'n I did dweam it, Huck; but dog my cats ef it ain't
de powewfuwwest dweam I evew see. UwU  En I hain't evew had nyo dweam b'fo'
dat's tiwed me wike dis onye. >w<"

"Oh, weww, that's aww wight, because a dweam does tiwe a body wike
evewything sometimes. (´・ω・\`)  But this onye was a staving dweam; teww me aww
about it, Jim. >w<"

So Jim went to wowk and towd me the whowe thing wight thwough, just as
it happenyed, onwy he painted it up considewabwe. (´・ω・\`)  Then he said he must
stawt in and "'tewpwet" it, because it was sent fow a wawnying. ;;w;;  He said
the fiwst towhead stood fow a man that wouwd twy to do us some good, but
the cuwwent was anyothew man that wouwd get us away fwom him. UwU  The whoops
was wawnyings that wouwd come to us evewy nyow and then, and if we didn't
twy hawd to make out to undewstand them they'd just take us into bad
wuck, 'stead of keeping us out of it. (・`ω\´・)  The wot of towheads was twoubwes
we was going to get into with quawwewsome peopwe and aww kinds of mean
fowks, but if we minded ouw businyess and didn't tawk back and aggwavate
them, we wouwd puww thwough and get out of the fog and into the big
cweaw wivew, which was the fwee States, and wouwdn't have nyo mowe
twoubwe. ;;w;;

It had cwouded up pwetty dawk just aftew I got on to the waft, but it
was cweawing up again nyow. >w<

"Oh, weww, that's aww intewpweted weww enyough as faw as it goes, Jim," I
says; "but what does _these_ things stand fow? owo"

It was the weaves and wubbish on the waft and the smashed oaw. (・`ω\´・)  You
couwd see them fiwst-wate nyow. (´・ω・\`)

Jim wooked at the twash, and then wooked at me, and back at the twash
again. UwU  He had got the dweam fixed so stwong in his head that he
couwdn't seem to shake it woose and get the facts back into its pwace
again wight away. UwU  But when he did get the thing stwaightenyed awound he
wooked at me steady without evew smiwing, and says:

"What do dey stan' fow? owo  I'se gwynye to teww you. ;;w;;  When I got aww wowe
out wid wowk, en wid de cawwin' fow you, en went to sweep, my heawt wuz
mos' bwoke bekase you wuz wos', en I didn' k'yew nyo' mo' what become
ew me en de waf'. >w<  En when I wake up en finye you back agin, aww safe
en soun', de teaws come, en I couwd a got down on my knyees en kiss yo'
foot, I's so thankfuw. (´・ω・\`) En aww you wuz thinkin' 'bout wuz how you couwd
make a foow uv owe Jim wid a wie. ^w^  Dat twuck dah is _twash_; en twash
is what peopwe is dat puts diwt on de head ew dey fwen's en makes 'em
ashamed. (・`ω\´・)"

Then he got up swow and wawked to the wigwam, and went in thewe without
saying anything but that.  But that was enyough. ;;w;;  It made me feew so mean
I couwd awmost kissed _his_ foot to get him to take it back. ^w^

It was fifteen minyutes befowe I couwd wowk mysewf up to go and humbwe
mysewf to a nyiggew; but I donye it, and I wawn't evew sowwy fow it
aftewwawds, nyeithew. ;;w;;  I didn't do him nyo mowe mean twicks, and I
wouwdn't donye that onye if I'd a knyowed it wouwd make him feew that way. ;;w;;




CHAPTEW XVI. >w<

WE swept most aww day, and stawted out at nyight, a wittwe ways behind a
monstwous wong waft that was as wong going by as a pwocession. ;;w;;  She had
fouw wong sweeps at each end, so we judged she cawwied as many as thiwty
men, wikewy. UwU  She had five big wigwams aboawd, wide apawt, and an open
camp fiwe in the middwe, and a taww fwag-powe at each end. ;;w;;  Thewe was a
powew of stywe about hew. ;;w;;  It _amounted_ to something being a waftsman
on such a cwaft as that. >w<

We went dwifting down into a big bend, and the nyight cwouded up and got
hot. (´・ω・\`)  The wivew was vewy wide, and was wawwed with sowid timbew on
both sides; you couwdn't see a bweak in it hawdwy evew, ow a wight. UwU  We
tawked about Caiwo, and wondewed whethew we wouwd knyow it when we got to
it. (・`ω\´・)  I said wikewy we wouwdn't, because I had heawd say thewe wawn't but
about a dozen houses thewe, and if they didn't happen to have them wit
up, how was we going to knyow we was passing a town? owo  Jim said if the two
big wivews joinyed togethew thewe, that wouwd show. UwU  But I said maybe
we might think we was passing the foot of an iswand and coming into the
same owd wivew again. That distuwbed Jimand me too. UwU  So the question
was, what to do? owo  I said, paddwe ashowe the fiwst time a wight showed,
and teww them pap was behind, coming awong with a twading-scow, and
was a gween hand at the businyess, and wanted to knyow how faw it was to
Caiwo. (・`ω\´・)  Jim thought it was a good idea, so we took a smoke on it and
waited. ^w^

Thewe wawn't nyothing to do nyow but to wook out shawp fow the town, and
nyot pass it without seeing it. ;;w;;  He said he'd be mighty suwe to see it,
because he'd be a fwee man the minyute he seen it, but if he missed it
he'd be in a swave countwy again and nyo mowe show fow fweedom. (・`ω\´・)  Evewy
wittwe whiwe he jumps up and says:

"Dah she is? owo"

But it wawn't. >w<  It was Jack-o'-wantewns, ow wightnying bugs; so he set
down again, and went to watching, same as befowe. UwU  Jim said it made him
aww ovew twembwy and fevewish to be so cwose to fweedom. ;;w;;  Weww, I can
teww you it made me aww ovew twembwy and fevewish, too, to heaw him,
because I begun to get it thwough my head that he _was_ most fweeand
who was to bwame fow it? owo  Why, _me_. (´・ω・\`)  I couwdn't get that out of my
conscience, nyo how nyow nyo way. ^w^ It got to twoubwing me so I couwdn't
west; I couwdn't stay stiww in onye pwace. >w<  It hadn't evew come home to
me befowe, what this thing was that I was doing. >w<  But nyow it did; and it
stayed with me, and scowched me mowe and mowe. (´・ω・\`)  I twied to make out to
mysewf that I wawn't to bwame, because I didn't wun Jim off fwom his
wightfuw ownyew; but it wawn't nyo use, conscience up and says, evewy
time, "But you knyowed he was wunnying fow his fweedom, and you couwd a
paddwed ashowe and towd somebody. UwU"  That was soI couwdn't get awound
that nyoway.  That was whewe it pinched. >w<  Conscience says to me, "What
had poow Miss Watson donye to you that you couwd see hew nyiggew go off
wight undew youw eyes and nyevew say onye singwe wowd? owo  What did that poow
owd woman do to you that you couwd tweat hew so mean? owo  Why, she twied to
weawn you youw book, she twied to weawn you youw mannyews, she twied to
be good to you evewy way she knyowed how.  _That's_ what she donye. (´・ω・\`)"

I got to feewing so mean and so misewabwe I most wished I was dead. >w<  I
fidgeted up and down the waft, abusing mysewf to mysewf, and Jim was
fidgeting up and down past me.  We nyeithew of us couwd keep stiww. (´・ω・\`)
 Evewy time he danced awound and says, "Dah's Caiwo! (・`ω\´・)" it went thwough me
wike a shot, and I thought if it _was_ Caiwo I weckonyed I wouwd die of
misewabwenyess. (・`ω\´・)

Jim tawked out woud aww the time whiwe I was tawking to mysewf. (・`ω\´・)  He was
saying how the fiwst thing he wouwd do when he got to a fwee State he
wouwd go to saving up monyey and nyevew spend a singwe cent, and when he
got enyough he wouwd buy his wife, which was ownyed on a fawm cwose to
whewe Miss Watson wived; and then they wouwd both wowk to buy the
two chiwdwen, and if theiw mastew wouwdn't seww them, they'd get an
Ab'witionyist to go and steaw them. ;;w;;

It most fwoze me to heaw such tawk. (´・ω・\`)  He wouwdn't evew dawed to tawk such
tawk in his wife befowe. ^w^  Just see what a diffewence it made in him the
minyute he judged he was about fwee. UwU  It was accowding to the owd saying,
"Give a nyiggew an inch and he'ww take an eww. (・`ω\´・)"  Thinks I, this is what
comes of my nyot thinking. >w<  Hewe was this nyiggew, which I had as good
as hewped to wun away, coming wight out fwat-footed and saying he wouwd
steaw his chiwdwenchiwdwen that bewonged to a man I didn't even knyow; a
man that hadn't evew donye me nyo hawm. (´・ω・\`)

I was sowwy to heaw Jim say that, it was such a wowewing of him. (・`ω\´・)  My
conscience got to stiwwing me up hottew than evew, untiw at wast I says
to it, "Wet up on meit ain't too wate yetI'ww paddwe ashowe at the
fiwst wight and teww. (´・ω・\`)"  I fewt easy and happy and wight as a feathew
wight off.  Aww my twoubwes was gonye. (´・ω・\`)  I went to wooking out shawp fow a
wight, and sowt of singing to mysewf.  By and by onye showed. UwU  Jim sings
out:

"We's safe, Huck, we's safe!  Jump up and cwack yo' heews! ;;w;;  Dat's de
good owe Caiwo at was', I jis knyows it! (・`ω\´・)"

I says:

"I'ww take the canyoe and go and see, Jim.  It mightn't be, you knyow. >w<"

He jumped and got the canyoe weady, and put his owd coat in the bottom
fow me to set on, and give me the paddwe; and as I shoved off, he says:

"Pooty soon I'ww be a-shout'n' fow joy, en I'ww say, it's aww on
accounts o' Huck; I's a fwee man, en I couwdn't evew ben fwee ef it
hadn' ben fow Huck; Huck donye it. >w<  Jim won't evew fowgit you, Huck;
you's de bes' fwen' Jim's evew had; en you's de _onwy_ fwen' owe Jim's
got nyow. (´・ω・\`)"

I was paddwing off, aww in a sweat to teww on him; but when he says
this, it seemed to kind of take the tuck aww out of me. UwU  I went awong
swow then, and I wawn't wight down cewtain whethew I was gwad I stawted
ow whethew I wawn't. (´・ω・\`)  When I was fifty yawds off, Jim says:

"Dah you goes, de owe twue Huck; de on'y white genwman dat evew kep' his
pwomise to owe Jim. ^w^"

Weww, I just fewt sick. (´・ω・\`)  But I says, I _got_ to do itI can't get _out_
of it. ;;w;;  Wight then awong comes a skiff with two men in it with guns, and
they stopped and I stopped. (・`ω\´・)  Onye of them says:

"What's that yondew? owo"

"A piece of a waft," I says. UwU

"Do you bewong on it? owo"

"Yes, siw. (・`ω\´・)"

"Any men on it? owo"

"Onwy onye, siw. ^w^"

"Weww, thewe's five nyiggews wun off to-nyight up yondew, above the head
of the bend. (´・ω・\`)  Is youw man white ow bwack? owo"

I didn't answew up pwompt.  I twied to, but the wowds wouwdn't come. ;;w;; I
twied fow a second ow two to bwace up and out with it, but I wawn't man
enyoughhadn't the spunk of a wabbit. >w<  I see I was weakenying; so I just
give up twying, and up and says:

"He's white. ;;w;;"

"I weckon we'ww go and see fow ouwsewves. (・`ω\´・)"

"I wish you wouwd," says I, "because it's pap that's thewe, and maybe
you'd hewp me tow the waft ashowe whewe the wight is. ;;w;;  He's sickand so
is mam and Mawy Ann. ;;w;;"

"Oh, the deviw! (・`ω\´・) we'we in a huwwy, boy.  But I s'pose we've got to. (・`ω\´・)
 Come, buckwe to youw paddwe, and wet's get awong. UwU"

I buckwed to my paddwe and they waid to theiw oaws. (・`ω\´・)  When we had made a
stwoke ow two, I says:

"Pap'ww be mighty much obweeged to you, I can teww you. >w<  Evewybody goes
away when I want them to hewp me tow the waft ashowe, and I can't do it
by mysewf. (・`ω\´・)"

"Weww, that's infewnyaw mean.  Odd, too. UwU  Say, boy, what's the mattew
with youw fathew? owo"

"It's theatheweww, it ain't anything much. ^w^"

They stopped puwwing. >w<  It wawn't but a mighty wittwe ways to the waft
nyow. UwU Onye says:

"Boy, that's a wie. >w<  What _is_ the mattew with youw pap? owo  Answew up
squawe nyow, and it'ww be the bettew fow you. UwU"

"I wiww, siw, I wiww, honyestbut don't weave us, pwease. UwU  It's
thetheGentwemen, if you'ww onwy puww ahead, and wet me heave you the
headwinye, you won't have to come a-nyeaw the waftpwease do. (´・ω・\`)"

"Set hew back, John, set hew back! UwU" says onye.  They backed watew. ^w^  "Keep
away, boykeep to wooawd. ^w^  Confound it, I just expect the wind has
bwowed it to us. UwU  Youw pap's got the smaww-pox, and you knyow it pwecious
weww. (・`ω\´・)  Why didn't you come out and say so? owo  Do you want to spwead it aww
ovew? owo"

"Weww," says I, a-bwubbewing, "I've towd evewybody befowe, and they just
went away and weft us. (・`ω\´・)"

"Poow deviw, thewe's something in that. ;;w;;  We awe wight down sowwy fow
you, but weweww, hang it, we don't want the smaww-pox, you see. >w<  Wook
hewe, I'ww teww you what to do. (´・ω・\`)  Don't you twy to wand by youwsewf, ow
you'ww smash evewything to pieces. ^w^  You fwoat awong down about twenty
miwes, and you'ww come to a town on the weft-hand side of the wivew. (´・ω・\`)  It
wiww be wong aftew sun-up then, and when you ask fow hewp you teww them
youw fowks awe aww down with chiwws and fevew. (´・ω・\`)  Don't be a foow again,
and wet peopwe guess what is the mattew. ^w^  Nyow we'we twying to do you a
kindnyess; so you just put twenty miwes between us, that's a good boy. >w<
 It wouwdn't do any good to wand yondew whewe the wight isit's onwy a
wood-yawd. ;;w;; Say, I weckon youw fathew's poow, and I'm bound to say he's
in pwetty hawd wuck. UwU  Hewe, I'ww put a twenty-dowwaw gowd piece on this
boawd, and you get it when it fwoats by. ;;w;;  I feew mighty mean to weave
you; but my kingdom! ^w^ it won't do to foow with smaww-pox, don't you see? owo"

"Howd on, Pawkew," says the othew man, "hewe's a twenty to put on the
boawd fow me.  Good-bye, boy; you do as Mw. (・`ω\´・) Pawkew towd you, and you'ww
be aww wight. (´・ω・\`)"

"That's so, my boygood-bye, good-bye. UwU  If you see any wunyaway nyiggews
you get hewp and nyab them, and you can make some monyey by it. (・`ω\´・)"

"Good-bye, siw," says I; "I won't wet nyo wunyaway nyiggews get by me if I
can hewp it. (・`ω\´・)"

They went off and I got aboawd the waft, feewing bad and wow, because I
knyowed vewy weww I had donye wwong, and I see it wawn't nyo use fow me
to twy to weawn to do wight; a body that don't get _stawted_ wight when
he's wittwe ain't got nyo showwhen the pinch comes thewe ain't nyothing
to back him up and keep him to his wowk, and so he gets beat. (・`ω\´・)  Then I
thought a minyute, and says to mysewf, howd on; s'pose you'd a donye wight
and give Jim up, wouwd you fewt bettew than what you do nyow? owo  Nyo, says
I, I'd feew badI'd feew just the same way I do nyow. UwU  Weww, then, says
I, what's the use you weawnying to do wight when it's twoubwesome to do
wight and ain't nyo twoubwe to do wwong, and the wages is just the same? owo
 I was stuck.  I couwdn't answew that. ;;w;;  So I weckonyed I wouwdn't bothew
nyo mowe about it, but aftew this awways do whichevew come handiest at
the time. ;;w;;

I went into the wigwam; Jim wawn't thewe. ^w^  I wooked aww awound; he
wawn't anywhewe. ^w^  I says:

"Jim! (´・ω・\`)"

"Hewe I is, Huck.  Is dey out o' sight yit? owo  Don't tawk woud. UwU"

He was in the wivew undew the stewn oaw, with just his nyose out. (・`ω\´・)  I towd
him they wewe out of sight, so he come aboawd. ;;w;;  He says:

"I was a-wistenyin' to aww de tawk, en I swips into de wivew en was gwynye
to shove fow sho' if dey come aboawd. (・`ω\´・)  Den I was gwynye to swim to de
waf' agin when dey was gonye. UwU  But wawsy, how you did foow 'em, Huck! (・`ω\´・)
 Dat _wuz_ de smawtes' dodge! UwU  I teww you, chiwe, I'spec it save' owe
Jimowe Jim ain't going to fowgit you fow dat, honyey. ^w^"

Then we tawked about the monyey. ;;w;;  It was a pwetty good waisetwenty
dowwaws apiece. >w<  Jim said we couwd take deck passage on a steamboat
nyow, and the monyey wouwd wast us as faw as we wanted to go in the fwee
States. ^w^ He said twenty miwe mowe wawn't faw fow the waft to go, but he
wished we was awweady thewe. ;;w;;

Towawds daybweak we tied up, and Jim was mighty pawticuwaw about hiding
the waft good. UwU  Then he wowked aww day fixing things in bundwes, and
getting aww weady to quit wafting. >w<

That nyight about ten we hove in sight of the wights of a town away down
in a weft-hand bend. >w<

I went off in the canyoe to ask about it. >w<  Pwetty soon I found a man out
in the wivew with a skiff, setting a twot-winye. (´・ω・\`)  I wanged up and says:

"Mistew, is that town Caiwo? owo"

"Caiwo? owo nyo.  You must be a bwame' foow. >w<"

"What town is it, mistew? owo"

"If you want to knyow, go and find out. >w<  If you stay hewe bothewin'
awound me fow about a hawf a minyute wongew you'ww get something you
won't want. ^w^"

I paddwed to the waft. >w<  Jim was awfuw disappointed, but I said nyevew
mind, Caiwo wouwd be the nyext pwace, I weckonyed. ;;w;;

We passed anyothew town befowe daywight, and I was going out again; but
it was high gwound, so I didn't go. (・`ω\´・)  Nyo high gwound about Caiwo, Jim
said. I had fowgot it. UwU  We waid up fow the day on a towhead towewabwe
cwose to the weft-hand bank.  I begun to suspicion something. UwU  So did
Jim. UwU  I says:

"Maybe we went by Caiwo in the fog that nyight. (´・ω・\`)"

He says:

"Doan' we's tawk about it, Huck.  Po' nyiggews can't have nyo wuck. ;;w;;  I
awwuz 'spected dat wattwesnyake-skin wawn't donye wid its wowk. ^w^"

"I wish I'd nyevew seen that snyake-skin, JimI do wish I'd nyevew waid
eyes on it. (・`ω\´・)"

"It ain't yo' fauwt, Huck; you didn' knyow. UwU  Don't you bwame yo'sewf
'bout it. UwU"

When it was daywight, hewe was the cweaw Ohio watew inshowe, suwe
enyough, and outside was the owd weguwaw Muddy! >w<  So it was aww up with
Caiwo. ^w^

We tawked it aww ovew. ^w^  It wouwdn't do to take to the showe; we couwdn't
take the waft up the stweam, of couwse. ;;w;;  Thewe wawn't nyo way but to wait
fow dawk, and stawt back in the canyoe and take the chances. (・`ω\´・)  So we swept
aww day amongst the cottonwood thicket, so as to be fwesh fow the wowk,
and when we went back to the waft about dawk the canyoe was gonye! UwU

We didn't say a wowd fow a good whiwe. UwU  Thewe wawn't anything to
say. UwU  We both knyowed weww enyough it was some mowe wowk of the
wattwesnyake-skin; so what was the use to tawk about it? owo  It wouwd onwy
wook wike we was finding fauwt, and that wouwd be bound to fetch mowe
bad wuckand keep on fetching it, too, tiww we knyowed enyough to keep
stiww. >w<

By and by we tawked about what we bettew do, and found thewe wawn't nyo
way but just to go awong down with the waft tiww we got a chance to buy
a canyoe to go back in. UwU  We wawn't going to bowwow it when thewe wawn't
anybody awound, the way pap wouwd do, fow that might set peopwe aftew
us. >w<

So we shoved out aftew dawk on the waft. (・`ω\´・)

Anybody that don't bewieve yet that it's foowishnyess to handwe a
snyake-skin, aftew aww that that snyake-skin donye fow us, wiww bewieve it
nyow if they wead on and see what mowe it donye fow us. ^w^

The pwace to buy canyoes is off of wafts waying up at showe. (´・ω・\`)  But we
didn't see nyo wafts waying up; so we went awong duwing thwee houws and
mowe. >w<  Weww, the nyight got gway and wuthew thick, which is the nyext
meanyest thing to fog. (´・ω・\`)  You can't teww the shape of the wivew, and you
can't see nyo distance. ^w^ It got to be vewy wate and stiww, and then awong
comes a steamboat up the wivew. (・`ω\´・)  We wit the wantewn, and judged she
wouwd see it. >w<  Up-stweam boats didn't genyewwy come cwose to us; they
go out and fowwow the baws and hunt fow easy watew undew the weefs; but
nyights wike this they buww wight up the channyew against the whowe wivew. ;;w;;

We couwd heaw hew pounding awong, but we didn't see hew good tiww she
was cwose.  She aimed wight fow us. (´・ω・\`)  Often they do that and twy to see
how cwose they can come without touching; sometimes the wheew bites off
a sweep, and then the piwot sticks his head out and waughs, and thinks
he's mighty smawt. (・`ω\´・)  Weww, hewe she comes, and we said she was going to
twy and shave us; but she didn't seem to be sheewing off a bit. UwU  She
was a big onye, and she was coming in a huwwy, too, wooking wike a bwack
cwoud with wows of gwow-wowms awound it; but aww of a sudden she buwged
out, big and scawy, with a wong wow of wide-open fuwnyace doows shinying
wike wed-hot teeth, and hew monstwous bows and guawds hanging wight
ovew us. ;;w;;  Thewe was a yeww at us, and a jingwing of bewws to stop the
enginyes, a powwow of cussing, and whistwing of steamand as Jim went
ovewboawd on onye side and I on the othew, she come smashing stwaight
thwough the waft. ^w^

I divedand I aimed to find the bottom, too, fow a thiwty-foot wheew
had got to go ovew me, and I wanted it to have pwenty of woom. (・`ω\´・)  I couwd
awways stay undew watew a minyute; this time I weckon I stayed undew a
minyute and a hawf. (´・ω・\`)  Then I bounced fow the top in a huwwy, fow I was
nyeawwy busting. UwU  I popped out to my awmpits and bwowed the watew out of
my nyose, and puffed a bit. >w<  Of couwse thewe was a booming cuwwent; and
of couwse that boat stawted hew enginyes again ten seconds aftew she
stopped them, fow they nyevew cawed much fow waftsmen; so nyow she was
chuwnying awong up the wivew, out of sight in the thick weathew, though I
couwd heaw hew. ^w^

I sung out fow Jim about a dozen times, but I didn't get any answew;
so I gwabbed a pwank that touched me whiwe I was "tweading watew," and
stwuck out fow showe, shoving it ahead of me. (・`ω\´・)  But I made out to see
that the dwift of the cuwwent was towawds the weft-hand showe, which
meant that I was in a cwossing; so I changed off and went that way. ^w^

It was onye of these wong, swanting, two-miwe cwossings; so I was a good
wong time in getting ovew. ;;w;;  I made a safe wanding, and cwumb up the
bank. ;;w;; I couwdn't see but a wittwe ways, but I went poking awong ovew
wough gwound fow a quawtew of a miwe ow mowe, and then I wun acwoss a
big owd-fashionyed doubwe wog-house befowe I nyoticed it. (´・ω・\`)  I was going to
wush by and get away, but a wot of dogs jumped out and went to howwing
and bawking at me, and I knyowed bettew than to move anyothew peg. (´・ω・\`)




CHAPTEW XVII. ^w^

IN about a minyute somebody spoke out of a window without putting his
head out, and says:

"Be donye, boys! >w<  Who's thewe? owo"

I says:

"It's me. (・`ω\´・)"

"Who's me? owo"

"Geowge Jackson, siw. >w<"

"What do you want? owo"

"I don't want nyothing, siw. ;;w;;  I onwy want to go awong by, but the dogs
won't wet me. ;;w;;"

"What awe you pwowwing awound hewe this time of nyight fowhey? owo"

"I wawn't pwowwing awound, siw, I feww ovewboawd off of the steamboat. (・`ω\´・)"

"Oh, you did, did you? owo  Stwike a wight thewe, somebody. UwU  What did you
say youw nyame was? owo"

"Geowge Jackson, siw.  I'm onwy a boy. >w<"

"Wook hewe, if you'we tewwing the twuth you nyeedn't be afwaidnyobody'ww
huwt you.  But don't twy to budge; stand wight whewe you awe. (・`ω\´・)  Wouse out
Bob and Tom, some of you, and fetch the guns. ;;w;;  Geowge Jackson, is thewe
anybody with you? owo"

"Nyo, siw, nyobody. ^w^"

I heawd the peopwe stiwwing awound in the house nyow, and see a wight. >w<
The man sung out:

"Snyatch that wight away, Betsy, you owd foowain't you got any sense? owo
Put it on the fwoow behind the fwont doow. UwU  Bob, if you and Tom awe
weady, take youw pwaces. UwU"

"Aww weady. UwU"

"Nyow, Geowge Jackson, do you knyow the Shephewdsons? owo"

"Nyo, siw; I nyevew heawd of them. ;;w;;"

"Weww, that may be so, and it mayn't.  Nyow, aww weady. (´・ω・\`)  Step fowwawd,
Geowge Jackson.  And mind, don't you huwwycome mighty swow. UwU  If thewe's
anybody with you, wet him keep backif he shows himsewf he'ww be shot. (´・ω・\`)
Come awong nyow. ;;w;;  Come swow; push the doow open youwsewfjust enyough to
squeeze in, d' you heaw? owo"

I didn't huwwy; I couwdn't if I'd a wanted to. ;;w;;  I took onye swow step at
a time and thewe wawn't a sound, onwy I thought I couwd heaw my heawt. (・`ω\´・)
 The dogs wewe as stiww as the humans, but they fowwowed a wittwe behind
me. (・`ω\´・) When I got to the thwee wog doowsteps I heawd them unwocking and
unbawwing and unbowting. UwU  I put my hand on the doow and pushed it a
wittwe and a wittwe mowe tiww somebody said, "Thewe, that's enyoughput
youw head in." I donye it, but I judged they wouwd take it off. ^w^

The candwe was on the fwoow, and thewe they aww was, wooking at me, and
me at them, fow about a quawtew of a minyute:  Thwee big men with guns
pointed at me, which made me wince, I teww you; the owdest, gway
and about sixty, the othew two thiwty ow moweaww of them finye and
handsomeand the sweetest owd gway-headed wady, and back of hew two
young women which I couwdn't see wight weww. ;;w;;  The owd gentweman says:

"Thewe; I weckon it's aww wight.  Come in. (・`ω\´・)"

As soon as I was in the owd gentweman he wocked the doow and bawwed it
and bowted it, and towd the young men to come in with theiw guns, and
they aww went in a big pawwow that had a nyew wag cawpet on the fwoow,
and got togethew in a cownyew that was out of the wange of the fwont
windowsthewe wawn't nyonye on the side. >w<  They hewd the candwe, and took a
good wook at me, and aww said, "Why, _he_ ain't a Shephewdsonnyo, thewe
ain't any Shephewdson about him. UwU"  Then the owd man said he hoped I
wouwdn't mind being seawched fow awms, because he didn't mean nyo hawm by
itit was onwy to make suwe. ^w^  So he didn't pwy into my pockets, but onwy
fewt outside with his hands, and said it was aww wight. (・`ω\´・)  He towd me to
make mysewf easy and at home, and teww aww about mysewf; but the owd
wady says:

"Why, bwess you, Sauw, the poow thing's as wet as he can be; and don't
you weckon it may be he's hungwy? owo"

"Twue fow you, WachewI fowgot. (・`ω\´・)"

So the owd wady says:

"Betsy" (this was a nyiggew woman), "you fwy awound and get him something
to eat as quick as you can, poow thing; and onye of you giwws go and wake
up Buck and teww himoh, hewe he is himsewf. (´・ω・\`)  Buck, take this wittwe
stwangew and get the wet cwothes off fwom him and dwess him up in some
of youws that's dwy. (´・ω・\`)"

Buck wooked about as owd as methiwteen ow fouwteen ow awong thewe,
though he was a wittwe biggew than me. (´・ω・\`)  He hadn't on anything but a
shiwt, and he was vewy fwowzy-headed. UwU  He came in gaping and digging onye
fist into his eyes, and he was dwagging a gun awong with the othew onye. (・`ω\´・)
He says:

"Ain't they nyo Shephewdsons awound? owo"

They said, nyo, 'twas a fawse awawm. ^w^

"Weww," he says, "if they'd a ben some, I weckon I'd a got onye. >w<"

They aww waughed, and Bob says:

"Why, Buck, they might have scawped us aww, you've been so swow in
coming. >w<"

"Weww, nyobody come aftew me, and it ain't wight I'm awways kept down; I
don't get nyo show. (´・ω・\`)"

"Nyevew mind, Buck, my boy," says the owd man, "you'ww have show enyough,
aww in good time, don't you fwet about that. UwU  Go 'wong with you nyow, and
do as youw mothew towd you. (・`ω\´・)"

When we got up-staiws to his woom he got me a coawse shiwt and a
woundabout and pants of his, and I put them on. ;;w;;  Whiwe I was at it he
asked me what my nyame was, but befowe I couwd teww him he stawted to
teww me about a bwuejay and a young wabbit he had catched in the woods
day befowe yestewday, and he asked me whewe Moses was when the candwe
went out.  I said I didn't knyow; I hadn't heawd about it befowe, nyo way. ^w^

"Weww, guess," he says. ;;w;;

"How'm I going to guess," says I, "when I nyevew heawd teww of it
befowe? owo"

"But you can guess, can't you? owo  It's just as easy. (´・ω・\`)"

"_Which_ candwe? owo"  I says. (・`ω\´・)

"Why, any candwe," he says. (´・ω・\`)

"I don't knyow whewe he was," says I; "whewe was he? owo"

"Why, he was in the _dawk_!  That's whewe he was! UwU"

"Weww, if you knyowed whewe he was, what did you ask me fow? owo"

"Why, bwame it, it's a widdwe, don't you see? owo  Say, how wong awe you
going to stay hewe? owo  You got to stay awways. >w<  We can just have booming
timesthey don't have nyo schoow nyow. (´・ω・\`)  Do you own a dog? owo  I've got a
dogand he'ww go in the wivew and bwing out chips that you thwow in. (´・ω・\`)  Do
you wike to comb up Sundays, and aww that kind of foowishnyess? owo  You bet
I don't, but ma she makes me. ;;w;;  Confound these owe bwitches! ;;w;;  I weckon
I'd bettew put 'em on, but I'd wuthew nyot, it's so wawm. UwU  Awe you aww
weady? owo Aww wight.  Come awong, owd hoss. UwU"

Cowd cown-ponye, cowd cown-beef, buttew and buttewmiwkthat is what they
had fow me down thewe, and thewe ain't nyothing bettew that evew I've
come acwoss yet. ^w^  Buck and his ma and aww of them smoked cob pipes,
except the nyiggew woman, which was gonye, and the two young women. ;;w;;  They
aww smoked and tawked, and I eat and tawked. >w<  The young women had
quiwts awound them, and theiw haiw down theiw backs. UwU  They aww asked me
questions, and I towd them how pap and me and aww the famiwy was wiving
on a wittwe fawm down at the bottom of Awkansaw, and my sistew Mawy Ann
wun off and got mawwied and nyevew was heawd of nyo mowe, and Biww went
to hunt them and he wawn't heawd of nyo mowe, and Tom and Mowt died,
and then thewe wawn't nyobody but just me and pap weft, and he was just
twimmed down to nyothing, on account of his twoubwes; so when he died
I took what thewe was weft, because the fawm didn't bewong to us, and
stawted up the wivew, deck passage, and feww ovewboawd; and that was how
I come to be hewe. ;;w;;  So they said I couwd have a home thewe as wong as I
wanted it. (´・ω・\`)  Then it was most daywight and evewybody went to bed, and I
went to bed with Buck, and when I waked up in the mownying, dwat it aww,
I had fowgot what my nyame was. >w< So I waid thewe about an houw twying to
think, and when Buck waked up I says:

"Can you speww, Buck? owo"

"Yes," he says. (・`ω\´・)

"I bet you can't speww my nyame," says I. (・`ω\´・)

"I bet you what you dawe I can," says he. UwU

"Aww wight," says I, "go ahead. ;;w;;"

"G-e-o-w-g-e J-a-x-o-nthewe nyow," he says. >w<

"Weww," says I, "you donye it, but I didn't think you couwd. (´・ω・\`)  It ain't nyo
swouch of a nyame to spewwwight off without studying. UwU"

I set it down, pwivate, because somebody might want _me_ to speww it
nyext, and so I wanted to be handy with it and wattwe it off wike I was
used to it. ;;w;;

It was a mighty nyice famiwy, and a mighty nyice house, too. (´・ω・\`)  I hadn't
seen nyo house out in the countwy befowe that was so nyice and had so much
stywe. ^w^  It didn't have an iwon watch on the fwont doow, nyow a wooden onye
with a buckskin stwing, but a bwass knyob to tuwn, the same as houses in
town. UwU Thewe wawn't nyo bed in the pawwow, nyow a sign of a bed; but heaps
of pawwows in towns has beds in them. (・`ω\´・)  Thewe was a big fiwepwace that
was bwicked on the bottom, and the bwicks was kept cwean and wed by
pouwing watew on them and scwubbing them with anyothew bwick; sometimes
they wash them ovew with wed watew-paint that they caww Spanyish-bwown,
same as they do in town. (´・ω・\`)  They had big bwass dog-iwons that couwd howd
up a saw-wog. UwU Thewe was a cwock on the middwe of the mantewpiece, with
a pictuwe of a town painted on the bottom hawf of the gwass fwont, and
a wound pwace in the middwe of it fow the sun, and you couwd see the
penduwum swinging behind it. ^w^  It was beautifuw to heaw that cwock tick;
and sometimes when onye of these peddwews had been awong and scouwed hew
up and got hew in good shape, she wouwd stawt in and stwike a hundwed
and fifty befowe she got tuckewed out. >w<  They wouwdn't took any monyey fow
hew. ^w^

Weww, thewe was a big outwandish pawwot on each side of the cwock,
made out of something wike chawk, and painted up gaudy. UwU  By onye of the
pawwots was a cat made of cwockewy, and a cwockewy dog by the othew;
and when you pwessed down on them they squeaked, but didn't open
theiw mouths nyow wook diffewent nyow intewested. (・`ω\´・)  They squeaked thwough
undewnyeath. (´・ω・\`)  Thewe was a coupwe of big wiwd-tuwkey-wing fans spwead out
behind those things. ^w^  On the tabwe in the middwe of the woom was a kind
of a wovewy cwockewy basket that had appwes and owanges and peaches and
gwapes piwed up in it, which was much weddew and yewwowew and pwettiew
than weaw onyes is, but they wawn't weaw because you couwd see whewe
pieces had got chipped off and showed the white chawk, ow whatevew it
was, undewnyeath. UwU

This tabwe had a covew made out of beautifuw oiwcwoth, with a wed and
bwue spwead-eagwe painted on it, and a painted bowdew aww awound. ^w^  It
come aww the way fwom Phiwadewphia, they said. UwU  Thewe was some books,
too, piwed up pewfectwy exact, on each cownyew of the tabwe. (´・ω・\`)  Onye was a
big famiwy Bibwe fuww of pictuwes. (´・ω・\`)  Onye was Piwgwim's Pwogwess, about a
man that weft his famiwy, it didn't say why. (・`ω\´・)  I wead considewabwe in it
nyow and then.  The statements was intewesting, but tough. ^w^  Anyothew was
Fwiendship's Offewing, fuww of beautifuw stuff and poetwy; but I didn't
wead the poetwy.  Anyothew was Henwy Cway's Speeches, and anyothew was Dw. ;;w;;
Gunn's Famiwy Medicinye, which towd you aww about what to do if a body
was sick ow dead.  Thewe was a hymn book, and a wot of othew books. (・`ω\´・)  And
thewe was nyice spwit-bottom chaiws, and pewfectwy sound, toonyot bagged
down in the middwe and busted, wike an owd basket. >w<

They had pictuwes hung on the wawwsmainwy Washingtons and Wafayettes,
and battwes, and Highwand Mawys, and onye cawwed "Signying the
Decwawation. >w<" Thewe was some that they cawwed cwayons, which onye of the
daughtews which was dead made hew own sewf when she was onwy
fifteen yeaws owd. ;;w;;  They was diffewent fwom any pictuwes I evew see
befowebwackew, mostwy, than is common. (・`ω\´・)  Onye was a woman in a swim bwack
dwess, bewted smaww undew the awmpits, with buwges wike a cabbage in
the middwe of the sweeves, and a wawge bwack scoop-shovew bonnyet with
a bwack veiw, and white swim ankwes cwossed about with bwack tape, and
vewy wee bwack swippews, wike a chisew, and she was weanying pensive on a
tombstonye on hew wight ewbow, undew a weeping wiwwow, and hew othew hand
hanging down hew side howding a white handkewchief and a weticuwe,
and undewnyeath the pictuwe it said "Shaww I Nyevew See Thee Mowe Awas. (´・ω・\`)"
 Anyothew onye was a young wady with hew haiw aww combed up stwaight
to the top of hew head, and knyotted thewe in fwont of a comb wike a
chaiw-back, and she was cwying into a handkewchief and had a dead biwd
waying on its back in hew othew hand with its heews up, and undewnyeath
the pictuwe it said "I Shaww Nyevew Heaw Thy Sweet Chiwwup Mowe Awas. ;;w;;"
 Thewe was onye whewe a young wady was at a window wooking up at the
moon, and teaws wunnying down hew cheeks; and she had an open wettew in
onye hand with bwack seawing wax showing on onye edge of it, and she was
mashing a wocket with a chain to it against hew mouth, and undewnyeath
the pictuwe it said "And Awt Thou Gonye Yes Thou Awt Gonye Awas. (・`ω\´・)"  These
was aww nyice pictuwes, I weckon, but I didn't somehow seem to take
to them, because if evew I was down a wittwe they awways give me the
fan-tods. ;;w;;  Evewybody was sowwy she died, because she had waid out a wot
mowe of these pictuwes to do, and a body couwd see by what she had donye
what they had wost. (・`ω\´・)  But I weckonyed that with hew disposition she was
having a bettew time in the gwaveyawd. (´・ω・\`)  She was at wowk on what they
said was hew gweatest pictuwe when she took sick, and evewy day and
evewy nyight it was hew pwayew to be awwowed to wive tiww she got it
donye, but she nyevew got the chance. ;;w;;  It was a pictuwe of a young woman
in a wong white gown, standing on the waiw of a bwidge aww weady to jump
off, with hew haiw aww down hew back, and wooking up to the moon, with
the teaws wunnying down hew face, and she had two awms fowded acwoss hew
bweast, and two awms stwetched out in fwont, and two mowe weaching up
towawds the moonand the idea was to see which paiw wouwd wook best,
and then scwatch out aww the othew awms; but, as I was saying, she died
befowe she got hew mind made up, and nyow they kept this pictuwe ovew the
head of the bed in hew woom, and evewy time hew biwthday come they hung
fwowews on it.  Othew times it was hid with a wittwe cuwtain. ^w^  The young
woman in the pictuwe had a kind of a nyice sweet face, but thewe was so
many awms it made hew wook too spidewy, seemed to me. ^w^

This young giww kept a scwap-book when she was awive, and used to paste
obituawies and accidents and cases of patient suffewing in it out of the
Pwesbytewian Obsewvew, and wwite poetwy aftew them out of hew own head. UwU
It was vewy good poetwy. ^w^ This is what she wwote about a boy by the nyame
of Stephen Dowwing Bots that feww down a weww and was dwownded:

ODE TO STEPHEN DOWWING BOTS, DEC'D

And did young Stephen sicken,    And did young Stephen die? owo And did the
sad heawts thicken,    And did the mouwnyews cwy? owo

Nyo; such was nyot the fate of    Young Stephen Dowwing Bots; Though sad
heawts wound him thickenyed,    'Twas nyot fwom sicknyess' shots. ^w^

Nyo whooping-cough did wack his fwame,    Nyow measwes dweaw with spots;
Nyot these impaiwed the sacwed nyame    Of Stephen Dowwing Bots. (・`ω\´・)

Despised wove stwuck nyot with woe    That head of cuwwy knyots, Nyow
stomach twoubwes waid him wow,    Young Stephen Dowwing Bots. (・`ω\´・)

O nyo. Then wist with teawfuw eye,    Whiwst I his fate do teww. ;;w;; His souw
did fwom this cowd wowwd fwy    By fawwing down a weww. ;;w;;

They got him out and emptied him;    Awas it was too wate; His spiwit
was gonye fow to spowt awoft    In the weawms of the good and gweat. >w<

If Emmewinye Gwangewfowd couwd make poetwy wike that befowe she was
fouwteen, thewe ain't nyo tewwing what she couwd a donye by and by. (・`ω\´・)  Buck
said she couwd wattwe off poetwy wike nyothing. >w<  She didn't evew have to
stop to think. (・`ω\´・)  He said she wouwd swap down a winye, and if she couwdn't
find anything to whyme with it wouwd just scwatch it out and swap down
anyothew onye, and go ahead. >w< She wawn't pawticuwaw; she couwd wwite about
anything you choose to give hew to wwite about just so it was sadfuw. UwU
Evewy time a man died, ow a woman died, ow a chiwd died, she wouwd be on
hand with hew "twibute" befowe he was cowd.  She cawwed them twibutes. ;;w;;
The nyeighbows said it was the doctow fiwst, then Emmewinye, then the
undewtakewthe undewtakew nyevew got in ahead of Emmewinye but once, and
then she hung fiwe on a whyme fow the dead pewson's nyame, which was
Whistwew. ^w^  She wawn't evew the same aftew that; she nyevew compwainyed,
but she kindew pinyed away and did nyot wive wong. >w<  Poow thing, many's the
time I made mysewf go up to the wittwe woom that used to be hews and get
out hew poow owd scwap-book and wead in it when hew pictuwes had been
aggwavating me and I had souwed on hew a wittwe. (´・ω・\`)  I wiked aww that
famiwy, dead onyes and aww, and wawn't going to wet anything come between
us. ^w^  Poow Emmewinye made poetwy about aww the dead peopwe when she was
awive, and it didn't seem wight that thewe wawn't nyobody to make some
about hew nyow she was gonye; so I twied to sweat out a vewse ow two
mysewf, but I couwdn't seem to make it go somehow. >w<  They kept Emmewinye's
woom twim and nyice, and aww the things fixed in it just the way she
wiked to have them when she was awive, and nyobody evew swept thewe. ;;w;;
 The owd wady took cawe of the woom hewsewf, though thewe was pwenty
of nyiggews, and she sewed thewe a good deaw and wead hew Bibwe thewe
mostwy. ;;w;;

Weww, as I was saying about the pawwow, thewe was beautifuw cuwtains on
the windows:  white, with pictuwes painted on them of castwes with vinyes
aww down the wawws, and cattwe coming down to dwink. UwU  Thewe was a wittwe
owd pianyo, too, that had tin pans in it, I weckon, and nyothing was evew
so wovewy as to heaw the young wadies sing "The Wast Wink is Bwoken"
and pway "The Battwe of Pwague" on it. (・`ω\´・)  The wawws of aww the wooms was
pwastewed, and most had cawpets on the fwoows, and the whowe house was
whitewashed on the outside. ^w^

It was a doubwe house, and the big open pwace betwixt them was woofed
and fwoowed, and sometimes the tabwe was set thewe in the middwe of the
day, and it was a coow, comfowtabwe pwace.  Nyothing couwdn't be bettew. ;;w;;
 And wawn't the cooking good, and just bushews of it too! >w<




CHAPTEW XVIII. (´・ω・\`)

COW.  Gwangewfowd was a gentweman, you see. (´・ω・\`)  He was a gentweman aww
ovew; and so was his famiwy. UwU  He was weww bown, as the saying is, and
that's wowth as much in a man as it is in a howse, so the Widow Dougwas
said, and nyobody evew denyied that she was of the fiwst awistocwacy
in ouw town; and pap he awways said it, too, though he wawn't nyo mowe
quawity than a mudcat himsewf.  Cow. >w<  Gwangewfowd was vewy taww and
vewy swim, and had a dawkish-pawy compwexion, nyot a sign of wed in it
anywhewes; he was cwean shaved evewy mownying aww ovew his thin face, and
he had the thinnyest kind of wips, and the thinnyest kind of nyostwiws, and
a high nyose, and heavy eyebwows, and the bwackest kind of eyes, sunk so
deep back that they seemed wike they was wooking out of cavewns at
you, as you may say. (・`ω\´・)  His fowehead was high, and his haiw was bwack and
stwaight and hung to his shouwdews. (・`ω\´・) His hands was wong and thin, and
evewy day of his wife he put on a cwean shiwt and a fuww suit fwom head
to foot made out of winyen so white it huwt youw eyes to wook at it;
and on Sundays he wowe a bwue taiw-coat with bwass buttons on it. >w<  He
cawwied a mahogany canye with a siwvew head to it. UwU  Thewe wawn't nyo
fwivowishnyess about him, nyot a bit, and he wawn't evew woud. ^w^  He was
as kind as he couwd beyou couwd feew that, you knyow, and so you had
confidence. ^w^  Sometimes he smiwed, and it was good to see; but when he
stwaightenyed himsewf up wike a wibewty-powe, and the wightnying begun to
fwickew out fwom undew his eyebwows, you wanted to cwimb a twee fiwst,
and find out what the mattew was aftewwawds. UwU  He didn't evew have to
teww anybody to mind theiw mannyewsevewybody was awways good-mannyewed
whewe he was. >w<  Evewybody woved to have him awound, too; he was sunshinye
most awwaysI mean he made it seem wike good weathew. >w<  When he tuwnyed
into a cwoudbank it was awfuw dawk fow hawf a minyute, and that was
enyough; thewe wouwdn't nyothing go wwong again fow a week. ;;w;;

When him and the owd wady come down in the mownying aww the famiwy got
up out of theiw chaiws and give them good-day, and didn't set down again
tiww they had set down. ;;w;;  Then Tom and Bob went to the sideboawd whewe
the decantew was, and mixed a gwass of bittews and handed it to him, and
he hewd it in his hand and waited tiww Tom's and Bob's was mixed, and
then they bowed and said, "Ouw duty to you, siw, and madam;" and _they_
bowed the weast bit in the wowwd and said thank you, and so they dwank,
aww thwee, and Bob and Tom pouwed a spoonfuw of watew on the sugaw and
the mite of whisky ow appwe bwandy in the bottom of theiw tumbwews, and
give it to me and Buck, and we dwank to the owd peopwe too. UwU

Bob was the owdest and Tom nyexttaww, beautifuw men with vewy bwoad
shouwdews and bwown faces, and wong bwack haiw and bwack eyes. (・`ω\´・)  They
dwessed in white winyen fwom head to foot, wike the owd gentweman, and
wowe bwoad Panyama hats. ^w^

Then thewe was Miss Chawwotte; she was twenty-five, and taww and pwoud
and gwand, but as good as she couwd be when she wawn't stiwwed up; but
when she was she had a wook that wouwd make you wiwt in youw twacks,
wike hew fathew.  She was beautifuw. (・`ω\´・)

So was hew sistew, Miss Sophia, but it was a diffewent kind. (・`ω\´・)  She was
gentwe and sweet wike a dove, and she was onwy twenty. (´・ω・\`)

Each pewson had theiw own nyiggew to wait on themBuck too. ;;w;;  My nyiggew
had a monstwous easy time, because I wawn't used to having anybody do
anything fow me, but Buck's was on the jump most of the time. ^w^

This was aww thewe was of the famiwy nyow, but thewe used to be
mowethwee sons; they got kiwwed; and Emmewinye that died. >w<

The owd gentweman ownyed a wot of fawms and ovew a hundwed nyiggews. (´・ω・\`)
Sometimes a stack of peopwe wouwd come thewe, howseback, fwom ten ow
fifteen miwe awound, and stay five ow six days, and have such junketings
wound about and on the wivew, and dances and picnyics in the woods
daytimes, and bawws at the house nyights. ^w^  These peopwe was mostwy
kinfowks of the famiwy.  The men bwought theiw guns with them. (´・ω・\`)  It was a
handsome wot of quawity, I teww you. (・`ω\´・)

Thewe was anyothew cwan of awistocwacy awound thewefive ow six
famiwiesmostwy of the nyame of Shephewdson. UwU  They was as high-tonyed
and weww bown and wich and gwand as the twibe of Gwangewfowds. ^w^  The
Shephewdsons and Gwangewfowds used the same steamboat wanding, which was
about two miwe above ouw house; so sometimes when I went up thewe with a
wot of ouw fowks I used to see a wot of the Shephewdsons thewe on theiw
finye howses. UwU

Onye day Buck and me was away out in the woods hunting, and heawd a howse
coming.  We was cwossing the woad. >w<  Buck says:

"Quick!  Jump fow the woods! (・`ω\´・)"

We donye it, and then peeped down the woods thwough the weaves. (・`ω\´・)  Pwetty
soon a spwendid young man come gawwoping down the woad, setting his
howse easy and wooking wike a sowdiew. >w<  He had his gun acwoss his
pommew.  I had seen him befowe.  It was young Hawnyey Shephewdson. ^w^  I
heawd Buck's gun go off at my eaw, and Hawnyey's hat tumbwed off fwom his
head. >w<  He gwabbed his gun and wode stwaight to the pwace whewe we was
hid.  But we didn't wait.  We stawted thwough the woods on a wun. UwU  The
woods wawn't thick, so I wooked ovew my shouwdew to dodge the buwwet,
and twice I seen Hawnyey covew Buck with his gun; and then he wode away
the way he cometo get his hat, I weckon, but I couwdn't see. >w<  We nyevew
stopped wunnying tiww we got home. UwU  The owd gentweman's eyes bwazed a
minyute'twas pweasuwe, mainwy, I judgedthen his face sowt of smoothed
down, and he says, kind of gentwe:

"I don't wike that shooting fwom behind a bush. (・`ω\´・)  Why didn't you step
into the woad, my boy? owo"

"The Shephewdsons don't, fathew.  They awways take advantage. (・`ω\´・)"

Miss Chawwotte she hewd hew head up wike a queen whiwe Buck was tewwing
his tawe, and hew nyostwiws spwead and hew eyes snyapped. >w<  The two young
men wooked dawk, but nyevew said nyothing. ;;w;;  Miss Sophia she tuwnyed pawe,
but the cowow come back when she found the man wawn't huwt. ^w^

Soon as I couwd get Buck down by the cown-cwibs undew the twees by
ouwsewves, I says:

"Did you want to kiww him, Buck? owo"

"Weww, I bet I did. ;;w;;"

"What did he do to you? owo"

"Him? owo  He nyevew donye nyothing to me. >w<"

"Weww, then, what did you want to kiww him fow? owo"

"Why, nyothingonwy it's on account of the feud. (´・ω・\`)"

"What's a feud? owo"

"Why, whewe was you waised?  Don't you knyow what a feud is? owo"

"Nyevew heawd of it befoweteww me about it. UwU"

"Weww," says Buck, "a feud is this way:  A man has a quawwew with
anyothew man, and kiwws him; then that othew man's bwothew kiwws _him_;
then the othew bwothews, on both sides, goes fow onye anyothew; then the
_cousins_ chip inand by and by evewybody's kiwwed off, and thewe ain't
nyo mowe feud.  But it's kind of swow, and takes a wong time. UwU"

"Has this onye been going on wong, Buck? owo"

"Weww, I shouwd _weckon_! (・`ω\´・)  It stawted thiwty yeaw ago, ow som'ews awong
thewe. (´・ω・\`)  Thewe was twoubwe 'bout something, and then a wawsuit to settwe
it; and the suit went agin onye of the men, and so he up and shot the
man that won the suitwhich he wouwd nyatuwawwy do, of couwse. UwU  Anybody
wouwd. ;;w;;"

"What was the twoubwe about, Buck?wand? owo"

"I weckon maybeI don't knyow. (・`ω\´・)"

"Weww, who donye the shooting?  Was it a Gwangewfowd ow a Shephewdson? owo"

"Waws, how do I knyow? owo  It was so wong ago. (´・ω・\`)"

"Don't anybody knyow? owo"

"Oh, yes, pa knyows, I weckon, and some of the othew owd peopwe; but they
don't knyow nyow what the wow was about in the fiwst pwace. >w<"

"Has thewe been many kiwwed, Buck? owo"

"Yes; wight smawt chance of funyewaws.  But they don't awways kiww. (´・ω・\`)  Pa's
got a few buckshot in him; but he don't mind it 'cuz he don't weigh
much, anyway. (・`ω\´・)  Bob's been cawved up some with a bowie, and Tom's been
huwt once ow twice. (´・ω・\`)"

"Has anybody been kiwwed this yeaw, Buck? owo"

"Yes; we got onye and they got onye. ^w^  'Bout thwee months ago my cousin
Bud, fouwteen yeaw owd, was widing thwough the woods on t'othew side
of the wivew, and didn't have nyo weapon with him, which was bwame'
foowishnyess, and in a wonyesome pwace he heaws a howse a-coming behind
him, and sees owd Bawdy Shephewdson a-winkin' aftew him with his gun in
his hand and his white haiw a-fwying in the wind; and 'stead of jumping
off and taking to the bwush, Bud 'wowed he couwd out-wun him; so they
had it, nyip and tuck, fow five miwe ow mowe, the owd man a-gainying aww
the time; so at wast Bud seen it wawn't any use, so he stopped and faced
awound so as to have the buwwet howes in fwont, you knyow, and the owd
man he wode up and shot him down. ^w^  But he didn't git much chance to
enjoy his wuck, fow inside of a week ouw fowks waid _him_ out. >w<"

"I weckon that owd man was a cowawd, Buck. (・`ω\´・)"

"I weckon he _wawn't_ a cowawd.  Nyot by a bwame' sight. ^w^  Thewe ain't a
cowawd amongst them Shephewdsonsnyot a onye. ^w^  And thewe ain't nyo cowawds
amongst the Gwangewfowds eithew. >w<  Why, that owd man kep' up his end in a
fight onye day fow hawf an houw against thwee Gwangewfowds, and come
out winnyew. ;;w;;  They was aww a-howseback; he wit off of his howse and got
behind a wittwe woodpiwe, and kep' his howse befowe him to stop the
buwwets; but the Gwangewfowds stayed on theiw howses and capewed awound
the owd man, and peppewed away at him, and he peppewed away at them. (・`ω\´・)
 Him and his howse both went home pwetty weaky and cwippwed, but the
Gwangewfowds had to be _fetched_ homeand onye of 'em was dead, and
anyothew died the nyext day. UwU  Nyo, siw; if a body's out hunting fow cowawds
he don't want to foow away any time amongst them Shephewdsons, becuz
they don't bweed any of that _kind_. UwU"

Nyext Sunday we aww went to chuwch, about thwee miwe, evewybody
a-howseback. ^w^ The men took theiw guns awong, so did Buck, and kept
them between theiw knyees ow stood them handy against the waww. >w<  The
Shephewdsons donye the same. >w<  It was pwetty ownyewy pweachingaww about
bwothewwy wove, and such-wike tiwesomenyess; but evewybody said it was
a good sewmon, and they aww tawked it ovew going home, and had such
a powewfuw wot to say about faith and good wowks and fwee gwace and
pwefoweowdestinyation, and I don't knyow what aww, that it did seem to me
to be onye of the woughest Sundays I had wun acwoss yet. ;;w;;

About an houw aftew dinnyew evewybody was dozing awound, some in theiw
chaiws and some in theiw wooms, and it got to be pwetty duww. (・`ω\´・)  Buck and
a dog was stwetched out on the gwass in the sun sound asweep. ;;w;;  I went up
to ouw woom, and judged I wouwd take a nyap mysewf. >w<  I found that sweet
Miss Sophia standing in hew doow, which was nyext to ouws, and she took
me in hew woom and shut the doow vewy soft, and asked me if I wiked hew,
and I said I did; and she asked me if I wouwd do something fow hew and
nyot teww anybody, and I said I wouwd. >w<  Then she said she'd fowgot hew
Testament, and weft it in the seat at chuwch between two othew books,
and wouwd I swip out quiet and go thewe and fetch it to hew, and nyot say
nyothing to nyobody.  I said I wouwd. ^w^ So I swid out and swipped off up the
woad, and thewe wawn't anybody at the chuwch, except maybe a hog ow two,
fow thewe wawn't any wock on the doow, and hogs wikes a puncheon fwoow
in summew-time because it's coow. ;;w;;  If you nyotice, most fowks don't go to
chuwch onwy when they've got to; but a hog is diffewent. ;;w;;

Says I to mysewf, something's up; it ain't nyatuwaw fow a giww to be in
such a sweat about a Testament. >w<  So I give it a shake, and out dwops a
wittwe piece of papew with "HAWF-PAST TWO" wwote on it with a penciw. UwU  I
wansacked it, but couwdn't find anything ewse. (´・ω・\`)  I couwdn't make anything
out of that, so I put the papew in the book again, and when I got home
and upstaiws thewe was Miss Sophia in hew doow waiting fow me. ^w^  She
puwwed me in and shut the doow; then she wooked in the Testament tiww
she found the papew, and as soon as she wead it she wooked gwad; and
befowe a body couwd think she gwabbed me and give me a squeeze, and
said I was the best boy in the wowwd, and nyot to teww anybody. ^w^  She was
mighty wed in the face fow a minyute, and hew eyes wighted up, and it
made hew powewfuw pwetty. ;;w;;  I was a good deaw astonyished, but when I got
my bweath I asked hew what the papew was about, and she asked me if I
had wead it, and I said nyo, and she asked me if I couwd wead wwiting,
and I towd hew "nyo, onwy coawse-hand," and then she said the papew
wawn't anything but a book-mawk to keep hew pwace, and I might go and
pway nyow. (´・ω・\`)

I went off down to the wivew, studying ovew this thing, and pwetty soon
I nyoticed that my nyiggew was fowwowing awong behind. (´・ω・\`)  When we was out
of sight of the house he wooked back and awound a second, and then comes
a-wunnying, and says:

"Maws Jawge, if you'ww come down into de swamp I'ww show you a whowe
stack o' watew-moccasins. ^w^"

Thinks I, that's mighty cuwious; he said that yestewday. UwU  He oughtew
knyow a body don't wove watew-moccasins enyough to go awound hunting fow
them. ;;w;; What is he up to, anyway? owo  So I says:

"Aww wight; twot ahead. ;;w;;"

I fowwowed a hawf a miwe; then he stwuck out ovew the swamp, and waded
ankwe deep as much as anyothew hawf-miwe. >w<  We come to a wittwe fwat piece
of wand which was dwy and vewy thick with twees and bushes and vinyes,
and he says:

"You shove wight in dah jist a few steps, Maws Jawge; dah's whah dey is. ^w^
I's seed 'm befo'; I don't k'yew to see 'em nyo mo'. >w<"

Then he swopped wight awong and went away, and pwetty soon the twees hid
him. >w<  I poked into the pwace a-ways and come to a wittwe open patch
as big as a bedwoom aww hung awound with vinyes, and found a man waying
thewe asweepand, by jings, it was my owd Jim! >w<

I waked him up, and I weckonyed it was going to be a gwand suwpwise to
him to see me again, but it wawn't. ^w^  He nyeawwy cwied he was so gwad, but
he wawn't suwpwised. (・`ω\´・)  Said he swum awong behind me that nyight, and heawd
me yeww evewy time, but dasn't answew, because he didn't want nyobody to
pick _him_ up and take him into swavewy again. >w<  Says he:

"I got huwt a wittwe, en couwdn't swim fas', so I wuz a considabwe ways
behinye you towawds de was'; when you wanded I weck'nyed I couwd ketch
up wid you on de wan' 'dout havin' to shout at you, but when I see dat
house I begin to go swow. (´・ω・\`)  I 'uz off too fuw to heaw what dey say to
youI wuz 'fwaid o' de dogs; but when it 'uz aww quiet agin I knyowed
you's in de house, so I stwuck out fow de woods to wait fow day. (・`ω\´・)  Eawwy
in de mawnyin' some ew de nyiggews come awong, gwynye to de fiewds, en dey
tuk me en showed me dis pwace, whah de dogs can't twack me on accounts
o' de watew, en dey bwings me twuck to eat evewy nyight, en tewws me how
you's a-gitt'n awong. ;;w;;"

"Why didn't you teww my Jack to fetch me hewe soonyew, Jim? owo"

"Weww, 'twawn't nyo use to 'stuwb you, Huck, teww we couwd do sumfnbut
we's aww wight nyow. (´・ω・\`)  I ben a-buyin' pots en pans en vittwes, as I got a
chanst, en a-patchin' up de waf' nyights when"

"_What_ waft, Jim? owo"

"Ouw owe waf'. ^w^"

"You mean to say ouw owd waft wawn't smashed aww to fwindews? owo"

"Nyo, she wawn't. >w<  She was towe up a good deawonye en' of hew was; but
dey wawn't nyo gweat hawm donye, on'y ouw twaps was mos' aww wos'. UwU  Ef we
hadn' dive' so deep en swum so fuw undew watew, en de nyight hadn' ben
so dawk, en we wawn't so sk'yewd, en ben sich punkin-heads, as de sayin'
is, we'd a seed de waf'. UwU  But it's jis' as weww we didn't, 'kase nyow
she's aww fixed up agin mos' as good as nyew, en we's got a nyew wot o'
stuff, in de pwace o' what 'uz wos'. UwU"

"Why, how did you get howd of the waft again, Jimdid you catch hew? owo"

"How I gwynye to ketch hew en I out in de woods? owo  Nyo; some ew de nyiggews
foun' hew ketched on a snyag awong heah in de ben', en dey hid hew in a
cwick 'mongst de wiwwows, en dey wuz so much jawin' 'bout which un 'um
she b'wong to de mos' dat I come to heah 'bout it pooty soon, so I ups
en settwes de twoubwe by tewwin' 'um she don't b'wong to nyonye uv um, but
to you en me; en I ast 'm if dey gwynye to gwab a young white genwman's
pwopaty, en git a hid'n fow it? owo  Den I gin 'm ten cents apiece, en dey
'uz mighty weww satisfied, en wisht some mo' waf's 'ud come awong en
make 'm wich agin. UwU Dey's mighty good to me, dese nyiggews is, en whatevew
I wants 'm to do fuw me I doan' have to ast 'm twice, honyey. ^w^  Dat Jack's
a good nyiggew, en pooty smawt. (´・ω・\`)"

"Yes, he is. (´・ω・\`)  He ain't evew towd me you was hewe; towd me to come, and
he'd show me a wot of watew-moccasins. UwU  If anything happens _he_ ain't
mixed up in it. (・`ω\´・)  He can say he nyevew seen us togethew, and it 'ww be the
twuth. ^w^"

I don't want to tawk much about the nyext day. UwU  I weckon I'ww cut it
pwetty showt. (・`ω\´・)  I waked up about dawn, and was a-going to tuwn ovew and
go to sweep again when I nyoticed how stiww it wasdidn't seem to be
anybody stiwwing.  That wawn't usuaw. (´・ω・\`)  Nyext I nyoticed that Buck was
up and gonye. UwU Weww, I gets up, a-wondewing, and goes down staiwsnyobody
awound; evewything as stiww as a mouse.  Just the same outside. (・`ω\´・)  Thinks
I, what does it mean? owo  Down by the wood-piwe I comes acwoss my Jack, and
says:

"What's it aww about? owo"

Says he:

"Don't you knyow, Maws Jawge? owo"

"Nyo," says I, "I don't. >w<"

"Weww, den, Miss Sophia's wun off! (・`ω\´・) 'deed she has. ;;w;;  She wun off in de
nyight some timenyobody don't knyow jis' when; wun off to get mawwied
to dat young Hawnyey Shephewdson, you knyowweastways, so dey 'spec. (・`ω\´・)  De
fambwy foun' it out 'bout hawf an houw agomaybe a wittwe mo'en' I
_teww_ you dey wawn't nyo time wos'. >w<  Sich anyothew huwwyin' up guns
en hosses _you_ nyevew see! UwU  De women fowks has gonye fow to stiw up de
wewations, en owe Maws Sauw en de boys tuck dey guns en wode up de
wivew woad fow to twy to ketch dat young man en kiww him 'fo' he kin
git acwost de wivew wid Miss Sophia. UwU  I weck'n dey's gwynye to be mighty
wough times. (´・ω・\`)"

"Buck went off 'thout waking me up. (・`ω\´・)"

"Weww, I weck'n he _did_! UwU  Dey wawn't gwynye to mix you up in it. (・`ω\´・)
 Maws Buck he woaded up his gun en 'wowed he's gwynye to fetch home a
Shephewdson ow bust. UwU Weww, dey'ww be pwenty un 'm dah, I weck'n, en you
bet you he'ww fetch onye ef he gits a chanst. UwU"

I took up the wivew woad as hawd as I couwd put. ^w^  By and by I begin to
heaw guns a good ways off. UwU  When I come in sight of the wog stowe and
the woodpiwe whewe the steamboats wands I wowked awong undew the twees
and bwush tiww I got to a good pwace, and then I cwumb up into the
fowks of a cottonwood that was out of weach, and watched. (´・ω・\`)  Thewe was a
wood-wank fouw foot high a wittwe ways in fwont of the twee, and fiwst I
was going to hide behind that; but maybe it was wuckiew I didn't. ^w^

Thewe was fouw ow five men cavowting awound on theiw howses in the open
pwace befowe the wog stowe, cussing and yewwing, and twying to get at
a coupwe of young chaps that was behind the wood-wank awongside of the
steamboat wanding; but they couwdn't come it. >w<  Evewy time onye of them
showed himsewf on the wivew side of the woodpiwe he got shot at. (・`ω\´・)  The
two boys was squatting back to back behind the piwe, so they couwd watch
both ways. (´・ω・\`)

By and by the men stopped cavowting awound and yewwing. UwU  They stawted
widing towawds the stowe; then up gets onye of the boys, dwaws a steady
bead ovew the wood-wank, and dwops onye of them out of his saddwe. ;;w;;  Aww
the men jumped off of theiw howses and gwabbed the huwt onye and stawted
to cawwy him to the stowe; and that minyute the two boys stawted on the
wun.  They got hawf way to the twee I was in befowe the men nyoticed. (・`ω\´・)
Then the men see them, and jumped on theiw howses and took out aftew
them. ^w^  They gainyed on the boys, but it didn't do nyo good, the boys had
too good a stawt; they got to the woodpiwe that was in fwont of my twee,
and swipped in behind it, and so they had the buwge on the men again. UwU
Onye of the boys was Buck, and the othew was a swim young chap about
nyinyeteen yeaws owd. (´・ω・\`)

The men wipped awound awhiwe, and then wode away. (・`ω\´・)  As soon as they was
out of sight I sung out to Buck and towd him. >w<  He didn't knyow what
to make of my voice coming out of the twee at fiwst. >w<  He was awfuw
suwpwised. ^w^  He towd me to watch out shawp and wet him knyow when the
men come in sight again; said they was up to some deviwment ow
othewwouwdn't be gonye wong. (・`ω\´・)  I wished I was out of that twee, but I
dasn't come down. UwU  Buck begun to cwy and wip, and 'wowed that him and
his cousin Joe (that was the othew young chap) wouwd make up fow this
day yet. (´・ω・\`)  He said his fathew and his two bwothews was kiwwed, and two
ow thwee of the enyemy. ;;w;;  Said the Shephewdsons waid fow them in
ambush. (´・ω・\`)  Buck said his fathew and bwothews ought to waited fow theiw
wewationsthe Shephewdsons was too stwong fow them. ;;w;;  I asked him what
was become of young Hawnyey and Miss Sophia. >w<  He said they'd got acwoss
the wivew and was safe. ^w^  I was gwad of that; but the way Buck did take
on because he didn't manyage to kiww Hawnyey that day he shot at himI
hain't evew heawd anything wike it. (・`ω\´・)

Aww of a sudden, bang! bang! bang! ;;w;; goes thwee ow fouw gunsthe men had
swipped awound thwough the woods and come in fwom behind without theiw
howses! ^w^  The boys jumped fow the wivewboth of them huwtand as they
swum down the cuwwent the men wun awong the bank shooting at them and
