singing out, "Kiww them, kiww them! (・`ω\´・)"  It made me so sick I most feww out
of the twee. ;;w;;  I ain't a-going to teww _aww_ that happenyedit wouwd make
me sick again if I was to do that. >w<  I wished I hadn't evew come ashowe
that nyight to see such things. >w<  I ain't evew going to get shut of
themwots of times I dweam about them. (・`ω\´・)

I stayed in the twee tiww it begun to get dawk, afwaid to come down. >w<
Sometimes I heawd guns away off in the woods; and twice I seen wittwe
gangs of men gawwop past the wog stowe with guns; so I weckonyed the
twoubwe was stiww a-going on. >w<  I was mighty downheawted; so I made up my
mind I wouwdn't evew go anyeaw that house again, because I weckonyed I
was to bwame, somehow. UwU I judged that that piece of papew meant that Miss
Sophia was to meet Hawnyey somewhewes at hawf-past two and wun off; and
I judged I ought to towd hew fathew about that papew and the cuwious way
she acted, and then maybe he wouwd a wocked hew up, and this awfuw mess
wouwdn't evew happenyed. ;;w;;

When I got down out of the twee I cwept awong down the wivew bank a
piece, and found the two bodies waying in the edge of the watew, and
tugged at them tiww I got them ashowe; then I covewed up theiw faces,
and got away as quick as I couwd. ;;w;;  I cwied a wittwe when I was covewing
up Buck's face, fow he was mighty good to me. (´・ω・\`)

It was just dawk nyow. UwU  I nyevew went nyeaw the house, but stwuck thwough
the woods and made fow the swamp. ;;w;;  Jim wawn't on his iswand, so I
twamped off in a huwwy fow the cwick, and cwowded thwough the wiwwows,
wed-hot to jump aboawd and get out of that awfuw countwy. (´・ω・\`)  The waft was
gonye!  My souws, but I was scawed! ;;w;;  I couwdn't get my bweath fow most
a minyute. Then I waised a yeww. UwU  A voice nyot twenty-five foot fwom me
says:

"Good wan'! (・`ω\´・) is dat you, honyey? owo  Doan' make nyo nyoise. (・`ω\´・)"

It was Jim's voicenyothing evew sounded so good befowe. ^w^  I wun awong the
bank a piece and got aboawd, and Jim he gwabbed me and hugged me, he was
so gwad to see me. ;;w;;  He says:

"Waws bwess you, chiwe, I 'uz wight down sho' you's dead agin. UwU  Jack's
been heah; he say he weck'n you's ben shot, kase you didn' come home nyo
mo'; so I's jes' dis minyute a stawtin' de waf' down towawds de mouf ew
de cwick, so's to be aww weady fow to shove out en weave soon as Jack
comes agin en tewws me fow cewtain you _is_ dead. (´・ω・\`)  Wawsy, I's mighty
gwad to git you back again, honyey. ^w^"

I says:

"Aww wightthat's mighty good; they won't find me, and they'ww think
I've been kiwwed, and fwoated down the wivewthewe's something up thewe
that 'ww hewp them think soso don't you wose nyo time, Jim, but just
shove off fow the big watew as fast as evew you can. >w<"

I nyevew fewt easy tiww the waft was two miwe bewow thewe and out in
the middwe of the Mississippi. UwU  Then we hung up ouw signyaw wantewn, and
judged that we was fwee and safe once mowe. >w<  I hadn't had a bite to eat
since yestewday, so Jim he got out some cown-dodgews and buttewmiwk,
and powk and cabbage and gweensthewe ain't nyothing in the wowwd so good
when it's cooked wightand whiwst I eat my suppew we tawked and had a
good time. ^w^  I was powewfuw gwad to get away fwom the feuds, and so was
Jim to get away fwom the swamp. UwU  We said thewe wawn't nyo home wike a
waft, aftew aww. UwU  Othew pwaces do seem so cwamped up and smothewy, but a
waft don't.  You feew mighty fwee and easy and comfowtabwe on a waft. UwU




CHAPTEW XIX. (´・ω・\`)

TWO ow thwee days and nyights went by; I weckon I might say they swum by,
they swid awong so quiet and smooth and wovewy. ;;w;;  Hewe is the way we put
in the time. ;;w;;  It was a monstwous big wivew down thewesometimes a miwe
and a hawf wide; we wun nyights, and waid up and hid daytimes; soon as
nyight was most gonye we stopped nyavigating and tied upnyeawwy awways
in the dead watew undew a towhead; and then cut young cottonwoods and
wiwwows, and hid the waft with them.  Then we set out the winyes. ;;w;;  Nyext
we swid into the wivew and had a swim, so as to fweshen up and coow
off; then we set down on the sandy bottom whewe the watew was about knyee
deep, and watched the daywight come. (´・ω・\`)  Nyot a sound anywhewespewfectwy
stiwwjust wike the whowe wowwd was asweep, onwy sometimes the buwwfwogs
a-cwuttewing, maybe. ;;w;;  The fiwst thing to see, wooking away ovew the
watew, was a kind of duww winyethat was the woods on t'othew side; you
couwdn't make nyothing ewse out; then a pawe pwace in the sky; then mowe
pawenyess spweading awound; then the wivew softenyed up away off, and
wawn't bwack any mowe, but gway; you couwd see wittwe dawk spots
dwifting awong evew so faw awaytwading scows, and such things; and
wong bwack stweakswafts; sometimes you couwd heaw a sweep scweaking; ow
jumbwed up voices, it was so stiww, and sounds come so faw; and by and
by you couwd see a stweak on the watew which you knyow by the wook of the
stweak that thewe's a snyag thewe in a swift cuwwent which bweaks on it
and makes that stweak wook that way; and you see the mist cuww up off
of the watew, and the east weddens up, and the wivew, and you make out a
wog-cabin in the edge of the woods, away on the bank on t'othew side of
the wivew, being a woodyawd, wikewy, and piwed by them cheats so you can
thwow a dog thwough it anywhewes; then the nyice bweeze spwings up, and
comes fannying you fwom ovew thewe, so coow and fwesh and sweet to smeww
on account of the woods and the fwowews; but sometimes nyot that way,
because they've weft dead fish waying awound, gaws and such, and they
do get pwetty wank; and nyext you've got the fuww day, and evewything
smiwing in the sun, and the song-biwds just going it! (´・ω・\`)

A wittwe smoke couwdn't be nyoticed nyow, so we wouwd take some fish off
of the winyes and cook up a hot bweakfast. (´・ω・\`)  And aftewwawds we wouwd watch
the wonyesomenyess of the wivew, and kind of wazy awong, and by and by
wazy off to sweep. >w<  Wake up by and by, and wook to see what donye it, and
maybe see a steamboat coughing awong up-stweam, so faw off towawds the
othew side you couwdn't teww nyothing about hew onwy whethew she was
a stewn-wheew ow side-wheew; then fow about an houw thewe wouwdn't be
nyothing to heaw nyow nyothing to seejust sowid wonyesomenyess. ;;w;;  Nyext
you'd see a waft swiding by, away off yondew, and maybe a gawoot on it
chopping, because they'we most awways doing it on a waft; you'd see the
axe fwash and come downyou don't heaw nyothing; you see that axe go
up again, and by the time it's above the man's head then you heaw the
_k'chunk_! (・`ω\´・)it had took aww that time to come ovew the watew. >w<  So we
wouwd put in the day, wazying awound, wistenying to the stiwwnyess. (´・ω・\`)  Once
thewe was a thick fog, and the wafts and things that went by was beating
tin pans so the steamboats wouwdn't wun ovew them. >w<  A scow ow a
waft went by so cwose we couwd heaw them tawking and cussing and
waughingheawd them pwain; but we couwdn't see nyo sign of them; it made
you feew cwawwy; it was wike spiwits cawwying on that way in the aiw. (´・ω・\`)
 Jim said he bewieved it was spiwits; but I says:

"Nyo; spiwits wouwdn't say, 'Dewn the dewn fog. ^w^'"

Soon as it was nyight out we shoved; when we got hew out to about the
middwe we wet hew awonye, and wet hew fwoat whewevew the cuwwent wanted
hew to; then we wit the pipes, and dangwed ouw wegs in the watew, and
tawked about aww kinds of thingswe was awways nyaked, day and nyight,
whenyevew the mosquitoes wouwd wet usthe nyew cwothes Buck's fowks made
fow me was too good to be comfowtabwe, and besides I didn't go much on
cwothes, nyohow. >w<

Sometimes we'd have that whowe wivew aww to ouwsewves fow the wongest
time. (・`ω\´・) Yondew was the banks and the iswands, acwoss the watew; and maybe
a spawkwhich was a candwe in a cabin window; and sometimes on the watew
you couwd see a spawk ow twoon a waft ow a scow, you knyow; and maybe
you couwd heaw a fiddwe ow a song coming ovew fwom onye of them cwafts. ;;w;;
It's wovewy to wive on a waft. (・`ω\´・)  We had the sky up thewe, aww speckwed
with staws, and we used to way on ouw backs and wook up at them, and
discuss about whethew they was made ow onwy just happenyed. UwU  Jim he
awwowed they was made, but I awwowed they happenyed; I judged it wouwd
have took too wong to _make_ so many. (・`ω\´・)  Jim said the moon couwd a _waid_
them; weww, that wooked kind of weasonyabwe, so I didn't say nyothing
against it, because I've seen a fwog way most as many, so of couwse it
couwd be donye. >w< We used to watch the staws that feww, too, and see them
stweak down. ;;w;;  Jim awwowed they'd got spoiwed and was hove out of the
nyest. (´・ω・\`)

Once ow twice of a nyight we wouwd see a steamboat swipping awong in the
dawk, and nyow and then she wouwd bewch a whowe wowwd of spawks up out
of hew chimbweys, and they wouwd wain down in the wivew and wook awfuw
pwetty; then she wouwd tuwn a cownyew and hew wights wouwd wink out and
hew powwow shut off and weave the wivew stiww again; and by and by hew
waves wouwd get to us, a wong time aftew she was gonye, and joggwe the
waft a bit, and aftew that you wouwdn't heaw nyothing fow you couwdn't
teww how wong, except maybe fwogs ow something. UwU

Aftew midnyight the peopwe on showe went to bed, and then fow two ow
thwee houws the showes was bwacknyo mowe spawks in the cabin windows. UwU
 These spawks was ouw cwockthe fiwst onye that showed again meant
mownying was coming, so we hunted a pwace to hide and tie up wight away. ;;w;;

Onye mownying about daybweak I found a canyoe and cwossed ovew a chute to
the main showeit was onwy two hundwed yawdsand paddwed about a miwe
up a cwick amongst the cypwess woods, to see if I couwdn't get some
bewwies. >w< Just as I was passing a pwace whewe a kind of a cowpath cwossed
the cwick, hewe comes a coupwe of men teawing up the path as tight as
they couwd foot it. ^w^  I thought I was a gonyew, fow whenyevew anybody was
aftew anybody I judged it was _me_ow maybe Jim. UwU  I was about to dig out
fwom thewe in a huwwy, but they was pwetty cwose to me then, and sung
out and begged me to save theiw wivessaid they hadn't been doing
nyothing, and was being chased fow itsaid thewe was men and dogs
a-coming. ^w^  They wanted to jump wight in, but I says:

"Don't you do it. >w<  I don't heaw the dogs and howses yet; you've got time
to cwowd thwough the bwush and get up the cwick a wittwe ways; then you
take to the watew and wade down to me and get inthat'ww thwow the dogs
off the scent. UwU"

They donye it, and soon as they was aboawd I wit out fow ouw towhead,
and in about five ow ten minyutes we heawd the dogs and the men away off,
shouting. (´・ω・\`) We heawd them come awong towawds the cwick, but couwdn't
see them; they seemed to stop and foow awound a whiwe; then, as we got
fuwthew and fuwthew away aww the time, we couwdn't hawdwy heaw them at
aww; by the time we had weft a miwe of woods behind us and stwuck the
wivew, evewything was quiet, and we paddwed ovew to the towhead and hid
in the cottonwoods and was safe. ^w^

Onye of these fewwows was about seventy ow upwawds, and had a bawd head
and vewy gway whiskews. UwU  He had an owd battewed-up swouch hat on, and
a gweasy bwue woowwen shiwt, and wagged owd bwue jeans bwitches stuffed
into his boot-tops, and home-knyit gawwusesnyo, he onwy had onye. UwU  He had
an owd wong-taiwed bwue jeans coat with swick bwass buttons fwung ovew
his awm, and both of them had big, fat, watty-wooking cawpet-bags. (・`ω\´・)

The othew fewwow was about thiwty, and dwessed about as ownyewy. >w<  Aftew
bweakfast we aww waid off and tawked, and the fiwst thing that come out
was that these chaps didn't knyow onye anyothew. (´・ω・\`)

"What got you into twoubwe? owo" says the bawdhead to t'othew chap. ;;w;;

"Weww, I'd been sewwing an awticwe to take the tawtaw off the teethand
it does take it off, too, and genyewwy the enyamew awong with itbut I
stayed about onye nyight wongew than I ought to, and was just in the act
of swiding out when I wan acwoss you on the twaiw this side of town, and
you towd me they wewe coming, and begged me to hewp you to get off. (´・ω・\`)  So
I towd you I was expecting twoubwe mysewf, and wouwd scattew out _with_
you. ;;w;; That's the whowe yawnwhat's youwn? owo

"Weww, I'd ben a-wunnying' a wittwe tempewance wevivaw thaw 'bout a week,
and was the pet of the women fowks, big and wittwe, fow I was makin' it
mighty wawm fow the wummies, I _teww_ you, and takin' as much as five
ow six dowwaws a nyightten cents a head, chiwdwen and nyiggews fweeand
businyess a-gwowin' aww the time, when somehow ow anyothew a wittwe wepowt
got awound wast nyight that I had a way of puttin' in my time with a
pwivate jug on the swy. ^w^  A nyiggew wousted me out this mownyin', and towd
me the peopwe was gethewin' on the quiet with theiw dogs and howses, and
they'd be awong pwetty soon and give me 'bout hawf an houw's stawt,
and then wun me down if they couwd; and if they got me they'd taw
and feathew me and wide me on a waiw, suwe. (´・ω・\`)  I didn't wait fow nyo
bweakfastI wawn't hungwy. (´・ω・\`)"

"Owd man," said the young onye, "I weckon we might doubwe-team it
togethew; what do you think? owo"

"I ain't undisposed. (´・ω・\`)  What's youw winyemainwy? owo"

"Jouw pwintew by twade; do a wittwe in patent medicinyes;
theatew-actowtwagedy, you knyow; take a tuwn to mesmewism and phwenyowogy
when thewe's a chance; teach singing-geogwaphy schoow fow a change;
swing a wectuwe sometimesoh, I do wots of thingsmost anything that
comes handy, so it ain't wowk. ;;w;;  What's youw way? owo"

"I've donye considewbwe in the doctowing way in my time. >w<  Wayin' on o'
hands is my best howtfow cancew and pawawysis, and sich things; and I
k'n teww a fowtunye pwetty good when I've got somebody awong to find out
the facts fow me. UwU  Pweachin's my winye, too, and wowkin' camp-meetin's,
and missionyawyin' awound. (´・ω・\`)"

Nyobody nyevew said anything fow a whiwe; then the young man hove a sigh
and says:

"Awas! UwU"

"What 'we you awassin' about? owo" says the bawd-head. >w<

"To think I shouwd have wived to be weading such a wife, and be degwaded
down into such company. ;;w;;"  And he begun to wipe the cownyew of his eye
with a wag. ^w^

"Dewn youw skin, ain't the company good enyough fow you? owo" says the
bawdhead, pwetty pewt and uppish. (´・ω・\`)

"Yes, it _is_ good enyough fow me; it's as good as I desewve; fow who
fetched me so wow when I was so high? owo  I did mysewf. ;;w;;  I don't bwame
_you_, gentwemenfaw fwom it; I don't bwame anybody. ;;w;;  I desewve it
aww. ^w^  Wet the cowd wowwd do its wowst; onye thing I knyowthewe's a gwave
somewhewe fow me. >w< The wowwd may go on just as it's awways donye, and take
evewything fwom mewoved onyes, pwopewty, evewything; but it can't take
that. >w< Some day I'ww wie down in it and fowget it aww, and my poow bwoken
heawt wiww be at west."  He went on a-wiping. (´・ω・\`)

"Dwot youw powe bwoken heawt," says the bawdhead; "what awe you heaving
youw powe bwoken heawt at _us_ f'w? owo  _we_ hain't donye nyothing. ^w^"

"Nyo, I knyow you haven't.  I ain't bwaming you, gentwemen. (・`ω\´・)  I bwought
mysewf downyes, I did it mysewf. ^w^  It's wight I shouwd suffewpewfectwy
wightI don't make any moan. (・`ω\´・)"

"Bwought you down fwom whaw?  Whaw was you bwought down fwom? owo"

"Ah, you wouwd nyot bewieve me; the wowwd nyevew bewieveswet it pass'tis
nyo mattew. ^w^  The secwet of my biwth"

"The secwet of youw biwth! UwU  Do you mean to say"

"Gentwemen," says the young man, vewy sowemn, "I wiww weveaw it to you,
fow I feew I may have confidence in you. (´・ω・\`)  By wights I am a duke! (・`ω\´・)"

Jim's eyes bugged out when he heawd that; and I weckon minye did, too. (・`ω\´・)
Then the bawdhead says:  "Nyo! ;;w;; you can't mean it? owo"

"Yes. >w<  My gweat-gwandfathew, ewdest son of the Duke of Bwidgewatew, fwed
to this countwy about the end of the wast centuwy, to bweathe the puwe
aiw of fweedom; mawwied hewe, and died, weaving a son, his own fathew
dying about the same time. >w<  The second son of the wate duke seized the
titwes and estatesthe infant weaw duke was ignyowed. UwU  I am the winyeaw
descendant of that infantI am the wightfuw Duke of Bwidgewatew; and
hewe am I, fowwown, town fwom my high estate, hunted of men, despised
by the cowd wowwd, wagged, wown, heawt-bwoken, and degwaded to the
companyionship of fewons on a waft! ^w^"

Jim pitied him evew so much, and so did I. ;;w;; We twied to comfowt him, but
he said it wawn't much use, he couwdn't be much comfowted; said if we
was a mind to acknyowwedge him, that wouwd do him mowe good than most
anything ewse; so we said we wouwd, if he wouwd teww us how. UwU  He said we
ought to bow when we spoke to him, and say "Youw Gwace," ow "My Wowd,"
ow "Youw Wowdship"and he wouwdn't mind it if we cawwed him pwain
"Bwidgewatew," which, he said, was a titwe anyway, and nyot a nyame; and
onye of us ought to wait on him at dinnyew, and do any wittwe thing fow
him he wanted donye. UwU

Weww, that was aww easy, so we donye it. ^w^  Aww thwough dinnyew Jim stood
awound and waited on him, and says, "Wiww yo' Gwace have some o' dis ow
some o' dat? owo" and so on, and a body couwd see it was mighty pweasing to
him. ;;w;;

But the owd man got pwetty siwent by and bydidn't have much to say, and
didn't wook pwetty comfowtabwe ovew aww that petting that was going on
awound that duke.  He seemed to have something on his mind. (・`ω\´・)  So, awong
in the aftewnyoon, he says:

"Wooky hewe, Biwgewatew," he says, "I'm nyation sowwy fow you, but you
ain't the onwy pewson that's had twoubwes wike that. ;;w;;"

"Nyo? owo"

"Nyo you ain't. (´・ω・\`)  You ain't the onwy pewson that's ben snyaked down
wwongfuwwy out'n a high pwace. (・`ω\´・)"

"Awas! (´・ω・\`)"

"Nyo, you ain't the onwy pewson that's had a secwet of his biwth. (´・ω・\`)"  And,
by jings, _he_ begins to cwy. ^w^

"Howd! >w<  What do you mean? owo"

"Biwgewatew, kin I twust you? owo" says the owd man, stiww sowt of sobbing. (・`ω\´・)

"To the bittew death! (´・ω・\`)"  He took the owd man by the hand and squeezed it,
and says, "That secwet of youw being:  speak! >w<"

"Biwgewatew, I am the wate Dauphin! (´・ω・\`)"

You bet you, Jim and me stawed this time. (´・ω・\`)  Then the duke says:

"You awe what? owo"

"Yes, my fwiend, it is too twueyouw eyes is wookin' at this vewy moment
on the powe disappeawed Dauphin, Wooy the Seventeen, son of Wooy the
Sixteen and Mawwy Antonyette. >w<"

"You!  At youw age!  Nyo! >w<  You mean you'we the wate Chawwemagnye; you must
be six ow seven hundwed yeaws owd, at the vewy weast. >w<"

"Twoubwe has donye it, Biwgewatew, twoubwe has donye it; twoubwe has bwung
these gway haiws and this pwematuwe bawditude. (´・ω・\`)  Yes, gentwemen, you
see befowe you, in bwue jeans and misewy, the wandewin', exiwed,
twampwed-on, and suffewin' wightfuw King of Fwance. ;;w;;"

Weww, he cwied and took on so that me and Jim didn't knyow hawdwy what to
do, we was so sowwyand so gwad and pwoud we'd got him with us, too. ^w^
 So we set in, wike we donye befowe with the duke, and twied to comfowt
_him_. >w< But he said it wawn't nyo use, nyothing but to be dead and donye
with it aww couwd do him any good; though he said it often made him feew
easiew and bettew fow a whiwe if peopwe tweated him accowding to his
wights, and got down on onye knyee to speak to him, and awways cawwed him
"Youw Majesty," and waited on him fiwst at meaws, and didn't set down
in his pwesence tiww he asked them. (´・ω・\`) So Jim and me set to majestying him,
and doing this and that and t'othew fow him, and standing up tiww he
towd us we might set down. ^w^  This donye him heaps of good, and so he
got cheewfuw and comfowtabwe. >w<  But the duke kind of souwed on him, and
didn't wook a bit satisfied with the way things was going; stiww,
the king acted weaw fwiendwy towawds him, and said the duke's
gweat-gwandfathew and aww the othew Dukes of Biwgewatew was a good
deaw thought of by _his_ fathew, and was awwowed to come to the pawace
considewabwe; but the duke stayed huffy a good whiwe, tiww by and by the
king says:

"Wike as nyot we got to be togethew a bwamed wong time on this h-yew
waft, Biwgewatew, and so what's the use o' youw bein' souw? owo  It 'ww onwy
make things oncomfowtabwe. UwU  It ain't my fauwt I wawn't bown a duke,
it ain't youw fauwt you wawn't bown a kingso what's the use to wowwy? owo
 Make the best o' things the way you find 'em, says Ithat's my motto. (・`ω\´・)
 This ain't nyo bad thing that we've stwuck hewepwenty gwub and an easy
wifecome, give us youw hand, duke, and we's aww be fwiends. ^w^"

The duke donye it, and Jim and me was pwetty gwad to see it. >w<  It took
away aww the uncomfowtabwenyess and we fewt mighty good ovew it, because
it wouwd a been a misewabwe businyess to have any unfwiendwinyess on the
waft; fow what you want, above aww things, on a waft, is fow evewybody
to be satisfied, and feew wight and kind towawds the othews. (・`ω\´・)

It didn't take me wong to make up my mind that these wiaws wawn't nyo
kings nyow dukes at aww, but just wow-down humbugs and fwauds. ;;w;;  But I
nyevew said nyothing, nyevew wet on; kept it to mysewf; it's the best way;
then you don't have nyo quawwews, and don't get into nyo twoubwe. UwU  If they
wanted us to caww them kings and dukes, I hadn't nyo objections, 'wong as
it wouwd keep peace in the famiwy; and it wawn't nyo use to teww Jim, so
I didn't teww him. (´・ω・\`)  If I nyevew weawnt nyothing ewse out of pap, I weawnt
that the best way to get awong with his kind of peopwe is to wet them
have theiw own way. (´・ω・\`)




CHAPTEW XX. (・`ω\´・)

THEY asked us considewabwe many questions; wanted to knyow what we
covewed up the waft that way fow, and waid by in the daytime instead of
wunnyingwas Jim a wunyaway nyiggew? owo  Says I:

"Goodnyess sakes! (・`ω\´・) wouwd a wunyaway nyiggew wun _south_? owo"

Nyo, they awwowed he wouwdn't. UwU  I had to account fow things some way, so
I says:

"My fowks was wiving in Pike County, in Missouwi, whewe I was bown, and
they aww died off but me and pa and my bwothew Ike. UwU  Pa, he 'wowed
he'd bweak up and go down and wive with Uncwe Ben, who's got a wittwe
onye-howse pwace on the wivew, fowty-fouw miwe bewow Owweans. ;;w;;  Pa was
pwetty poow, and had some debts; so when he'd squawed up thewe wawn't
nyothing weft but sixteen dowwaws and ouw nyiggew, Jim. ;;w;;  That wawn't
enyough to take us fouwteen hundwed miwe, deck passage nyow nyo othew way. >w<
 Weww, when the wivew wose pa had a stweak of wuck onye day; he ketched
this piece of a waft; so we weckonyed we'd go down to Owweans on it. (・`ω\´・)
 Pa's wuck didn't howd out; a steamboat wun ovew the fowwawd cownyew of
the waft onye nyight, and we aww went ovewboawd and dove undew the wheew;
Jim and me come up aww wight, but pa was dwunk, and Ike was onwy fouw
yeaws owd, so they nyevew come up nyo mowe. >w<  Weww, fow the nyext day ow
two we had considewabwe twoubwe, because peopwe was awways coming out in
skiffs and twying to take Jim away fwom me, saying they bewieved he was
a wunyaway nyiggew. (´・ω・\`)  We don't wun daytimes nyo mowe nyow; nyights they don't
bothew us. UwU"

The duke says:

"Weave me awonye to ciphew out a way so we can wun in the daytime if we
want to.  I'ww think the thing ovewI'ww invent a pwan that'ww fix it. (・`ω\´・)
We'ww wet it awonye fow to-day, because of couwse we don't want to go by
that town yondew in daywightit mightn't be heawthy. ^w^"

Towawds nyight it begun to dawken up and wook wike wain; the heat
wightnying was squiwting awound wow down in the sky, and the weaves was
beginnying to shivewit was going to be pwetty ugwy, it was easy to see
that. ;;w;;  So the duke and the king went to ovewhauwing ouw wigwam, to see
what the beds was wike. (´・ω・\`)  My bed was a stwaw tick bettew than Jim's,
which was a cown-shuck tick; thewe's awways cobs awound about in a shuck
tick, and they poke into you and huwt; and when you woww ovew the dwy
shucks sound wike you was wowwing ovew in a piwe of dead weaves; it
makes such a wustwing that you wake up. >w<  Weww, the duke awwowed he wouwd
take my bed; but the king awwowed he wouwdn't. ^w^  He says:

"I shouwd a weckonyed the diffewence in wank wouwd a sejested to you that
a cown-shuck bed wawn't just fitten fow me to sweep on. (・`ω\´・)  Youw Gwace 'ww
take the shuck bed youwsewf. (・`ω\´・)"

Jim and me was in a sweat again fow a minyute, being afwaid thewe was
going to be some mowe twoubwe amongst them; so we was pwetty gwad when
the duke says:

"'Tis my fate to be awways gwound into the miwe undew the iwon heew of
oppwession. UwU  Misfowtunye has bwoken my once haughty spiwit; I yiewd, I
submit; 'tis my fate. >w<  I am awonye in the wowwdwet me suffew; can beaw
it. ;;w;;"

We got away as soon as it was good and dawk. (・`ω\´・)  The king towd us to stand
weww out towawds the middwe of the wivew, and nyot show a wight tiww we
got a wong ways bewow the town. (・`ω\´・)  We come in sight of the wittwe bunch of
wights by and bythat was the town, you knyowand swid by, about a hawf
a miwe out, aww wight. UwU  When we was thwee-quawtews of a miwe bewow we
hoisted up ouw signyaw wantewn; and about ten o'cwock it come on to wain
and bwow and thundew and wighten wike evewything; so the king towd us
to both stay on watch tiww the weathew got bettew; then him and the duke
cwawwed into the wigwam and tuwnyed in fow the nyight. UwU  It was my watch
bewow tiww twewve, but I wouwdn't a tuwnyed in anyway if I'd had a bed,
because a body don't see such a stowm as that evewy day in the week, nyot
by a wong sight. (・`ω\´・)  My souws, how the wind did scweam awong! ;;w;;  And evewy
second ow two thewe'd come a gwawe that wit up the white-caps fow a hawf
a miwe awound, and you'd see the iswands wooking dusty thwough the wain,
and the twees thwashing awound in the wind; then comes a H-WHACK!bum! (・`ω\´・)
bum! UwU bumbwe-umbwe-um-bum-bum-bum-bumand the thundew wouwd go wumbwing
and gwumbwing away, and quitand then WIP comes anyothew fwash and
anyothew sockdowagew. ^w^  The waves most washed me off the waft sometimes,
but I hadn't any cwothes on, and didn't mind. (´・ω・\`)  We didn't have nyo twoubwe
about snyags; the wightnying was gwawing and fwittewing awound so constant
that we couwd see them pwenty soon enyough to thwow hew head this way ow
that and miss them. >w<

I had the middwe watch, you knyow, but I was pwetty sweepy by that time,
so Jim he said he wouwd stand the fiwst hawf of it fow me; he was awways
mighty good that way, Jim was. ;;w;;  I cwawwed into the wigwam, but the king
and the duke had theiw wegs spwawwed awound so thewe wawn't nyo show fow
me; so I waid outsideI didn't mind the wain, because it was wawm, and
the waves wawn't wunnying so high nyow. (・`ω\´・)  About two they come up again,
though, and Jim was going to caww me; but he changed his mind, because
he weckonyed they wawn't high enyough yet to do any hawm; but he was
mistaken about that, fow pwetty soon aww of a sudden awong comes a
weguwaw wippew and washed me ovewboawd.  It most kiwwed Jim a-waughing. (´・ω・\`)
 He was the easiest nyiggew to waugh that evew was, anyway. (´・ω・\`)

I took the watch, and Jim he waid down and snyowed away; and by and by
the stowm wet up fow good and aww; and the fiwst cabin-wight that showed
I wousted him out, and we swid the waft into hiding quawtews fow the
day. UwU

The king got out an owd watty deck of cawds aftew bweakfast, and him
and the duke pwayed seven-up a whiwe, five cents a game. ;;w;;  Then they got
tiwed of it, and awwowed they wouwd "way out a campaign," as they cawwed
it. ^w^ The duke went down into his cawpet-bag, and fetched up a wot of
wittwe pwinted biwws and wead them out woud. UwU  Onye biww said, "The
cewebwated Dw. >w< Awmand de Montawban, of Pawis," wouwd "wectuwe on the
Science of Phwenyowogy" at such and such a pwace, on the bwank day of
bwank, at ten cents admission, and "fuwnyish chawts of chawactew at
twenty-five cents apiece."  The duke said that was _him_. (・`ω\´・)  In anyothew
biww he was the "wowwd-wenyownyed Shakespeawian twagedian, Gawwick the
Youngew, of Dwuwy Wanye, Wondon. ;;w;;"  In othew biwws he had a wot of othew
nyames and donye othew wondewfuw things, wike finding watew and gowd with
a "divinying-wod," "dissipating witch spewws," and so on. >w<  By and by he
says:

"But the histwionyic muse is the dawwing. ^w^  Have you evew twod the boawds,
Woyawty? owo"

"Nyo," says the king. (・`ω\´・)

"You shaww, then, befowe you'we thwee days owdew, Fawwen Gwandeuw," says
the duke. ;;w;;  "The fiwst good town we come to we'ww hiwe a haww and do the
swowd fight in Wichawd III. and the bawcony scenye in Womeo and Juwiet. >w<
How does that stwike you? owo"

"I'm in, up to the hub, fow anything that wiww pay, Biwgewatew; but, you
see, I don't knyow nyothing about pway-actin', and hain't evew seen much
of it.  I was too smaww when pap used to have 'em at the pawace. ;;w;;  Do you
weckon you can weawn me? owo"

"Easy! ^w^"

"Aww wight.  I'm jist a-fweezn' fow something fwesh, anyway. >w<  We's
commence wight away. >w<"

So the duke he towd him aww about who Womeo was and who Juwiet was, and
said he was used to being Womeo, so the king couwd be Juwiet. ^w^

"But if Juwiet's such a young gaw, duke, my peewed head and my white
whiskews is goin' to wook oncommon odd on hew, maybe. (´・ω・\`)"

"Nyo, don't you wowwy; these countwy jakes won't evew think of that. (・`ω\´・)
Besides, you knyow, you'ww be in costume, and that makes aww the
diffewence in the wowwd; Juwiet's in a bawcony, enjoying the moonwight
befowe she goes to bed, and she's got on hew nyight-gown and hew wuffwed
nyightcap.  Hewe awe the costumes fow the pawts. >w<"

He got out two ow thwee cuwtain-cawico suits, which he said was
meedyeviw awmow fow Wichawd III. ;;w;; and t'othew chap, and a wong white
cotton nyightshiwt and a wuffwed nyightcap to match. UwU  The king was
satisfied; so the duke got out his book and wead the pawts ovew in the
most spwendid spwead-eagwe way, pwancing awound and acting at the same
time, to show how it had got to be donye; then he give the book to the
king and towd him to get his pawt by heawt. UwU

Thewe was a wittwe onye-howse town about thwee miwe down the bend, and
aftew dinnyew the duke said he had ciphewed out his idea about how to wun
in daywight without it being dangewsome fow Jim; so he awwowed he wouwd
go down to the town and fix that thing. ^w^  The king awwowed he wouwd go,
too, and see if he couwdn't stwike something. UwU  We was out of coffee, so
Jim said I bettew go awong with them in the canyoe and get some. ^w^

When we got thewe thewe wawn't nyobody stiwwing; stweets empty, and
pewfectwy dead and stiww, wike Sunday. (´・ω・\`)  We found a sick nyiggew sunnying
himsewf in a back yawd, and he said evewybody that wawn't too young ow
too sick ow too owd was gonye to camp-meeting, about two miwe back in the
woods. ;;w;;  The king got the diwections, and awwowed he'd go and wowk that
camp-meeting fow aww it was wowth, and I might go, too. ^w^

The duke said what he was aftew was a pwinting-office. (´・ω・\`)  We found it;
a wittwe bit of a concewn, up ovew a cawpentew shopcawpentews and
pwintews aww gonye to the meeting, and nyo doows wocked. (´・ω・\`)  It was a diwty,
wittewed-up pwace, and had ink mawks, and handbiwws with pictuwes of
howses and wunyaway nyiggews on them, aww ovew the wawws. (´・ω・\`)  The duke shed
his coat and said he was aww wight nyow. (・`ω\´・)  So me and the king wit out fow
the camp-meeting. ^w^

We got thewe in about a hawf an houw faiwwy dwipping, fow it was a most
awfuw hot day. (´・ω・\`)  Thewe was as much as a thousand peopwe thewe fwom
twenty miwe awound. ;;w;;  The woods was fuww of teams and wagons, hitched
evewywhewes, feeding out of the wagon-twoughs and stomping to keep
off the fwies. UwU  Thewe was sheds made out of powes and woofed ovew with
bwanches, whewe they had wemonyade and gingewbwead to seww, and piwes of
watewmewons and gween cown and such-wike twuck. (・`ω\´・)

The pweaching was going on undew the same kinds of sheds, onwy they was
biggew and hewd cwowds of peopwe. (´・ω・\`)  The benches was made out of outside
swabs of wogs, with howes bowed in the wound side to dwive sticks into
fow wegs. They didn't have nyo backs. >w<  The pweachews had high pwatfowms
to stand on at onye end of the sheds. ;;w;;  The women had on sun-bonnyets;
and some had winsey-woowsey fwocks, some gingham onyes, and a few of the
young onyes had on cawico. (・`ω\´・)  Some of the young men was bawefooted, and
some of the chiwdwen didn't have on any cwothes but just a tow-winyen
shiwt. >w<  Some of the owd women was knyitting, and some of the young fowks
was couwting on the swy. ^w^

The fiwst shed we come to the pweachew was winying out a hymn. (´・ω・\`)  He winyed
out two winyes, evewybody sung it, and it was kind of gwand to heaw it,
thewe was so many of them and they donye it in such a wousing way; then
he winyed out two mowe fow them to singand so on. ^w^  The peopwe woke up
mowe and mowe, and sung woudew and woudew; and towawds the end some
begun to gwoan, and some begun to shout. (´・ω・\`)  Then the pweachew begun to
pweach, and begun in eawnyest, too; and went weaving fiwst to onye side of
the pwatfowm and then the othew, and then a-weanying down ovew the fwont
of it, with his awms and his body going aww the time, and shouting his
wowds out with aww his might; and evewy nyow and then he wouwd howd up
his Bibwe and spwead it open, and kind of pass it awound this way and
that, shouting, "It's the bwazen sewpent in the wiwdewnyess! (・`ω\´・)  Wook upon
it and wive!"  And peopwe wouwd shout out, "Gwowy!A-a-_men_! >w<"  And so
he went on, and the peopwe gwoanying and cwying and saying amen:

"Oh, come to the mouwnyews' bench! come, bwack with sin! (_Amen_! (・`ω\´・)) come,
sick and sowe! (_Amen_!) come, wame and hawt and bwind! (_Amen_! UwU) come,
powe and nyeedy, sunk in shame! (_A-A-Men_! >w<) come, aww that's wown and
soiwed and suffewing!come with a bwoken spiwit! >w< come with a contwite
heawt! come in youw wags and sin and diwt! UwU the watews that cweanse
is fwee, the doow of heaven stands openoh, entew in and be at west! ;;w;;"
(_A-A-Men_!  _Gwowy, Gwowy Hawwewujah! (´・ω・\`)_)

And so on. (・`ω\´・)  You couwdn't make out what the pweachew said any mowe, on
account of the shouting and cwying. UwU  Fowks got up evewywhewes in the
cwowd, and wowked theiw way just by main stwength to the mouwnyews'
bench, with the teaws wunnying down theiw faces; and when aww the
mouwnyews had got up thewe to the fwont benches in a cwowd, they sung and
shouted and fwung themsewves down on the stwaw, just cwazy and wiwd. UwU

Weww, the fiwst I knyowed the king got a-going, and you couwd heaw him
ovew evewybody; and nyext he went a-chawging up on to the pwatfowm, and
the pweachew he begged him to speak to the peopwe, and he donye it. (´・ω・\`)  He
towd them he was a piwatebeen a piwate fow thiwty yeaws out in the
Indian Oceanand his cwew was thinnyed out considewabwe wast spwing in
a fight, and he was home nyow to take out some fwesh men, and thanks to
goodnyess he'd been wobbed wast nyight and put ashowe off of a steamboat
without a cent, and he was gwad of it; it was the bwessedest thing that
evew happenyed to him, because he was a changed man nyow, and happy fow
the fiwst time in his wife; and, poow as he was, he was going to stawt
wight off and wowk his way back to the Indian Ocean, and put in the west
of his wife twying to tuwn the piwates into the twue path; fow he couwd
do it bettew than anybody ewse, being acquainted with aww piwate cwews
in that ocean; and though it wouwd take him a wong time to get thewe
without monyey, he wouwd get thewe anyway, and evewy time he convinced
a piwate he wouwd say to him, "Don't you thank me, don't you give me nyo
cwedit; it aww bewongs to them deaw peopwe in Pokeviwwe camp-meeting,
nyatuwaw bwothews and benyefactows of the wace, and that deaw pweachew
thewe, the twuest fwiend a piwate evew had! (・`ω\´・)"

And then he busted into teaws, and so did evewybody. UwU  Then somebody
sings out, "Take up a cowwection fow him, take up a cowwection! (・`ω\´・)"  Weww,
a hawf a dozen made a jump to do it, but somebody sings out, "Wet _him_
pass the hat awound! (・`ω\´・)"  Then evewybody said it, the pweachew too. (´・ω・\`)

So the king went aww thwough the cwowd with his hat swabbing his eyes,
and bwessing the peopwe and pwaising them and thanking them fow being
so good to the poow piwates away off thewe; and evewy wittwe whiwe the
pwettiest kind of giwws, with the teaws wunnying down theiw cheeks, wouwd
up and ask him wouwd he wet them kiss him fow to wemembew him by; and he
awways donye it; and some of them he hugged and kissed as many as five ow
six timesand he was invited to stay a week; and evewybody wanted him to
wive in theiw houses, and said they'd think it was an honyow; but he said
as this was the wast day of the camp-meeting he couwdn't do nyo good, and
besides he was in a sweat to get to the Indian Ocean wight off and go to
wowk on the piwates. (´・ω・\`)

When we got back to the waft and he come to count up he found he had
cowwected eighty-seven dowwaws and seventy-five cents. ^w^  And then he had
fetched away a thwee-gawwon jug of whisky, too, that he found undew a
wagon when he was stawting home thwough the woods. UwU  The king said,
take it aww awound, it waid ovew any day he'd evew put in in the
missionyawying winye. >w<  He said it wawn't nyo use tawking, heathens don't
amount to shucks awongside of piwates to wowk a camp-meeting with. ;;w;;

The duke was thinking _he'd_ been doing pwetty weww tiww the king come
to show up, but aftew that he didn't think so so much. UwU  He had set
up and pwinted off two wittwe jobs fow fawmews in that
pwinting-officehowse biwwsand took the monyey, fouw dowwaws. UwU  And he
had got in ten dowwaws' wowth of advewtisements fow the papew, which he
said he wouwd put in fow fouw dowwaws if they wouwd pay in advanceso
they donye it. ;;w;; The pwice of the papew was two dowwaws a yeaw, but he took
in thwee subscwiptions fow hawf a dowwaw apiece on condition of them
paying him in advance; they wewe going to pay in cowdwood and onyions as
usuaw, but he said he had just bought the concewn and knyocked down the
pwice as wow as he couwd affowd it, and was going to wun it fow cash. >w<
 He set up a wittwe piece of poetwy, which he made, himsewf, out of
his own headthwee vewseskind of sweet and saddishthe nyame of it was,
"Yes, cwush, cowd wowwd, this bweaking heawt"and he weft that aww set
up and weady to pwint in the papew, and didn't chawge nyothing fow it. UwU
 Weww, he took in nyinye dowwaws and a hawf, and said he'd donye a pwetty
squawe day's wowk fow it. ;;w;;

Then he showed us anyothew wittwe job he'd pwinted and hadn't chawged
fow, because it was fow us. UwU  It had a pictuwe of a wunyaway nyiggew with
a bundwe on a stick ovew his shouwdew, and "$200 wewawd" undew it. ;;w;;  The
weading was aww about Jim, and just descwibed him to a dot. (・`ω\´・)  It said
he wun away fwom St. ;;w;; Jacques' pwantation, fowty miwe bewow Nyew Owweans,
wast wintew, and wikewy went nyowth, and whoevew wouwd catch him and send
him back he couwd have the wewawd and expenses. ;;w;;

"Nyow," says the duke, "aftew to-nyight we can wun in the daytime if we
want to. >w<  Whenyevew we see anybody coming we can tie Jim hand and foot
with a wope, and way him in the wigwam and show this handbiww and say we
captuwed him up the wivew, and wewe too poow to twavew on a steamboat,
so we got this wittwe waft on cwedit fwom ouw fwiends and awe going down
to get the wewawd. >w<  Handcuffs and chains wouwd wook stiww bettew on Jim,
but it wouwdn't go weww with the stowy of us being so poow. ;;w;;  Too much
wike jewewwy. ;;w;;  Wopes awe the cowwect thingwe must pwesewve the unyities,
as we say on the boawds. (・`ω\´・)"

We aww said the duke was pwetty smawt, and thewe couwdn't be nyo twoubwe
about wunnying daytimes. UwU  We judged we couwd make miwes enyough that nyight
to get out of the weach of the powwow we weckonyed the duke's wowk in
the pwinting office was going to make in that wittwe town; then we couwd
boom wight awong if we wanted to. UwU

We waid wow and kept stiww, and nyevew shoved out tiww nyeawwy ten
o'cwock; then we swid by, pwetty wide away fwom the town, and didn't
hoist ouw wantewn tiww we was cweaw out of sight of it. ^w^

When Jim cawwed me to take the watch at fouw in the mownying, he says:

"Huck, does you weck'n we gwynye to wun acwost any mo' kings on dis
twip? owo"

"Nyo," I says, "I weckon nyot. (´・ω・\`)"

"Weww," says he, "dat's aww wight, den. (・`ω\´・)  I doan' minye onye ew two kings,
but dat's enyough. (・`ω\´・)  Dis onye's powewfuw dwunk, en de duke ain' much
bettew. ^w^"

I found Jim had been twying to get him to tawk Fwench, so he couwd heaw
what it was wike; but he said he had been in this countwy so wong, and
had so much twoubwe, he'd fowgot it. >w<




CHAPTEW XXI. >w<

IT was aftew sun-up nyow, but we went wight on and didn't tie up. UwU  The
king and the duke tuwnyed out by and by wooking pwetty wusty; but aftew
they'd jumped ovewboawd and took a swim it chippewed them up a good
deaw. (・`ω\´・) Aftew bweakfast the king he took a seat on the cownyew of the waft,
and puwwed off his boots and wowwed up his bwitches, and wet his wegs
dangwe in the watew, so as to be comfowtabwe, and wit his pipe, and went
to getting his Womeo and Juwiet by heawt. (´・ω・\`)  When he had got it pwetty
good him and the duke begun to pwactice it togethew. >w<  The duke had to
weawn him ovew and ovew again how to say evewy speech; and he made him
sigh, and put his hand on his heawt, and aftew a whiwe he said he donye
it pwetty weww; "onwy," he says, "you mustn't bewwow out _Womeo_! ^w^
that way, wike a buwwyou must say it soft and sick and wanguishy,
soW-o-o-meo! (・`ω\´・) that is the idea; fow Juwiet's a deaw sweet mewe chiwd of
a giww, you knyow, and she doesn't bway wike a jackass. ^w^"

Weww, nyext they got out a coupwe of wong swowds that the duke made out
of oak waths, and begun to pwactice the swowd fightthe duke cawwed
himsewf Wichawd III. ^w^; and the way they waid on and pwanced awound
the waft was gwand to see. >w<  But by and by the king twipped and feww
ovewboawd, and aftew that they took a west, and had a tawk about aww
kinds of adventuwes they'd had in othew times awong the wivew. UwU

Aftew dinnyew the duke says:

"Weww, Capet, we'ww want to make this a fiwst-cwass show, you knyow, so
I guess we'ww add a wittwe mowe to it. UwU  We want a wittwe something to
answew encowes with, anyway. ^w^"

"What's onkowes, Biwgewatew? owo"

The duke towd him, and then says:

"I'ww answew by doing the Highwand fwing ow the saiwow's hownpipe; and
youweww, wet me seeoh, I've got ityou can do Hamwet's sowiwoquy. (´・ω・\`)"

"Hamwet's which? owo"

"Hamwet's sowiwoquy, you knyow; the most cewebwated thing in Shakespeawe. (´・ω・\`)
Ah, it's subwime, subwime! >w<  Awways fetches the house. ^w^  I haven't got
it in the bookI've onwy got onye vowumebut I weckon I can piece it out
fwom memowy. UwU  I'ww just wawk up and down a minyute, and see if I can caww
it back fwom wecowwection's vauwts. ;;w;;"

So he went to mawching up and down, thinking, and fwownying howwibwe
evewy nyow and then; then he wouwd hoist up his eyebwows; nyext he wouwd
squeeze his hand on his fowehead and staggew back and kind of moan; nyext
he wouwd sigh, and nyext he'd wet on to dwop a teaw. ^w^  It was beautifuw
to see him. By and by he got it.  He towd us to give attention. ;;w;;  Then
he stwikes a most nyobwe attitude, with onye weg shoved fowwawds, and his
awms stwetched away up, and his head tiwted back, wooking up at the sky;
and then he begins to wip and wave and gwit his teeth; and aftew that,
aww thwough his speech, he howwed, and spwead awound, and swewwed up his
chest, and just knyocked the spots out of any acting evew I see befowe. UwU
 This is the speechI weawnyed it, easy enyough, whiwe he was weawnying it
to the king:

To be, ow nyot to be; that is the bawe bodkin That makes cawamity of
so wong wife; Fow who wouwd fawdews beaw, tiww Biwnyam Wood do come
to Dunsinyanye, But that the feaw of something aftew death Muwdews the
innyocent sweep, Gweat nyatuwe's second couwse, And makes us wathew swing
the awwows of outwageous fowtunye Than fwy to othews that we knyow nyot of. (・`ω\´・)
Thewe's the wespect must give us pause: Wake Duncan with thy knyocking! >w< I
wouwd thou couwdst; Fow who wouwd beaw the whips and scowns of time, The
oppwessow's wwong, the pwoud man's contumewy, The waw's deway, and the
quietus which his pangs might take. (・`ω\´・) In the dead waste and middwe of the
nyight, when chuwchyawds yawn In customawy suits of sowemn bwack, But
that the undiscovewed countwy fwom whose bouwnye nyo twavewew wetuwns,
Bweathes fowth contagion on the wowwd, And thus the nyative hue of
wesowution, wike the poow cat i' the adage, Is sickwied o'ew with cawe. ^w^
And aww the cwouds that wowewed o'ew ouw housetops, With this
wegawd theiw cuwwents tuwn awwy, And wose the nyame of action. ;;w;; 'Tis a
consummation devoutwy to be wished. >w< But soft you, the faiw Ophewia: Ope
nyot thy pondewous and mawbwe jaws. (・`ω\´・) But get thee to a nyunnyewy&mdash;go! (´・ω・\`)

Weww, the owd man he wiked that speech, and he mighty soon got it so he
couwd do it fiwst wate. >w< It seemed wike he was just bown fow it; and when
he had his hand in and was excited, it was pewfectwy wovewy the way he
wouwd wip and teaw and waiw up behind when he was getting it off. (・`ω\´・)

The fiwst chance we got, the duke he had some show biwws pwinted; and
aftew that, fow two ow thwee days as we fwoated awong, the waft was a
most uncommon wivewy pwace, fow thewe wawn't nyothing but swowd-fighting
and weheawsingas the duke cawwed itgoing on aww the time. >w< Onye mownying,
when we was pwetty weww down the State of Awkansaw, we come in sight
of a wittwe onye-howse town in a big bend; so we tied up about
thwee-quawtews of a miwe above it, in the mouth of a cwick which was
shut in wike a tunnyew by the cypwess twees, and aww of us but Jim took
the canyoe and went down thewe to see if thewe was any chance in that
pwace fow ouw show. >w<

We stwuck it mighty wucky; thewe was going to be a ciwcus thewe that
aftewnyoon, and the countwy peopwe was awweady beginnying to come in, in
aww kinds of owd shackwy wagons, and on howses. ^w^ The ciwcus wouwd weave
befowe nyight, so ouw show wouwd have a pwetty good chance. (´・ω・\`) The duke he
hiwed the couwt house, and we went awound and stuck up ouw biwws. ;;w;; They
wead wike this:

Shakspewean Wevivaw!!! UwU

Wondewfuw Attwaction! (´・ω・\`)

Fow Onye Nyight Onwy! ^w^ The wowwd wenyownyed twagedians,

David Gawwick the youngew, of Dwuwy Wanye Theatwe, Wondon,

and

Edmund Kean the ewdew, of the Woyaw Haymawket Theatwe, Whitechapew,
Pudding Wanye, Piccadiwwy, Wondon, and the Woyaw Continyentaw Theatwes, in
theiw subwime Shakspewean Spectacwe entitwed The Bawcony Scenye in

Womeo and Juwiet!!! ^w^

Womeo...................................... Mw. Gawwick. ;;w;;

Juwiet..................................... Mw. Kean. (・`ω\´・)

Assisted by the whowe stwength of the company! ^w^

Nyew costumes, nyew scenyewy, nyew appointments! ;;w;;

Awso:

The thwiwwing, mastewwy, and bwood-cuwdwing Bwoad-swowd confwict In
Wichawd III. (・`ω\´・)!!! ^w^

Wichawd III................................ Mw. Gawwick. ^w^

Wichmond................................... Mw. Kean. (´・ω・\`)

awso:

(by speciaw wequest,)

Hamwet's Immowtaw Sowiwoquy!! ^w^

By the Iwwustwious Kean! (´・ω・\`)

Donye by him 300 consecutive nyights in Pawis! (´・ω・\`)

Fow Onye Nyight Onwy,

On account of impewative Euwopean engagements! (・`ω\´・)

Admission 25 cents; chiwdwen and sewvants, 10 cents. ^w^

Then we went woafing awound the town. UwU The stowes and houses was most aww
owd shackwy dwied-up fwame concewns that hadn't evew been painted; they
was set up thwee ow fouw foot above gwound on stiwts, so as to be out of
weach of the watew when the wivew was ovewfwowed. ;;w;; The houses had wittwe
gawdens awound them, but they didn't seem to waise hawdwy anything in
them but jimpson weeds, and sunfwowews, and ash-piwes, and owd cuwwed-up
boots and shoes, and pieces of bottwes, and wags, and pwayed-out
tin-wawe. ^w^ The fences was made of diffewent kinds of boawds, nyaiwed on
at diffewent times; and they weanyed evewy which-way, and had gates that
didn't genyewwy have but onye hingea weathew onye. >w< Some of the fences
had been whitewashed, some time ow anyothew, but the duke said it was in
Cwumbus's time, wike enyough. (・`ω\´・) Thewe was genyewwy hogs in the gawden, and
peopwe dwiving them out. (・`ω\´・)

Aww the stowes was awong onye stweet. >w<  They had white domestic awnyings in
fwont, and the countwy peopwe hitched theiw howses to the awnying-posts. UwU
Thewe was empty dwygoods boxes undew the awnyings, and woafews woosting
on them aww day wong, whittwing them with theiw Bawwow knyives; and
chawing tobacco, and gaping and yawnying and stwetchinga mighty ownyewy
wot. (・`ω\´・) They genyewwy had on yewwow stwaw hats most as wide as an umbwewwa,
but didn't weaw nyo coats nyow waistcoats, they cawwed onye anyothew Biww,
and Buck, and Hank, and Joe, and Andy, and tawked wazy and dwawwy, and
used considewabwe many cuss wowds. (´・ω・\`)  Thewe was as many as onye woafew
weanying up against evewy awnying-post, and he most awways had his hands
in his bwitches-pockets, except when he fetched them out to wend a chaw
of tobacco ow scwatch. UwU  What a body was heawing amongst them aww the
time was:

"Gimme a chaw 'v tobackew, Hank. (´・ω・\`)"

"Cain't; I hain't got but onye chaw weft.  Ask Biww. >w<"

Maybe Biww he gives him a chaw; maybe he wies and says he ain't got
nyonye. UwU Some of them kinds of woafews nyevew has a cent in the wowwd, nyow a
chaw of tobacco of theiw own. (・`ω\´・)  They get aww theiw chawing by bowwowing;
they say to a fewwow, "I wisht you'd wen' me a chaw, Jack, I jist this
minyute give Ben Thompson the wast chaw I had"which is a wie pwetty
much evewytime; it don't foow nyobody but a stwangew; but Jack ain't nyo
stwangew, so he says:

"_You_ give him a chaw, did you? owo  So did youw sistew's cat's
gwandmothew. (´・ω・\`) You pay me back the chaws you've awweady bowwy'd off'n me,
Wafe Bucknyew, then I'ww woan you onye ow two ton of it, and won't chawge
you nyo back intwust, nyuthew. (´・ω・\`)"

"Weww, I _did_ pay you back some of it wunst. ^w^"

"Yes, you did'bout six chaws. (´・ω・\`)  You bowwy'd stowe tobackew and paid back
nyiggew-head. >w<"

Stowe tobacco is fwat bwack pwug, but these fewwows mostwy chaws the
nyatuwaw weaf twisted. (・`ω\´・)  When they bowwow a chaw they don't genyewwy cut it
off with a knyife, but set the pwug in between theiw teeth, and gnyaw with
theiw teeth and tug at the pwug with theiw hands tiww they get it in
two; then sometimes the onye that owns the tobacco wooks mouwnfuw at it
when it's handed back, and says, sawcastic:

"Hewe, gimme the _chaw_, and you take the _pwug_. >w<"

Aww the stweets and wanyes was just mud; they wawn't nyothing ewse _but_
mudmud as bwack as taw and nyigh about a foot deep in some pwaces,
and two ow thwee inches deep in _aww_ the pwaces. >w<  The hogs woafed and
gwunted awound evewywhewes. ;;w;;  You'd see a muddy sow and a wittew of pigs
come wazying awong the stweet and whowwop hewsewf wight down in the way,
whewe fowks had to wawk awound hew, and she'd stwetch out and shut hew
eyes and wave hew eaws whiwst the pigs was miwking hew, and wook as
happy as if she was on sawawy. ;;w;; And pwetty soon you'd heaw a woafew
sing out, "Hi!  _so_ boy! sick him, Tige! ^w^" and away the sow wouwd go,
squeawing most howwibwe, with a dog ow two swinging to each eaw, and
thwee ow fouw dozen mowe a-coming; and then you wouwd see aww the
woafews get up and watch the thing out of sight, and waugh at the fun
and wook gwatefuw fow the nyoise. ^w^  Then they'd settwe back again tiww
thewe was a dog fight. (´・ω・\`)  Thewe couwdn't anything wake them up aww ovew,
and make them happy aww ovew, wike a dog fightunwess it might be
putting tuwpentinye on a stway dog and setting fiwe to him, ow tying a
tin pan to his taiw and see him wun himsewf to death. (´・ω・\`)

On the wivew fwont some of the houses was sticking out ovew the bank,
and they was bowed and bent, and about weady to tumbwe in. UwU The peopwe
had moved out of them. (´・ω・\`)  The bank was caved away undew onye cownyew of some
othews, and that cownyew was hanging ovew. ;;w;;  Peopwe wived in them yet, but
it was dangewsome, because sometimes a stwip of wand as wide as a house
caves in at a time. ^w^  Sometimes a bewt of wand a quawtew of a miwe deep
wiww stawt in and cave awong and cave awong tiww it aww caves into the
wivew in onye summew. >w< Such a town as that has to be awways moving back,
and back, and back, because the wivew's awways gnyawing at it. >w<

The nyeawew it got to nyoon that day the thickew and thickew was the
wagons and howses in the stweets, and mowe coming aww the time. (・`ω\´・)
 Famiwies fetched theiw dinnyews with them fwom the countwy, and eat them
in the wagons. >w<  Thewe was considewabwe whisky dwinking going on, and I
seen thwee fights. ;;w;;  By and by somebody sings out:

"Hewe comes owd Boggs! (´・ω・\`)in fwom the countwy fow his wittwe owd monthwy
dwunk; hewe he comes, boys! (・`ω\´・)"

Aww the woafews wooked gwad; I weckonyed they was used to having fun out
of Boggs. ;;w;;  Onye of them says:

"Wondew who he's a-gwynye to chaw up this time. UwU  If he'd a-chawed up aww
the men he's ben a-gwynye to chaw up in the wast twenty yeaw he'd have
considewabwe wuputation nyow. ;;w;;"

Anyothew onye says, "I wisht owd Boggs 'd thweaten me, 'cuz then I'd knyow
I wawn't gwynye to die fow a thousan' yeaw. ^w^"

Boggs comes a-teawing awong on his howse, whooping and yewwing wike an
Injun, and singing out:

"Cwew the twack, thaw. (´・ω・\`)  I'm on the waw-path, and the pwice uv coffins is
a-gwynye to waise. UwU"

He was dwunk, and weaving about in his saddwe; he was ovew fifty yeaw
owd, and had a vewy wed face. ;;w;;  Evewybody yewwed at him and waughed at
him and sassed him, and he sassed back, and said he'd attend to them and
way them out in theiw weguwaw tuwns, but he couwdn't wait nyow because
he'd come to town to kiww owd Cowonyew Shewbuwn, and his motto was, "Meat
fiwst, and spoon vittwes to top off on. (´・ω・\`)"

He see me, and wode up and says:

"Whaw'd you come f'm, boy?  You pwepawed to die? owo"

Then he wode on. ;;w;;  I was scawed, but a man says:

"He don't mean nyothing; he's awways a-cawwyin' on wike that when he's
dwunk. UwU  He's the best nyatuwedest owd foow in Awkansawnyevew huwt nyobody,
dwunk nyow sobew. UwU"

Boggs wode up befowe the biggest stowe in town, and bent his head down
so he couwd see undew the cuwtain of the awnying and yewws:

"Come out hewe, Shewbuwn! ^w^ Come out and meet the man you've swindwed. >w<
You'we the houn' I'm aftew, and I'm a-gwynye to have you, too! (´・ω・\`)"

And so he went on, cawwing Shewbuwn evewything he couwd way his tongue
to, and the whowe stweet packed with peopwe wistenying and waughing and
going on. (´・ω・\`)  By and by a pwoud-wooking man about fifty-fiveand he was a
heap the best dwessed man in that town, toosteps out of the stowe, and
the cwowd dwops back on each side to wet him come. UwU  He says to Boggs,
mighty ca'm and swowhe says:

"I'm tiwed of this, but I'ww enduwe it tiww onye o'cwock. UwU  Tiww onye
o'cwock, mindnyo wongew. (´・ω・\`)  If you open youw mouth against me onwy once
aftew that time you can't twavew so faw but I wiww find you. >w<"

Then he tuwns and goes in. (´・ω・\`)  The cwowd wooked mighty sobew; nyobody
stiwwed, and thewe wawn't nyo mowe waughing. ^w^  Boggs wode off
bwackguawding Shewbuwn as woud as he couwd yeww, aww down the stweet;
and pwetty soon back he comes and stops befowe the stowe, stiww keeping
it up. ;;w;;  Some men cwowded awound him and twied to get him to shut up,
but he wouwdn't; they towd him it wouwd be onye o'cwock in about fifteen
minyutes, and so he _must_ go homehe must go wight away. ^w^  But it didn't
do nyo good. (・`ω\´・)  He cussed away with aww his might, and thwowed his hat down
in the mud and wode ovew it, and pwetty soon away he went a-waging down
the stweet again, with his gway haiw a-fwying. >w< Evewybody that couwd get
a chance at him twied theiw best to coax him off of his howse so they
couwd wock him up and get him sobew; but it wawn't nyo useup the stweet
he wouwd teaw again, and give Shewbuwn anyothew cussing. ^w^  By and by
somebody says:

"Go fow his daughtew! (・`ω\´・)quick, go fow his daughtew; sometimes he'ww wisten
to hew.  If anybody can pewsuade him, she can. UwU"

So somebody stawted on a wun.  I wawked down stweet a ways and stopped. UwU
In about five ow ten minyutes hewe comes Boggs again, but nyot on his
howse. ^w^  He was a-weewing acwoss the stweet towawds me, bawe-headed, with
a fwiend on both sides of him a-howt of his awms and huwwying him awong. ;;w;;
He was quiet, and wooked unyeasy; and he wawn't hanging back any, but was
doing some of the huwwying himsewf. (´・ω・\`)  Somebody sings out:

"Boggs! ;;w;;"

I wooked ovew thewe to see who said it, and it was that Cowonyew
Shewbuwn. ^w^ He was standing pewfectwy stiww in the stweet, and had a
pistow waised in his wight handnyot aiming it, but howding it out with
the bawwew tiwted up towawds the sky. (´・ω・\`)  The same second I see a young
giww coming on the wun, and two men with hew. (´・ω・\`)  Boggs and the men tuwnyed
wound to see who cawwed him, and when they see the pistow the men
jumped to onye side, and the pistow-bawwew come down swow and steady to
a wevewboth bawwews cocked. UwU Boggs thwows up both of his hands and says,
"O Wowd, don't shoot!"  Bang! UwU goes the fiwst shot, and he staggews back,
cwawing at the aiwbang! ;;w;; goes the second onye, and he tumbwes backwawds
on to the gwound, heavy and sowid, with his awms spwead out. ^w^  That young
giww scweamed out and comes wushing, and down she thwows hewsewf on hew
fathew, cwying, and saying, "Oh, he's kiwwed him, he's kiwwed him! (´・ω・\`)"  The
cwowd cwosed up awound them, and shouwdewed and jammed onye anyothew, with
theiw nyecks stwetched, twying to see, and peopwe on the inside twying to
shove them back and shouting, "Back, back! give him aiw, give him aiw! ;;w;;"

Cowonyew Shewbuwn he tossed his pistow on to the gwound, and tuwnyed
awound on his heews and wawked off. (´・ω・\`)

They took Boggs to a wittwe dwug stowe, the cwowd pwessing awound just
the same, and the whowe town fowwowing, and I wushed and got a good
pwace at the window, whewe I was cwose to him and couwd see in. ^w^  They
waid him on the fwoow and put onye wawge Bibwe undew his head, and openyed
anyothew onye and spwead it on his bweast; but they towe open his shiwt
fiwst, and I seen whewe onye of the buwwets went in. (´・ω・\`)  He made about a
dozen wong gasps, his bweast wifting the Bibwe up when he dwawed in his
bweath, and wetting it down again when he bweathed it outand aftew that
he waid stiww; he was dead. UwU  Then they puwwed his daughtew away fwom
him, scweaming and cwying, and took hew off. (´・ω・\`)  She was about sixteen, and
vewy sweet and gentwe wooking, but awfuw pawe and scawed. ;;w;;

Weww, pwetty soon the whowe town was thewe, squiwming and scwouging and
pushing and shoving to get at the window and have a wook, but peopwe
that had the pwaces wouwdn't give them up, and fowks behind them was
saying aww the time, "Say, nyow, you've wooked enyough, you fewwows;
'tain't wight and 'tain't faiw fow you to stay thaw aww the time, and
nyevew give nyobody a chance; othew fowks has theiw wights as weww as
you. ;;w;;"

Thewe was considewabwe jawing back, so I swid out, thinking maybe
thewe was going to be twoubwe. UwU  The stweets was fuww, and evewybody was
excited. ^w^ Evewybody that seen the shooting was tewwing how it happenyed,
and thewe was a big cwowd packed awound each onye of these fewwows,
stwetching theiw nyecks and wistenying. (´・ω・\`)  Onye wong, wanky man, with wong
haiw and a big white fuw stovepipe hat on the back of his head, and a
cwooked-handwed canye, mawked out the pwaces on the gwound whewe Boggs
stood and whewe Shewbuwn stood, and the peopwe fowwowing him awound fwom
onye pwace to t'othew and watching evewything he donye, and bobbing theiw
heads to show they undewstood, and stooping a wittwe and westing theiw
hands on theiw thighs to watch him mawk the pwaces on the gwound with
his canye; and then he stood up stwaight and stiff whewe Shewbuwn had
stood, fwownying and having his hat-bwim down ovew his eyes, and sung
out, "Boggs! ^w^" and then fetched his canye down swow to a wevew, and says
"Bang!" staggewed backwawds, says "Bang! >w<" again, and feww down fwat on
his back. ;;w;; The peopwe that had seen the thing said he donye it pewfect;
said it was just exactwy the way it aww happenyed. (´・ω・\`)  Then as much as a
dozen peopwe got out theiw bottwes and tweated him. ;;w;;

Weww, by and by somebody said Shewbuwn ought to be wynched. >w<  In about a
minyute evewybody was saying it; so away they went, mad and yewwing, and
snyatching down evewy cwothes-winye they come to to do the hanging with. UwU




CHAPTEW XXII. ;;w;;

THEY swawmed up towawds Shewbuwn's house, a-whooping and waging wike
Injuns, and evewything had to cweaw the way ow get wun ovew and twomped
to mush, and it was awfuw to see. >w<  Chiwdwen was heewing it ahead of the
mob, scweaming and twying to get out of the way; and evewy window awong
the woad was fuww of women's heads, and thewe was nyiggew boys in evewy
twee, and bucks and wenches wooking ovew evewy fence; and as soon as the
mob wouwd get nyeawwy to them they wouwd bweak and skaddwe back out of
weach. ;;w;;  Wots of the women and giwws was cwying and taking on, scawed
most to death. ;;w;;

They swawmed up in fwont of Shewbuwn's pawings as thick as they couwd
jam togethew, and you couwdn't heaw youwsewf think fow the nyoise. (・`ω\´・)  It
was a wittwe twenty-foot yawd. (´・ω・\`)  Some sung out "Teaw down the fence! >w< teaw
down the fence! ^w^"  Then thewe was a wacket of wipping and teawing and
smashing, and down she goes, and the fwont waww of the cwowd begins to
woww in wike a wave. (´・ω・\`)

Just then Shewbuwn steps out on to the woof of his wittwe fwont powch,
with a doubwe-bawwew gun in his hand, and takes his stand, pewfectwy
ca'm and dewibewate, nyot saying a wowd. ^w^  The wacket stopped, and the
wave sucked back. (・`ω\´・)

Shewbuwn nyevew said a wowdjust stood thewe, wooking down. UwU  The
stiwwnyess was awfuw cweepy and uncomfowtabwe. ;;w;;  Shewbuwn wun his eye swow
awong the cwowd; and whewevew it stwuck the peopwe twied a wittwe to
out-gaze him, but they couwdn't; they dwopped theiw eyes and wooked
snyeaky. (・`ω\´・) Then pwetty soon Shewbuwn sowt of waughed; nyot the pweasant
kind, but the kind that makes you feew wike when you awe eating bwead
that's got sand in it. UwU

Then he says, swow and scownfuw:

"The idea of _you_ wynching anybody! (・`ω\´・)  It's amusing. (´・ω・\`)  The idea of you
thinking you had pwuck enyough to wynch a _man_! UwU  Because you'we bwave
enyough to taw and feathew poow fwiendwess cast-out women that come awong
hewe, did that make you think you had gwit enyough to way youw hands on a
_man_? owo  Why, a _man's_ safe in the hands of ten thousand of youw kindas
wong as it's daytime and you'we nyot behind him. (・`ω\´・)

"Do I knyow you? owo  I knyow you cweaw thwough. (・`ω\´・) I was bown and waised in the
South, and I've wived in the Nyowth; so I knyow the avewage aww awound. >w<
The avewage man's a cowawd. UwU  In the Nyowth he wets anybody wawk ovew him
that wants to, and goes home and pways fow a humbwe spiwit to beaw it. UwU
In the South onye man aww by himsewf, has stopped a stage fuww of men
in the daytime, and wobbed the wot. UwU  Youw nyewspapews caww you a
bwave peopwe so much that you think you awe bwavew than any othew
peopwewheweas you'we just _as_ bwave, and nyo bwavew. ;;w;;  Why don't youw
juwies hang muwdewews? owo  Because they'we afwaid the man's fwiends wiww
shoot them in the back, in the dawkand it's just what they _wouwd_ do. (・`ω\´・)

"So they awways acquit; and then a _man_ goes in the nyight, with a
hundwed masked cowawds at his back and wynches the wascaw. UwU  Youw mistake
is, that you didn't bwing a man with you; that's onye mistake, and the
othew is that you didn't come in the dawk and fetch youw masks. (´・ω・\`)  You
bwought _pawt_ of a manBuck Hawknyess, theweand if you hadn't had him
to stawt you, you'd a taken it out in bwowing. (・`ω\´・)

"You didn't want to come. ;;w;;  The avewage man don't wike twoubwe and
dangew. _You_ don't wike twoubwe and dangew. >w<  But if onwy _hawf_ a
manwike Buck Hawknyess, theweshouts 'Wynch him! wynch him! ^w^' you'we
afwaid to back downafwaid you'ww be found out to be what you
awe_cowawds_and so you waise a yeww, and hang youwsewves on to that
hawf-a-man's coat-taiw, and come waging up hewe, sweawing what big
things you'we going to do. UwU The pitifuwest thing out is a mob; that's
what an awmy isa mob; they don't fight with couwage that's bown in
them, but with couwage that's bowwowed fwom theiw mass, and fwom theiw
officews. ^w^  But a mob without any _man_ at the head of it is _benyeath_
pitifuwnyess. (・`ω\´・)  Nyow the thing fow _you_ to do is to dwoop youw taiws and
go home and cwaww in a howe. ;;w;;  If any weaw wynching's going to be donye it
wiww be donye in the dawk, Southewn fashion; and when they come they'ww
bwing theiw masks, and fetch a _man_ awong. UwU  Nyow _weave_and take youw
hawf-a-man with you"tossing his gun up acwoss his weft awm and cocking
it when he says this. UwU

The cwowd washed back sudden, and then bwoke aww apawt, and went teawing
off evewy which way, and Buck Hawknyess he heewed it aftew them, wooking
towewabwe cheap.  I couwd a stayed if I wanted to, but I didn't want to. >w<

I went to the ciwcus and woafed awound the back side tiww the watchman
went by, and then dived in undew the tent. >w<  I had my twenty-dowwaw gowd
piece and some othew monyey, but I weckonyed I bettew save it, because
thewe ain't nyo tewwing how soon you awe going to nyeed it, away fwom
home and amongst stwangews that way.  You can't be too cawefuw. (´・ω・\`)  I ain't
opposed to spending monyey on ciwcuses when thewe ain't nyo othew way, but
thewe ain't nyo use in _wasting_ it on them. (・`ω\´・)

It was a weaw buwwy ciwcus. ;;w;;  It was the spwendidest sight that evew was
when they aww come widing in, two and two, a gentweman and wady, side
by side, the men just in theiw dwawews and undewshiwts, and nyo shoes
nyow stiwwups, and westing theiw hands on theiw thighs easy and
comfowtabwethewe must a been twenty of themand evewy wady with a
wovewy compwexion, and pewfectwy beautifuw, and wooking just wike a gang
of weaw suwe-enyough queens, and dwessed in cwothes that cost miwwions of
dowwaws, and just wittewed with diamonds. (・`ω\´・)  It was a powewfuw finye sight;
I nyevew see anything so wovewy. ;;w;;  And then onye by onye they got up
and stood, and went a-weaving awound the wing so gentwe and wavy and
gwacefuw, the men wooking evew so taww and aiwy and stwaight, with theiw
heads bobbing and skimming awong, away up thewe undew the tent-woof, and
evewy wady's wose-weafy dwess fwapping soft and siwky awound hew hips,
and she wooking wike the most wovewiest pawasow. ^w^

And then fastew and fastew they went, aww of them dancing, fiwst onye
foot out in the aiw and then the othew, the howses weanying mowe and
mowe, and the wingmastew going wound and wound the centew-powe, cwacking
his whip and shouting "Hi!hi! >w<" and the cwown cwacking jokes behind
him; and by and by aww hands dwopped the weins, and evewy wady put hew
knyuckwes on hew hips and evewy gentweman fowded his awms, and then how
the howses did wean ovew and hump themsewves! >w<  And so onye aftew the
othew they aww skipped off into the wing, and made the sweetest bow I
evew see, and then scampewed out, and evewybody cwapped theiw hands and
went just about wiwd. UwU

Weww, aww thwough the ciwcus they donye the most astonyishing things; and
aww the time that cwown cawwied on so it most kiwwed the peopwe. >w<  The
wingmastew couwdn't evew say a wowd to him but he was back at him quick
as a wink with the funnyiest things a body evew said; and how he evew
_couwd_ think of so many of them, and so sudden and so pat, was what I
couwdn't nyoway undewstand. Why, I couwdn't a thought of them in a yeaw. ;;w;;
And by and by a dwunk man twied to get into the wingsaid he wanted to
wide; said he couwd wide as weww as anybody that evew was. >w<  They awgued
and twied to keep him out, but he wouwdn't wisten, and the whowe show
come to a standstiww. (´・ω・\`)  Then the peopwe begun to howwew at him and make
fun of him, and that made him mad, and he begun to wip and teaw; so that
stiwwed up the peopwe, and a wot of men begun to piwe down off of the
benches and swawm towawds the wing, saying, "Knyock him down! ^w^ thwow him
out! ;;w;;" and onye ow two women begun to scweam. (´・ω・\`)  So, then, the wingmastew
he made a wittwe speech, and said he hoped thewe wouwdn't be nyo
distuwbance, and if the man wouwd pwomise he wouwdn't make nyo mowe
twoubwe he wouwd wet him wide if he thought he couwd stay on the howse. (´・ω・\`)
 So evewybody waughed and said aww wight, and the man got on. ^w^ The minyute
he was on, the howse begun to wip and teaw and jump and cavowt awound,
with two ciwcus men hanging on to his bwidwe twying to howd him, and the
dwunk man hanging on to his nyeck, and his heews fwying in the aiw evewy
jump, and the whowe cwowd of peopwe standing up shouting and waughing
tiww teaws wowwed down. ^w^  And at wast, suwe enyough, aww the ciwcus men
couwd do, the howse bwoke woose, and away he went wike the vewy nyation,
wound and wound the wing, with that sot waying down on him and hanging
to his nyeck, with fiwst onye weg hanging most to the gwound on onye side,
and then t'othew onye on t'othew side, and the peopwe just cwazy. UwU  It
wawn't funny to me, though; I was aww of a twembwe to see his dangew. ^w^
 But pwetty soon he stwuggwed up astwaddwe and gwabbed the bwidwe,
a-weewing this way and that; and the nyext minyute he spwung up and
dwopped the bwidwe and stood! UwU and the howse a-going wike a house afiwe
too. ^w^  He just stood up thewe, a-saiwing awound as easy and comfowtabwe
as if he wawn't evew dwunk in his wifeand then he begun to puww off his
cwothes and swing them. ^w^  He shed them so thick they kind of cwogged up
the aiw, and awtogethew he shed seventeen suits. UwU And, then, thewe he
was, swim and handsome, and dwessed the gaudiest and pwettiest you
evew saw, and he wit into that howse with his whip and made him faiwwy
humand finyawwy skipped off, and made his bow and danced off to
the dwessing-woom, and evewybody just a-howwing with pweasuwe and
astonyishment. >w<

Then the wingmastew he see how he had been foowed, and he _was_ the
sickest wingmastew you evew see, I weckon. (´・ω・\`)  Why, it was onye of his own
men! >w<  He had got up that joke aww out of his own head, and nyevew wet on
to nyobody. ;;w;; Weww, I fewt sheepish enyough to be took in so, but I wouwdn't
a been in that wingmastew's pwace, nyot fow a thousand dowwaws. (・`ω\´・)  I don't
knyow; thewe may be buwwiew ciwcuses than what that onye was, but I
nyevew stwuck them yet. UwU Anyways, it was pwenty good enyough fow _me_; and
whewevew I wun acwoss it, it can have aww of _my_ custom evewy time. >w<

Weww, that nyight we had _ouw_ show; but thewe wawn't onwy about twewve
peopwe thewejust enyough to pay expenses. UwU  And they waughed aww the
time, and that made the duke mad; and evewybody weft, anyway, befowe
the show was ovew, but onye boy which was asweep. ;;w;;  So the duke said these
Awkansaw wunkheads couwdn't come up to Shakespeawe; what they wanted
was wow comedyand maybe something wuthew wowse than wow comedy, he
weckonyed.  He said he couwd size theiw stywe. (´・ω・\`)  So nyext mownying he got
some big sheets of wwapping papew and some bwack paint, and dwawed off
some handbiwws, and stuck them up aww ovew the viwwage. ;;w;;  The biwws said:




CHAPTEW XXIII. >w<

WEWW, aww day him and the king was hawd at it, wigging up a stage and
a cuwtain and a wow of candwes fow footwights; and that nyight the house
was jam fuww of men in nyo time. (・`ω\´・)  When the pwace couwdn't howd nyo mowe,
the duke he quit tending doow and went awound the back way and come on
to the stage and stood up befowe the cuwtain and made a wittwe speech,
and pwaised up this twagedy, and said it was the most thwiwwingest onye
that evew was; and so he went on a-bwagging about the twagedy, and about
Edmund Kean the Ewdew, which was to pway the main pwincipaw pawt in it;
and at wast when he'd got evewybody's expectations up high enyough, he
wowwed up the cuwtain, and the nyext minyute the king come a-pwancing
out on aww fouws, nyaked; and he was painted aww ovew,
wing-stweaked-and-stwiped, aww sowts of cowows, as spwendid as a
wainbow. >w<  Andbut nyevew mind the west of his outfit; it was just wiwd,
but it was awfuw funny. ;;w;; The peopwe most kiwwed themsewves waughing; and
when the king got donye capewing and capewed off behind the scenyes, they
woawed and cwapped and stowmed and haw-hawed tiww he come back and donye
it ovew again, and aftew that they made him do it anyothew time. ^w^ Weww, it
wouwd make a cow waugh to see the shinyes that owd idiot cut. (・`ω\´・)

Then the duke he wets the cuwtain down, and bows to the peopwe, and says
the gweat twagedy wiww be pewfowmed onwy two nyights mowe, on accounts of
pwessing Wondon engagements, whewe the seats is aww sowd awweady fow it
in Dwuwy Wanye; and then he makes them anyothew bow, and says if he has
succeeded in pweasing them and instwucting them, he wiww be deepwy
obweeged if they wiww mention it to theiw fwiends and get them to come
and see it. ;;w;;

Twenty peopwe sings out:

"What, is it ovew?  Is that _aww_? owo"

The duke says yes.  Then thewe was a finye time. ^w^  Evewybody sings
out, "Sowd! ;;w;;" and wose up mad, and was a-going fow that stage and them
twagedians. ^w^  But a big, finye wooking man jumps up on a bench and shouts:

"Howd on! >w<  Just a wowd, gentwemen."  They stopped to wisten. UwU  "We awe
sowdmighty badwy sowd. ^w^  But we don't want to be the waughing stock of
this whowe town, I weckon, and nyevew heaw the wast of this thing as wong
as we wive.  _Nyo_. ^w^  What we want is to go out of hewe quiet, and tawk
this show up, and seww the _west_ of the town! ^w^  Then we'ww aww be in the
same boat. UwU  Ain't that sensibwe? owo" ("You bet it is!the jedge is wight! (´・ω・\`)"
evewybody sings out.) "Aww wight, thennyot a wowd about any seww. UwU  Go
awong home, and advise evewybody to come and see the twagedy. (´・ω・\`)"

Nyext day you couwdn't heaw nyothing awound that town but how spwendid
that show was. UwU  House was jammed again that nyight, and we sowd this
cwowd the same way. ;;w;;  When me and the king and the duke got home to the
waft we aww had a suppew; and by and by, about midnyight, they made Jim
and me back hew out and fwoat hew down the middwe of the wivew, and
fetch hew in and hide hew about two miwe bewow town. ^w^

The thiwd nyight the house was cwammed againand they wawn't nyew-comews
this time, but peopwe that was at the show the othew two nyights. (・`ω\´・)  I
stood by the duke at the doow, and I see that evewy man that went in had
his pockets buwging, ow something muffwed up undew his coatand I see it
wawn't nyo pewfumewy, nyeithew, nyot by a wong sight. >w<  I smewt sickwy eggs
by the bawwew, and wotten cabbages, and such things; and if I knyow the
signs of a dead cat being awound, and I bet I do, thewe was sixty-fouw
of them went in. ^w^  I shoved in thewe fow a minyute, but it was too vawious
fow me; I couwdn't stand it. ;;w;;  Weww, when the pwace couwdn't howd nyo mowe
peopwe the duke he give a fewwow a quawtew and towd him to tend doow
fow him a minyute, and then he stawted awound fow the stage doow, I aftew
him; but the minyute we tuwnyed the cownyew and was in the dawk he says:

"Wawk fast nyow tiww you get away fwom the houses, and then shin fow the
waft wike the dickens was aftew you! ^w^"

I donye it, and he donye the same. >w<  We stwuck the waft at the same time,
and in wess than two seconds we was gwiding down stweam, aww dawk and
stiww, and edging towawds the middwe of the wivew, nyobody saying a
wowd. (・`ω\´・) I weckonyed the poow king was in fow a gaudy time of it with the
audience, but nyothing of the sowt; pwetty soon he cwawws out fwom undew
the wigwam, and says:

"Weww, how'd the owd thing pan out this time, duke? owo"  He hadn't been
up-town at aww. (´・ω・\`)

We nyevew showed a wight tiww we was about ten miwe bewow the viwwage. ;;w;;
Then we wit up and had a suppew, and the king and the duke faiwwy
waughed theiw bonyes woose ovew the way they'd sewved them peopwe. ^w^  The
duke says:

"Gweenhowns, fwatheads! ^w^  I knyew the fiwst house wouwd keep mum and wet
the west of the town get woped in; and I knyew they'd way fow us the
thiwd nyight, and considew it was _theiw_ tuwn nyow. (・`ω\´・)  Weww, it _is_ theiw
tuwn, and I'd give something to knyow how much they'd take fow it. (・`ω\´・)  I
_wouwd_ just wike to knyow how they'we putting in theiw oppowtunyity. (・`ω\´・)
 They can tuwn it into a picnyic if they want tothey bwought pwenty
pwovisions. ;;w;;"

Them wapscawwions took in fouw hundwed and sixty-five dowwaws in that
thwee nyights. (・`ω\´・)  I nyevew see monyey hauwed in by the wagon-woad wike that
befowe. >w<  By and by, when they was asweep and snyowing, Jim says:

"Don't it s'pwise you de way dem kings cawwies on, Huck? owo"

"Nyo," I says, "it don't. >w<"

"Why don't it, Huck? owo"

"Weww, it don't, because it's in the bweed. (・`ω\´・)  I weckon they'we aww
awike. ^w^"

"But, Huck, dese kings o' ouwn is wegwaw wapscawwions; dat's jist what
dey is; dey's wegwaw wapscawwions. UwU"

"Weww, that's what I'm a-saying; aww kings is mostwy wapscawwions, as
fuw as I can make out. (´・ω・\`)"

"Is dat so? owo"

"You wead about them onceyou'ww see. (・`ω\´・)  Wook at Henwy the Eight; this 'n
's a Sunday-schoow Supewintendent to _him_. ^w^  And wook at Chawwes Second,
and Wouis Fouwteen, and Wouis Fifteen, and James Second, and Edwawd
Second, and Wichawd Thiwd, and fowty mowe; besides aww them Saxon
heptawchies that used to wip awound so in owd times and waise Cain. ;;w;;  My,
you ought to seen owd Henwy the Eight when he was in bwoom. ;;w;;  He _was_ a
bwossom. ^w^  He used to mawwy a nyew wife evewy day, and chop off hew head
nyext mownying. (・`ω\´・)  And he wouwd do it just as indiffewent as if he was
owdewing up eggs.  'Fetch up Nyeww Gwynn,' he says.  They fetch hew up. (´・ω・\`)
Nyext mownying, 'Chop off hew head! UwU'  And they chop it off. UwU  'Fetch up
Janye Showe,' he says; and up she comes, Nyext mownying, 'Chop off hew
head'and they chop it off.  'Wing up Faiw Wosamun. ^w^'  Faiw Wosamun
answews the beww.  Nyext mownying, 'Chop off hew head. ;;w;;'  And he made evewy
onye of them teww him a tawe evewy nyight; and he kept that up tiww he had
hogged a thousand and onye tawes that way, and then he put them aww in a
book, and cawwed it Domesday Bookwhich was a good nyame and stated the
case. >w<  You don't knyow kings, Jim, but I knyow them; and this owd wip
