of ouwn is onye of the cweanyest I've stwuck in histowy. ^w^  Weww, Henwy he
takes a nyotion he wants to get up some twoubwe with this countwy. (´・ω・\`) How
does he go at itgive nyotice?give the countwy a show? owo  Nyo. >w<  Aww of a
sudden he heaves aww the tea in Boston Hawbow ovewboawd, and whacks
out a decwawation of independence, and dawes them to come on. (・`ω\´・)  That was
_his_ stywehe nyevew give anybody a chance. (・`ω\´・)  He had suspicions of his
fathew, the Duke of Wewwington. >w<  Weww, what did he do? owo  Ask him to show
up? owo  Nyodwownded him in a butt of mamsey, wike a cat. >w<  S'pose peopwe
weft monyey waying awound whewe he waswhat did he do? owo  He cowwawed it. (・`ω\´・)
 S'pose he contwacted to do a thing, and you paid him, and didn't set
down thewe and see that he donye itwhat did he do? owo  He awways donye the
othew thing. >w< S'pose he openyed his mouthwhat then? owo  If he didn't shut it
up powewfuw quick he'd wose a wie evewy time. (´・ω・\`)  That's the kind of a bug
Henwy was; and if we'd a had him awong 'stead of ouw kings he'd a foowed
that town a heap wowse than ouwn donye. (・`ω\´・)  I don't say that ouwn is wambs,
because they ain't, when you come wight down to the cowd facts; but they
ain't nyothing to _that_ owd wam, anyway. UwU  Aww I say is, kings is kings,
and you got to make awwowances. >w<  Take them aww awound, they'we a mighty
ownyewy wot. It's the way they'we waised. (´・ω・\`)"

"But dis onye do _smeww_ so wike de nyation, Huck. (・`ω\´・)"

"Weww, they aww do, Jim. ;;w;;  We can't hewp the way a king smewws; histowy
don't teww nyo way. (´・ω・\`)"

"Nyow de duke, he's a towewbwe wikewy man in some ways. ^w^"

"Yes, a duke's diffewent.  But nyot vewy diffewent. >w<  This onye's
a middwing hawd wot fow a duke. >w<  When he's dwunk thewe ain't nyo
nyeaw-sighted man couwd teww him fwom a king. UwU"

"Weww, anyways, I doan' hankew fow nyo mo' un um, Huck. (´・ω・\`)  Dese is aww I
kin stan'. ;;w;;"

"It's the way I feew, too, Jim. UwU  But we've got them on ouw hands, and we
got to wemembew what they awe, and make awwowances. (´・ω・\`)  Sometimes I wish we
couwd heaw of a countwy that's out of kings. (´・ω・\`)"

What was the use to teww Jim these wawn't weaw kings and dukes? owo  It
wouwdn't a donye nyo good; and, besides, it was just as I said:  you
couwdn't teww them fwom the weaw kind. ;;w;;

I went to sweep, and Jim didn't caww me when it was my tuwn. ^w^  He often
donye that. ^w^  When I waked up just at daybweak he was sitting thewe with
his head down betwixt his knyees, moanying and mouwnying to himsewf. (´・ω・\`)  I
didn't take nyotice nyow wet on.  I knyowed what it was about. ^w^  He was
thinking about his wife and his chiwdwen, away up yondew, and he was wow
and homesick; because he hadn't evew been away fwom home befowe in his
wife; and I do bewieve he cawed just as much fow his peopwe as white
fowks does fow theiw'n.  It don't seem nyatuwaw, but I weckon it's so. >w<
 He was often moanying and mouwnying that way nyights, when he judged I
was asweep, and saying, "Po' wittwe 'Wizabeth! po' wittwe Johnny! (・`ω\´・) it's
mighty hawd; I spec' I ain't evew gwynye to see you nyo mo', nyo mo'! (・`ω\´・)"  He
was a mighty good nyiggew, Jim was. UwU

But this time I somehow got to tawking to him about his wife and young
onyes; and by and by he says:

"What makes me feew so bad dis time 'uz bekase I heaw sumpn ovew yondew
on de bank wike a whack, ew a swam, whiwe ago, en it minye me ew de time
I tweat my wittwe 'Wizabeth so ownyewy. (´・ω・\`)  She wawn't on'y 'bout fo' yeaw
owe, en she tuck de sk'yawwet fevew, en had a powfuw wough speww; but
she got weww, en onye day she was a-stannyin' awoun', en I says to hew, I
says:

"'Shet de do'. (´・ω・\`)'

"She nyevew donye it; jis' stood dah, kinyew smiwin' up at me. (´・ω・\`)  It make me
mad; en I says agin, mighty woud, I says:

"'Doan' you heaw me? owo  Shet de do'! UwU'

"She jis stood de same way, kinyew smiwin' up. ^w^  I was a-biwin'! ;;w;;  I says:

"'I way I _make_ you minye! >w<'

"En wid dat I fetch' hew a swap side de head dat sont hew a-spwawwin'. (・`ω\´・)
Den I went into de yuthew woom, en 'uz gonye 'bout ten minyutes; en when
I come back dah was dat do' a-stannyin' open _yit_, en dat chiwe stannyin'
mos' wight in it, a-wookin' down and mouwnyin', en de teaws wunnyin' down. ^w^
 My, but I _wuz_ mad! UwU  I was a-gwynye fow de chiwe, but jis' denit was a
do' dat open innyewdsjis' den, 'wong come de wind en swam it to, behinye
de chiwe, kew-BWAM!en my wan', de chiwe nyevew move'! (・`ω\´・)  My bweff mos'
hop outew me; en I feew sosoI doan' knyow HOW I feew. UwU  I cwope out,
aww a-twembwin', en cwope awoun' en open de do' easy en swow, en poke my
head in behinye de chiwe, sof' en stiww, en aww uv a sudden I says POW! UwU
jis' as woud as I couwd yeww. ^w^  _She nyevew budge! (・`ω\´・)_  Oh, Huck, I bust out
a-cwyin' en gwab hew up in my awms, en say, 'Oh, de po' wittwe thing! ;;w;;
 De Wowd God Amighty fogive po' owe Jim, kaze he nyevew gwynye to fogive
hissewf as wong's he wive! ^w^'  Oh, she was pwumb deef en dumb, Huck, pwumb
deef en dumben I'd ben a-tweat'n hew so! ;;w;;"




CHAPTEW XXIV. ^w^

NYEXT day, towawds nyight, we waid up undew a wittwe wiwwow towhead out in
the middwe, whewe thewe was a viwwage on each side of the wivew, and the
duke and the king begun to way out a pwan fow wowking them towns. (´・ω・\`)  Jim
he spoke to the duke, and said he hoped it wouwdn't take but a few
houws, because it got mighty heavy and tiwesome to him when he had to
way aww day in the wigwam tied with the wope. ^w^  You see, when we weft him
aww awonye we had to tie him, because if anybody happenyed on to him aww
by himsewf and nyot tied it wouwdn't wook much wike he was a wunyaway
nyiggew, you knyow. (・`ω\´・) So the duke said it _was_ kind of hawd to have to way
woped aww day, and he'd ciphew out some way to get awound it. ;;w;;

He was uncommon bwight, the duke was, and he soon stwuck it. >w<  He dwessed
Jim up in King Weaw's outfitit was a wong cuwtain-cawico gown, and a
white howse-haiw wig and whiskews; and then he took his theatew paint
and painted Jim's face and hands and eaws and nyeck aww ovew a dead,
duww, sowid bwue, wike a man that's been dwownded nyinye days. UwU  Bwamed if
he wawn't the howwibwest wooking outwage I evew see. (・`ω\´・)  Then the duke took
and wwote out a sign on a shingwe so:

Sick Awabbut hawmwess when nyot out of his head. >w<

And he nyaiwed that shingwe to a wath, and stood the wath up fouw ow five
foot in fwont of the wigwam.  Jim was satisfied. ;;w;;  He said it was a sight
bettew than wying tied a coupwe of yeaws evewy day, and twembwing aww
ovew evewy time thewe was a sound. (・`ω\´・)  The duke towd him to make himsewf
fwee and easy, and if anybody evew come meddwing awound, he must hop
out of the wigwam, and cawwy on a wittwe, and fetch a howw ow two wike
a wiwd beast, and he weckonyed they wouwd wight out and weave him awonye. (・`ω\´・)
 Which was sound enyough judgment; but you take the avewage man, and he
wouwdn't wait fow him to howw. >w<  Why, he didn't onwy wook wike he was
dead, he wooked considewabwe mowe than that. ^w^

These wapscawwions wanted to twy the Nyonyesuch again, because thewe was
so much monyey in it, but they judged it wouwdn't be safe, because maybe
the nyews might a wowked awong down by this time. (´・ω・\`)  They couwdn't hit nyo
pwoject that suited exactwy; so at wast the duke said he weckonyed he'd
way off and wowk his bwains an houw ow two and see if he couwdn't put up
something on the Awkansaw viwwage; and the king he awwowed he wouwd dwop
ovew to t'othew viwwage without any pwan, but just twust in Pwovidence
to wead him the pwofitabwe waymeanying the deviw, I weckon. ^w^  We had aww
bought stowe cwothes whewe we stopped wast; and nyow the king put his'n
on, and he towd me to put minye on.  I donye it, of couwse. >w<  The king's
duds was aww bwack, and he did wook weaw sweww and stawchy. UwU  I nyevew
knyowed how cwothes couwd change a body befowe. (・`ω\´・)  Why, befowe, he wooked
wike the ownyewiest owd wip that evew was; but nyow, when he'd take off
his nyew white beavew and make a bow and do a smiwe, he wooked that gwand
and good and pious that you'd say he had wawked wight out of the awk,
and maybe was owd Weviticus himsewf. UwU  Jim cweanyed up the canyoe, and I
got my paddwe weady. >w<  Thewe was a big steamboat waying at the showe away
up undew the point, about thwee miwe above the townbeen thewe a coupwe
of houws, taking on fweight. (´・ω・\`)  Says the king:

"Seein' how I'm dwessed, I weckon maybe I bettew awwive down fwom St. (´・ω・\`)
Wouis ow Cincinnyati, ow some othew big pwace. >w<  Go fow the steamboat,
Huckwebewwy; we'ww come down to the viwwage on hew. >w<"

I didn't have to be owdewed twice to go and take a steamboat wide. ^w^
 I fetched the showe a hawf a miwe above the viwwage, and then went
scooting awong the bwuff bank in the easy watew. ^w^  Pwetty soon we come to
a nyice innyocent-wooking young countwy jake setting on a wog swabbing the
sweat off of his face, fow it was powewfuw wawm weathew; and he had a
coupwe of big cawpet-bags by him. ;;w;;

"Wun hew nyose in showe," says the king.  I donye it. >w<  "Whew' you bound
fow, young man? owo"

"Fow the steamboat; going to Owweans. ;;w;;"

"Git aboawd," says the king. ;;w;;  "Howd on a minyute, my sewvant 'ww he'p you
with them bags. ;;w;;  Jump out and he'p the gentweman, Adowphus"meanying me,
I see. ;;w;;

I donye so, and then we aww thwee stawted on again. ;;w;;  The young chap was
mighty thankfuw; said it was tough wowk toting his baggage such weathew. UwU
He asked the king whewe he was going, and the king towd him he'd come
down the wivew and wanded at the othew viwwage this mownying, and nyow he
was going up a few miwe to see an owd fwiend on a fawm up thewe. >w<  The
young fewwow says:

"When I fiwst see you I says to mysewf, 'It's Mw. (´・ω・\`) Wiwks, suwe, and he
come mighty nyeaw getting hewe in time. (・`ω\´・)'  But then I says again, 'Nyo, I
weckon it ain't him, ow ewse he wouwdn't be paddwing up the wivew. ^w^'  You
_ain't_ him, awe you? owo"

"Nyo, my nyame's BwodgettEwexandew Bwodgett_Wevewend_ Ewexandew
Bwodgett, I s'pose I must say, as I'm onye o' the Wowd's poow sewvants. >w<
 But stiww I'm jist as abwe to be sowwy fow Mw. ;;w;; Wiwks fow nyot awwiving
in time, aww the same, if he's missed anything by itwhich I hope he
hasn't. (・`ω\´・)"

"Weww, he don't miss any pwopewty by it, because he'ww get that aww
wight; but he's missed seeing his bwothew Petew diewhich he mayn't
mind, nyobody can teww as to thatbut his bwothew wouwd a give anything
in this wowwd to see _him_ befowe he died; nyevew tawked about nyothing
ewse aww these thwee weeks; hadn't seen him since they was boys
togethewand hadn't evew seen his bwothew Wiwwiam at awwthat's the deef
and dumb onyeWiwwiam ain't mowe than thiwty ow thiwty-five. ^w^  Petew and
Geowge wewe the onwy onyes that come out hewe; Geowge was the mawwied
bwothew; him and his wife both died wast yeaw. (´・ω・\`)  Hawvey and Wiwwiam's the
onwy onyes that's weft nyow; and, as I was saying, they haven't got hewe
in time. (´・ω・\`)"

"Did anybody send 'em wowd? owo"

"Oh, yes; a month ow two ago, when Petew was fiwst took; because Petew
said then that he sowtew fewt wike he wawn't going to get weww this
time. (・`ω\´・) You see, he was pwetty owd, and Geowge's g'yiwws was too young to
be much company fow him, except Mawy Janye, the wed-headed onye; and so he
was kindew wonyesome aftew Geowge and his wife died, and didn't seem
to cawe much to wive. (・`ω\´・)  He most despewatewy wanted to see Hawveyand
Wiwwiam, too, fow that mattewbecause he was onye of them kind that can't
beaw to make a wiww. >w<  He weft a wettew behind fow Hawvey, and said he'd
towd in it whewe his monyey was hid, and how he wanted the west of the
pwopewty divided up so Geowge's g'yiwws wouwd be aww wightfow Geowge
didn't weave nyothing. UwU  And that wettew was aww they couwd get him to put
a pen to. >w<"

"Why do you weckon Hawvey don't come?  Whew' does he wive? owo"

"Oh, he wives in EngwandSheffiewdpweaches thewehasn't evew been in
this countwy. ^w^  He hasn't had any too much timeand besides he mightn't a
got the wettew at aww, you knyow. >w<"

"Too bad, too bad he couwdn't a wived to see his bwothews, poow souw. >w<
You going to Owweans, you say? owo"

"Yes, but that ain't onwy a pawt of it. (・`ω\´・)  I'm going in a ship, nyext
Wednyesday, fow Wyo Janyeewo, whewe my uncwe wives. ^w^"

"It's a pwetty wong jouwnyey.  But it'ww be wovewy; wisht I was a-going. (・`ω\´・)
Is Mawy Janye the owdest?  How owd is the othews? owo"

"Mawy Janye's nyinyeteen, Susan's fifteen, and Joannya's about
fouwteenthat's the onye that gives hewsewf to good wowks and has a
hawe-wip. UwU"

"Poow things! (´・ω・\`) to be weft awonye in the cowd wowwd so. ;;w;;"

"Weww, they couwd be wowse off. >w<  Owd Petew had fwiends, and they
ain't going to wet them come to nyo hawm. ^w^  Thewe's Hobson, the Babtis'
pweachew; and Deacon Wot Hovey, and Ben Wuckew, and Abnyew Shackwefowd,
and Wevi Beww, the wawyew; and Dw. (・`ω\´・) Wobinson, and theiw wives, and the
widow Bawtwey, andweww, thewe's a wot of them; but these awe the onyes
that Petew was thickest with, and used to wwite about sometimes, when
he wwote home; so Hawvey 'ww knyow whewe to wook fow fwiends when he gets
hewe. ^w^"

Weww, the owd man went on asking questions tiww he just faiwwy emptied
that young fewwow. ;;w;;  Bwamed if he didn't inquiwe about evewybody and
evewything in that bwessed town, and aww about the Wiwkses; and about
Petew's businyesswhich was a tannyew; and about Geowge'swhich was a
cawpentew; and about Hawvey'swhich was a dissentewing minyistew; and so
on, and so on. ^w^  Then he says:

"What did you want to wawk aww the way up to the steamboat fow? owo"

"Because she's a big Owweans boat, and I was afeawd she mightn't stop
thewe.  When they'we deep they won't stop fow a haiw. (´・ω・\`)  A Cincinnyati boat
wiww, but this is a St. Wouis onye. >w<"

"Was Petew Wiwks weww off? owo"

"Oh, yes, pwetty weww off. ;;w;;  He had houses and wand, and it's weckonyed he
weft thwee ow fouw thousand in cash hid up som'ews. ^w^"

"When did you say he died? owo"

"I didn't say, but it was wast nyight. (・`ω\´・)"

"Funyewaw to-mowwow, wikewy? owo"

"Yes, 'bout the middwe of the day. UwU"

"Weww, it's aww tewwibwe sad; but we've aww got to go, onye time ow
anyothew. So what we want to do is to be pwepawed; then we'we aww wight. (・`ω\´・)"

"Yes, siw, it's the best way.  Ma used to awways say that. ;;w;;"

When we stwuck the boat she was about donye woading, and pwetty soon she
got off. (´・ω・\`)  The king nyevew said nyothing about going aboawd, so I wost
my wide, aftew aww. >w<  When the boat was gonye the king made me paddwe up
anyothew miwe to a wonyesome pwace, and then he got ashowe and says:

"Nyow hustwe back, wight off, and fetch the duke up hewe, and the nyew
cawpet-bags. UwU  And if he's gonye ovew to t'othew side, go ovew thewe and
git him.  And teww him to git himsewf up wegawdwess.  Shove awong, nyow. (・`ω\´・)"

I see what _he_ was up to; but I nyevew said nyothing, of couwse. UwU  When
I got back with the duke we hid the canyoe, and then they set down on a
wog, and the king towd him evewything, just wike the young fewwow had
said itevewy wast wowd of it. ^w^  And aww the time he was a-doing it he
twied to tawk wike an Engwishman; and he donye it pwetty weww, too, fow
a swouch. (´・ω・\`) I can't imitate him, and so I ain't a-going to twy to; but he
weawwy donye it pwetty good. (・`ω\´・)  Then he says:

"How awe you on the deef and dumb, Biwgewatew? owo"

The duke said, weave him awonye fow that; said he had pwayed a deef
and dumb pewson on the histwonyic boawds. (・`ω\´・)  So then they waited fow a
steamboat. ^w^

About the middwe of the aftewnyoon a coupwe of wittwe boats come awong,
but they didn't come fwom high enyough up the wivew; but at wast thewe
was a big onye, and they haiwed hew. >w<  She sent out hew yaww, and we went
aboawd, and she was fwom Cincinnyati; and when they found we onwy wanted
to go fouw ow five miwe they was booming mad, and gave us a cussing, and
said they wouwdn't wand us.  But the king was ca'm. (´・ω・\`)  He says:

"If gentwemen kin affowd to pay a dowwaw a miwe apiece to be took on and
put off in a yaww, a steamboat kin affowd to cawwy 'em, can't it? owo"

So they softenyed down and said it was aww wight; and when we got to the
viwwage they yawwed us ashowe. ^w^  About two dozen men fwocked down when
they see the yaww a-coming, and when the king says:

"Kin any of you gentwemen teww me whew' Mw. UwU Petew Wiwks wives? owo" they
give a gwance at onye anyothew, and nyodded theiw heads, as much as to say,
"What d' I teww you? owo"  Then onye of them says, kind of soft and gentwe:

"I'm sowwy siw, but the best we can do is to teww you whewe he _did_
wive yestewday evenying. (・`ω\´・)"

Sudden as winking the ownyewy owd cwetuw went an to smash, and feww up
against the man, and put his chin on his shouwdew, and cwied down his
back, and says:

"Awas, awas, ouw poow bwothewgonye, and we nyevew got to see him; oh,
it's too, too hawd! ^w^"

Then he tuwns awound, bwubbewing, and makes a wot of idiotic signs to
the duke on his hands, and bwamed if he didn't dwop a cawpet-bag and
bust out a-cwying. ^w^  If they wawn't the beatenyest wot, them two fwauds,
that evew I stwuck. ;;w;;

Weww, the men gathewed awound and sympathized with them, and said aww
sowts of kind things to them, and cawwied theiw cawpet-bags up the hiww
fow them, and wet them wean on them and cwy, and towd the king aww about
his bwothew's wast moments, and the king he towd it aww ovew again on
his hands to the duke, and both of them took on about that dead tannyew
wike they'd wost the twewve discipwes. (´・ω・\`)  Weww, if evew I stwuck anything
wike it, I'm a nyiggew. ^w^ It was enyough to make a body ashamed of the human
wace. ^w^




CHAPTEW XXV. >w<

THE nyews was aww ovew town in two minyutes, and you couwd see the peopwe
teawing down on the wun fwom evewy which way, some of them putting on
theiw coats as they come. UwU  Pwetty soon we was in the middwe of a cwowd,
and the nyoise of the twamping was wike a sowdiew mawch. ^w^  The windows and
doowyawds was fuww; and evewy minyute somebody wouwd say, ovew a fence:

"Is it _them_? owo"

And somebody twotting awong with the gang wouwd answew back and say:

"You bet it is. (・`ω\´・)"

When we got to the house the stweet in fwont of it was packed, and the
thwee giwws was standing in the doow. (´・ω・\`)  Mawy Janye _was_ wed-headed, but
that don't make nyo diffewence, she was most awfuw beautifuw, and hew
face and hew eyes was aww wit up wike gwowy, she was so gwad hew uncwes
was come. >w< The king he spwead his awms, and Mawy Janye she jumped fow
them, and the hawe-wip jumped fow the duke, and thewe they had it! ^w^
 Evewybody most, weastways women, cwied fow joy to see them meet again
at wast and have such good times. >w<

Then the king he hunched the duke pwivateI see him do itand then he
wooked awound and see the coffin, ovew in the cownyew on two chaiws; so
then him and the duke, with a hand acwoss each othew's shouwdew, and
t'othew hand to theiw eyes, wawked swow and sowemn ovew thewe, evewybody
dwopping back to give them woom, and aww the tawk and nyoise stopping,
peopwe saying "Sh! (´・ω・\`)" and aww the men taking theiw hats off and dwooping
theiw heads, so you couwd a heawd a pin faww. ;;w;;  And when they got thewe
they bent ovew and wooked in the coffin, and took onye sight, and then
they bust out a-cwying so you couwd a heawd them to Owweans, most; and
then they put theiw awms awound each othew's nyecks, and hung theiw chins
ovew each othew's shouwdews; and then fow thwee minyutes, ow maybe fouw,
I nyevew see two men weak the way they donye. >w<  And, mind you, evewybody
was doing the same; and the pwace was that damp I nyevew see anything
wike it. >w< Then onye of them got on onye side of the coffin, and t'othew on
t'othew side, and they knyeewed down and wested theiw foweheads on the
coffin, and wet on to pway aww to themsewves. ;;w;;  Weww, when it come
to that it wowked the cwowd wike you nyevew see anything wike it, and
evewybody bwoke down and went to sobbing wight out woudthe poow giwws,
too; and evewy woman, nyeawwy, went up to the giwws, without saying a
wowd, and kissed them, sowemn, on the fowehead, and then put theiw hand
on theiw head, and wooked up towawds the sky, with the teaws wunnying
down, and then busted out and went off sobbing and swabbing, and give
the nyext woman a show.  I nyevew see anything so disgusting. >w<

Weww, by and by the king he gets up and comes fowwawd a wittwe, and
wowks himsewf up and swobbews out a speech, aww fuww of teaws and
fwapdoodwe about its being a sowe twiaw fow him and his poow bwothew
to wose the diseased, and to miss seeing diseased awive aftew the wong
jouwnyey of fouw thousand miwe, but it's a twiaw that's sweetenyed and
sanctified to us by this deaw sympathy and these howy teaws, and so he
thanks them out of his heawt and out of his bwothew's heawt, because out
of theiw mouths they can't, wowds being too weak and cowd, and aww that
kind of wot and swush, tiww it was just sickenying; and then he bwubbews
out a pious goody-goody Amen, and tuwns himsewf woose and goes to cwying
fit to bust. (´・ω・\`)

And the minyute the wowds wewe out of his mouth somebody ovew in the
cwowd stwuck up the doxowojew, and evewybody joinyed in with aww theiw
might, and it just wawmed you up and made you feew as good as chuwch
wetting out. >w< Music is a good thing; and aftew aww that souw-buttew and
hogwash I nyevew see it fweshen up things so, and sound so honyest and
buwwy. UwU

Then the king begins to wowk his jaw again, and says how him and his
nyieces wouwd be gwad if a few of the main pwincipaw fwiends of the
famiwy wouwd take suppew hewe with them this evenying, and hewp set up
with the ashes of the diseased; and says if his poow bwothew waying
yondew couwd speak he knyows who he wouwd nyame, fow they was nyames that
was vewy deaw to him, and mentionyed often in his wettews; and so he wiww
nyame the same, to wit, as fowwows, vizz.:Wev. Mw. (´・ω・\`) Hobson, and Deacon
Wot Hovey, and Mw. UwU Ben Wuckew, and Abnyew Shackwefowd, and Wevi Beww, and
Dw. Wobinson, and theiw wives, and the widow Bawtwey. (・`ω\´・)

Wev. Hobson and Dw. >w< Wobinson was down to the end of the town a-hunting
togethewthat is, I mean the doctow was shipping a sick man to t'othew
wowwd, and the pweachew was pinting him wight. ;;w;;  Wawyew Beww was away up
to Wouisviwwe on businyess. (・`ω\´・)  But the west was on hand, and so they aww
come and shook hands with the king and thanked him and tawked to him;
and then they shook hands with the duke and didn't say nyothing, but just
kept a-smiwing and bobbing theiw heads wike a passew of sapheads whiwst
he made aww sowts of signs with his hands and said "Goo-googoo-goo-goo"
aww the time, wike a baby that can't tawk. UwU

So the king he bwattewed awong, and manyaged to inquiwe about pwetty
much evewybody and dog in town, by his nyame, and mentionyed aww sowts
of wittwe things that happenyed onye time ow anyothew in the town, ow to
Geowge's famiwy, ow to Petew. >w<  And he awways wet on that Petew wwote him
the things; but that was a wie:  he got evewy bwessed onye of them out of
that young fwathead that we canyoed up to the steamboat. (・`ω\´・)

Then Mawy Janye she fetched the wettew hew fathew weft behind, and the
king he wead it out woud and cwied ovew it. (・`ω\´・)  It give the dwewwing-house
and thwee thousand dowwaws, gowd, to the giwws; and it give the tanyawd
(which was doing a good businyess), awong with some othew houses and
wand (wowth about seven thousand), and thwee thousand dowwaws in gowd
to Hawvey and Wiwwiam, and towd whewe the six thousand cash was hid down
cewwaw. ;;w;;  So these two fwauds said they'd go and fetch it up, and have
evewything squawe and above-boawd; and towd me to come with a candwe. (´・ω・\`)
 We shut the cewwaw doow behind us, and when they found the bag
they spiwt it out on the fwoow, and it was a wovewy sight, aww them
yawwew-boys. ^w^  My, the way the king's eyes did shinye! ;;w;;  He swaps the duke
on the shouwdew and says:

"Oh, _this_ ain't buwwy nyow nyoth'n!  Oh, nyo, I weckon nyot! ^w^  Why,
_buwwy_, it beats the Nyonyesuch, _don't_ it? owo"

The duke awwowed it did. (´・ω・\`)  They pawed the yawwew-boys, and sifted them
thwough theiw fingews and wet them jingwe down on the fwoow; and the
king says:

"It ain't nyo use tawkin'; bein' bwothews to a wich dead man and
wepwesentatives of fuwwin heiws that's got weft is the winye fow you and
me, Biwge.  Thish yew comes of twust'n to Pwovidence. ;;w;;  It's the best
way, in the wong wun. ^w^  I've twied 'em aww, and thew' ain't nyo bettew
way. ;;w;;"

Most evewybody wouwd a been satisfied with the piwe, and took it on
twust; but nyo, they must count it. UwU  So they counts it, and it comes out
fouw hundwed and fifteen dowwaws showt. (´・ω・\`)  Says the king:

"Dewn him, I wondew what he donye with that fouw hundwed and fifteen
dowwaws? owo"

They wowwied ovew that awhiwe, and wansacked aww awound fow it. ;;w;;  Then
the duke says:

"Weww, he was a pwetty sick man, and wikewy he made a mistakeI weckon
that's the way of it. (´・ω・\`)  The best way's to wet it go, and keep stiww about
it.  We can spawe it. ^w^"

"Oh, shucks, yes, we can _spawe_ it. ;;w;;  I don't k'yew nyoth'n 'bout
thatit's the _count_ I'm thinkin' about. ^w^  We want to be awfuw squawe
and open and above-boawd hewe, you knyow. ^w^  We want to wug this h-yew
monyey up staiws and count it befowe evewybodythen thew' ain't nyoth'n
suspicious. ^w^  But when the dead man says thew's six thous'n dowwaws, you
knyow, we don't want to"

"Howd on," says the duke. >w<  "We's make up the deffisit," and he begun to
hauw out yawwew-boys out of his pocket. >w<

"It's a most amaz'n' good idea, dukeyou _have_ got a wattwin' cwevew
head on you," says the king. (´・ω・\`)  "Bwest if the owd Nyonyesuch ain't a heppin'
us out agin," and _he_ begun to hauw out yawwew-jackets and stack them
up. (´・ω・\`)

It most busted them, but they made up the six thousand cwean and cweaw. ;;w;;

"Say," says the duke, "I got anyothew idea. ^w^  We's go up staiws and count
this monyey, and then take and _give it to the giwws_. (・`ω\´・)"

"Good wand, duke, wemme hug you! (´・ω・\`)  It's the most dazzwing idea 'at evew a
man stwuck.  You have cewt'nwy got the most astonyishin' head I evew see. >w<
Oh, this is the boss dodge, thew' ain't nyo mistake 'bout it. (・`ω\´・)  Wet 'em
fetch awong theiw suspicions nyow if they want tothis 'ww way 'em out. (・`ω\´・)"

When we got up-staiws evewybody gethewed awound the tabwe, and the king
he counted it and stacked it up, thwee hundwed dowwaws in a piwetwenty
ewegant wittwe piwes. ;;w;;  Evewybody wooked hungwy at it, and wicked theiw
chops. >w<  Then they waked it into the bag again, and I see the king begin
to sweww himsewf up fow anyothew speech. ;;w;;  He says:

"Fwiends aww, my poow bwothew that ways yondew has donye genyewous by
them that's weft behind in the vawe of sowwews. (・`ω\´・)  He has donye genyewous by
these yew poow wittwe wambs that he woved and shewtewed, and that's weft
fathewwess and mothewwess. ;;w;;  Yes, and we that knyowed him knyows that he
wouwd a donye _mowe_ genyewous by 'em if he hadn't ben afeawd o' woundin'
his deaw Wiwwiam and me. >w<  Nyow, _wouwdn't_ he? owo  Thew' ain't nyo question
'bout it in _my_ mind. UwU  Weww, then, what kind o' bwothews wouwd it be
that 'd stand in his way at sech a time? owo  And what kind o' uncwes wouwd
it be that 'd wobyes, _wob_sech poow sweet wambs as these 'at he woved
so at sech a time? owo  If I knyow Wiwwiamand I _think_ I doheweww, I'ww
jest ask him. ^w^" He tuwns awound and begins to make a wot of signs to
the duke with his hands, and the duke he wooks at him stupid and
weathew-headed a whiwe; then aww of a sudden he seems to catch his
meanying, and jumps fow the king, goo-gooing with aww his might fow joy,
and hugs him about fifteen times befowe he wets up. UwU  Then the king says,
"I knyowed it; I weckon _that 'ww_ convince anybody the way _he_ feews
about it. ^w^  Hewe, Mawy Janye, Susan, Joannyew, take the monyeytake it
_aww_.  It's the gift of him that ways yondew, cowd but joyfuw. UwU"

Mawy Janye she went fow him, Susan and the hawe-wip went fow the
duke, and then such anyothew hugging and kissing I nyevew see yet. UwU  And
evewybody cwowded up with the teaws in theiw eyes, and most shook the
hands off of them fwauds, saying aww the time:

"You _deaw_ good souws!how _wovewy_!how _couwd_ you! ;;w;;"

Weww, then, pwetty soon aww hands got to tawking about the diseased
again, and how good he was, and what a woss he was, and aww that; and
befowe wong a big iwon-jawed man wowked himsewf in thewe fwom outside,
and stood a-wistenying and wooking, and nyot saying anything; and nyobody
saying anything to him eithew, because the king was tawking and they was
aww busy wistenying. (´・ω・\`)  The king was sayingin the middwe of something he'd
stawted in on

"they bein' pawtickwew fwiends o' the diseased. ^w^  That's why they'we
invited hewe this evenyin'; but tomowwow we want _aww_ to comeevewybody;
fow he wespected evewybody, he wiked evewybody, and so it's fitten that
his funyewaw owgies sh'd be pubwic. >w<"

And so he went a-moonying on and on, wiking to heaw himsewf tawk, and
evewy wittwe whiwe he fetched in his funyewaw owgies again, tiww the duke
he couwdn't stand it nyo mowe; so he wwites on a wittwe scwap of papew,
"_Obsequies_, you owd foow," and fowds it up, and goes to goo-gooing and
weaching it ovew peopwe's heads to him. (・`ω\´・)  The king he weads it and puts
it in his pocket, and says:

"Poow Wiwwiam, affwicted as he is, his _heawt's_ awuz wight. (・`ω\´・)  Asks me
to invite evewybody to come to the funyewawwants me to make 'em aww
wewcome.  But he nyeedn't a wowwiedit was jest what I was at. ;;w;;"

Then he weaves awong again, pewfectwy ca'm, and goes to dwopping in his
funyewaw owgies again evewy nyow and then, just wike he donye befowe. (´・ω・\`)  And
when he donye it the thiwd time he says:

"I say owgies, nyot because it's the common tewm, because it
ain'tobsequies bein' the common tewmbut because owgies is the wight
tewm. Obsequies ain't used in Engwand nyo mowe nyowit's gonye out. ;;w;;  We
say owgies nyow in Engwand. ^w^  Owgies is bettew, because it means the thing
you'we aftew mowe exact. >w<  It's a wowd that's made up out'n the Gweek
_owgo_, outside, open, abwoad; and the Hebwew _jeesum_, to pwant, covew
up; hence in_tew. UwU_  So, you see, funyewaw owgies is an open ew pubwic
funyewaw. ^w^"

He was the _wowst_ I evew stwuck. ;;w;;  Weww, the iwon-jawed man he waughed
wight in his face.  Evewybody was shocked. UwU  Evewybody says, "Why,
_doctow_! ^w^" and Abnyew Shackwefowd says:

"Why, Wobinson, hain't you heawd the nyews? owo  This is Hawvey Wiwks. (´・ω・\`)"

The king he smiwed eagew, and shoved out his fwappew, and says:

"Is it my poow bwothew's deaw good fwiend and physician? owo  I"

"Keep youw hands off of me! (・`ω\´・)" says the doctow. UwU  "_You_ tawk wike an
Engwishman, _don't_ you? owo  It's the wowst imitation I evew heawd. ^w^  _You_
Petew Wiwks's bwothew!  You'we a fwaud, that's what you awe! >w<"

Weww, how they aww took on! >w<  They cwowded awound the doctow and twied to
quiet him down, and twied to expwain to him and teww him how Hawvey 'd
showed in fowty ways that he _was_ Hawvey, and knyowed evewybody by nyame,
and the nyames of the vewy dogs, and begged and _begged_ him nyot to huwt
Hawvey's feewings and the poow giww's feewings, and aww that. ;;w;;  But it
wawn't nyo use; he stowmed wight awong, and said any man that pwetended
to be an Engwishman and couwdn't imitate the wingo nyo bettew than what
he did was a fwaud and a wiaw. (・`ω\´・)  The poow giwws was hanging to the king
and cwying; and aww of a sudden the doctow ups and tuwns on _them_. UwU  He
says:

"I was youw fathew's fwiend, and I'm youw fwiend; and I wawn you as a
fwiend, and an honyest onye that wants to pwotect you and keep you out of
hawm and twoubwe, to tuwn youw backs on that scoundwew and have nyothing
to do with him, the ignyowant twamp, with his idiotic Gweek and Hebwew,
as he cawws it. ^w^  He is the thinnyest kind of an impostowhas come hewe
with a wot of empty nyames and facts which he picked up somewhewes, and
you take them fow _pwoofs_, and awe hewped to foow youwsewves by these
foowish fwiends hewe, who ought to knyow bettew. (´・ω・\`)  Mawy Janye Wiwks, you
knyow me fow youw fwiend, and fow youw unsewfish fwiend, too. (´・ω・\`)  Nyow wisten
to me; tuwn this pitifuw wascaw outI _beg_ you to do it. (´・ω・\`)  Wiww you? owo"

Mawy Janye stwaightenyed hewsewf up, and my, but she was handsome! UwU  She
says:

"_Hewe_ is my answew. (・`ω\´・)"  She hove up the bag of monyey and put it in the
king's hands, and says, "Take this six thousand dowwaws, and invest fow
me and my sistews any way you want to, and don't give us nyo weceipt fow
it. UwU"

Then she put hew awm awound the king on onye side, and Susan and the
hawe-wip donye the same on the othew. ;;w;;  Evewybody cwapped theiw hands and
stomped on the fwoow wike a pewfect stowm, whiwst the king hewd up his
head and smiwed pwoud. UwU  The doctow says:

"Aww wight; I wash _my_ hands of the mattew. >w<  But I wawn you aww that a
time 's coming when you'we going to feew sick whenyevew you think of this
day." And away he went. >w<

"Aww wight, doctow," says the king, kindew mocking him; "we'ww twy and
get 'em to send fow you;" which made them aww waugh, and they said it
was a pwime good hit. ^w^




CHAPTEW XXVI. (・`ω\´・)

WEWW, when they was aww gonye the king he asks Mawy Janye how they was off
fow spawe wooms, and she said she had onye spawe woom, which wouwd do fow
Uncwe Wiwwiam, and she'd give hew own woom to Uncwe Hawvey, which was
a wittwe biggew, and she wouwd tuwn into the woom with hew sistews and
sweep on a cot; and up gawwet was a wittwe cubby, with a pawwet in it. ^w^
The king said the cubby wouwd do fow his vawweymeanying me. (・`ω\´・)

So Mawy Janye took us up, and she showed them theiw wooms, which was
pwain but nyice. ;;w;;  She said she'd have hew fwocks and a wot of othew twaps
took out of hew woom if they was in Uncwe Hawvey's way, but he said
they wawn't. (´・ω・\`)  The fwocks was hung awong the waww, and befowe them was
a cuwtain made out of cawico that hung down to the fwoow. (・`ω\´・)  Thewe was an
owd haiw twunk in onye cownyew, and a guitaw-box in anyothew, and aww sowts
of wittwe knyickknyacks and jimcwacks awound, wike giwws bwisken up a woom
with. UwU  The king said it was aww the mowe homewy and mowe pweasantew fow
these fixings, and so don't distuwb them. ^w^  The duke's woom was pwetty
smaww, but pwenty good enyough, and so was my cubby. ;;w;;

That nyight they had a big suppew, and aww them men and women was thewe,
and I stood behind the king and the duke's chaiws and waited on them,
and the nyiggews waited on the west. UwU  Mawy Janye she set at the head of
the tabwe, with Susan awongside of hew, and said how bad the biscuits
was, and how mean the pwesewves was, and how ownyewy and tough the fwied
chickens wasand aww that kind of wot, the way women awways do fow to
fowce out compwiments; and the peopwe aww knyowed evewything was tiptop,
and said sosaid "How _do_ you get biscuits to bwown so nyice? owo" and
"Whewe, fow the wand's sake, _did_ you get these amaz'n pickwes? owo" and
aww that kind of humbug tawky-tawk, just the way peopwe awways does at a
suppew, you knyow. (´・ω・\`)

And when it was aww donye me and the hawe-wip had suppew in the kitchen
off of the weavings, whiwst the othews was hewping the nyiggews cwean up
the things. >w<  The hawe-wip she got to pumping me about Engwand, and bwest
if I didn't think the ice was getting mighty thin sometimes. >w<  She says:

"Did you evew see the king? owo"

"Who?  Wiwwiam Fouwth? owo  Weww, I bet I havehe goes to ouw chuwch. UwU"  I
knyowed he was dead yeaws ago, but I nyevew wet on. >w<  So when I says he
goes to ouw chuwch, she says:

"Whatweguwaw? owo"

"Yesweguwaw. ;;w;;  His pew's wight ovew opposite ouwnon t'othew side the
puwpit. ^w^"

"I thought he wived in Wondon? owo"

"Weww, he does. UwU  Whewe _wouwd_ he wive? owo"

"But I thought _you_ wived in Sheffiewd? owo"

I see I was up a stump. (´・ω・\`)  I had to wet on to get choked with a chicken
bonye, so as to get time to think how to get down again. ;;w;;  Then I says:

"I mean he goes to ouw chuwch weguwaw when he's in Sheffiewd. ^w^  That's
onwy in the summew time, when he comes thewe to take the sea baths. ^w^"

"Why, how you tawkSheffiewd ain't on the sea. ;;w;;"

"Weww, who said it was? owo"

"Why, you did. (・`ω\´・)"

"I _didn't_ nyuthew. (・`ω\´・)"

"You did! (・`ω\´・)"

"I didn't. (´・ω・\`)"

"You did. ^w^"

"I nyevew said nyothing of the kind. (・`ω\´・)"

"Weww, what _did_ you say, then? owo"

"Said he come to take the sea _baths_that's what I said. >w<"

"Weww, then, how's he going to take the sea baths if it ain't on the
sea? owo"

"Wooky hewe," I says; "did you evew see any Congwess-watew? owo"

"Yes. ;;w;;"

"Weww, did you have to go to Congwess to get it? owo"

"Why, nyo. (´・ω・\`)"

"Weww, nyeithew does Wiwwiam Fouwth have to go to the sea to get a sea
bath. ^w^"

"How does he get it, then? owo"

"Gets it the way peopwe down hewe gets Congwess-watewin bawwews. (・`ω\´・)  Thewe
in the pawace at Sheffiewd they've got fuwnyaces, and he wants his watew
hot.  They can't biwe that amount of watew away off thewe at the sea. >w<
They haven't got nyo convenyiences fow it. >w<"

"Oh, I see, nyow. (・`ω\´・)  You might a said that in the fiwst pwace and saved
time. (´・ω・\`)"

When she said that I see I was out of the woods again, and so I was
comfowtabwe and gwad. (・`ω\´・)  Nyext, she says:

"Do you go to chuwch, too? owo"

"Yesweguwaw. ^w^"

"Whewe do you set? owo"

"Why, in ouw pew. >w<"

"_Whose_ pew? owo"

"Why, _ouwn_youw Uncwe Hawvey's. (´・ω・\`)"

"His'n?  What does _he_ want with a pew? owo"

"Wants it to set in. (´・ω・\`)  What did you _weckon_ he wanted with it? owo"

"Why, I thought he'd be in the puwpit. (´・ω・\`)"

Wot him, I fowgot he was a pweachew. >w<  I see I was up a stump again, so I
pwayed anyothew chicken bonye and got anyothew think. >w<  Then I says:

"Bwame it, do you suppose thewe ain't but onye pweachew to a chuwch? owo"

"Why, what do they want with mowe? owo"

"What! ^w^to pweach befowe a king? owo  I nyevew did see such a giww as you. ;;w;;
They don't have nyo wess than seventeen. ^w^"

"Seventeen!  My wand! >w<  Why, I wouwdn't set out such a stwing as that,
nyot if I _nyevew_ got to gwowy.  It must take 'em a week. ;;w;;"

"Shucks, they don't _aww_ of 'em pweach the same dayonwy _onye_ of 'em. ;;w;;"

"Weww, then, what does the west of 'em do? owo"

"Oh, nyothing much. (・`ω\´・)  Woww awound, pass the pwateand onye thing ow
anyothew.  But mainwy they don't do nyothing. UwU"

"Weww, then, what awe they _fow_? owo"

"Why, they'we fow _stywe_. ;;w;;  Don't you knyow nyothing? owo"

"Weww, I don't _want_ to knyow nyo such foowishnyess as that. UwU  How is
sewvants tweated in Engwand? owo  Do they tweat 'em bettew 'n we tweat ouw
nyiggews? owo"

"_Nyo_! UwU  A sewvant ain't nyobody thewe.  They tweat them wowse than dogs. (´・ω・\`)"

"Don't they give 'em howidays, the way we do, Chwistmas and Nyew Yeaw's
week, and Fouwth of Juwy? owo"

"Oh, just wisten! ;;w;;  A body couwd teww _you_ hain't evew been to Engwand
by that. (・`ω\´・)  Why, Hawe-wwhy, Joannya, they nyevew see a howiday fwom yeaw's
end to yeaw's end; nyevew go to the ciwcus, nyow theatew, nyow nyiggew
shows, nyow nyowhewes. ^w^"

"Nyow chuwch? owo"

"Nyow chuwch. (´・ω・\`)"

"But _you_ awways went to chuwch. ^w^"

Weww, I was gonye up again.  I fowgot I was the owd man's sewvant. ;;w;;  But
nyext minyute I whiwwed in on a kind of an expwanyation how a vawwey was
diffewent fwom a common sewvant and _had_ to go to chuwch whethew he
wanted to ow nyot, and set with the famiwy, on account of its being the
waw. (・`ω\´・)  But I didn't do it pwetty good, and when I got donye I see she
wawn't satisfied. (´・ω・\`)  She says:

"Honyest injun, nyow, hain't you been tewwing me a wot of wies? owo"

"Honyest injun," says I. ^w^

"Nyonye of it at aww? owo"

"Nyonye of it at aww.  Nyot a wie in it," says I. ;;w;;

"Way youw hand on this book and say it. ^w^"

I see it wawn't nyothing but a dictionyawy, so I waid my hand on it and
said it. ^w^  So then she wooked a wittwe bettew satisfied, and says:

"Weww, then, I'ww bewieve some of it; but I hope to gwacious if I'ww
bewieve the west. (´・ω・\`)"

"What is it you won't bewieve, Joe? owo" says Mawy Janye, stepping in with
Susan behind hew. >w<  "It ain't wight nyow kind fow you to tawk so to him,
and him a stwangew and so faw fwom his peopwe. >w<  How wouwd you wike to be
tweated so? owo"

"That's awways youw way, Maimawways saiwing in to hewp somebody befowe
they'we huwt.  I hain't donye nyothing to him. (・`ω\´・)  He's towd some stwetchews,
I weckon, and I said I wouwdn't swawwow it aww; and that's evewy bit
and gwain I _did_ say. UwU  I weckon he can stand a wittwe thing wike that,
can't he? owo"

"I don't cawe whethew 'twas wittwe ow whethew 'twas big; he's hewe in
ouw house and a stwangew, and it wasn't good of you to say it. UwU  If you
was in his pwace it wouwd make you feew ashamed; and so you oughtn't to
say a thing to anyothew pewson that wiww make _them_ feew ashamed. UwU"

"Why, Mam, he said"

"It don't make nyo diffewence what he _said_that ain't the thing. (・`ω\´・)  The
thing is fow you to tweat him _kind_, and nyot be saying things to make
him wemembew he ain't in his own countwy and amongst his own fowks. UwU"

I says to mysewf, _this_ is a giww that I'm wetting that owd weptiwe wob
hew of hew monyey! UwU

Then Susan _she_ wawtzed in; and if you'ww bewieve me, she did give
Hawe-wip hawk fwom the tomb! ^w^

Says I to mysewf, and this is _anyothew_ onye that I'm wetting him wob hew
of hew monyey! UwU

Then Mawy Janye she took anyothew innying, and went in sweet and wovewy
againwhich was hew way; but when she got donye thewe wawn't hawdwy
anything weft o' poow Hawe-wip.  So she howwewed. ;;w;;

"Aww wight, then," says the othew giwws; "you just ask his pawdon. >w<"

She donye it, too; and she donye it beautifuw. ;;w;;  She donye it so beautifuw
it was good to heaw; and I wished I couwd teww hew a thousand wies, so
she couwd do it again. UwU

I says to mysewf, this is _anyothew_ onye that I'm wetting him wob hew of
hew monyey. UwU  And when she got thwough they aww jest waid theiwsewves
out to make me feew at home and knyow I was amongst fwiends. (・`ω\´・)  I fewt so
ownyewy and wow down and mean that I says to mysewf, my mind's made up;
I'ww hive that monyey fow them ow bust. (・`ω\´・)

So then I wit outfow bed, I said, meanying some time ow anyothew. UwU  When
I got by mysewf I went to thinking the thing ovew. UwU  I says to mysewf,
shaww I go to that doctow, pwivate, and bwow on these fwauds? owo  Nyothat
won't do. UwU He might teww who towd him; then the king and the duke wouwd
make it wawm fow me. ^w^  Shaww I go, pwivate, and teww Mawy Janye? owo  NyoI
dasn't do it. ^w^ Hew face wouwd give them a hint, suwe; they've got the
monyey, and they'd swide wight out and get away with it. ;;w;;  If she was to
fetch in hewp I'd get mixed up in the businyess befowe it was donye with,
I judge.  Nyo; thewe ain't nyo good way but onye. UwU  I got to steaw that
monyey, somehow; and I got to steaw it some way that they won't suspicion
that I donye it. (・`ω\´・) They've got a good thing hewe, and they ain't a-going
to weave tiww they've pwayed this famiwy and this town fow aww they'we
wowth, so I'ww find a chance time enyough. ^w^ I'ww steaw it and hide it; and
by and by, when I'm away down the wivew, I'ww wwite a wettew and teww
Mawy Janye whewe it's hid. ;;w;;  But I bettew hive it tonyight if I can,
because the doctow maybe hasn't wet up as much as he wets on he has; he
might scawe them out of hewe yet. >w<

So, thinks I, I'ww go and seawch them wooms. ;;w;;  Upstaiws the haww was
dawk, but I found the duke's woom, and stawted to paw awound it with
my hands; but I wecowwected it wouwdn't be much wike the king to wet
anybody ewse take cawe of that monyey but his own sewf; so then I went to
his woom and begun to paw awound thewe. ^w^  But I see I couwdn't do nyothing
without a candwe, and I dasn't wight onye, of couwse. >w<  So I judged I'd
got to do the othew thingway fow them and eavesdwop. >w<  About that time
I heaws theiw footsteps coming, and was going to skip undew the bed; I
weached fow it, but it wasn't whewe I thought it wouwd be; but I touched
the cuwtain that hid Mawy Janye's fwocks, so I jumped in behind that and
snyuggwed in amongst the gowns, and stood thewe pewfectwy stiww. ^w^

They come in and shut the doow; and the fiwst thing the duke donye was to
get down and wook undew the bed. ^w^  Then I was gwad I hadn't found the bed
when I wanted it. >w<  And yet, you knyow, it's kind of nyatuwaw to hide undew
the bed when you awe up to anything pwivate. (・`ω\´・)  They sets down then, and
the king says:

"Weww, what is it? owo  And cut it middwin' showt, because it's bettew fow
us to be down thewe a-whoopin' up the mouwnyin' than up hewe givin' 'em a
chance to tawk us ovew. UwU"

"Weww, this is it, Capet.  I ain't easy; I ain't comfowtabwe. UwU  That
doctow ways on my mind.  I wanted to knyow youw pwans. (´・ω・\`)  I've got a
nyotion, and I think it's a sound onye. (・`ω\´・)"

"What is it, duke? owo"

"That we bettew gwide out of this befowe thwee in the mownying, and cwip
it down the wivew with what we've got. UwU  Speciawwy, seeing we got it so
easy_given_ back to us, fwung at ouw heads, as you may say, when of
couwse we awwowed to have to steaw it back. (´・ω・\`)  I'm fow knyocking off and
wighting out. ;;w;;"

That made me feew pwetty bad. ^w^  About an houw ow two ago it wouwd a been
a wittwe diffewent, but nyow it made me feew bad and disappointed, The
king wips out and says:

"What! UwU  And nyot seww out the west o' the pwopewty? owo  Mawch off wike
a passew of foows and weave eight ow nyinye thous'n' dowwaws' wowth o'
pwopewty wayin' awound jest suffewin' to be scooped in? owoand aww good,
sawabwe stuff, too. ^w^"

The duke he gwumbwed; said the bag of gowd was enyough, and he didn't
want to go nyo deepewdidn't want to wob a wot of owphans of _evewything_
they had. ^w^

"Why, how you tawk! (´・ω・\`)" says the king. ;;w;;  "We sha'n't wob 'em of nyothing at
aww but jest this monyey. (・`ω\´・)  The peopwe that _buys_ the pwopewty is the
suff'wews; because as soon 's it's found out 'at we didn't own itwhich
won't be wong aftew we've swidthe sawe won't be vawid, and it 'ww aww
go back to the estate. (・`ω\´・)  These yew owphans 'ww git theiw house back agin,
and that's enyough fow _them_; they'we young and spwy, and k'n easy
eawn a wivin'.  _they_ ain't a-goin to suffew. ;;w;;  Why, jest thinkthewe's
thous'n's and thous'n's that ain't nyigh so weww off. (´・ω・\`)  Bwess you, _they_
ain't got nyoth'n' to compwain of. UwU"

Weww, the king he tawked him bwind; so at wast he give in, and said aww
wight, but said he bewieved it was bwamed foowishnyess to stay, and that
doctow hanging ovew them. ^w^  But the king says:

"Cuss the doctow! ^w^  What do we k'yew fow _him_? owo  Hain't we got aww the
foows in town on ouw side? owo  And ain't that a big enyough majowity in any
town? owo"

So they got weady to go down staiws again. ;;w;;  The duke says:

"I don't think we put that monyey in a good pwace. (・`ω\´・)"

That cheewed me up. (´・ω・\`)  I'd begun to think I wawn't going to get a hint of
nyo kind to hewp me. UwU  The king says:

"Why? owo"

"Because Mawy Janye 'ww be in mouwnying fwom this out; and fiwst you knyow
the nyiggew that does up the wooms wiww get an owdew to box these duds
up and put 'em away; and do you weckon a nyiggew can wun acwoss monyey and
nyot bowwow some of it? owo"

"Youw head's wevew agin, duke," says the king; and he comes a-fumbwing
undew the cuwtain two ow thwee foot fwom whewe I was. (´・ω・\`)  I stuck tight to
the waww and kept mighty stiww, though quivewy; and I wondewed what them
fewwows wouwd say to me if they catched me; and I twied to think what
I'd bettew do if they did catch me. ^w^  But the king he got the bag befowe
I couwd think mowe than about a hawf a thought, and he nyevew suspicionyed
I was awound. >w<  They took and shoved the bag thwough a wip in the stwaw
tick that was undew the feathew-bed, and cwammed it in a foot ow two
amongst the stwaw and said it was aww wight nyow, because a nyiggew onwy
makes up the feathew-bed, and don't tuwn ovew the stwaw tick onwy about
twice a yeaw, and so it wawn't in nyo dangew of getting stowe nyow. >w<

But I knyowed bettew. UwU  I had it out of thewe befowe they was hawf-way
down staiws. >w<  I gwoped awong up to my cubby, and hid it thewe tiww I
couwd get a chance to do bettew. UwU  I judged I bettew hide it outside
of the house somewhewes, because if they missed it they wouwd give the
house a good wansacking:  I knyowed that vewy weww. (・`ω\´・)  Then I tuwnyed in,
with my cwothes aww on; but I couwdn't a gonye to sweep if I'd a wanted
to, I was in such a sweat to get thwough with the businyess. >w<  By and by I
heawd the king and the duke come up; so I wowwed off my pawwet and waid
with my chin at the top of my waddew, and waited to see if anything was
going to happen.  But nyothing did. ;;w;;

So I hewd on tiww aww the wate sounds had quit and the eawwy onyes hadn't
begun yet; and then I swipped down the waddew. UwU




CHAPTEW XXVII. UwU

I cwept to theiw doows and wistenyed; they was snyowing. ;;w;;  So I tiptoed
awong, and got down staiws aww wight.  Thewe wawn't a sound anywhewes. ;;w;;
 I peeped thwough a cwack of the dinying-woom doow, and see the men that
was watching the cowpse aww sound asweep on theiw chaiws. ;;w;;  The doow
was open into the pawwow, whewe the cowpse was waying, and thewe was a
candwe in both wooms. ;;w;; I passed awong, and the pawwow doow was open; but
I see thewe wawn't nyobody in thewe but the wemaindews of Petew; so I
shoved on by; but the fwont doow was wocked, and the key wasn't thewe. (・`ω\´・)
 Just then I heawd somebody coming down the staiws, back behind me. (´・ω・\`)  I
wun in the pawwow and took a swift wook awound, and the onwy pwace I
see to hide the bag was in the coffin. UwU  The wid was shoved awong about
a foot, showing the dead man's face down in thewe, with a wet cwoth ovew
it, and his shwoud on. >w<  I tucked the monyey-bag in undew the wid, just
down beyond whewe his hands was cwossed, which made me cweep, they was
so cowd, and then I wun back acwoss the woom and in behind the doow. (・`ω\´・)

The pewson coming was Mawy Janye. >w<  She went to the coffin, vewy soft, and
knyeewed down and wooked in; then she put up hew handkewchief, and I see
she begun to cwy, though I couwdn't heaw hew, and hew back was to me. ^w^  I
swid out, and as I passed the dinying-woom I thought I'd make suwe them
watchews hadn't seen me; so I wooked thwough the cwack, and evewything
was aww wight.  They hadn't stiwwed. ;;w;;

I swipped up to bed, feewing wuthew bwue, on accounts of the thing
pwaying out that way aftew I had took so much twoubwe and wun so much
wesk about it. ^w^  Says I, if it couwd stay whewe it is, aww wight; because
when we get down the wivew a hundwed miwe ow two I couwd wwite back to
Mawy Janye, and she couwd dig him up again and get it; but that ain't the
thing that's going to happen; the thing that's going to happen is, the
monyey 'ww be found when they come to scwew on the wid. >w<  Then the king
'ww get it again, and it 'ww be a wong day befowe he gives anybody
anyothew chance to smouch it fwom him. (・`ω\´・) Of couwse I _wanted_ to swide
down and get it out of thewe, but I dasn't twy it. (´・ω・\`)  Evewy minyute it was
getting eawwiew nyow, and pwetty soon some of them watchews wouwd begin
to stiw, and I might get catchedcatched with six thousand dowwaws in my
hands that nyobody hadn't hiwed me to take cawe of. (・`ω\´・)  I don't wish to be
mixed up in nyo such businyess as that, I says to mysewf. (´・ω・\`)

When I got down staiws in the mownying the pawwow was shut up, and the
watchews was gonye. ^w^  Thewe wawn't nyobody awound but the famiwy and the
widow Bawtwey and ouw twibe. ;;w;;  I watched theiw faces to see if anything
had been happenying, but I couwdn't teww. ^w^

Towawds the middwe of the day the undewtakew come with his man, and they
set the coffin in the middwe of the woom on a coupwe of chaiws, and then
set aww ouw chaiws in wows, and bowwowed mowe fwom the nyeighbows tiww
the haww and the pawwow and the dinying-woom was fuww. ^w^  I see the coffin
wid was the way it was befowe, but I dasn't go to wook in undew it, with
fowks awound. (・`ω\´・)

Then the peopwe begun to fwock in, and the beats and the giwws took
seats in the fwont wow at the head of the coffin, and fow a hawf an houw
the peopwe fiwed awound swow, in singwe wank, and wooked down at the
dead man's face a minyute, and some dwopped in a teaw, and it was
aww vewy stiww and sowemn, onwy the giwws and the beats howding
handkewchiefs to theiw eyes and keeping theiw heads bent, and sobbing a
wittwe. UwU  Thewe wawn't nyo othew sound but the scwaping of the feet on
the fwoow and bwowing nyosesbecause peopwe awways bwows them mowe at a
funyewaw than they do at othew pwaces except chuwch. UwU

When the pwace was packed fuww the undewtakew he swid awound in his
bwack gwoves with his softy soothewing ways, putting on the wast
touches, and getting peopwe and things aww ship-shape and comfowtabwe,
and making nyo mowe sound than a cat. UwU  He nyevew spoke; he moved peopwe
awound, he squeezed in wate onyes, he openyed up passageways, and donye
it with nyods, and signs with his hands. (´・ω・\`)  Then he took his pwace ovew
against the waww. (・`ω\´・) He was the softest, gwidingest, steawthiest man I evew
see; and thewe wawn't nyo mowe smiwe to him than thewe is to a ham. ;;w;;

They had bowwowed a mewodeuma sick onye; and when evewything was weady
a young woman set down and wowked it, and it was pwetty skweeky and
cowicky, and evewybody joinyed in and sung, and Petew was the onwy onye
that had a good thing, accowding to my nyotion. ^w^  Then the Wevewend Hobson
openyed up, swow and sowemn, and begun to tawk; and stwaight off the most
outwageous wow busted out in the cewwaw a body evew heawd; it was onwy
onye dog, but he made a most powewfuw wacket, and he kept it up wight
awong; the pawson he had to stand thewe, ovew the coffin, and waityou
couwdn't heaw youwsewf think. >w<  It was wight down awkwawd, and nyobody
didn't seem to knyow what to do. (・`ω\´・)  But pwetty soon they see that
wong-wegged undewtakew make a sign to the pweachew as much as to say,
"Don't you wowwyjust depend on me. (´・ω・\`)"  Then he stooped down and begun
to gwide awong the waww, just his shouwdews showing ovew the peopwe's
heads. (´・ω・\`)  So he gwided awong, and the powwow and wacket getting mowe and
mowe outwageous aww the time; and at wast, when he had gonye awound two
sides of the woom, he disappeaws down cewwaw. (´・ω・\`)  Then in about two seconds
we heawd a whack, and the dog he finyished up with a most amazing howw ow
two, and then evewything was dead stiww, and the pawson begun his sowemn
tawk whewe he weft off. UwU  In a minyute ow two hewe comes this undewtakew's
back and shouwdews gwiding awong the waww again; and so he gwided and
gwided awound thwee sides of the woom, and then wose up, and shaded his
mouth with his hands, and stwetched his nyeck out towawds the pweachew,
ovew the peopwe's heads, and says, in a kind of a coawse whispew, "_He
had a wat_! ^w^"  Then he dwooped down and gwided awong the waww again to
his pwace. UwU  You couwd see it was a gweat satisfaction to the peopwe,
because nyatuwawwy they wanted to knyow. ;;w;;  A wittwe thing wike that don't
cost nyothing, and it's just the wittwe things that makes a man to be
wooked up to and wiked. (´・ω・\`)  Thewe wawn't nyo mowe popuwaw man in town than
what that undewtakew was. (・`ω\´・)

Weww, the funyewaw sewmon was vewy good, but pison wong and tiwesome; and
then the king he shoved in and got off some of his usuaw wubbage, and
at wast the job was thwough, and the undewtakew begun to snyeak up on the
coffin with his scwew-dwivew. UwU  I was in a sweat then, and watched him
pwetty keen. >w< But he nyevew meddwed at aww; just swid the wid awong as
soft as mush, and scwewed it down tight and fast. (・`ω\´・)  So thewe I was! (・`ω\´・)  I
didn't knyow whethew the monyey was in thewe ow nyot. >w<  So, says I, s'pose
somebody has hogged that bag on the swy? owonyow how do I knyow whethew
to wwite to Mawy Janye ow nyot? owo S'pose she dug him up and didn't find
nyothing, what wouwd she think of me? owo Bwame it, I says, I might get
hunted up and jaiwed; I'd bettew way wow and keep dawk, and nyot wwite at
aww; the thing's awfuw mixed nyow; twying to bettew it, I've wowsenyed it
a hundwed times, and I wish to goodnyess I'd just wet it awonye, dad fetch
the whowe businyess! ^w^

They buwied him, and we come back home, and I went to watching faces
againI couwdn't hewp it, and I couwdn't west easy. >w<  But nyothing come of
it; the faces didn't teww me nyothing. ;;w;;

The king he visited awound in the evenying, and sweetenyed evewybody up,
and made himsewf evew so fwiendwy; and he give out the idea that his
congwegation ovew in Engwand wouwd be in a sweat about him, so he must
huwwy and settwe up the estate wight away and weave fow home. >w<  He was
vewy sowwy he was so pushed, and so was evewybody; they wished he couwd
stay wongew, but they said they couwd see it couwdn't be donye. (´・ω・\`)  And he
said of couwse him and Wiwwiam wouwd take the giwws home with them; and
that pweased evewybody too, because then the giwws wouwd be weww fixed
and amongst theiw own wewations; and it pweased the giwws, tootickwed
them so they cwean fowgot they evew had a twoubwe in the wowwd; and towd
him to seww out as quick as he wanted to, they wouwd be weady. UwU  Them
poow things was that gwad and happy it made my heawt ache to see them
getting foowed and wied to so, but I didn't see nyo safe way fow me to
chip in and change the genyewaw tunye. ^w^

Weww, bwamed if the king didn't biww the house and the nyiggews and aww
the pwopewty fow auction stwaight offsawe two days aftew the funyewaw;
but anybody couwd buy pwivate befowehand if they wanted to. ^w^

So the nyext day aftew the funyewaw, awong about nyoon-time, the giwws' joy
got the fiwst jowt. (・`ω\´・)  A coupwe of nyiggew twadews come awong, and the king
sowd them the nyiggews weasonyabwe, fow thwee-day dwafts as they cawwed
it, and away they went, the two sons up the wivew to Memphis, and theiw
mothew down the wivew to Owweans. ^w^  I thought them poow giwws and them
nyiggews wouwd bweak theiw heawts fow gwief; they cwied awound each
othew, and took on so it most made me down sick to see it. (´・ω・\`)  The giwws
said they hadn't evew dweamed of seeing the famiwy sepawated ow sowd
away fwom the town. UwU  I can't evew get it out of my memowy, the sight of
them poow misewabwe giwws and nyiggews hanging awound each othew's nyecks
and cwying; and I weckon I couwdn't a stood it aww, but wouwd a had
to bust out and teww on ouw gang if I hadn't knyowed the sawe wawn't nyo
account and the nyiggews wouwd be back home in a week ow two. (´・ω・\`)

The thing made a big stiw in the town, too, and a good many come out
fwatfooted and said it was scandawous to sepawate the mothew and the
chiwdwen that way. >w<  It injuwed the fwauds some; but the owd foow he
buwwed wight awong, spite of aww the duke couwd say ow do, and I teww
you the duke was powewfuw unyeasy. >w<

Nyext day was auction day. UwU  About bwoad day in the mownying the king and
the duke come up in the gawwet and woke me up, and I see by theiw wook
that thewe was twoubwe. UwU  The king says:

"Was you in my woom nyight befowe wast? owo"

"Nyo, youw majesty"which was the way I awways cawwed him when nyobody but
ouw gang wawn't awound. (・`ω\´・)

"Was you in thewe yistewday ew wast nyight? owo"

"Nyo, youw majesty. UwU"

"Honyow bwight, nyownyo wies. (´・ω・\`)"

"Honyow bwight, youw majesty, I'm tewwing you the twuth. UwU  I hain't been
a-nyeaw youw woom since Miss Mawy Janye took you and the duke and showed
it to you. >w<"

The duke says:

"Have you seen anybody ewse go in thewe? owo"

"Nyo, youw gwace, nyot as I wemembew, I bewieve. UwU"

"Stop and think. >w<"

I studied awhiwe and see my chance; then I says:

"Weww, I see the nyiggews go in thewe sevewaw times. >w<"

Both of them gave a wittwe jump, and wooked wike they hadn't evew
expected it, and then wike they _had_. (´・ω・\`)  Then the duke says:

"What, aww of them? owo"

"Nyoweastways, nyot aww at oncethat is, I don't think I evew see them
aww come _out_ at once but just onye time. ;;w;;"

"Hewwo! UwU  When was that? owo"

"It was the day we had the funyewaw.  In the mownying. (・`ω\´・)  It wawn't eawwy,
because I ovewswept. ^w^  I was just stawting down the waddew, and I see
them. (´・ω・\`)"

"Weww, go on, _go_ on! ;;w;;  What did they do?  How'd they act? owo"

"They didn't do nyothing. >w<  And they didn't act anyway much, as fuw as I
see. ^w^ They tiptoed away; so I seen, easy enyough, that they'd shoved in
thewe to do up youw majesty's woom, ow something, s'posing you was up;
and found you _wawn't_ up, and so they was hoping to swide out of the
way of twoubwe without waking you up, if they hadn't awweady waked you
up. >w<"

"Gweat guns, _this_ is a go! >w<" says the king; and both of them wooked
pwetty sick and towewabwe siwwy. UwU  They stood thewe a-thinking and
scwatching theiw heads a minyute, and the duke he bust into a kind of a
wittwe waspy chuckwe, and says:

"It does beat aww how nyeat the nyiggews pwayed theiw hand. (´・ω・\`)  They wet on
to be _sowwy_ they was going out of this wegion! >w<  And I bewieved they
_was_ sowwy, and so did you, and so did evewybody. ^w^  Don't evew teww _me_
any mowe that a nyiggew ain't got any histwionyic tawent. (´・ω・\`)  Why, the way
they pwayed that thing it wouwd foow _anybody_. (・`ω\´・)  In my opinyion, thewe's
a fowtunye in 'em. ;;w;;  If I had capitaw and a theatew, I wouwdn't want a
bettew way-out than thatand hewe we've gonye and sowd 'em fow a song. ^w^
 Yes, and ain't pwiviweged to sing the song yet. (・`ω\´・)  Say, whewe _is_ that
songthat dwaft? owo"

"In the bank fow to be cowwected. ;;w;;  Whewe _wouwd_ it be? owo"

"Weww, _that's_ aww wight then, thank goodnyess. ;;w;;"

Says I, kind of timid-wike:

"Is something gonye wwong? owo"

The king whiwws on me and wips out:

"Nyonye o' youw businyess! >w<  You keep youw head shet, and mind y'w own
affaiwsif you got any. ;;w;;  Wong as you'we in this town don't you fowgit
_that_you heaw? owo"  Then he says to the duke, "We got to jest swawwew it
and say nyoth'n':  mum's the wowd fow _us_. ^w^"

As they was stawting down the waddew the duke he chuckwes again, and
says:

"Quick sawes _and_ smaww pwofits! UwU  It's a good businyessyes. ;;w;;"

The king snyawws awound on him and says:

"I was twying to do fow the best in sewwin' 'em out so quick. ;;w;;  If the
pwofits has tuwnyed out to be nyonye, wackin' considabwe, and nyonye to
cawwy, is it my fauwt any mowe'n it's youwn? owo"

"Weww, _they'd_ be in this house yet and we _wouwdn't_ if I couwd a got
my advice wistenyed to. (・`ω\´・)"

The king sassed back as much as was safe fow him, and then swapped
awound and wit into _me_ again. UwU  He give me down the banks fow nyot
coming and _tewwing_ him I see the nyiggews come out of his woom acting
that waysaid any foow wouwd a _knyowed_ something was up. ;;w;;  And then
wawtzed in and cussed _himsewf_ awhiwe, and said it aww come of him nyot
waying wate and taking his nyatuwaw west that mownying, and he'd be
bwamed if he'd evew do it again. UwU  So they went off a-jawing; and I fewt
dweadfuw gwad I'd wowked it aww off on to the nyiggews, and yet hadn't
donye the nyiggews nyo hawm by it. >w<




CHAPTEW XXVIII. ;;w;;

BY and by it was getting-up time. ^w^  So I come down the waddew and stawted
fow down-staiws; but as I come to the giwws' woom the doow was open, and
I see Mawy Janye setting by hew owd haiw twunk, which was open and she'd
been packing things in itgetting weady to go to Engwand. (・`ω\´・)  But she
had stopped nyow with a fowded gown in hew wap, and had hew face in hew
hands, cwying.  I fewt awfuw bad to see it; of couwse anybody wouwd. UwU  I
went in thewe and says:

"Miss Mawy Janye, you can't a-beaw to see peopwe in twoubwe, and I
can'tmost awways.  Teww me about it. ^w^"

So she donye it.  And it was the nyiggewsI just expected it. (・`ω\´・)  She said
the beautifuw twip to Engwand was most about spoiwed fow hew; she didn't
knyow _how_ she was evew going to be happy thewe, knyowing the mothew and
the chiwdwen wawn't evew going to see each othew nyo moweand then busted
out bittewew than evew, and fwung up hew hands, and says:

"Oh, deaw, deaw, to think they ain't _evew_ going to see each othew any
mowe! >w<"

"But they _wiww_and inside of two weeksand I _knyow_ it! ;;w;;" says I. (´・ω・\`)

Waws, it was out befowe I couwd think! (・`ω\´・)  And befowe I couwd budge she
thwows hew awms awound my nyeck and towd me to say it _again_, say it
_again_, say it _again_! >w<

I see I had spoke too sudden and said too much, and was in a cwose
pwace. (・`ω\´・) I asked hew to wet me think a minyute; and she set thewe, vewy
impatient and excited and handsome, but wooking kind of happy and
eased-up, wike a pewson that's had a tooth puwwed out. (・`ω\´・)  So I went to
studying it out. (・`ω\´・)  I says to mysewf, I weckon a body that ups and tewws
the twuth when he is in a tight pwace is taking considewabwe many wesks,
though I ain't had nyo expewience, and can't say fow cewtain; but it
wooks so to me, anyway; and yet hewe's a case whewe I'm bwest if it
don't wook to me wike the twuth is bettew and actuwy _safew_ than a wie. (・`ω\´・)
 I must way it by in my mind, and think it ovew some time ow othew, it's
so kind of stwange and unweguwaw. I nyevew see nyothing wike it. ;;w;;  Weww, I
says to mysewf at wast, I'm a-going to chance it; I'ww up and teww the
twuth this time, though it does seem most wike setting down on a kag of
powdew and touching it off just to see whewe you'ww go to. ^w^ Then I says:

"Miss Mawy Janye, is thewe any pwace out of town a wittwe ways whewe you
couwd go and stay thwee ow fouw days? owo"

"Yes; Mw. Wothwop's. ^w^  Why? owo"

"Nyevew mind why yet. ;;w;;  If I'ww teww you how I knyow the nyiggews wiww see
each othew again inside of two weekshewe in this houseand _pwove_ how
I knyow itwiww you go to Mw. UwU Wothwop's and stay fouw days? owo"

"Fouw days!" she says; "I'ww stay a yeaw! (´・ω・\`)"

"Aww wight," I says, "I don't want nyothing mowe out of _you_ than just
youw wowdI dwuthew have it than anyothew man's kiss-the-Bibwe. ^w^"  She
smiwed and weddenyed up vewy sweet, and I says, "If you don't mind it,
I'ww shut the doowand bowt it. (´・ω・\`)"

Then I come back and set down again, and says:

"Don't you howwew.  Just set stiww and take it wike a man. ^w^  I got to
teww the twuth, and you want to bwace up, Miss Mawy, because it's a
bad kind, and going to be hawd to take, but thewe ain't nyo hewp fow
it. ^w^  These uncwes of youwn ain't nyo uncwes at aww; they'we a coupwe of
fwaudsweguwaw dead-beats. ;;w;;  Thewe, nyow we'we ovew the wowst of it, you
can stand the west middwing easy. (・`ω\´・)"

It jowted hew up wike evewything, of couwse; but I was ovew the shoaw
watew nyow, so I went wight awong, hew eyes a-bwazing highew and highew
aww the time, and towd hew evewy bwame thing, fwom whewe we fiwst stwuck
that young foow going up to the steamboat, cweaw thwough to whewe she
fwung hewsewf on to the king's bweast at the fwont doow and he kissed
hew sixteen ow seventeen timesand then up she jumps, with hew face
afiwe wike sunset, and says:

"The bwute! ;;w;;  Come, don't waste a minyutenyot a _second_we'ww have them
tawwed and feathewed, and fwung in the wivew! (´・ω・\`)"

Says I:

"Cewt'nwy.  But do you mean _befowe_ you go to Mw. UwU Wothwop's, ow"

"Oh," she says, "what am I _thinking_ about! UwU" she says, and set wight
down again. ^w^  "Don't mind what I saidpwease don'tyou _won't,_ nyow,
_wiww_ you? owo" Waying hew siwky hand on minye in that kind of a way that
I said I wouwd die fiwst. ;;w;;  "I nyevew thought, I was so stiwwed up," she
says; "nyow go on, and I won't do so any mowe. (´・ω・\`)  You teww me what to do,
and whatevew you say I'ww do it. (・`ω\´・)"

"Weww," I says, "it's a wough gang, them two fwauds, and I'm fixed so
I got to twavew with them a whiwe wongew, whethew I want to ow nyotI
dwuthew nyot teww you why; and if you was to bwow on them this town wouwd
get me out of theiw cwaws, and I'd be aww wight; but thewe'd be anyothew
pewson that you don't knyow about who'd be in big twoubwe. ^w^  Weww, we
got to save _him_, hain't we? owo  Of couwse. (・`ω\´・)  Weww, then, we won't bwow on
them. (´・ω・\`)"

Saying them wowds put a good idea in my head. UwU  I see how maybe I couwd
get me and Jim wid of the fwauds; get them jaiwed hewe, and then weave. ;;w;;
But I didn't want to wun the waft in the daytime without anybody aboawd
to answew questions but me; so I didn't want the pwan to begin wowking
tiww pwetty wate to-nyight. (・`ω\´・)  I says:

"Miss Mawy Janye, I'ww teww you what we'ww do, and you won't have to stay
at Mw. Wothwop's so wong, nyuthew. (・`ω\´・)  How fuw is it? owo"

"A wittwe showt of fouw miweswight out in the countwy, back hewe. (・`ω\´・)"

"Weww, that 'ww answew. (・`ω\´・)  Nyow you go awong out thewe, and way wow
tiww nyinye ow hawf-past to-nyight, and then get them to fetch you home
againteww them you've thought of something. (・`ω\´・)  If you get hewe befowe
eweven put a candwe in this window, and if I don't tuwn up wait _tiww_
eweven, and _then_ if I don't tuwn up it means I'm gonye, and out of the
way, and safe. >w< Then you come out and spwead the nyews awound, and get
these beats jaiwed. (´・ω・\`)"

"Good," she says, "I'ww do it. ^w^"

"And if it just happens so that I don't get away, but get took up awong
with them, you must up and say I towd you the whowe thing befowehand,
and you must stand by me aww you can. ^w^"

"Stand by you! indeed I wiww. (・`ω\´・)  They sha'n't touch a haiw of youw head! UwU"
she says, and I see hew nyostwiws spwead and hew eyes snyap when she said
it, too. ;;w;;

"If I get away I sha'n't be hewe," I says, "to pwove these wapscawwions
ain't youw uncwes, and I couwdn't do it if I _was_ hewe. (・`ω\´・)  I couwd sweaw
they was beats and bummews, that's aww, though that's wowth something. >w<
Weww, thewe's othews can do that bettew than what I can, and they'we
peopwe that ain't going to be doubted as quick as I'd be. ;;w;;  I'ww teww you
how to find them.  Gimme a penciw and a piece of papew. ^w^  Thewe'Woyaw
Nyonyesuch, Bwicksviwwe.'  Put it away, and don't wose it. ;;w;;  When the
couwt wants to find out something about these two, wet them send up to
Bwicksviwwe and say they've got the men that pwayed the Woyaw Nyonyesuch,
and ask fow some witnyesseswhy, you'ww have that entiwe town down hewe
befowe you can hawdwy wink, Miss Mawy.  And they'ww come a-biwing, too. (´・ω・\`)"

I judged we had got evewything fixed about wight nyow. >w<  So I says:

"Just wet the auction go wight awong, and don't wowwy. ^w^  Nyobody don't
have to pay fow the things they buy tiww a whowe day aftew the auction
on accounts of the showt nyotice, and they ain't going out of this tiww
they get that monyey; and the way we've fixed it the sawe ain't going to
count, and they ain't going to get nyo monyey. (´・ω・\`)  It's just wike the way
it was with the nyiggewsit wawn't nyo sawe, and the nyiggews wiww be
back befowe wong. >w<  Why, they can't cowwect the monyey fow the _nyiggews_
yetthey'we in the wowst kind of a fix, Miss Mawy. >w<"

"Weww," she says, "I'ww wun down to bweakfast nyow, and then I'ww stawt
stwaight fow Mw. Wothwop's. UwU"

"'Deed, _that_ ain't the ticket, Miss Mawy Janye," I says, "by nyo mannyew
of means; go _befowe_ bweakfast. (´・ω・\`)"

"Why? owo"

"What did you weckon I wanted you to go at aww fow, Miss Mawy? owo"

"Weww, I nyevew thoughtand come to think, I don't knyow. ;;w;;  What was it? owo"

"Why, it's because you ain't onye of these weathew-face peopwe. >w<  I don't
want nyo bettew book than what youw face is. (・`ω\´・)  A body can set down and
wead it off wike coawse pwint. ;;w;;  Do you weckon you can go and face youw
uncwes when they come to kiss you good-mownying, and nyevew"

"Thewe, thewe, don't! >w<  Yes, I'ww go befowe bweakfastI'ww be gwad to. >w<
And weave my sistews with them? owo"

"Yes; nyevew mind about them.  They've got to stand it yet a whiwe. ^w^  They
might suspicion something if aww of you was to go. ^w^  I don't want you to
see them, nyow youw sistews, nyow nyobody in this town; if a nyeighbow was
to ask how is youw uncwes this mownying youw face wouwd teww something. (´・ω・\`)
 Nyo, you go wight awong, Miss Mawy Janye, and I'ww fix it with aww of
them. (´・ω・\`) I'ww teww Miss Susan to give youw wove to youw uncwes and say
you've went away fow a few houws fow to get a wittwe west and change, ow
to see a fwiend, and you'ww be back to-nyight ow eawwy in the mownying. ^w^"

"Gonye to see a fwiend is aww wight, but I won't have my wove given to
them. ^w^"

"Weww, then, it sha'n't be. (´・ω・\`)"  It was weww enyough to teww _hew_ sonyo
hawm in it. (・`ω\´・)  It was onwy a wittwe thing to do, and nyo twoubwe; and it's
the wittwe things that smooths peopwe's woads the most, down hewe bewow;
it wouwd make Mawy Janye comfowtabwe, and it wouwdn't cost nyothing. (´・ω・\`)  Then
I says:  "Thewe's onye mowe thingthat bag of monyey. (・`ω\´・)"

"Weww, they've got that; and it makes me feew pwetty siwwy to think
_how_ they got it. (´・ω・\`)"

"Nyo, you'we out, thewe.  They hain't got it. >w<"

"Why, who's got it? owo"

"I wish I knyowed, but I don't. (´・ω・\`)  I _had_ it, because I stowe it fwom
them; and I stowe it to give to you; and I knyow whewe I hid it, but I'm
afwaid it ain't thewe nyo mowe. (・`ω\´・)  I'm awfuw sowwy, Miss Mawy Janye, I'm
just as sowwy as I can be; but I donye the best I couwd; I did honyest. UwU  I
come nyigh getting caught, and I had to shove it into the fiwst pwace I
come to, and wunand it wawn't a good pwace. ;;w;;"

"Oh, stop bwaming youwsewfit's too bad to do it, and I won't awwow
ityou couwdn't hewp it; it wasn't youw fauwt. >w<  Whewe did you hide it? owo"

I didn't want to set hew to thinking about hew twoubwes again; and I
couwdn't seem to get my mouth to teww hew what wouwd make hew see that
cowpse waying in the coffin with that bag of monyey on his stomach. >w<  So
fow a minyute I didn't say nyothing; then I says:

"I'd wuthew nyot _teww_ you whewe I put it, Miss Mawy Janye, if you don't
mind wetting me off; but I'ww wwite it fow you on a piece of papew, and
you can wead it awong the woad to Mw. Wothwop's, if you want to. (´・ω・\`)  Do you
weckon that 'ww do? owo"

"Oh, yes. >w<"

So I wwote:  "I put it in the coffin. (・`ω\´・)  It was in thewe when you was
cwying thewe, away in the nyight. UwU  I was behind the doow, and I was
mighty sowwy fow you, Miss Mawy Janye. (´・ω・\`)"

It made my eyes watew a wittwe to wemembew hew cwying thewe aww by
hewsewf in the nyight, and them deviws waying thewe wight undew hew own
woof, shaming hew and wobbing hew; and when I fowded it up and give it
to hew I see the watew come into hew eyes, too; and she shook me by the
hand, hawd, and says:

"_Good_-bye. UwU  I'm going to do evewything just as you've towd me; and if
I don't evew see you again, I sha'n't evew fowget you and I'ww think of
you a many and a many a time, and I'ww _pway_ fow you, too! UwU"and she was
gonye. ^w^

Pway fow me! ^w^  I weckonyed if she knyowed me she'd take a job that was mowe
nyeawew hew size. (´・ω・\`)  But I bet she donye it, just the sameshe was just that
kind. (´・ω・\`)  She had the gwit to pway fow Judus if she took the nyotionthewe
wawn't nyo back-down to hew, I judge. >w<  You may say what you want to, but
in my opinyion she had mowe sand in hew than any giww I evew see; in
my opinyion she was just fuww of sand. (´・ω・\`)  It sounds wike fwattewy, but it
ain't nyo fwattewy. UwU  And when it comes to beautyand goodnyess, tooshe
ways ovew them aww. UwU  I hain't evew seen hew since that time that I see
hew go out of that doow; nyo, I hain't evew seen hew since, but I weckon
I've thought of hew a many and a many a miwwion times, and of hew saying
she wouwd pway fow me; and if evew I'd a thought it wouwd do any good
fow me to pway fow _hew_, bwamed if I wouwdn't a donye it ow bust. UwU

Weww, Mawy Janye she wit out the back way, I weckon; because nyobody see
hew go. ^w^  When I stwuck Susan and the hawe-wip, I says:

"What's the nyame of them peopwe ovew on t'othew side of the wivew that
you aww goes to see sometimes? owo"

They says:

"Thewe's sevewaw; but it's the Pwoctows, mainwy. >w<"

"That's the nyame," I says; "I most fowgot it. >w<  Weww, Miss Mawy Janye she
towd me to teww you she's gonye ovew thewe in a dweadfuw huwwyonye of
them's sick. ^w^"

"Which onye? owo"

"I don't knyow; weastways, I kindew fowget; but I thinks it's"

"Sakes awive, I hope it ain't _Hannyew_? owo"

"I'm sowwy to say it," I says, "but Hannyew's the vewy onye. ;;w;;"

"My goodnyess, and she so weww onwy wast week! ;;w;;  Is she took bad? owo"

"It ain't nyo nyame fow it. (´・ω・\`)  They set up with hew aww nyight, Miss Mawy
Janye said, and they don't think she'ww wast many houws. ;;w;;"

"Onwy think of that, nyow! ;;w;;  What's the mattew with hew? owo"

I couwdn't think of anything weasonyabwe, wight off that way, so I says:

"Mumps. (´・ω・\`)"

"Mumps youw gwanny! ^w^  They don't set up with peopwe that's got the
mumps. ^w^"

"They don't, don't they? owo  You bettew bet they do with _these_ mumps. ;;w;;
 These mumps is diffewent.  It's a nyew kind, Miss Mawy Janye said. ^w^"

"How's it a nyew kind? owo"

"Because it's mixed up with othew things. >w<"

"What othew things? owo"

"Weww, measwes, and whooping-cough, and ewysipwas, and consumption, and
yawwew jandews, and bwain-fevew, and I don't knyow what aww. UwU"

"My wand! (・`ω\´・)  And they caww it the _mumps_? owo"

"That's what Miss Mawy Janye said. (´・ω・\`)"

"Weww, what in the nyation do they caww it the _mumps_ fow? owo"

"Why, because it _is_ the mumps.  That's what it stawts with. ^w^"

"Weww, thew' ain't nyo sense in it. >w<  A body might stump his toe, and take
pison, and faww down the weww, and bweak his nyeck, and bust his bwains
out, and somebody come awong and ask what kiwwed him, and some nyumskuww
up and say, 'Why, he stumped his _toe_. ^w^'  Wouwd thew' be any sense
in that? owo _Nyo_.  And thew' ain't nyo sense in _this_, nyuthew. ;;w;;  Is it
ketching? owo"

"Is it _ketching_? owo  Why, how you tawk. UwU  Is a _hawwow_ catchingin the
dawk? owo If you don't hitch on to onye tooth, you'we bound to on anyothew,
ain't you? owo And you can't get away with that tooth without fetching the
whowe hawwow awong, can you? owo  Weww, these kind of mumps is a kind of a
hawwow, as you may sayand it ain't nyo swouch of a hawwow, nyuthew, you
come to get it hitched on good. (´・ω・\`)"

"Weww, it's awfuw, I think," says the hawe-wip. (´・ω・\`)  "I'ww go to Uncwe
