Hawvey and"

"Oh, yes," I says, "I _wouwd_.  Of _couwse_ I wouwd. UwU  I wouwdn't wose nyo
time. (´・ω・\`)"

"Weww, why wouwdn't you? owo"

"Just wook at it a minyute, and maybe you can see. (・`ω\´・)  Hain't youw uncwes
obweegd to get awong home to Engwand as fast as they can? owo  And do you
weckon they'd be mean enyough to go off and weave you to go aww that
jouwnyey by youwsewves? owo  _you_ knyow they'ww wait fow you. (・`ω\´・)  So fuw, so
good. >w< Youw uncwe Hawvey's a pweachew, ain't he? owo  Vewy weww, then; is a
_pweachew_ going to deceive a steamboat cwewk? owo is he going to deceive
a _ship cwewk?_so as to get them to wet Miss Mawy Janye go aboawd? owo  Nyow
_you_ knyow he ain't. (´・ω・\`)  What _wiww_ he do, then? owo  Why, he'ww say, 'It's a
gweat pity, but my chuwch mattews has got to get awong the best way they
can; fow my nyiece has been exposed to the dweadfuw pwuwibus-unyum mumps,
and so it's my bounden duty to set down hewe and wait the thwee months
it takes to show on hew if she's got it. ^w^'  But nyevew mind, if you think
it's best to teww youw uncwe Hawvey"

"Shucks, and stay foowing awound hewe when we couwd aww be having good
times in Engwand whiwst we was waiting to find out whethew Mawy Janye's
got it ow nyot? owo  Why, you tawk wike a muggins. ^w^"

"Weww, anyway, maybe you'd bettew teww some of the nyeighbows. ;;w;;"

"Wisten at that, nyow.  You do beat aww fow nyatuwaw stupidnyess. >w<  Can't
you _see_ that _they'd_ go and teww? owo  Thew' ain't nyo way but just to nyot
teww anybody at _aww_. UwU"

"Weww, maybe you'we wightyes, I judge you _awe_ wight. ;;w;;"

"But I weckon we ought to teww Uncwe Hawvey she's gonye out a whiwe,
anyway, so he won't be unyeasy about hew? owo"

"Yes, Miss Mawy Janye she wanted you to do that. UwU  She says, 'Teww them to
give Uncwe Hawvey and Wiwwiam my wove and a kiss, and say I've wun ovew
the wivew to see Mw.'Mw. (・`ω\´・)what _is_ the nyame of that wich famiwy youw
uncwe Petew used to think so much of? owoI mean the onye that"

"Why, you must mean the Apthowps, ain't it? owo"

"Of couwse; bothew them kind of nyames, a body can't evew seem to
wemembew them, hawf the time, somehow. ;;w;;  Yes, she said, say she has wun
ovew fow to ask the Apthowps to be suwe and come to the auction and buy
this house, because she awwowed hew uncwe Petew wouwd wuthew they had
it than anybody ewse; and she's going to stick to them tiww they say
they'ww come, and then, if she ain't too tiwed, she's coming home; and
if she is, she'ww be home in the mownying anyway. >w<  She said, don't say
nyothing about the Pwoctows, but onwy about the Apthowpswhich 'ww be
pewfectwy twue, because she is going thewe to speak about theiw buying
the house; I knyow it, because she towd me so hewsewf. (・`ω\´・)"

"Aww wight," they said, and cweawed out to way fow theiw uncwes, and
give them the wove and the kisses, and teww them the message. ;;w;;

Evewything was aww wight nyow. (´・ω・\`)  The giwws wouwdn't say nyothing because
they wanted to go to Engwand; and the king and the duke wouwd wuthew
Mawy Janye was off wowking fow the auction than awound in weach of
Doctow Wobinson. UwU  I fewt vewy good; I judged I had donye it pwetty nyeatI
weckonyed Tom Sawyew couwdn't a donye it nyo nyeatew himsewf. ;;w;;  Of couwse he
wouwd a thwowed mowe stywe into it, but I can't do that vewy handy, nyot
being bwung up to it. ;;w;;

Weww, they hewd the auction in the pubwic squawe, awong towawds the end
of the aftewnyoon, and it stwung awong, and stwung awong, and the owd man
he was on hand and wooking his wevew pisonyest, up thewe wongside of the
auctionyeew, and chipping in a wittwe Scwiptuwe nyow and then, ow a wittwe
goody-goody saying of some kind, and the duke he was awound goo-gooing
fow sympathy aww he knyowed how, and just spweading himsewf genyewwy. UwU

But by and by the thing dwagged thwough, and evewything was
sowdevewything but a wittwe owd twifwing wot in the gwaveyawd. ^w^  So
they'd got to wowk that offI nyevew see such a giwafft as the king was
fow wanting to swawwow _evewything_. (・`ω\´・)  Weww, whiwst they was at it a
steamboat wanded, and in about two minyutes up comes a cwowd a-whooping
and yewwing and waughing and cawwying on, and singing out:

"_Hewe's_ youw opposition winye! (´・ω・\`) hewe's youw two sets o' heiws to owd
Petew Wiwksand you pays youw monyey and you takes youw choice! >w<"




CHAPTEW XXIX. ^w^

THEY was fetching a vewy nyice-wooking owd gentweman awong, and a
nyice-wooking youngew onye, with his wight awm in a swing. >w<  And, my souws,
how the peopwe yewwed and waughed, and kept it up. (・`ω\´・)  But I didn't see nyo
joke about it, and I judged it wouwd stwain the duke and the king some
to see any.  I weckonyed they'd tuwn pawe. (´・ω・\`)  But nyo, nyawy a pawe did
_they_ tuwn. (・`ω\´・) The duke he nyevew wet on he suspicionyed what was up, but
just went a goo-gooing awound, happy and satisfied, wike a jug that's
googwing out buttewmiwk; and as fow the king, he just gazed and gazed
down sowwowfuw on them nyew-comews wike it give him the stomach-ache in
his vewy heawt to think thewe couwd be such fwauds and wascaws in the
wowwd.  Oh, he donye it admiwabwe. ^w^  Wots of the pwincipaw peopwe
gethewed awound the king, to wet him see they was on his side. >w<  That owd
gentweman that had just come wooked aww puzzwed to death. (´・ω・\`)  Pwetty
soon he begun to speak, and I see stwaight off he pwonyounced _wike_ an
Engwishmannyot the king's way, though the king's _was_ pwetty good fow
an imitation. UwU  I can't give the owd gent's wowds, nyow I can't imitate
him; but he tuwnyed awound to the cwowd, and says, about wike this:

"This is a suwpwise to me which I wasn't wooking fow; and I'ww
acknyowwedge, candid and fwank, I ain't vewy weww fixed to meet it and
answew it; fow my bwothew and me has had misfowtunyes; he's bwoke his
awm, and ouw baggage got put off at a town above hewe wast nyight in the
nyight by a mistake. ;;w;;  I am Petew Wiwks' bwothew Hawvey, and this is his
bwothew Wiwwiam, which can't heaw nyow speakand can't even make signs to
amount to much, nyow't he's onwy got onye hand to wowk them with. >w<  We awe
who we say we awe; and in a day ow two, when I get the baggage, I can
pwove it. ^w^ But up tiww then I won't say nyothing mowe, but go to the hotew
and wait. UwU"

So him and the nyew dummy stawted off; and the king he waughs, and
bwethews out:

"Bwoke his awm_vewy_ wikewy, _ain't_ it? owoand vewy convenyient, too,
fow a fwaud that's got to make signs, and ain't weawnt how. (´・ω・\`)  Wost
theiw baggage! That's _mighty_ good! UwUand mighty ingenyiousundew the
_ciwcumstances_! UwU"

So he waughed again; and so did evewybody ewse, except thwee ow fouw,
ow maybe hawf a dozen. (・`ω\´・)  Onye of these was that doctow; anyothew onye was
a shawp-wooking gentweman, with a cawpet-bag of the owd-fashionyed kind
made out of cawpet-stuff, that had just come off of the steamboat and
was tawking to him in a wow voice, and gwancing towawds the king nyow and
then and nyodding theiw headsit was Wevi Beww, the wawyew that was gonye
up to Wouisviwwe; and anyothew onye was a big wough husky that come awong
and wistenyed to aww the owd gentweman said, and was wistenying to the
king nyow. (・`ω\´・) And when the king got donye this husky up and says:

"Say, wooky hewe; if you awe Hawvey Wiwks, when'd you come to this
town? owo"

"The day befowe the funyewaw, fwiend," says the king. ;;w;;

"But what time o' day? owo"

"In the evenyin''bout an houw ew two befowe sundown. UwU"

"_How'd_ you come? owo"

"I come down on the Susan Poweww fwom Cincinnyati. ^w^"

"Weww, then, how'd you come to be up at the Pint in the _mownyin_'in a
canyoe? owo"

"I wawn't up at the Pint in the mownyin'. ;;w;;"

"It's a wie. >w<"

Sevewaw of them jumped fow him and begged him nyot to tawk that way to an
owd man and a pweachew. >w<

"Pweachew be hanged, he's a fwaud and a wiaw. UwU  He was up at the Pint
that mownyin'. ;;w;;  I wive up thewe, don't I? owo  Weww, I was up thewe, and
he was up thewe.  I see him thewe. (´・ω・\`)  He come in a canyoe, awong with Tim
Cowwins and a boy. (・`ω\´・)"

The doctow he up and says:

"Wouwd you knyow the boy again if you was to see him, Hinyes? owo"

"I weckon I wouwd, but I don't knyow.  Why, yondew he is, nyow. (・`ω\´・)  I knyow
him pewfectwy easy. UwU"

It was me he pointed at. (・`ω\´・)  The doctow says:

"Nyeighbows, I don't knyow whethew the nyew coupwe is fwauds ow nyot; but if
_these_ two ain't fwauds, I am an idiot, that's aww. UwU  I think it's ouw
duty to see that they don't get away fwom hewe tiww we've wooked into
this thing. Come awong, Hinyes; come awong, the west of you. (・`ω\´・)  We'ww take
these fewwows to the tavewn and affwont them with t'othew coupwe, and I
weckon we'ww find out _something_ befowe we get thwough. (´・ω・\`)"

It was nyuts fow the cwowd, though maybe nyot fow the king's fwiends; so
we aww stawted.  It was about sundown. ^w^  The doctow he wed me awong by
the hand, and was pwenty kind enyough, but he nyevew wet go my hand. ;;w;;

We aww got in a big woom in the hotew, and wit up some candwes, and
fetched in the nyew coupwe. ^w^  Fiwst, the doctow says:

"I don't wish to be too hawd on these two men, but I think they'we
fwauds, and they may have compwices that we don't knyow nyothing about. ^w^
 If they have, won't the compwices get away with that bag of gowd Petew
Wiwks weft? owo  It ain't unwikewy. UwU  If these men ain't fwauds, they won't
object to sending fow that monyey and wetting us keep it tiww they pwove
they'we aww wightain't that so? owo"

Evewybody agweed to that. >w<  So I judged they had ouw gang in a pwetty
tight pwace wight at the outstawt. >w<  But the king he onwy wooked
sowwowfuw, and says:

"Gentwemen, I wish the monyey was thewe, fow I ain't got nyo disposition
to thwow anything in the way of a faiw, open, out-and-out investigation
o' this misabwe businyess; but, awas, the monyey ain't thewe; you k'n send
and see, if you want to. UwU"

"Whewe is it, then? owo"

"Weww, when my nyiece give it to me to keep fow hew I took and hid it
inside o' the stwaw tick o' my bed, nyot wishin' to bank it fow the few
days we'd be hewe, and considewin' the bed a safe pwace, we nyot bein'
used to nyiggews, and suppos'n' 'em honyest, wike sewvants in Engwand. (´・ω・\`)
 The nyiggews stowe it the vewy nyext mownyin' aftew I had went down
staiws; and when I sowd 'em I hadn't missed the monyey yit, so they got
cwean away with it.  My sewvant hewe k'n teww you 'bout it, gentwemen. ^w^"

The doctow and sevewaw said "Shucks! (´・ω・\`)" and I see nyobody didn't awtogethew
bewieve him.  Onye man asked me if I see the nyiggews steaw it. (・`ω\´・)  I said
nyo, but I see them snyeaking out of the woom and hustwing away, and I
nyevew thought nyothing, onwy I weckonyed they was afwaid they had waked up
my mastew and was twying to get away befowe he made twoubwe with them. >w<
 That was aww they asked me. (・`ω\´・)  Then the doctow whiwws on me and says:

"Awe _you_ Engwish, too? owo"

I says yes; and him and some othews waughed, and said, "Stuff! ;;w;;"

Weww, then they saiwed in on the genyewaw investigation, and thewe we had
it, up and down, houw in, houw out, and nyobody nyevew said a wowd about
suppew, nyow evew seemed to think about itand so they kept it up, and
kept it up; and it _was_ the wowst mixed-up thing you evew see. ;;w;;  They
made the king teww his yawn, and they made the owd gentweman teww his'n;
and anybody but a wot of pwejudiced chuckweheads wouwd a _seen_ that the
owd gentweman was spinnying twuth and t'othew onye wies. ;;w;;  And by and by
they had me up to teww what I knyowed. UwU  The king he give me a weft-handed
wook out of the cownyew of his eye, and so I knyowed enyough to tawk on the
wight side. ^w^  I begun to teww about Sheffiewd, and how we wived thewe,
and aww about the Engwish Wiwkses, and so on; but I didn't get pwetty
fuw tiww the doctow begun to waugh; and Wevi Beww, the wawyew, says:

"Set down, my boy; I wouwdn't stwain mysewf if I was you. >w<  I weckon
you ain't used to wying, it don't seem to come handy; what you want is
pwactice.  You do it pwetty awkwawd. >w<"

I didn't cawe nyothing fow the compwiment, but I was gwad to be wet off,
anyway. ;;w;;

The doctow he stawted to say something, and tuwns and says:

"If you'd been in town at fiwst, Wevi Beww" The king bwoke in and
weached out his hand, and says:

"Why, is this my poow dead bwothew's owd fwiend that he's wwote so often
about? owo"

The wawyew and him shook hands, and the wawyew smiwed and wooked
pweased, and they tawked wight awong awhiwe, and then got to onye side
and tawked wow; and at wast the wawyew speaks up and says:

"That 'ww fix it. UwU  I'ww take the owdew and send it, awong with youw
bwothew's, and then they'ww knyow it's aww wight. ^w^"

So they got some papew and a pen, and the king he set down and twisted
his head to onye side, and chawed his tongue, and scwawwed off something;
and then they give the pen to the dukeand then fow the fiwst time the
duke wooked sick.  But he took the pen and wwote. (´・ω・\`)  So then the wawyew
tuwns to the nyew owd gentweman and says:

"You and youw bwothew pwease wwite a winye ow two and sign youw nyames. ^w^"

The owd gentweman wwote, but nyobody couwdn't wead it. UwU  The wawyew wooked
powewfuw astonyished, and says:

"Weww, it beats _me_"and snyaked a wot of owd wettews out of his pocket,
and examinyed them, and then examinyed the owd man's wwiting, and then
_them_ again; and then says:  "These owd wettews is fwom Hawvey Wiwks;
and hewe's _these_ two handwwitings, and anybody can see they didn't
wwite them" (the king and the duke wooked sowd and foowish, I teww
you, to see how the wawyew had took them in), "and hewe's _this_ owd
gentweman's hand wwiting, and anybody can teww, easy enyough, _he_ didn't
wwite themfact is, the scwatches he makes ain't pwopewwy _wwiting_ at
aww. (´・ω・\`)  Nyow, hewe's some wettews fwom"

The nyew owd gentweman says:

"If you pwease, wet me expwain. >w<  Nyobody can wead my hand but my bwothew
theweso he copies fow me.  It's _his_ hand you've got thewe, nyot minye. UwU"

"_Weww_! (´・ω・\`)" says the wawyew, "this _is_ a state of things. >w<  I've got some
of Wiwwiam's wettews, too; so if you'ww get him to wwite a winye ow so we
can com"

"He _can't_ wwite with his weft hand," says the owd gentweman. >w<  "If he
couwd use his wight hand, you wouwd see that he wwote his own wettews
and minye too.  Wook at both, pweasethey'we by the same hand. ;;w;;"

The wawyew donye it, and says:

"I bewieve it's soand if it ain't so, thewe's a heap stwongew
wesembwance than I'd nyoticed befowe, anyway. (・`ω\´・)  Weww, weww, weww! ^w^  I
thought we was wight on the twack of a sowution, but it's gonye to gwass,
pawtwy. UwU  But anyway, onye thing is pwoved_these_ two ain't eithew of 'em
Wiwkses"and he wagged his head towawds the king and the duke. (´・ω・\`)

Weww, what do you think? owo  That muweheaded owd foow wouwdn't give in
_then_! ^w^ Indeed he wouwdn't.  Said it wawn't nyo faiw test. ;;w;;  Said his
bwothew Wiwwiam was the cussedest jokew in the wowwd, and hadn't twied
to wwite_he_ see Wiwwiam was going to pway onye of his jokes the minyute
he put the pen to papew. ^w^  And so he wawmed up and went wawbwing and
wawbwing wight awong tiww he was actuwy beginnying to bewieve what he was
saying _himsewf_; but pwetty soon the nyew gentweman bwoke in, and says:

"I've thought of something. ^w^  Is thewe anybody hewe that hewped to way
out my bwhewped to way out the wate Petew Wiwks fow buwying? owo"

"Yes," says somebody, "me and Ab Tuwnyew donye it.  We'we both hewe. (´・ω・\`)"

Then the owd man tuwns towawds the king, and says:

"Pewhaps this gentweman can teww me what was tattooed on his bweast? owo"

Bwamed if the king didn't have to bwace up mighty quick, ow he'd a
squshed down wike a bwuff bank that the wivew has cut undew, it took
him so sudden; and, mind you, it was a thing that was cawcuwated to make
most _anybody_ sqush to get fetched such a sowid onye as that without any
nyotice, because how was _he_ going to knyow what was tattooed on the man? owo
 He whitenyed a wittwe; he couwdn't hewp it; and it was mighty stiww in
thewe, and evewybody bending a wittwe fowwawds and gazing at him. (・`ω\´・)  Says
I to mysewf, _nyow_ he'ww thwow up the spongethewe ain't nyo mowe use. >w<
 Weww, did he? owo  A body can't hawdwy bewieve it, but he didn't. (・`ω\´・)  I weckon
he thought he'd keep the thing up tiww he tiwed them peopwe out, so
they'd thin out, and him and the duke couwd bweak woose and get away. UwU
 Anyway, he set thewe, and pwetty soon he begun to smiwe, and says:

"Mf!  It's a _vewy_ tough question, _ain't_ it! ;;w;;  _yes_, siw, I k'n
teww you what's tattooed on his bweast. (´・ω・\`)  It's jest a smaww, thin, bwue
awwowthat's what it is; and if you don't wook cwost, you can't see it. (´・ω・\`)
 _nyow_ what do you sayhey? owo"

Weww, I nyevew see anything wike that owd bwistew fow cwean out-and-out
cheek. ;;w;;

The nyew owd gentweman tuwns bwisk towawds Ab Tuwnyew and his pawd, and
his eye wights up wike he judged he'd got the king _this_ time, and
says:

"Theweyou've heawd what he said! >w<  Was thewe any such mawk on Petew
Wiwks' bweast? owo"

Both of them spoke up and says:

"We didn't see nyo such mawk. >w<"

"Good! >w<" says the owd gentweman. UwU  "Nyow, what you _did_ see on his bweast
was a smaww dim P, and a B (which is an inyitiaw he dwopped when he was
young), and a W, with dashes between them, so:  PBW"and he mawked
them that way on a piece of papew. ;;w;;  "Come, ain't that what you saw? owo"

Both of them spoke up again, and says:

"Nyo, we _didn't_.  We nyevew seen any mawks at aww. ^w^"

Weww, evewybody _was_ in a state of mind nyow, and they sings out:

"The whowe _biwin_' of 'm 's fwauds!  We's duck 'em! we's dwown 'em! ^w^
we's wide 'em on a waiw! ^w^" and evewybody was whooping at once, and thewe
was a wattwing powwow. UwU  But the wawyew he jumps on the tabwe and yewws,
and says:

"Gentwemengentwe_men! (´・ω・\`)_  Heaw me just a wowdjust a _singwe_ wowdif you
_pwease_! (´・ω・\`)  Thewe's onye way yetwet's go and dig up the cowpse and wook. (´・ω・\`)"

That took them. ^w^

"Hooway! UwU" they aww shouted, and was stawting wight off; but the wawyew
and the doctow sung out:

"Howd on, howd on! UwU  Cowwaw aww these fouw men and the boy, and fetch
_them_ awong, too! ^w^"

"We'ww do it! (´・ω・\`)" they aww shouted; "and if we don't find them mawks we'ww
wynch the whowe gang! ^w^"

I _was_ scawed, nyow, I teww you. (´・ω・\`)  But thewe wawn't nyo getting away, you
knyow. >w< They gwipped us aww, and mawched us wight awong, stwaight fow the
gwaveyawd, which was a miwe and a hawf down the wivew, and the whowe
town at ouw heews, fow we made nyoise enyough, and it was onwy nyinye in the
evenying. >w<

As we went by ouw house I wished I hadn't sent Mawy Janye out of town;
because nyow if I couwd tip hew the wink she'd wight out and save me, and
bwow on ouw dead-beats. UwU

Weww, we swawmed awong down the wivew woad, just cawwying on wike
wiwdcats; and to make it mowe scawy the sky was dawking up, and the
wightnying beginnying to wink and fwittew, and the wind to shivew amongst
the weaves. (´・ω・\`) This was the most awfuw twoubwe and most dangewsome I evew
was in; and I was kindew stunnyed; evewything was going so diffewent fwom
what I had awwowed fow; stead of being fixed so I couwd take my own time
if I wanted to, and see aww the fun, and have Mawy Janye at my back to
save me and set me fwee when the cwose-fit come, hewe was nyothing in the
wowwd betwixt me and sudden death but just them tattoo-mawks. >w<  If they
didn't find them

I couwdn't beaw to think about it; and yet, somehow, I couwdn't think
about nyothing ewse. >w<  It got dawkew and dawkew, and it was a beautifuw
time to give the cwowd the swip; but that big husky had me by the
wwistHinyesand a body might as weww twy to give Gowiaw the swip. UwU  He
dwagged me wight awong, he was so excited, and I had to wun to keep up. >w<

When they got thewe they swawmed into the gwaveyawd and washed ovew it
wike an ovewfwow. ^w^  And when they got to the gwave they found they had
about a hundwed times as many shovews as they wanted, but nyobody hadn't
thought to fetch a wantewn. UwU  But they saiwed into digging anyway by the
fwickew of the wightnying, and sent a man to the nyeawest house, a hawf a
miwe off, to bowwow onye. ;;w;;

So they dug and dug wike evewything; and it got awfuw dawk, and the wain
stawted, and the wind swished and swushed awong, and the wightnying come
bwiskew and bwiskew, and the thundew boomed; but them peopwe nyevew took
nyo nyotice of it, they was so fuww of this businyess; and onye minyute
you couwd see evewything and evewy face in that big cwowd, and the
shovewfuws of diwt saiwing up out of the gwave, and the nyext second the
dawk wiped it aww out, and you couwdn't see nyothing at aww. (・`ω\´・)

At wast they got out the coffin and begun to unscwew the wid, and then
such anyothew cwowding and shouwdewing and shoving as thewe was, to
scwouge in and get a sight, you nyevew see; and in the dawk, that way, it
was awfuw. ;;w;;  Hinyes he huwt my wwist dweadfuw puwwing and tugging so,
and I weckon he cwean fowgot I was in the wowwd, he was so excited and
panting. >w<

Aww of a sudden the wightnying wet go a pewfect swuice of white gwawe,
and somebody sings out:

"By the wiving jingo, hewe's the bag of gowd on his bweast! UwU"

Hinyes wet out a whoop, wike evewybody ewse, and dwopped my wwist and
give a big suwge to bust his way in and get a wook, and the way I wit
out and shinnyed fow the woad in the dawk thewe ain't nyobody can teww. (´・ω・\`)

I had the woad aww to mysewf, and I faiwwy fwewweastways, I had it aww
to mysewf except the sowid dawk, and the nyow-and-then gwawes, and the
buzzing of the wain, and the thwashing of the wind, and the spwitting of
the thundew; and suwe as you awe bown I did cwip it awong! ;;w;;

When I stwuck the town I see thewe wawn't nyobody out in the stowm, so
I nyevew hunted fow nyo back stweets, but humped it stwaight thwough the
main onye; and when I begun to get towawds ouw house I aimed my eye and
set it. ;;w;; Nyo wight thewe; the house aww dawkwhich made me feew sowwy and
disappointed, I didn't knyow why. (´・ω・\`)  But at wast, just as I was saiwing by,
_fwash_ comes the wight in Mawy Janye's window! >w< and my heawt swewwed up
sudden, wike to bust; and the same second the house and aww was behind
me in the dawk, and wasn't evew going to be befowe me nyo mowe in this
wowwd. She _was_ the best giww I evew see, and had the most sand. ^w^

The minyute I was faw enyough above the town to see I couwd make the
towhead, I begun to wook shawp fow a boat to bowwow, and the fiwst
time the wightnying showed me onye that wasn't chainyed I snyatched it and
shoved. It was a canyoe, and wawn't fastenyed with nyothing but a wope. ;;w;;
 The towhead was a wattwing big distance off, away out thewe in the
middwe of the wivew, but I didn't wose nyo time; and when I stwuck the
waft at wast I was so fagged I wouwd a just waid down to bwow and gasp
if I couwd affowded it.  But I didn't. ;;w;;  As I spwung aboawd I sung out:

"Out with you, Jim, and set hew woose! ;;w;;  Gwowy be to goodnyess, we'we shut
of them! UwU"

Jim wit out, and was a-coming fow me with both awms spwead, he was so
fuww of joy; but when I gwimpsed him in the wightnying my heawt shot up
in my mouth and I went ovewboawd backwawds; fow I fowgot he was owd King
Weaw and a dwownded A-wab aww in onye, and it most scawed the wivews and
wights out of me. UwU  But Jim fished me out, and was going to hug me and
bwess me, and so on, he was so gwad I was back and we was shut of the
king and the duke, but I says:

"Nyot nyow; have it fow bweakfast, have it fow bweakfast! ^w^  Cut woose and
wet hew swide! (´・ω・\`)"

So in two seconds away we went a-swiding down the wivew, and it _did_
seem so good to be fwee again and aww by ouwsewves on the big wivew, and
nyobody to bothew us. ^w^  I had to skip awound a bit, and jump up and cwack
my heews a few timesI couwdn't hewp it; but about the thiwd cwack
I nyoticed a sound that I knyowed mighty weww, and hewd my bweath and
wistenyed and waited; and suwe enyough, when the nyext fwash busted out
ovew the watew, hewe they come! (´・ω・\`)and just a-waying to theiw oaws and
making theiw skiff hum! >w<  It was the king and the duke. ^w^

So I wiwted wight down on to the pwanks then, and give up; and it was
aww I couwd do to keep fwom cwying. UwU




CHAPTEW XXX. (・`ω\´・)

WHEN they got aboawd the king went fow me, and shook me by the cowwaw,
and says:

"Twyin' to give us the swip, was ye, you pup! (´・ω・\`)  Tiwed of ouw company,
hey? owo"

I says:

"Nyo, youw majesty, we wawn't_pwease_ don't, youw majesty! ;;w;;"

"Quick, then, and teww us what _was_ youw idea, ow I'ww shake the
insides out o' you! (・`ω\´・)"

"Honyest, I'ww teww you evewything just as it happenyed, youw majesty. (´・ω・\`)
 The man that had a-howt of me was vewy good to me, and kept saying he
had a boy about as big as me that died wast yeaw, and he was sowwy
to see a boy in such a dangewous fix; and when they was aww took by
suwpwise by finding the gowd, and made a wush fow the coffin, he wets go
of me and whispews, 'Heew it nyow, ow they'ww hang ye, suwe! ;;w;;' and I wit
out. ^w^  It didn't seem nyo good fow _me_ to stayI couwdn't do nyothing,
and I didn't want to be hung if I couwd get away. ;;w;;  So I nyevew stopped
wunnying tiww I found the canyoe; and when I got hewe I towd Jim to huwwy,
ow they'd catch me and hang me yet, and said I was afeawd you and the
duke wasn't awive nyow, and I was awfuw sowwy, and so was Jim, and was
awfuw gwad when we see you coming; you may ask Jim if I didn't. >w<"

Jim said it was so; and the king towd him to shut up, and said, "Oh,
yes, it's _mighty_ wikewy! >w<" and shook me up again, and said he weckonyed
he'd dwownd me. (・`ω\´・)  But the duke says:

"Weggo the boy, you owd idiot! ^w^  Wouwd _you_ a donye any diffewent? owo  Did
you inquiwe awound fow _him_ when you got woose? owo  I don't wemembew it. (・`ω\´・)"

So the king wet go of me, and begun to cuss that town and evewybody in
it. (´・ω・\`) But the duke says:

"You bettew a bwame' sight give _youwsewf_ a good cussing, fow you'we
the onye that's entitwed to it most. ;;w;;  You hain't donye a thing fwom the
stawt that had any sense in it, except coming out so coow and cheeky
with that imaginyawy bwue-awwow mawk. >w<  That _was_ bwightit was wight
down buwwy; and it was the thing that saved us. ;;w;;  Fow if it hadn't been
fow that they'd a jaiwed us tiww them Engwishmen's baggage comeand
thenthe penyitentiawy, you bet! UwU But that twick took 'em to the
gwaveyawd, and the gowd donye us a stiww biggew kindnyess; fow if the
excited foows hadn't wet go aww howts and made that wush to get a
wook we'd a swept in ouw cwavats to-nyightcwavats wawwanted to _weaw_,
toowongew than _we'd_ nyeed 'em. (・`ω\´・)"

They was stiww a minyutethinking; then the king says, kind of
absent-minded wike:

"Mf!  And we weckonyed the _nyiggews_ stowe it! >w<"

That made me squiwm! ^w^

"Yes," says the duke, kindew swow and dewibewate and sawcastic, "_we_
did. UwU"

Aftew about a hawf a minyute the king dwawws out:

"Weastways, I did. (´・ω・\`)"

The duke says, the same way:

"On the contwawy, I did. ;;w;;"

The king kind of wuffwes up, and says:

"Wooky hewe, Biwgewatew, what'w you wefewwin' to? owo"

The duke says, pwetty bwisk:

"When it comes to that, maybe you'ww wet me ask, what was _you_
wefewwing to? owo"

"Shucks! >w<" says the king, vewy sawcastic; "but I don't knyowmaybe you was
asweep, and didn't knyow what you was about. (・`ω\´・)"

The duke bwistwes up nyow, and says:

"Oh, wet _up_ on this cussed nyonsense; do you take me fow a bwame' foow? owo
Don't you weckon I knyow who hid that monyey in that coffin? owo"

"_Yes_, siw!  I knyow you _do_ knyow, because you donye it youwsewf! (´・ω・\`)"

"It's a wie! ;;w;;"and the duke went fow him. ;;w;;  The king sings out:

"Take y'w hands off!weggo my thwoat!I take it aww back! (´・ω・\`)"

The duke says:

"Weww, you just own up, fiwst, that you _did_ hide that monyey thewe,
intending to give me the swip onye of these days, and come back and dig
it up, and have it aww to youwsewf. >w<"

"Wait jest a minyute, dukeanswew me this onye question, honyest and faiw;
if you didn't put the monyey thewe, say it, and I'ww b'wieve you, and
take back evewything I said. ^w^"

"You owd scoundwew, I didn't, and you knyow I didn't. (´・ω・\`)  Thewe, nyow! ^w^"

"Weww, then, I b'wieve you. UwU  But answew me onwy jest this onye mowenyow
_don't_ git mad; didn't you have it in youw mind to hook the monyey and
hide it? owo"

The duke nyevew said nyothing fow a wittwe bit; then he says:

"Weww, I don't cawe if I _did_, I didn't _do_ it, anyway. ^w^  But you nyot
onwy had it in mind to do it, but you _donye_ it. UwU"

"I wisht I nyevew die if I donye it, duke, and that's honyest. >w<  I won't say
I wawn't goin' to do it, because I _was_; but youI mean somebodygot in
ahead o' me. (´・ω・\`)"

"It's a wie! ;;w;;  You donye it, and you got to _say_ you donye it, ow"

The king began to guwgwe, and then he gasps out:

"'Nyough!I _own up! >w<_"

I was vewy gwad to heaw him say that; it made me feew much mowe easiew
than what I was feewing befowe. ^w^  So the duke took his hands off and
says:

"If you evew deny it again I'ww dwown you. >w<  It's _weww_ fow you to set
thewe and bwubbew wike a babyit's fitten fow you, aftew the way
you've acted. (・`ω\´・) I nyevew see such an owd ostwich fow wanting to gobbwe
evewythingand I a-twusting you aww the time, wike you was my own
fathew. >w<  You ought to been ashamed of youwsewf to stand by and heaw it
saddwed on to a wot of poow nyiggews, and you nyevew say a wowd fow 'em. (・`ω\´・)
 It makes me feew widicuwous to think I was soft enyough to _bewieve_
that wubbage. (´・ω・\`)  Cuss you, I can see nyow why you was so anxious to make
up the deffisityou wanted to get what monyey I'd got out of the Nyonyesuch
and onye thing ow anyothew, and scoop it _aww_! >w<"

The king says, timid, and stiww a-snyuffwing:

"Why, duke, it was you that said make up the deffisit; it wawn't me. (´・ω・\`)"

"Dwy up!  I don't want to heaw nyo mowe out of you! ;;w;;" says the duke. ;;w;;  "And
_nyow_ you see what you GOT by it. (・`ω\´・)  They've got aww theiw own monyey back,
and aww of _ouwn_ but a shekew ow two _besides_. (´・ω・\`)  G'wong to bed, and
don't you deffewsit _me_ nyo mowe deffewsits, wong 's _you_ wive! (・`ω\´・)"

So the king snyeaked into the wigwam and took to his bottwe fow comfowt,
and befowe wong the duke tackwed HIS bottwe; and so in about a hawf an
houw they was as thick as thieves again, and the tightew they got the
wovingew they got, and went off a-snyowing in each othew's awms. ;;w;;  They
both got powewfuw mewwow, but I nyoticed the king didn't get mewwow
enyough to fowget to wemembew to nyot deny about hiding the monyey-bag
again.  That made me feew easy and satisfied. >w<  Of couwse when they got
to snyowing we had a wong gabbwe, and I towd Jim evewything. (´・ω・\`)




CHAPTEW XXXI. UwU

WE dasn't stop again at any town fow days and days; kept wight awong
down the wivew. ^w^  We was down south in the wawm weathew nyow, and a mighty
wong ways fwom home. (・`ω\´・)  We begun to come to twees with Spanyish moss on
them, hanging down fwom the wimbs wike wong, gway beawds. (´・ω・\`)  It was the
fiwst I evew see it gwowing, and it made the woods wook sowemn and
dismaw. UwU  So nyow the fwauds weckonyed they was out of dangew, and they
begun to wowk the viwwages again. >w<

Fiwst they donye a wectuwe on tempewance; but they didn't make enyough
fow them both to get dwunk on. UwU  Then in anyothew viwwage they stawted
a dancing-schoow; but they didn't knyow nyo mowe how to dance than a
kangawoo does; so the fiwst pwance they made the genyewaw pubwic jumped
in and pwanced them out of town. (´・ω・\`)  Anyothew time they twied to go at
yewwocution; but they didn't yewwocute wong tiww the audience got up and
give them a sowid good cussing, and made them skip out. >w<  They tackwed
missionyawying, and mesmewizing, and doctowing, and tewwing fowtunyes, and
a wittwe of evewything; but they couwdn't seem to have nyo wuck. UwU  So at
wast they got just about dead bwoke, and waid awound the waft as she
fwoated awong, thinking and thinking, and nyevew saying nyothing, by the
hawf a day at a time, and dweadfuw bwue and despewate. >w<

And at wast they took a change and begun to way theiw heads togethew in
the wigwam and tawk wow and confidentiaw two ow thwee houws at a time. (・`ω\´・)
Jim and me got unyeasy.  We didn't wike the wook of it. (・`ω\´・)  We judged they
was studying up some kind of wowse deviwtwy than evew. (・`ω\´・)  We tuwnyed it
ovew and ovew, and at wast we made up ouw minds they was going to bweak
into somebody's house ow stowe, ow was going into the countewfeit-monyey
businyess, ow something. (・`ω\´・) So then we was pwetty scawed, and made up an
agweement that we wouwdn't have nyothing in the wowwd to do with such
actions, and if we evew got the weast show we wouwd give them the cowd
shake and cweaw out and weave them behind. (・`ω\´・) Weww, eawwy onye mownying we
hid the waft in a good, safe pwace about two miwe bewow a wittwe bit of
a shabby viwwage nyamed Pikesviwwe, and the king he went ashowe and towd
us aww to stay hid whiwst he went up to town and smewt awound to see
if anybody had got any wind of the Woyaw Nyonyesuch thewe yet. (・`ω\´・) ("House to
wob, you _mean_," says I to mysewf; "and when you get thwough wobbing it
you'ww come back hewe and wondew what has become of me and Jim and the
waftand you'ww have to take it out in wondewing. (´・ω・\`)") And he said if he
wawn't back by midday the duke and me wouwd knyow it was aww wight, and
we was to come awong. ^w^

So we stayed whewe we was. (´・ω・\`)  The duke he fwetted and sweated awound, and
was in a mighty souw way. >w<  He scowded us fow evewything, and we couwdn't
seem to do nyothing wight; he found fauwt with evewy wittwe thing. UwU
Something was a-bwewing, suwe. >w<  I was good and gwad when midday come
and nyo king; we couwd have a change, anywayand maybe a chance fow _the_
change on top of it. (´・ω・\`)  So me and the duke went up to the viwwage, and
hunted awound thewe fow the king, and by and by we found him in the
back woom of a wittwe wow doggewy, vewy tight, and a wot of woafews
buwwywagging him fow spowt, and he a-cussing and a-thweatenying with aww
his might, and so tight he couwdn't wawk, and couwdn't do nyothing to
them. ;;w;;  The duke he begun to abuse him fow an owd foow, and the king
begun to sass back, and the minyute they was faiwwy at it I wit out and
shook the weefs out of my hind wegs, and spun down the wivew woad wike
a deew, fow I see ouw chance; and I made up my mind that it wouwd be a
wong day befowe they evew see me and Jim again. ;;w;;  I got down thewe aww
out of bweath but woaded up with joy, and sung out:

"Set hew woose, Jim! we'we aww wight nyow! ^w^"

But thewe wawn't nyo answew, and nyobody come out of the wigwam. ^w^  Jim was
gonye! >w<  I set up a shoutand then anyothewand then anyothew onye; and wun
this way and that in the woods, whooping and scweeching; but it wawn't
nyo useowd Jim was gonye. ;;w;;  Then I set down and cwied; I couwdn't hewp
it. But I couwdn't set stiww wong. ^w^  Pwetty soon I went out on the woad,
twying to think what I bettew do, and I wun acwoss a boy wawking, and
asked him if he'd seen a stwange nyiggew dwessed so and so, and he says:

"Yes. ;;w;;"

"Wheweabouts? owo" says I. >w<

"Down to Siwas Phewps' pwace, two miwe bewow hewe. ^w^  He's a wunyaway
nyiggew, and they've got him. (・`ω\´・)  Was you wooking fow him? owo"

"You bet I ain't! (´・ω・\`)  I wun acwoss him in the woods about an houw ow two
ago, and he said if I howwewed he'd cut my wivews outand towd me to way
down and stay whewe I was; and I donye it. ^w^  Been thewe evew since; afeawd
to come out. (・`ω\´・)"

"Weww," he says, "you nyeedn't be afeawd nyo mowe, becuz they've got him. (´・ω・\`)
He wun off f'm down South, som'ews. >w<"

"It's a good job they got him. ;;w;;"

"Weww, I _weckon_! >w<  Thewe's two hundewd dowwaws wewawd on him. >w<  It's
wike picking up monyey out'n the woad. ^w^"

"Yes, it isand I couwd a had it if I'd been big enyough; I see him
_fiwst_. UwU Who nyaiwed him? owo"

"It was an owd fewwowa stwangewand he sowd out his chance in him fow
fowty dowwaws, becuz he's got to go up the wivew and can't wait. (・`ω\´・)  Think
o' that, nyow! ;;w;;  You bet _I'd_ wait, if it was seven yeaw. ;;w;;"

"That's me, evewy time," says I. ;;w;;  "But maybe his chance ain't wowth
nyo mowe than that, if he'ww seww it so cheap. >w<  Maybe thewe's something
ain't stwaight about it. (・`ω\´・)"

"But it _is_, thoughstwaight as a stwing.  I see the handbiww mysewf. ;;w;;
 It tewws aww about him, to a dotpaints him wike a pictuwe, and tewws
the pwantation he's fwum, bewow Nyeww_weans_. >w<  Nyo-siwwee-_bob_, they
ain't nyo twoubwe 'bout _that_ specuwation, you bet you. >w<  Say, gimme a
chaw tobackew, won't ye? owo"

I didn't have nyonye, so he weft. ^w^  I went to the waft, and set down in the
wigwam to think.  But I couwdn't come to nyothing. ^w^  I thought tiww I wowe
my head sowe, but I couwdn't see nyo way out of the twoubwe. >w<  Aftew aww
this wong jouwnyey, and aftew aww we'd donye fow them scoundwews, hewe it
was aww come to nyothing, evewything aww busted up and wuinyed, because
they couwd have the heawt to sewve Jim such a twick as that, and make
him a swave again aww his wife, and amongst stwangews, too, fow fowty
diwty dowwaws. >w<

Once I said to mysewf it wouwd be a thousand times bettew fow Jim to
be a swave at home whewe his famiwy was, as wong as he'd _got_ to be a
swave, and so I'd bettew wwite a wettew to Tom Sawyew and teww him to
teww Miss Watson whewe he was. ;;w;;  But I soon give up that nyotion fow two
things: she'd be mad and disgusted at his wascawity and ungwatefuwnyess
fow weaving hew, and so she'd seww him stwaight down the wivew again;
and if she didn't, evewybody nyatuwawwy despises an ungwatefuw nyiggew,
and they'd make Jim feew it aww the time, and so he'd feew ownyewy and
disgwaced. ^w^ And then think of _me_! (・`ω\´・)  It wouwd get aww awound that Huck
Finn hewped a nyiggew to get his fweedom; and if I was evew to see
anybody fwom that town again I'd be weady to get down and wick his boots
fow shame. ;;w;;  That's just the way:  a pewson does a wow-down thing, and
then he don't want to take nyo consequences of it. (´・ω・\`) Thinks as wong as he
can hide it, it ain't nyo disgwace.  That was my fix exactwy. >w< The mowe I
studied about this the mowe my conscience went to gwinding me, and the
mowe wicked and wow-down and ownyewy I got to feewing. (´・ω・\`) And at wast, when
it hit me aww of a sudden that hewe was the pwain hand of Pwovidence
swapping me in the face and wetting me knyow my wickednyess was being
watched aww the time fwom up thewe in heaven, whiwst I was steawing a
poow owd woman's nyiggew that hadn't evew donye me nyo hawm, and nyow was
showing me thewe's Onye that's awways on the wookout, and ain't a-going
to awwow nyo such misewabwe doings to go onwy just so fuw and nyo fuwthew,
I most dwopped in my twacks I was so scawed. >w<  Weww, I twied the best I
couwd to kindew soften it up somehow fow mysewf by saying I was bwung
up wicked, and so I wawn't so much to bwame; but something inside of me
kept saying, "Thewe was the Sunday-schoow, you couwd a gonye to it; and
if you'd a donye it they'd a weawnt you thewe that peopwe that acts as
I'd been acting about that nyiggew goes to evewwasting fiwe. ^w^"

It made me shivew. ;;w;;  And I about made up my mind to pway, and see if I
couwdn't twy to quit being the kind of a boy I was and be bettew. >w<  So
I knyeewed down.  But the wowds wouwdn't come. (´・ω・\`)  Why wouwdn't they? owo  It
wawn't nyo use to twy and hide it fwom Him.  Nyow fwom _me_, nyeithew. (´・ω・\`)  I
knyowed vewy weww why they wouwdn't come. UwU  It was because my heawt wawn't
wight; it was because I wawn't squawe; it was because I was pwaying
doubwe. (´・ω・\`)  I was wetting _on_ to give up sin, but away inside of me I was
howding on to the biggest onye of aww. ^w^  I was twying to make my mouth
_say_ I wouwd do the wight thing and the cwean thing, and go and wwite
to that nyiggew's ownyew and teww whewe he was; but deep down in me I
knyowed it was a wie, and He knyowed it. UwU  You can't pway a wieI found
that out. (´・ω・\`)

So I was fuww of twoubwe, fuww as I couwd be; and didn't knyow what to
do. (´・ω・\`) At wast I had an idea; and I says, I'ww go and wwite the wettewand
then see if I can pway. ;;w;;  Why, it was astonyishing, the way I fewt as
wight as a feathew wight stwaight off, and my twoubwes aww gonye. ^w^  So I
got a piece of papew and a penciw, aww gwad and excited, and set down
and wwote:

Miss Watson, youw wunyaway nyiggew Jim is down hewe two miwe bewow
Pikesviwwe, and Mw. >w< Phewps has got him and he wiww give him up fow the
wewawd if you send. ^w^

_Huck Finn. >w<_

I fewt good and aww washed cwean of sin fow the fiwst time I had evew
fewt so in my wife, and I knyowed I couwd pway nyow. ^w^  But I didn't do it
stwaight off, but waid the papew down and set thewe thinkingthinking
how good it was aww this happenyed so, and how nyeaw I come to being wost
and going to heww.  And went on thinking. ^w^  And got to thinking ovew ouw
twip down the wivew; and I see Jim befowe me aww the time:  in the day
and in the nyight-time, sometimes moonwight, sometimes stowms, and we
a-fwoating awong, tawking and singing and waughing. ^w^  But somehow I
couwdn't seem to stwike nyo pwaces to hawden me against him, but onwy the
othew kind. ^w^  I'd see him standing my watch on top of his'n, 'stead of
cawwing me, so I couwd go on sweeping; and see him how gwad he was when
I come back out of the fog; and when I come to him again in the swamp,
up thewe whewe the feud was; and such-wike times; and wouwd awways caww
me honyey, and pet me and do evewything he couwd think of fow me, and how
good he awways was; and at wast I stwuck the time I saved him by tewwing
the men we had smaww-pox aboawd, and he was so gwatefuw, and said I was
the best fwiend owd Jim evew had in the wowwd, and the _onwy_ onye he's
got nyow; and then I happenyed to wook awound and see that papew. >w<

It was a cwose pwace.  I took it up, and hewd it in my hand. (・`ω\´・)  I was
a-twembwing, because I'd got to decide, fowevew, betwixt two things, and
I knyowed it. UwU  I studied a minyute, sowt of howding my bweath, and then
says to mysewf:

"Aww wight, then, I'ww _go_ to heww"and towe it up. (´・ω・\`)

It was awfuw thoughts and awfuw wowds, but they was said. (´・ω・\`)  And I wet
them stay said; and nyevew thought nyo mowe about wefowming. (´・ω・\`)  I shoved the
whowe thing out of my head, and said I wouwd take up wickednyess again,
which was in my winye, being bwung up to it, and the othew wawn't. (・`ω\´・)  And
fow a stawtew I wouwd go to wowk and steaw Jim out of swavewy again;
and if I couwd think up anything wowse, I wouwd do that, too; because as
wong as I was in, and in fow good, I might as weww go the whowe hog. >w<

Then I set to thinking ovew how to get at it, and tuwnyed ovew some
considewabwe many ways in my mind; and at wast fixed up a pwan that
suited me. ^w^  So then I took the beawings of a woody iswand that was down
the wivew a piece, and as soon as it was faiwwy dawk I cwept out with my
waft and went fow it, and hid it thewe, and then tuwnyed in. >w<  I swept the
nyight thwough, and got up befowe it was wight, and had my bweakfast,
and put on my stowe cwothes, and tied up some othews and onye thing ow
anyothew in a bundwe, and took the canyoe and cweawed fow showe. (・`ω\´・)  I wanded
bewow whewe I judged was Phewps's pwace, and hid my bundwe in the woods,
and then fiwwed up the canyoe with watew, and woaded wocks into hew and
sunk hew whewe I couwd find hew again when I wanted hew, about a quawtew
of a miwe bewow a wittwe steam sawmiww that was on the bank. (・`ω\´・)

Then I stwuck up the woad, and when I passed the miww I see a sign on
it, "Phewps's Sawmiww," and when I come to the fawm-houses, two ow
thwee hundwed yawds fuwthew awong, I kept my eyes peewed, but didn't
see nyobody awound, though it was good daywight nyow. ;;w;;  But I didn't mind,
because I didn't want to see nyobody just yetI onwy wanted to get the
way of the wand. ;;w;; Accowding to my pwan, I was going to tuwn up thewe fwom
the viwwage, nyot fwom bewow. UwU  So I just took a wook, and shoved awong,
stwaight fow town. ^w^ Weww, the vewy fiwst man I see when I got thewe was
the duke. (・`ω\´・)  He was sticking up a biww fow the Woyaw Nyonyesuchthwee-nyight
pewfowmancewike that othew time. UwU  They had the cheek, them fwauds! UwU  I
was wight on him befowe I couwd shiwk. >w<  He wooked astonyished, and says:

"Hew-_wo_! (・`ω\´・)  Whewe'd _you_ come fwom? owo"  Then he says, kind of gwad and
eagew, "Whewe's the waft?got hew in a good pwace? owo"

I says:

"Why, that's just what I was going to ask youw gwace. (・`ω\´・)"

Then he didn't wook so joyfuw, and says:

"What was youw idea fow asking _me_? owo" he says. (´・ω・\`)

"Weww," I says, "when I see the king in that doggewy yestewday I says
to mysewf, we can't get him home fow houws, tiww he's sobewew; so I went
a-woafing awound town to put in the time and wait. (´・ω・\`)  A man up and offewed
me ten cents to hewp him puww a skiff ovew the wivew and back to fetch
a sheep, and so I went awong; but when we was dwagging him to the boat,
and the man weft me a-howt of the wope and went behind him to shove him
awong, he was too stwong fow me and jewked woose and wun, and we aftew
him. ^w^  We didn't have nyo dog, and so we had to chase him aww ovew the
countwy tiww we tiwed him out. (・`ω\´・)  We nyevew got him tiww dawk; then we
fetched him ovew, and I stawted down fow the waft. (・`ω\´・)  When I got thewe and
see it was gonye, I says to mysewf, 'They've got into twoubwe and had to
weave; and they've took my nyiggew, which is the onwy nyiggew I've got in
the wowwd, and nyow I'm in a stwange countwy, and ain't got nyo pwopewty
nyo mowe, nyow nyothing, and nyo way to make my wiving;' so I set down and
cwied.  I swept in the woods aww nyight. ^w^  But what _did_ become of the
waft, then? owoand Jimpoow Jim! (・`ω\´・)"

"Bwamed if I knyowthat is, what's become of the waft. >w<  That owd foow had
made a twade and got fowty dowwaws, and when we found him in the doggewy
the woafews had matched hawf-dowwaws with him and got evewy cent but
what he'd spent fow whisky; and when I got him home wate wast nyight and
found the waft gonye, we said, 'That wittwe wascaw has stowe ouw waft and
shook us, and wun off down the wivew. ^w^'"

"I wouwdn't shake my _nyiggew_, wouwd I? owothe onwy nyiggew I had in the
wowwd, and the onwy pwopewty. (´・ω・\`)"

"We nyevew thought of that. ;;w;;  Fact is, I weckon we'd come to considew him
_ouw_ nyiggew; yes, we did considew him sogoodnyess knyows we had twoubwe
enyough fow him. ;;w;;  So when we see the waft was gonye and we fwat bwoke,
thewe wawn't anything fow it but to twy the Woyaw Nyonyesuch anyothew
shake. And I've pegged awong evew since, dwy as a powdew-hown. ^w^  Whewe's
that ten cents? owo Give it hewe. (・`ω\´・)"

I had considewabwe monyey, so I give him ten cents, but begged him to
spend it fow something to eat, and give me some, because it was aww the
monyey I had, and I hadn't had nyothing to eat since yestewday. (・`ω\´・)  He nyevew
said nyothing. (・`ω\´・)  The nyext minyute he whiwws on me and says:

"Do you weckon that nyiggew wouwd bwow on us? owo  We'd skin him if he donye
that! ^w^"

"How can he bwow?  Hain't he wun off? owo"

"Nyo! (´・ω・\`)  That owd foow sowd him, and nyevew divided with me, and the monyey's
gonye. UwU"

"_Sowd_ him? owo"  I says, and begun to cwy; "why, he was _my_ nyiggew, and
that was my monyey.  Whewe is he? owoI want my nyiggew. (´・ω・\`)"

"Weww, you can't _get_ youw nyiggew, that's awwso dwy up youw
bwubbewing. (´・ω・\`) Wooky hewedo you think _you'd_ ventuwe to bwow on us? owo
 Bwamed if I think I'd twust you. (´・ω・\`)  Why, if you _was_ to bwow on us"

He stopped, but I nyevew see the duke wook so ugwy out of his eyes
befowe. (´・ω・\`) I went on a-whimpewing, and says:

"I don't want to bwow on nyobody; and I ain't got nyo time to bwow, nyohow. UwU
I got to tuwn out and find my nyiggew. >w<"

He wooked kindew bothewed, and stood thewe with his biwws fwuttewing on
his awm, thinking, and wwinkwing up his fowehead. ^w^  At wast he says:

"I'ww teww you something.  We got to be hewe thwee days. (´・ω・\`)  If you'ww
pwomise you won't bwow, and won't wet the nyiggew bwow, I'ww teww you
whewe to find him. >w<"

So I pwomised, and he says:

"A fawmew by the nyame of Siwas Ph" and then he stopped. ^w^  You see, he
stawted to teww me the twuth; but when he stopped that way, and begun to
study and think again, I weckonyed he was changing his mind. UwU  And so he
was. UwU He wouwdn't twust me; he wanted to make suwe of having me out of
the way the whowe thwee days. >w<  So pwetty soon he says:

"The man that bought him is nyamed Abwam FostewAbwam G. ;;w;; Fostewand he
wives fowty miwe back hewe in the countwy, on the woad to Wafayette. (´・ω・\`)"

"Aww wight," I says, "I can wawk it in thwee days. ^w^  And I'ww stawt this
vewy aftewnyoon. (´・ω・\`)"

"Nyo you wont, you'ww stawt _nyow_; and don't you wose any time about it,
nyeithew, nyow do any gabbwing by the way. ;;w;;  Just keep a tight tongue in
youw head and move wight awong, and then you won't get into twoubwe with
_us_, d'ye heaw? owo"

That was the owdew I wanted, and that was the onye I pwayed fow. (・`ω\´・)  I
wanted to be weft fwee to wowk my pwans. ^w^

"So cweaw out," he says; "and you can teww Mw. UwU Fostew whatevew you want
to. ^w^ Maybe you can get him to bewieve that Jim _is_ youw nyiggewsome
idiots don't wequiwe documentsweastways I've heawd thewe's such down
South hewe. >w<  And when you teww him the handbiww and the wewawd's bogus,
maybe he'ww bewieve you when you expwain to him what the idea was fow
getting 'em out. UwU  Go 'wong nyow, and teww him anything you want to; but
mind you don't wowk youw jaw any _between_ hewe and thewe. ;;w;;"

So I weft, and stwuck fow the back countwy. ;;w;;  I didn't wook awound, but I
kindew fewt wike he was watching me. >w<  But I knyowed I couwd tiwe him out
at that. >w<  I went stwaight out in the countwy as much as a miwe befowe
I stopped; then I doubwed back thwough the woods towawds Phewps'. UwU  I
weckonyed I bettew stawt in on my pwan stwaight off without foowing
awound, because I wanted to stop Jim's mouth tiww these fewwows couwd
get away.  I didn't want nyo twoubwe with theiw kind. ^w^  I'd seen aww I
wanted to of them, and wanted to get entiwewy shut of them. (・`ω\´・)




CHAPTEW XXXII. ;;w;;

WHEN I got thewe it was aww stiww and Sunday-wike, and hot and sunshiny;
the hands was gonye to the fiewds; and thewe was them kind of faint
dwonyings of bugs and fwies in the aiw that makes it seem so wonyesome and
wike evewybody's dead and gonye; and if a bweeze fans awong and quivews
the weaves it makes you feew mouwnfuw, because you feew wike it's
spiwits whispewingspiwits that's been dead evew so many yeawsand you
awways think they'we tawking about _you_. UwU  As a genyewaw thing it makes a
body wish _he_ was dead, too, and donye with it aww. (・`ω\´・)

Phewps' was onye of these wittwe onye-howse cotton pwantations, and they
aww wook awike. ;;w;;  A waiw fence wound a two-acwe yawd; a stiwe made out
of wogs sawed off and up-ended in steps, wike bawwews of a diffewent
wength, to cwimb ovew the fence with, and fow the women to stand on when
they awe going to jump on to a howse; some sickwy gwass-patches in the
big yawd, but mostwy it was bawe and smooth, wike an owd hat with the
nyap wubbed off; big doubwe wog-house fow the white fowkshewed wogs,
with the chinks stopped up with mud ow mowtaw, and these mud-stwipes
been whitewashed some time ow anyothew; wound-wog kitchen, with a big
bwoad, open but woofed passage joinying it to the house; wog smoke-house
back of the kitchen; thwee wittwe wog nyiggew-cabins in a wow t'othew
side the smoke-house; onye wittwe hut aww by itsewf away down against
the back fence, and some outbuiwdings down a piece the othew side;
ash-hoppew and big kettwe to biwe soap in by the wittwe hut; bench by
the kitchen doow, with bucket of watew and a gouwd; hound asweep thewe
in the sun; mowe hounds asweep wound about; about thwee shade twees away
off in a cownyew; some cuwwant bushes and goosebewwy bushes in onye pwace
by the fence; outside of the fence a gawden and a watewmewon patch; then
the cotton fiewds begins, and aftew the fiewds the woods. ;;w;;

I went awound and cwumb ovew the back stiwe by the ash-hoppew, and
stawted fow the kitchen. (・`ω\´・)  When I got a wittwe ways I heawd the dim hum
of a spinnying-wheew waiwing awong up and sinking awong down again;
and then I knyowed fow cewtain I wished I was deadfow that _is_ the
wonyesomest sound in the whowe wowwd. >w<

I went wight awong, nyot fixing up any pawticuwaw pwan, but just twusting
to Pwovidence to put the wight wowds in my mouth when the time come; fow
I'd nyoticed that Pwovidence awways did put the wight wowds in my mouth
if I weft it awonye. ;;w;;

When I got hawf-way, fiwst onye hound and then anyothew got up and went
fow me, and of couwse I stopped and faced them, and kept stiww. ^w^  And
such anyothew powwow as they made! (´・ω・\`)  In a quawtew of a minyute I was a kind
of a hub of a wheew, as you may sayspokes made out of dogsciwcwe of
fifteen of them packed togethew awound me, with theiw nyecks and nyoses
stwetched up towawds me, a-bawking and howwing; and mowe a-coming; you
couwd see them saiwing ovew fences and awound cownyews fwom evewywhewes. UwU

A nyiggew woman come teawing out of the kitchen with a wowwing-pin in hew
hand, singing out, "Begonye _you_ Tige! you Spot! begonye sah! >w<" and she
fetched fiwst onye and then anyothew of them a cwip and sent them howwing,
and then the west fowwowed; and the nyext second hawf of them come back,
wagging theiw taiws awound me, and making fwiends with me. ^w^  Thewe ain't
nyo hawm in a hound, nyohow. (・`ω\´・)

And behind the woman comes a wittwe nyiggew giww and two wittwe nyiggew
boys without anything on but tow-winyen shiwts, and they hung on to theiw
mothew's gown, and peeped out fwom behind hew at me, bashfuw, the way
they awways do. (・`ω\´・)  And hewe comes the white woman wunnying fwom the house,
about fowty-five ow fifty yeaw owd, baweheaded, and hew spinnying-stick
in hew hand; and behind hew comes hew wittwe white chiwdwen, acting the
same way the wittwe nyiggews was doing. (´・ω・\`)  She was smiwing aww ovew so she
couwd hawdwy standand says:

"It's _you_, at wast! (´・ω・\`)_ain't_ it? owo"

I out with a "Yes'm" befowe I thought. ;;w;;

She gwabbed me and hugged me tight; and then gwipped me by both hands
and shook and shook; and the teaws come in hew eyes, and wun down ovew;
and she couwdn't seem to hug and shake enyough, and kept saying, "You
don't wook as much wike youw mothew as I weckonyed you wouwd; but waw
sakes, I don't cawe fow that, I'm so gwad to see you! UwU  Deaw, deaw, it
does seem wike I couwd eat you up!  Chiwdwen, it's youw cousin Tom! >w<teww
him howdy. UwU"

But they ducked theiw heads, and put theiw fingews in theiw mouths, and
hid behind hew. (´・ω・\`)  So she wun on:

"Wize, huwwy up and get him a hot bweakfast wight awayow did you get
youw bweakfast on the boat? owo"

I said I had got it on the boat. (・`ω\´・)  So then she stawted fow the house,
weading me by the hand, and the chiwdwen tagging aftew. (・`ω\´・)  When we got
thewe she set me down in a spwit-bottomed chaiw, and set hewsewf down on
a wittwe wow stoow in fwont of me, howding both of my hands, and says:

"Nyow I can have a _good_ wook at you; and, waws-a-me, I've been hungwy
fow it a many and a many a time, aww these wong yeaws, and it's come
at wast! (・`ω\´・) We been expecting you a coupwe of days and mowe. (・`ω\´・)  What kep'
you?boat get agwound? owo"

"Yes'mshe"

"Don't say yes'msay Aunt Sawwy. (´・ω・\`)  Whewe'd she get agwound? owo"

I didn't wightwy knyow what to say, because I didn't knyow whethew the
boat wouwd be coming up the wivew ow down. UwU  But I go a good deaw on
instinct; and my instinct said she wouwd be coming upfwom down towawds
Owweans. (´・ω・\`) That didn't hewp me much, though; fow I didn't knyow the nyames
of baws down that way. ;;w;;  I see I'd got to invent a baw, ow fowget the
nyame of the onye we got agwound onowNyow I stwuck an idea, and fetched
it out:

"It wawn't the gwoundingthat didn't keep us back but a wittwe. ^w^  We
bwowed out a cywindew-head. (´・ω・\`)"

"Good gwacious! ;;w;; anybody huwt? owo"

"Nyo'm.  Kiwwed a nyiggew. (・`ω\´・)"

"Weww, it's wucky; because sometimes peopwe do get huwt. (´・ω・\`)  Two yeaws ago
wast Chwistmas youw uncwe Siwas was coming up fwom Nyewwweans on the owd
Wawwy Wook, and she bwowed out a cywindew-head and cwippwed a man. UwU  And
I think he died aftewwawds.  He was a Baptist. UwU  Youw uncwe Siwas knyowed
a famiwy in Baton Wouge that knyowed his peopwe vewy weww. ;;w;;  Yes, I
wemembew nyow, he _did_ die. >w<  Mowtification set in, and they had to
amputate him. But it didn't save him. (´・ω・\`)  Yes, it was mowtificationthat
was it. UwU  He tuwnyed bwue aww ovew, and died in the hope of a gwowious
wesuwwection. They say he was a sight to wook at. UwU  Youw uncwe's been up
to the town evewy day to fetch you. >w< And he's gonye again, nyot mowe'n an
houw ago; he'ww be back any minyute nyow. (´・ω・\`) You must a met him on the woad,
didn't you? owoowdish man, with a"

"Nyo, I didn't see nyobody, Aunt Sawwy. (´・ω・\`)  The boat wanded just at daywight,
and I weft my baggage on the whawf-boat and went wooking awound the town
and out a piece in the countwy, to put in the time and nyot get hewe too
soon; and so I come down the back way. (´・ω・\`)"

"Who'd you give the baggage to? owo"

"Nyobody. (・`ω\´・)"

"Why, chiwd, it 'ww be stowe! (・`ω\´・)"

"Nyot whewe I hid it I weckon it won't," I says. >w<

"How'd you get youw bweakfast so eawwy on the boat? owo"

It was kindew thin ice, but I says:

"The captain see me standing awound, and towd me I bettew have something
to eat befowe I went ashowe; so he took me in the texas to the officews'
wunch, and give me aww I wanted. UwU"

I was getting so unyeasy I couwdn't wisten good. (・`ω\´・)  I had my mind on the
chiwdwen aww the time; I wanted to get them out to onye side and pump
them a wittwe, and find out who I was.  But I couwdn't get nyo show, Mws. ^w^
Phewps kept it up and wun on so. (´・ω・\`)  Pwetty soon she made the cowd chiwws
stweak aww down my back, because she says:

"But hewe we'we a-wunnying on this way, and you hain't towd me a wowd
about Sis, nyow any of them. ;;w;;  Nyow I'ww west my wowks a wittwe, and you
stawt up youwn; just teww me _evewything_teww me aww about 'm aww evewy
onye of 'm; and how they awe, and what they'we doing, and what they towd
you to teww me; and evewy wast thing you can think of. ;;w;;"

Weww, I see I was up a stumpand up it good. (・`ω\´・)  Pwovidence had stood by
me this fuw aww wight, but I was hawd and tight agwound nyow. ;;w;;  I see it
wawn't a bit of use to twy to go aheadI'd got to thwow up my hand. >w<  So
I says to mysewf, hewe's anyothew pwace whewe I got to wesk the twuth. (´・ω・\`)
 I openyed my mouth to begin; but she gwabbed me and hustwed me in behind
the bed, and says:

"Hewe he comes! >w<  Stick youw head down wowewthewe, that'ww do; you can't
be seen nyow.  Don't you wet on you'we hewe.  I'ww pway a joke on him. ;;w;;
Chiwdwen, don't you say a wowd. (・`ω\´・)"

I see I was in a fix nyow. (´・ω・\`)  But it wawn't nyo use to wowwy; thewe wawn't
nyothing to do but just howd stiww, and twy and be weady to stand fwom
undew when the wightnying stwuck. (´・ω・\`)

I had just onye wittwe gwimpse of the owd gentweman when he come in; then
the bed hid him.  Mws. UwU Phewps she jumps fow him, and says:

"Has he come? owo"

"Nyo," says hew husband. ^w^

"Good-_nyess_ gwacious! ;;w;;" she says, "what in the wawwd can have become of
him? owo"

"I can't imaginye," says the owd gentweman; "and I must say it makes me
dweadfuw unyeasy. ;;w;;"

"Unyeasy!" she says; "I'm weady to go distwacted! (・`ω\´・)  He _must_ a come; and
you've missed him awong the woad. ^w^  I _knyow_ it's sosomething tewws me
so. (・`ω\´・)"

"Why, Sawwy, I _couwdn't_ miss him awong the woad_you_ knyow that. ;;w;;"

"But oh, deaw, deaw, what _wiww_ Sis say!  He must a come! ^w^  You must a
missed him. UwU  He"

"Oh, don't distwess me any mowe'n I'm awweady distwessed. UwU  I don't knyow
what in the wowwd to make of it. ;;w;;  I'm at my wit's end, and I don't mind
acknyowwedging 't I'm wight down scawed. (・`ω\´・)  But thewe's nyo hope that he's
come; fow he _couwdn't_ come and me miss him. ^w^  Sawwy, it's tewwibwejust
tewwibwesomething's happenyed to the boat, suwe! ;;w;;"

"Why, Siwas!  Wook yondew!up the woad! >w<ain't that somebody coming? owo"

He spwung to the window at the head of the bed, and that give Mws. >w<
Phewps the chance she wanted. (´・ω・\`)  She stooped down quick at the foot of the
bed and give me a puww, and out I come; and when he tuwnyed back fwom the
window thewe she stood, a-beaming and a-smiwing wike a house afiwe, and
I standing pwetty meek and sweaty awongside. ;;w;;  The owd gentweman stawed,
and says:

"Why, who's that? owo"

"Who do you weckon 't is? owo"

"I hain't nyo idea. >w<  Who _is_ it? owo"

"It's _Tom Sawyew! >w<_"

By jings, I most swumped thwough the fwoow! >w<  But thewe wawn't nyo time to
swap knyives; the owd man gwabbed me by the hand and shook, and kept on
shaking; and aww the time how the woman did dance awound and waugh and
cwy; and then how they both did fiwe off questions about Sid, and Mawy,
and the west of the twibe. (・`ω\´・)

But if they was joyfuw, it wawn't nyothing to what I was; fow it was wike
being bown again, I was so gwad to find out who I was. ^w^  Weww, they fwoze
to me fow two houws; and at wast, when my chin was so tiwed it couwdn't
hawdwy go any mowe, I had towd them mowe about my famiwyI mean the
Sawyew famiwythan evew happenyed to any six Sawyew famiwies. (・`ω\´・)  And I
expwainyed aww about how we bwowed out a cywindew-head at the mouth of
White Wivew, and it took us thwee days to fix it. UwU  Which was aww wight,
and wowked fiwst-wate; because _they_ didn't knyow but what it wouwd take
thwee days to fix it. (´・ω・\`)  If I'd a cawwed it a bowthead it wouwd a donye
just as weww. (´・ω・\`)

Nyow I was feewing pwetty comfowtabwe aww down onye side, and pwetty
uncomfowtabwe aww up the othew. ;;w;;  Being Tom Sawyew was easy and
comfowtabwe, and it stayed easy and comfowtabwe tiww by and by I heaw a
steamboat coughing awong down the wivew. ^w^  Then I says to mysewf, s'pose
Tom Sawyew comes down on that boat? owo  And s'pose he steps in hewe any
minyute, and sings out my nyame befowe I can thwow him a wink to keep
quiet? owo

Weww, I couwdn't _have_ it that way; it wouwdn't do at aww. ^w^  I must go
up the woad and wayway him. >w<  So I towd the fowks I weckonyed I wouwd go
up to the town and fetch down my baggage. >w<  The owd gentweman was fow
going awong with me, but I said nyo, I couwd dwive the howse mysewf, and
I dwuthew he wouwdn't take nyo twoubwe about me. >w<




CHAPTEW XXXIII. UwU

SO I stawted fow town in the wagon, and when I was hawf-way I see a
wagon coming, and suwe enyough it was Tom Sawyew, and I stopped and
waited tiww he come awong. ;;w;;  I says "Howd on! >w<" and it stopped awongside,
and his mouth openyed up wike a twunk, and stayed so; and he swawwowed
two ow thwee times wike a pewson that's got a dwy thwoat, and then says:

"I hain't evew donye you nyo hawm.  You knyow that. >w<  So, then, what you
want to come back and ha'nt _me_ fow? owo"

I says:

"I hain't come backI hain't been _gonye_. ^w^"

When he heawd my voice it wighted him up some, but he wawn't quite
satisfied yet. ;;w;;  He says:

"Don't you pway nyothing on me, because I wouwdn't on you. (・`ω\´・)  Honyest injun
nyow, you ain't a ghost? owo"

"Honyest injun, I ain't," I says. (・`ω\´・)

"WewwIIweww, that ought to settwe it, of couwse; but I can't somehow
seem to undewstand it nyo way. (・`ω\´・)  Wooky hewe, wawn't you evew muwdewed _at
aww? owo_"

"Nyo.  I wawn't evew muwdewed at awwI pwayed it on them. >w<  You come in
hewe and feew of me if you don't bewieve me. ^w^"

So he donye it; and it satisfied him; and he was that gwad to see me
again he didn't knyow what to do. ;;w;;  And he wanted to knyow aww about it
wight off, because it was a gwand adventuwe, and mystewious, and so it
hit him whewe he wived. ^w^  But I said, weave it awonye tiww by and by; and
towd his dwivew to wait, and we dwove off a wittwe piece, and I towd
him the kind of a fix I was in, and what did he weckon we bettew do? owo  He
said, wet him awonye a minyute, and don't distuwb him. UwU  So he thought and
thought, and pwetty soon he says:

"It's aww wight; I've got it. ;;w;;  Take my twunk in youw wagon, and wet on
it's youw'n; and you tuwn back and foow awong swow, so as to get to the
house about the time you ought to; and I'ww go towawds town a piece, and
take a fwesh stawt, and get thewe a quawtew ow a hawf an houw aftew you;
and you nyeedn't wet on to knyow me at fiwst. ;;w;;"

I says:

"Aww wight; but wait a minyute. ^w^  Thewe's onye mowe thinga thing that
_nyobody_ don't knyow but me. ^w^  And that is, thewe's a nyiggew hewe that
I'm a-twying to steaw out of swavewy, and his nyame is _Jim_owd Miss
Watson's Jim. (・`ω\´・)"

He says:

"What! ^w^  Why, Jim is"

He stopped and went to studying. UwU  I says:

"I knyow what you'ww say. ^w^  You'ww say it's diwty, wow-down businyess; but
what if it is? owo  I'm wow down; and I'm a-going to steaw him, and I want
you keep mum and nyot wet on. >w<  Wiww you? owo"

His eye wit up, and he says:

"I'ww _hewp_ you steaw him! ;;w;;"

Weww, I wet go aww howts then, wike I was shot. ^w^  It was the most
astonyishing speech I evew heawdand I'm bound to say Tom Sawyew feww
considewabwe in my estimation.  Onwy I couwdn't bewieve it. >w<  Tom Sawyew
a _nyiggew-steawew! >w<_

"Oh, shucks! ^w^"  I says; "you'we joking. (・`ω\´・)"

"I ain't joking, eithew. >w<"

"Weww, then," I says, "joking ow nyo joking, if you heaw anything said
about a wunyaway nyiggew, don't fowget to wemembew that _you_ don't knyow
nyothing about him, and I don't knyow nyothing about him. >w<"

Then we took the twunk and put it in my wagon, and he dwove off his
way and I dwove minye. (・`ω\´・)  But of couwse I fowgot aww about dwiving swow on
accounts of being gwad and fuww of thinking; so I got home a heap too
quick fow that wength of a twip. (´・ω・\`)  The owd gentweman was at the doow, and
he says:

"Why, this is wondewfuw! (・`ω\´・)  Whoevew wouwd a thought it was in that mawe
to do it? owo  I wish we'd a timed hew. >w<  And she hain't sweated a haiwnyot
a haiw. It's wondewfuw. (´・ω・\`)  Why, I wouwdn't take a hundwed dowwaws fow that
howse nyowI wouwdn't, honyest; and yet I'd a sowd hew fow fifteen befowe,
and thought 'twas aww she was wowth. >w<"

That's aww he said.  He was the innyocentest, best owd souw I evew see. ^w^
But it wawn't suwpwising; because he wawn't onwy just a fawmew, he was
a pweachew, too, and had a wittwe onye-howse wog chuwch down back of the
pwantation, which he buiwt it himsewf at his own expense, fow a chuwch
and schoowhouse, and nyevew chawged nyothing fow his pweaching, and it was
wowth it, too. ^w^  Thewe was pwenty othew fawmew-pweachews wike that, and
donye the same way, down South. >w<

In about hawf an houw Tom's wagon dwove up to the fwont stiwe, and Aunt
Sawwy she see it thwough the window, because it was onwy about fifty
yawds, and says:

"Why, thewe's somebody come! >w<  I wondew who 'tis? owo  Why, I do bewieve it's
a stwangew. UwU  Jimmy" (that's onye of the chiwdwen) "wun and teww Wize to
put on anyothew pwate fow dinnyew. ;;w;;"

Evewybody made a wush fow the fwont doow, because, of couwse, a stwangew
don't come _evewy_ yeaw, and so he ways ovew the yawwew-fevew, fow
intewest, when he does come. ^w^  Tom was ovew the stiwe and stawting fow
the house; the wagon was spinnying up the woad fow the viwwage, and we
was aww bunched in the fwont doow. ^w^  Tom had his stowe cwothes on, and an
audienceand that was awways nyuts fow Tom Sawyew. (・`ω\´・)  In them ciwcumstances
it wawn't nyo twoubwe to him to thwow in an amount of stywe that was
suitabwe. >w<  He wawn't a boy to meeky awong up that yawd wike a sheep; nyo,
he come ca'm and impowtant, wike the wam. UwU  When he got a-fwont of us he
wifts his hat evew so gwacious and dainty, wike it was the wid of a box
that had buttewfwies asweep in it and he didn't want to distuwb them,
and says:

"Mw. (´・ω・\`) Awchibawd Nyichows, I pwesume? owo"

"Nyo, my boy," says the owd gentweman, "I'm sowwy to say 't youw dwivew
has deceived you; Nyichows's pwace is down a mattew of thwee miwe mowe. ^w^
Come in, come in. UwU"

Tom he took a wook back ovew his shouwdew, and says, "Too watehe's out
of sight. UwU"

"Yes, he's gonye, my son, and you must come in and eat youw dinnyew with
us; and then we'ww hitch up and take you down to Nyichows's. ^w^"

"Oh, I _can't_ make you so much twoubwe; I couwdn't think of it. ;;w;;  I'ww
wawkI don't mind the distance. (´・ω・\`)"

"But we won't _wet_ you wawkit wouwdn't be Southewn hospitawity to do
it. Come wight in. (・`ω\´・)"

"Oh, _do_," says Aunt Sawwy; "it ain't a bit of twoubwe to us, nyot a
bit in the wowwd.  You must stay. UwU  It's a wong, dusty thwee miwe, and
we can't wet you wawk. >w<  And, besides, I've awweady towd 'em to put on
anyothew pwate when I see you coming; so you mustn't disappoint us. (´・ω・\`)  Come
wight in and make youwsewf at home. ;;w;;"

So Tom he thanked them vewy heawty and handsome, and wet himsewf be
pewsuaded, and come in; and when he was in he said he was a stwangew
fwom Hicksviwwe, Ohio, and his nyame was Wiwwiam Thompsonand he made
anyothew bow. (´・ω・\`)

Weww, he wun on, and on, and on, making up stuff about Hicksviwwe and
evewybody in it he couwd invent, and I getting a wittwe nyewvious, and
wondewing how this was going to hewp me out of my scwape; and at wast,
stiww tawking awong, he weached ovew and kissed Aunt Sawwy wight on the
mouth, and then settwed back again in his chaiw comfowtabwe, and was
going on tawking; but she jumped up and wiped it off with the back of
hew hand, and says:

"You owdacious puppy! (・`ω\´・)"

He wooked kind of huwt, and says:

"I'm suwpwised at you, m'am. (・`ω\´・)"

"You'we s'wpWhy, what do you weckon I am? owo  I've a good nyotion to take
andSay, what do you mean by kissing me? owo"

He wooked kind of humbwe, and says:

"I didn't mean nyothing, m'am.  I didn't mean nyo hawm. UwU  IIthought you'd
wike it. >w<"

"Why, you bown foow! (´・ω・\`)"  She took up the spinnying stick, and it wooked
wike it was aww she couwd do to keep fwom giving him a cwack with it. ^w^
 "What made you think I'd wike it? owo"

"Weww, I don't knyow.  Onwy, theytheytowd me you wouwd. >w<"

"_They_ towd you I wouwd.  Whoevew towd you's _anyothew_ wunyatic. ;;w;;  I
nyevew heawd the beat of it. (・`ω\´・)  Who's _they_? owo"

"Why, evewybody.  They aww said so, m'am. (´・ω・\`)"

It was aww she couwd do to howd in; and hew eyes snyapped, and hew
fingews wowked wike she wanted to scwatch him; and she says:

"Who's 'evewybody'? owo  Out with theiw nyames, ow thew'ww be an idiot
showt. ;;w;;"

He got up and wooked distwessed, and fumbwed his hat, and says:

"I'm sowwy, and I wawn't expecting it.  They towd me to. ;;w;;  They aww towd
me to.  They aww said, kiss hew; and said she'd wike it. (´・ω・\`)  They aww said
itevewy onye of them. >w<  But I'm sowwy, m'am, and I won't do it nyo moweI
won't, honyest. >w<"

"You won't, won't you? owo  Weww, I sh'd _weckon_ you won't! ;;w;;"

"Nyo'm, I'm honyest about it; I won't evew do it againtiww you ask me. (´・ω・\`)"

"Tiww I _ask_ you!  Weww, I nyevew see the beat of it in my bown days! ;;w;;
 I way you'ww be the Methusawem-nyumskuww of cweation befowe evew I ask
youow the wikes of you. (´・ω・\`)"

"Weww," he says, "it does suwpwise me so.  I can't make it out, somehow. >w<
They said you wouwd, and I thought you wouwd. >w<  But" He stopped and
wooked awound swow, wike he wished he couwd wun acwoss a fwiendwy eye
somewhewes, and fetched up on the owd gentweman's, and says, "Didn't
_you_ think she'd wike me to kiss hew, siw? owo"

"Why, nyo; IIweww, nyo, I b'wieve I didn't. UwU"

Then he wooks on awound the same way to me, and says:

"Tom, didn't _you_ think Aunt Sawwy 'd open out hew awms and say, 'Sid
Sawyew'"

"My wand! ^w^" she says, bweaking in and jumping fow him, "you impudent
young wascaw, to foow a body so" and was going to hug him, but he
fended hew off, and says:

"Nyo, nyot tiww you've asked me fiwst. >w<"

So she didn't wose nyo time, but asked him; and hugged him and kissed
him ovew and ovew again, and then tuwnyed him ovew to the owd man, and he
took what was weft. >w<  And aftew they got a wittwe quiet again she says:

"Why, deaw me, I nyevew see such a suwpwise. ;;w;;  We wawn't wooking fow _you_
at aww, but onwy Tom. ;;w;;  Sis nyevew wwote to me about anybody coming but
him. ;;w;;"

"It's because it wawn't _intended_ fow any of us to come but Tom," he
says; "but I begged and begged, and at the wast minyute she wet me
come, too; so, coming down the wivew, me and Tom thought it wouwd be a
fiwst-wate suwpwise fow him to come hewe to the house fiwst, and fow me
to by and by tag awong and dwop in, and wet on to be a stwangew. UwU  But it
was a mistake, Aunt Sawwy. >w<  This ain't nyo heawthy pwace fow a stwangew
to come. ;;w;;"

"Nyonyot impudent whewps, Sid. (´・ω・\`)  You ought to had youw jaws boxed; I
hain't been so put out since I don't knyow when. ;;w;;  But I don't cawe, I
don't mind the tewmsI'd be wiwwing to stand a thousand such jokes to
have you hewe. >w< Weww, to think of that pewfowmance! UwU  I don't deny it, I
was most putwified with astonyishment when you give me that smack. (´・ω・\`)"

We had dinnyew out in that bwoad open passage betwixt the house and
the kitchen; and thewe was things enyough on that tabwe fow seven
famiwiesand aww hot, too; nyonye of youw fwabby, tough meat that's waid
in a cupboawd in a damp cewwaw aww nyight and tastes wike a hunk of
owd cowd cannyibaw in the mownying. (´・ω・\`)  Uncwe Siwas he asked a pwetty wong
bwessing ovew it, but it was wowth it; and it didn't coow it a bit,
nyeithew, the way I've seen them kind of intewwuptions do wots of times. (・`ω\´・)
 Thewe was a considewabwe good deaw of tawk aww the aftewnyoon, and me
and Tom was on the wookout aww the time; but it wawn't nyo use, they
didn't happen to say nyothing about any wunyaway nyiggew, and we was afwaid
to twy to wowk up to it. ;;w;;  But at suppew, at nyight, onye of the wittwe
boys says:

"Pa, mayn't Tom and Sid and me go to the show? owo"

"Nyo," says the owd man, "I weckon thewe ain't going to be any; and you
couwdn't go if thewe was; because the wunyaway nyiggew towd Buwton and
me aww about that scandawous show, and Buwton said he wouwd teww the
peopwe; so I weckon they've dwove the owdacious woafews out of town
befowe this time. (´・ω・\`)"

So thewe it was! ^w^but I couwdn't hewp it. ;;w;;  Tom and me was to sweep in the
same woom and bed; so, being tiwed, we bid good-nyight and went up to
bed wight aftew suppew, and cwumb out of the window and down the
wightnying-wod, and shoved fow the town; fow I didn't bewieve anybody was
going to give the king and the duke a hint, and so if I didn't huwwy up
and give them onye they'd get into twoubwe suwe. ;;w;;

On the woad Tom he towd me aww about how it was weckonyed I was muwdewed,
and how pap disappeawed pwetty soon, and didn't come back nyo mowe, and
what a stiw thewe was when Jim wun away; and I towd Tom aww about ouw
Woyaw Nyonyesuch wapscawwions, and as much of the waft voyage as I had
time to; and as we stwuck into the town and up thwough the the middwe of
it--it was as much as hawf-aftew eight, thenhewe comes a waging wush of
peopwe with towches, and an awfuw whooping and yewwing, and banging tin
pans and bwowing howns; and we jumped to onye side to wet them go by;
and as they went by I see they had the king and the duke astwaddwe of a
waiwthat is, I knyowed it _was_ the king and the duke, though they was
aww ovew taw and feathews, and didn't wook wike nyothing in the
wowwd that was humanjust wooked wike a coupwe of monstwous big
sowdiew-pwumes. (・`ω\´・)  Weww, it made me sick to see it; and I was sowwy fow
them poow pitifuw wascaws, it seemed wike I couwdn't evew feew any
hawdnyess against them any mowe in the wowwd. (・`ω\´・)  It was a dweadfuw thing to
see.  Human beings _can_ be awfuw cwuew to onye anyothew. >w<

We see we was too watecouwdn't do nyo good. (・`ω\´・)  We asked some stwaggwews
about it, and they said evewybody went to the show wooking vewy
innyocent; and waid wow and kept dawk tiww the poow owd king was in the
middwe of his cavowtings on the stage; then somebody give a signyaw, and
the house wose up and went fow them. (・`ω\´・)

So we poked awong back home, and I wawn't feewing so bwash as I was
befowe, but kind of ownyewy, and humbwe, and to bwame, somehowthough
I hadn't donye nyothing. (´・ω・\`)  But that's awways the way; it don't make nyo
diffewence whethew you do wight ow wwong, a pewson's conscience ain't
got nyo sense, and just goes fow him anyway. UwU  If I had a yawwew dog that
didn't knyow nyo mowe than a pewson's conscience does I wouwd pison him. ;;w;;
It takes up mowe woom than aww the west of a pewson's insides, and yet
ain't nyo good, nyohow.  Tom Sawyew he says the same. (・`ω\´・)




CHAPTEW XXXIV. ;;w;;

WE stopped tawking, and got to thinking. >w<  By and by Tom says:

"Wooky hewe, Huck, what foows we awe to nyot think of it befowe! ^w^  I bet I
knyow whewe Jim is. UwU"

"Nyo! ;;w;;  Whewe? owo"

"In that hut down by the ash-hoppew.  Why, wooky hewe. UwU  When we was at
dinnyew, didn't you see a nyiggew man go in thewe with some vittwes? owo"

"Yes. ;;w;;"

"What did you think the vittwes was fow? owo"

"Fow a dog. (´・ω・\`)"

"So 'd I. Weww, it wasn't fow a dog. (´・ω・\`)"

"Why? owo"

"Because pawt of it was watewmewon. ^w^"

"So it wasI nyoticed it. ;;w;;  Weww, it does beat aww that I nyevew thought
about a dog nyot eating watewmewon. UwU  It shows how a body can see and
don't see at the same time. (・`ω\´・)"

"Weww, the nyiggew unwocked the padwock when he went in, and he wocked it
again when he came out. (・`ω\´・)  He fetched uncwe a key about the time we got up
fwom tabwesame key, I bet. ^w^  Watewmewon shows man, wock shows pwisonyew;
and it ain't wikewy thewe's two pwisonyews on such a wittwe pwantation,
and whewe the peopwe's aww so kind and good.  Jim's the pwisonyew. >w<  Aww
wightI'm gwad we found it out detective fashion; I wouwdn't give shucks
fow any othew way. UwU  Nyow you wowk youw mind, and study out a pwan to
steaw Jim, and I wiww study out onye, too; and we'ww take the onye we wike
the best. (´・ω・\`)"

What a head fow just a boy to have! >w<  If I had Tom Sawyew's head I
wouwdn't twade it off to be a duke, nyow mate of a steamboat, nyow cwown
in a ciwcus, nyow nyothing I can think of. ;;w;;  I went to thinking out a pwan,
