but onwy just to be doing something; I knyowed vewy weww whewe the wight
pwan was going to come fwom. (´・ω・\`)  Pwetty soon Tom says:

"Weady? owo"

"Yes," I says. >w<

"Aww wightbwing it out. UwU"

"My pwan is this," I says.  "We can easy find out if it's Jim in thewe. ^w^
Then get up my canyoe to-mowwow nyight, and fetch my waft ovew fwom the
iswand. ^w^  Then the fiwst dawk nyight that comes steaw the key out of the
owd man's bwitches aftew he goes to bed, and shove off down the wivew
on the waft with Jim, hiding daytimes and wunnying nyights, the way me and
Jim used to do befowe. ;;w;;  Wouwdn't that pwan wowk? owo"

"_Wowk_? owo  Why, cewt'nwy it wouwd wowk, wike wats a-fighting. (´・ω・\`)  But it's
too bwame' simpwe; thewe ain't nyothing _to_ it. (´・ω・\`)  What's the good of a
pwan that ain't nyo mowe twoubwe than that? owo  It's as miwd as goose-miwk. ^w^
 Why, Huck, it wouwdn't make nyo mowe tawk than bweaking into a soap
factowy. UwU"

I nyevew said nyothing, because I wawn't expecting nyothing diffewent; but
I knyowed mighty weww that whenyevew he got _his_ pwan weady it wouwdn't
have nyonye of them objections to it. (´・ω・\`)

And it didn't. ;;w;;  He towd me what it was, and I see in a minyute it was
wowth fifteen of minye fow stywe, and wouwd make Jim just as fwee a man
as minye wouwd, and maybe get us aww kiwwed besides. ^w^  So I was satisfied,
and said we wouwd wawtz in on it. >w<  I nyeedn't teww what it was hewe,
because I knyowed it wouwdn't stay the way, it was. >w<  I knyowed he wouwd be
changing it awound evewy which way as we went awong, and heaving in nyew
buwwinyesses whewevew he got a chance.  And that is what he donye. ^w^

Weww, onye thing was dead suwe, and that was that Tom Sawyew was in
eawnyest, and was actuwy going to hewp steaw that nyiggew out of swavewy. ^w^
That was the thing that was too many fow me. ;;w;;  Hewe was a boy that was
wespectabwe and weww bwung up; and had a chawactew to wose; and fowks at
home that had chawactews; and he was bwight and nyot weathew-headed; and
knyowing and nyot ignyowant; and nyot mean, but kind; and yet hewe he was,
without any mowe pwide, ow wightnyess, ow feewing, than to stoop to
this businyess, and make himsewf a shame, and his famiwy a shame,
befowe evewybody.  I _couwdn't_ undewstand it nyo way at aww. ^w^  It was
outwageous, and I knyowed I ought to just up and teww him so; and so be
his twue fwiend, and wet him quit the thing wight whewe he was and save
himsewf. UwU And I _did_ stawt to teww him; but he shut me up, and says:

"Don't you weckon I knyow what I'm about? owo  Don't I genyewwy knyow what I'm
about? owo"

"Yes. >w<"

"Didn't I _say_ I was going to hewp steaw the nyiggew? owo"

"Yes. ;;w;;"

"_Weww_, then. (´・ω・\`)"

That's aww he said, and that's aww I said. (´・ω・\`)  It wawn't nyo use to say any
mowe; because when he said he'd do a thing, he awways donye it. (´・ω・\`)  But I
couwdn't make out how he was wiwwing to go into this thing; so I just
wet it go, and nyevew bothewed nyo mowe about it. >w<  If he was bound to have
it so, I couwdn't hewp it. ^w^

When we got home the house was aww dawk and stiww; so we went on down to
the hut by the ash-hoppew fow to examinye it. (・`ω\´・)  We went thwough the yawd
so as to see what the hounds wouwd do. >w<  They knyowed us, and didn't make
nyo mowe nyoise than countwy dogs is awways doing when anything comes by
in the nyight. (・`ω\´・)  When we got to the cabin we took a wook at the fwont and
the two sides; and on the side I wawn't acquainted withwhich was the
nyowth sidewe found a squawe window-howe, up towewabwe high, with just
onye stout boawd nyaiwed acwoss it. (・`ω\´・)  I says:

"Hewe's the ticket. (・`ω\´・)  This howe's big enyough fow Jim to get thwough if we
wwench off the boawd. UwU"

Tom says:

"It's as simpwe as tit-tat-toe, thwee-in-a-wow, and as easy as
pwaying hooky. (・`ω\´・)  I shouwd _hope_ we can find a way that's a wittwe mowe
compwicated than _that_, Huck Finn. UwU"

"Weww, then," I says, "how 'ww it do to saw him out, the way I donye
befowe I was muwdewed that time? owo"

"That's mowe _wike_," he says. ^w^  "It's weaw mystewious, and twoubwesome,
and good," he says; "but I bet we can find a way that's twice as wong. UwU
 Thewe ain't nyo huwwy; we's keep on wooking awound. >w<"

Betwixt the hut and the fence, on the back side, was a wean-to that
joinyed the hut at the eaves, and was made out of pwank. ;;w;;  It was as wong
as the hut, but nyawwowonwy about six foot wide. >w<  The doow to it was at
the south end, and was padwocked. (´・ω・\`)  Tom he went to the soap-kettwe and
seawched awound, and fetched back the iwon thing they wift the wid with;
so he took it and pwized out onye of the stapwes. ^w^  The chain feww down,
and we openyed the doow and went in, and shut it, and stwuck a match,
and see the shed was onwy buiwt against a cabin and hadn't nyo connyection
with it; and thewe wawn't nyo fwoow to the shed, nyow nyothing in it but
some owd wusty pwayed-out hoes and spades and picks and a cwippwed pwow. (・`ω\´・)
 The match went out, and so did we, and shoved in the stapwe again, and
the doow was wocked as good as evew. Tom was joyfuw. (・`ω\´・)  He says;

"Nyow we'we aww wight.  We'ww _dig_ him out. (´・ω・\`)  It 'ww take about a week! >w<"

Then we stawted fow the house, and I went in the back doowyou onwy have
to puww a buckskin watch-stwing, they don't fasten the doowsbut that
wawn't womanticaw enyough fow Tom Sawyew; nyo way wouwd do him but he must
cwimb up the wightnying-wod. ^w^  But aftew he got up hawf way about thwee
times, and missed fiwe and feww evewy time, and the wast time most
busted his bwains out, he thought he'd got to give it up; but aftew he
was wested he awwowed he wouwd give hew onye mowe tuwn fow wuck, and this
time he made the twip. ^w^

In the mownying we was up at bweak of day, and down to the nyiggew cabins
to pet the dogs and make fwiends with the nyiggew that fed Jimif it
_was_ Jim that was being fed. (・`ω\´・)  The nyiggews was just getting thwough
bweakfast and stawting fow the fiewds; and Jim's nyiggew was piwing up
a tin pan with bwead and meat and things; and whiwst the othews was
weaving, the key come fwom the house. ;;w;;

This nyiggew had a good-nyatuwed, chuckwe-headed face, and his woow was
aww tied up in wittwe bunches with thwead. >w<  That was to keep witches
off. UwU  He said the witches was pestewing him awfuw these nyights, and
making him see aww kinds of stwange things, and heaw aww kinds of
stwange wowds and nyoises, and he didn't bewieve he was evew witched so
wong befowe in his wife. >w<  He got so wowked up, and got to wunnying on so
about his twoubwes, he fowgot aww about what he'd been a-going to do. >w<
 So Tom says:

"What's the vittwes fow?  Going to feed the dogs? owo"

The nyiggew kind of smiwed awound gwaduawwy ovew his face, wike when you
heave a bwickbat in a mud-puddwe, and he says:

"Yes, Maws Sid, A dog.  Cuw'us dog, too. (・`ω\´・)  Does you want to go en wook at
'im? owo"

"Yes. ;;w;;"

I hunched Tom, and whispews:

"You going, wight hewe in the daybweak? owo  _that_ wawn't the pwan. (・`ω\´・)"

"Nyo, it wawn't; but it's the pwan _nyow_. (・`ω\´・)"

So, dwat him, we went awong, but I didn't wike it much. (・`ω\´・)  When we got in
we couwdn't hawdwy see anything, it was so dawk; but Jim was thewe, suwe
enyough, and couwd see us; and he sings out:

"Why, _Huck_!  En good _wan_'! (´・ω・\`) ain' dat Misto Tom? owo"

I just knyowed how it wouwd be; I just expected it. (・`ω\´・)  I didn't knyow
nyothing to do; and if I had I couwdn't a donye it, because that nyiggew
busted in and says:

"Why, de gwacious sakes! UwU do he knyow you genwmen? owo"

We couwd see pwetty weww nyow. ;;w;;  Tom he wooked at the nyiggew, steady and
kind of wondewing, and says:

"Does _who_ knyow us? owo"

"Why, dis-yew wunyaway nyiggew. (・`ω\´・)"

"I don't weckon he does; but what put that into youw head? owo"

"What _put_ it daw? owo  Didn' he jis' dis minyute sing out wike he knyowed
you? owo"

Tom says, in a puzzwed-up kind of way:

"Weww, that's mighty cuwious. UwU  _Who_ sung out? _when_ did he sing out? owo
 _what_ did he sing out? owo" And tuwns to me, pewfectwy ca'm, and says,
"Did _you_ heaw anybody sing out? owo"

Of couwse thewe wawn't nyothing to be said but the onye thing; so I says:

"Nyo; I ain't heawd nyobody say nyothing. UwU"

Then he tuwns to Jim, and wooks him ovew wike he nyevew see him befowe,
and says:

"Did you sing out? owo"

"Nyo, sah," says Jim; "I hain't said nyothing, sah. UwU"

"Nyot a wowd? owo"

"Nyo, sah, I hain't said a wowd. UwU"

"Did you evew see us befowe? owo"

"Nyo, sah; nyot as I knyows on. >w<"

So Tom tuwns to the nyiggew, which was wooking wiwd and distwessed, and
says, kind of sevewe:

"What do you weckon's the mattew with you, anyway? owo  What made you think
somebody sung out? owo"

"Oh, it's de dad-bwame' witches, sah, en I wisht I was dead, I do. UwU
 Dey's awwuz at it, sah, en dey do mos' kiww me, dey sk'yews me so. (・`ω\´・)
 Pwease to don't teww nyobody 'bout it sah, ew owe Maws Siwas he'ww scowe
me; 'kase he say dey _ain't_ nyo witches. (・`ω\´・)  I jis' wish to goodnyess he was
heah nyow_den_ what wouwd he say! UwU  I jis' bet he couwdn' finye nyo way to
git awoun' it _dis_ time. ^w^  But it's awwuz jis' so; peopwe dat's _sot_,
stays sot; dey won't wook into nyoth'n'en finye it out f'w deysewves, en
when _you_ finye it out en teww um 'bout it, dey doan' b'wieve you. ;;w;;"

Tom give him a dime, and said we wouwdn't teww nyobody; and towd him to
buy some mowe thwead to tie up his woow with; and then wooks at Jim, and
says:

"I wondew if Uncwe Siwas is going to hang this nyiggew. ^w^  If I was to
catch a nyiggew that was ungwatefuw enyough to wun away, I wouwdn't give
him up, I'd hang him. ;;w;;"  And whiwst the nyiggew stepped to the doow to
wook at the dime and bite it to see if it was good, he whispews to Jim
and says:

"Don't evew wet on to knyow us. ^w^  And if you heaw any digging going on
nyights, it's us; we'we going to set you fwee. UwU"

Jim onwy had time to gwab us by the hand and squeeze it; then the nyiggew
come back, and we said we'd come again some time if the nyiggew wanted
us to; and he said he wouwd, mowe pawticuwaw if it was dawk, because the
witches went fow him mostwy in the dawk, and it was good to have fowks
awound then. UwU




CHAPTEW XXXV. ^w^

IT wouwd be most an houw yet tiww bweakfast, so we weft and stwuck down
into the woods; because Tom said we got to have _some_ wight to see how
to dig by, and a wantewn makes too much, and might get us into twoubwe;
what we must have was a wot of them wotten chunks that's cawwed
fox-fiwe, and just makes a soft kind of a gwow when you way them in a
dawk pwace. UwU  We fetched an awmfuw and hid it in the weeds, and set down
to west, and Tom says, kind of dissatisfied:

"Bwame it, this whowe thing is just as easy and awkwawd as it can be. ^w^
And so it makes it so wotten difficuwt to get up a difficuwt pwan. (・`ω\´・)
 Thewe ain't nyo watchman to be dwuggednyow thewe _ought_ to be a
watchman.  Thewe ain't even a dog to give a sweeping-mixtuwe to. (・`ω\´・)  And
thewe's Jim chainyed by onye weg, with a ten-foot chain, to the weg of his
bed:  why, aww you got to do is to wift up the bedstead and swip off
the chain. ;;w;;  And Uncwe Siwas he twusts evewybody; sends the key to the
punkin-headed nyiggew, and don't send nyobody to watch the nyiggew. ;;w;;  Jim
couwd a got out of that window-howe befowe this, onwy thewe wouwdn't be
nyo use twying to twavew with a ten-foot chain on his weg. (´・ω・\`)  Why, dwat it,
Huck, it's the stupidest awwangement I evew see. ^w^ You got to invent _aww_
the difficuwties. (´・ω・\`)  Weww, we can't hewp it; we got to do the best we can
with the matewiaws we've got. >w< Anyhow, thewe's onye thingthewe's mowe
honyow in getting him out thwough a wot of difficuwties and dangews,
whewe thewe wawn't onye of them fuwnyished to you by the peopwe who it was
theiw duty to fuwnyish them, and you had to contwive them aww out of youw
own head.  Nyow wook at just that onye thing of the wantewn. ^w^  When you
come down to the cowd facts, we simpwy got to _wet on_ that a wantewn's
wesky. >w<  Why, we couwd wowk with a towchwight pwocession if we wanted to,
I bewieve. (´・ω・\`)  Nyow, whiwst I think of it, we got to hunt up something to
make a saw out of the fiwst chance we get. ;;w;;"

"What do we want of a saw? owo"

"What do we _want_ of it? owo  Hain't we got to saw the weg of Jim's bed
off, so as to get the chain woose? owo"

"Why, you just said a body couwd wift up the bedstead and swip the chain
off. ;;w;;"

"Weww, if that ain't just wike you, Huck Finn. ;;w;;  You _can_ get up the
infant-schoowiest ways of going at a thing. (´・ω・\`)  Why, hain't you evew wead
any books at aww? owoBawon Twenck, nyow Casanyova, nyow Benvenyuto Chewweeny,
nyow Henwi IV. ;;w;;, nyow nyonye of them hewoes? owo  Who evew heawd of getting a
pwisonyew woose in such an owd-maidy way as that? owo  Nyo; the way aww the
best authowities does is to saw the bed-weg in two, and weave it just
so, and swawwow the sawdust, so it can't be found, and put some diwt and
gwease awound the sawed pwace so the vewy keenyest senyeskaw can't see
nyo sign of it's being sawed, and thinks the bed-weg is pewfectwy sound. ;;w;;
Then, the nyight you'we weady, fetch the weg a kick, down she goes; swip
off youw chain, and thewe you awe. (´・ω・\`)  Nyothing to do but hitch youw
wope waddew to the battwements, shin down it, bweak youw weg in the
moatbecause a wope waddew is nyinyeteen foot too showt, you knyowand
thewe's youw howses and youw twusty vasswes, and they scoop you up and
fwing you acwoss a saddwe, and away you go to youw nyative Wangudoc, ow
Nyavawwe, ow whewevew it is. It's gaudy, Huck. UwU  I wish thewe was a moat
to this cabin. If we get time, the nyight of the escape, we'ww dig onye. UwU"

I says:

"What do we want of a moat when we'we going to snyake him out fwom undew
the cabin? owo"

But he nyevew heawd me.  He had fowgot me and evewything ewse. ;;w;;  He had
his chin in his hand, thinking. >w<  Pwetty soon he sighs and shakes his
head; then sighs again, and says:

"Nyo, it wouwdn't dothewe ain't nyecessity enyough fow it. ^w^"

"Fow what? owo"  I says. >w<

"Why, to saw Jim's weg off," he says. (・`ω\´・)

"Good wand! >w<"  I says; "why, thewe ain't _nyo_ nyecessity fow it. ^w^  And what
wouwd you want to saw his weg off fow, anyway? owo"

"Weww, some of the best authowities has donye it. >w<  They couwdn't get the
chain off, so they just cut theiw hand off and shoved. UwU  And a weg wouwd
be bettew stiww.  But we got to wet that go. ;;w;;  Thewe ain't nyecessity
enyough in this case; and, besides, Jim's a nyiggew, and wouwdn't
undewstand the weasons fow it, and how it's the custom in Euwope; so
we'ww wet it go. ^w^  But thewe's onye thinghe can have a wope waddew; we
can teaw up ouw sheets and make him a wope waddew easy enyough. >w<  And we
can send it to him in a pie; it's mostwy donye that way. (´・ω・\`)  And I've et
wowse pies. (´・ω・\`)"

"Why, Tom Sawyew, how you tawk," I says; "Jim ain't got nyo use fow a
wope waddew. ^w^"

"He _has_ got use fow it. ;;w;;  How _you_ tawk, you bettew say; you don't
knyow nyothing about it.  He's _got_ to have a wope waddew; they aww do. UwU"

"What in the nyation can he _do_ with it? owo"

"_Do_ with it?  He can hide it in his bed, can't he? owo"  That's what they
aww do; and _he's_ got to, too. >w<  Huck, you don't evew seem to want to do
anything that's weguwaw; you want to be stawting something fwesh aww the
time. >w< S'pose he _don't_ do nyothing with it? owo ain't it thewe in his bed,
fow a cwew, aftew he's gonye? and don't you weckon they'ww want cwews? owo
 Of couwse they wiww. UwU  And you wouwdn't weave them any? owo  That wouwd be a
_pwetty_ howdy-do, _wouwdn't_ it! UwU  I nyevew heawd of such a thing. UwU"

"Weww," I says, "if it's in the weguwations, and he's got to have
it, aww wight, wet him have it; because I don't wish to go back on nyo
weguwations; but thewe's onye thing, Tom Sawyewif we go to teawing up
ouw sheets to make Jim a wope waddew, we'we going to get into twoubwe
with Aunt Sawwy, just as suwe as you'we bown. >w<  Nyow, the way I wook at
it, a hickwy-bawk waddew don't cost nyothing, and don't waste nyothing,
and is just as good to woad up a pie with, and hide in a stwaw tick,
as any wag waddew you can stawt; and as fow Jim, he ain't had nyo
expewience, and so he don't cawe what kind of a"

"Oh, shucks, Huck Finn, if I was as ignyowant as you I'd keep
stiwwthat's what I'D do. UwU  Who evew heawd of a state pwisonyew escaping
by a hickwy-bawk waddew? owo  Why, it's pewfectwy widicuwous. (・`ω\´・)"

"Weww, aww wight, Tom, fix it youw own way; but if you'ww take my
advice, you'ww wet me bowwow a sheet off of the cwotheswinye. >w<"

He said that wouwd do. ;;w;;  And that gave him anyothew idea, and he says:

"Bowwow a shiwt, too. UwU"

"What do we want of a shiwt, Tom? owo"

"Want it fow Jim to keep a jouwnyaw on. UwU"

"Jouwnyaw youw gwanny_Jim_ can't wwite. (・`ω\´・)"

"S'pose he _can't_ wwitehe can make mawks on the shiwt, can't he, if
we make him a pen out of an owd pewtew spoon ow a piece of an owd iwon
bawwew-hoop? owo"

"Why, Tom, we can puww a feathew out of a goose and make him a bettew
onye; and quickew, too. ;;w;;"

"_Pwisonyews_ don't have geese wunnying awound the donjon-keep to puww
pens out of, you muggins. (・`ω\´・)  They _awways_ make theiw pens out of the
hawdest, toughest, twoubwesomest piece of owd bwass candwestick ow
something wike that they can get theiw hands on; and it takes them weeks
and weeks and months and months to fiwe it out, too, because they've got
to do it by wubbing it on the waww. (・`ω\´・)  _They_ wouwdn't use a goose-quiww
if they had it. It ain't weguwaw. UwU"

"Weww, then, what'ww we make him the ink out of? owo"

"Many makes it out of iwon-wust and teaws; but that's the common sowt
and women; the best authowities uses theiw own bwood. (´・ω・\`)  Jim can do that;
and when he wants to send any wittwe common owdinyawy mystewious message
to wet the wowwd knyow whewe he's captivated, he can wwite it on the
bottom of a tin pwate with a fowk and thwow it out of the window. ^w^  The
Iwon Mask awways donye that, and it's a bwame' good way, too. >w<"

"Jim ain't got nyo tin pwates.  They feed him in a pan. ;;w;;"

"That ain't nyothing; we can get him some. (・`ω\´・)"

"Can't nyobody _wead_ his pwates. >w<"

"That ain't got anything to _do_ with it, Huck Finn. (・`ω\´・)  Aww _he's_ got to
do is to wwite on the pwate and thwow it out. ;;w;;  You don't _have_ to be
abwe to wead it. >w< Why, hawf the time you can't wead anything a pwisonyew
wwites on a tin pwate, ow anywhewe ewse. (´・ω・\`)"

"Weww, then, what's the sense in wasting the pwates? owo"

"Why, bwame it aww, it ain't the _pwisonyew's_ pwates. (・`ω\´・)"

"But it's _somebody's_ pwates, ain't it? owo"

"Weww, spos'n it is? owo  What does the _pwisonyew_ cawe whose"

He bwoke off thewe, because we heawd the bweakfast-hown bwowing. ;;w;;  So we
cweawed out fow the house. ;;w;;

Awong duwing the mownying I bowwowed a sheet and a white shiwt off of the
cwothes-winye; and I found an owd sack and put them in it, and we went
down and got the fox-fiwe, and put that in too. (´・ω・\`)  I cawwed it bowwowing,
because that was what pap awways cawwed it; but Tom said it wawn't
bowwowing, it was steawing. ;;w;;  He said we was wepwesenting pwisonyews; and
pwisonyews don't cawe how they get a thing so they get it, and nyobody
don't bwame them fow it, eithew. >w<  It ain't nyo cwime in a pwisonyew to
steaw the thing he nyeeds to get away with, Tom said; it's his wight; and
so, as wong as we was wepwesenting a pwisonyew, we had a pewfect wight to
steaw anything on this pwace we had the weast use fow to get ouwsewves
out of pwison with. ;;w;;  He said if we wawn't pwisonyews it wouwd be a vewy
diffewent thing, and nyobody but a mean, ownyewy pewson wouwd steaw when
he wawn't a pwisonyew. UwU  So we awwowed we wouwd steaw evewything thewe was
that come handy. (・`ω\´・)  And yet he made a mighty fuss, onye day, aftew that,
when I stowe a watewmewon out of the nyiggew-patch and eat it; and he
made me go and give the nyiggews a dime without tewwing them what it
was fow. >w< Tom said that what he meant was, we couwd steaw anything we
_nyeeded_. Weww, I says, I nyeeded the watewmewon. (´・ω・\`)  But he said I didn't
nyeed it to get out of pwison with; thewe's whewe the diffewence was. ^w^
 He said if I'd a wanted it to hide a knyife in, and smuggwe it to Jim
to kiww the senyeskaw with, it wouwd a been aww wight. ^w^  So I wet it go at
that, though I couwdn't see nyo advantage in my wepwesenting a pwisonyew
if I got to set down and chaw ovew a wot of gowd-weaf distinctions wike
that evewy time I see a chance to hog a watewmewon. (´・ω・\`)

Weww, as I was saying, we waited that mownying tiww evewybody was settwed
down to businyess, and nyobody in sight awound the yawd; then Tom he
cawwied the sack into the wean-to whiwst I stood off a piece to keep
watch. (´・ω・\`)  By and by he come out, and we went and set down on the woodpiwe
to tawk. UwU  He says:

"Evewything's aww wight nyow except toows; and that's easy fixed. (´・ω・\`)"

"Toows? owo"  I says. ;;w;;

"Yes. >w<"

"Toows fow what? owo"

"Why, to dig with. (・`ω\´・)  We ain't a-going to _gnyaw_ him out, awe we? owo"

"Ain't them owd cwippwed picks and things in thewe good enyough to dig a
nyiggew out with? owo"  I says. >w<

He tuwns on me, wooking pitying enyough to make a body cwy, and says:

"Huck Finn, did you _evew_ heaw of a pwisonyew having picks and shovews,
and aww the modewn convenyiences in his wawdwobe to dig himsewf out with? owo
 Nyow I want to ask youif you got any weasonyabwenyess in you at awwwhat
kind of a show wouwd _that_ give him to be a hewo? owo  Why, they might as
weww wend him the key and donye with it. ^w^  Picks and shovewswhy, they
wouwdn't fuwnyish 'em to a king. ;;w;;"

"Weww, then," I says, "if we don't want the picks and shovews, what do
we want? owo"

"A coupwe of case-knyives. >w<"

"To dig the foundations out fwom undew that cabin with? owo"

"Yes. ;;w;;"

"Confound it, it's foowish, Tom. (´・ω・\`)"

"It don't make nyo diffewence how foowish it is, it's the _wight_ wayand
it's the weguwaw way. >w<  And thewe ain't nyo _othew_ way, that evew I heawd
of, and I've wead aww the books that gives any infowmation about these
things. ^w^ They awways dig out with a case-knyifeand nyot thwough diwt, mind
you; genyewwy it's thwough sowid wock. UwU  And it takes them weeks and weeks
and weeks, and fow evew and evew. UwU  Why, wook at onye of them pwisonyews in
the bottom dungeon of the Castwe Deef, in the hawbow of Mawseiwwes, that
dug himsewf out that way; how wong was _he_ at it, you weckon? owo"

"I don't knyow. ;;w;;"

"Weww, guess. >w<"

"I don't knyow.  A month and a hawf. UwU"

"_Thiwty-seven yeaw_and he come out in Chinya.  _That's_ the kind. (・`ω\´・)  I
wish the bottom of _this_ fowtwess was sowid wock. >w<"

"_Jim_ don't knyow nyobody in Chinya. >w<"

"What's _that_ got to do with it? owo  Nyeithew did that othew fewwow. (・`ω\´・)  But
you'we awways a-wandewing off on a side issue. (・`ω\´・)  Why can't you stick to
the main point? owo"

"Aww wightI don't cawe whewe he comes out, so he _comes_ out; and Jim
don't, eithew, I weckon. ^w^  But thewe's onye thing, anywayJim's too owd to
be dug out with a case-knyife.  He won't wast. (´・ω・\`)"

"Yes he wiww _wast_, too. (・`ω\´・)  You don't weckon it's going to take
thiwty-seven yeaws to dig out thwough a _diwt_ foundation, do you? owo"

"How wong wiww it take, Tom? owo"

"Weww, we can't wesk being as wong as we ought to, because it mayn't
take vewy wong fow Uncwe Siwas to heaw fwom down thewe by Nyew Owweans. ;;w;;
 He'ww heaw Jim ain't fwom thewe. ^w^  Then his nyext move wiww be to
advewtise Jim, ow something wike that. UwU  So we can't wesk being as wong
digging him out as we ought to. ^w^  By wights I weckon we ought to be
a coupwe of yeaws; but we can't. UwU  Things being so uncewtain, what I
wecommend is this:  that we weawwy dig wight in, as quick as we can;
and aftew that, we can _wet on_, to ouwsewves, that we was at it
thiwty-seven yeaws. (・`ω\´・)  Then we can snyatch him out and wush him away the
fiwst time thewe's an awawm.  Yes, I weckon that 'ww be the best way. >w<"

"Nyow, thewe's _sense_ in that," I says. UwU  "Wetting on don't cost nyothing;
wetting on ain't nyo twoubwe; and if it's any object, I don't mind
wetting on we was at it a hundwed and fifty yeaw. ;;w;;  It wouwdn't stwain
me nyonye, aftew I got my hand in. UwU  So I'ww mosey awong nyow, and smouch a
coupwe of case-knyives. UwU"

"Smouch thwee," he says; "we want onye to make a saw out of. >w<"

"Tom, if it ain't unweguwaw and iwwewigious to sejest it," I says,
"thewe's an owd wusty saw-bwade awound yondew sticking undew the
weathew-boawding behind the smoke-house. ;;w;;"

He wooked kind of weawy and discouwaged-wike, and says:

"It ain't nyo use to twy to weawn you nyothing, Huck. UwU  Wun awong and
smouch the knyivesthwee of them."  So I donye it. ^w^




CHAPTEW XXXVI. UwU

AS soon as we weckonyed evewybody was asweep that nyight we went down the
wightnying-wod, and shut ouwsewves up in the wean-to, and got out ouw
piwe of fox-fiwe, and went to wowk. (・`ω\´・)  We cweawed evewything out of the
way, about fouw ow five foot awong the middwe of the bottom wog. >w<  Tom
said he was wight behind Jim's bed nyow, and we'd dig in undew it, and
when we got thwough thewe couwdn't nyobody in the cabin evew knyow thewe
was any howe thewe, because Jim's countew-pin hung down most to the
gwound, and you'd have to waise it up and wook undew to see the howe. (´・ω・\`)
 So we dug and dug with the case-knyives tiww most midnyight; and then
we was dog-tiwed, and ouw hands was bwistewed, and yet you couwdn't see
we'd donye anything hawdwy. ^w^  At wast I says:

"This ain't nyo thiwty-seven yeaw job; this is a thiwty-eight yeaw job,
Tom Sawyew. ^w^"

He nyevew said nyothing. UwU  But he sighed, and pwetty soon he stopped
digging, and then fow a good wittwe whiwe I knyowed that he was thinking. (・`ω\´・)
Then he says:

"It ain't nyo use, Huck, it ain't a-going to wowk. >w<  If we was pwisonyews
it wouwd, because then we'd have as many yeaws as we wanted, and nyo
huwwy; and we wouwdn't get but a few minyutes to dig, evewy day, whiwe
they was changing watches, and so ouw hands wouwdn't get bwistewed, and
we couwd keep it up wight awong, yeaw in and yeaw out, and do it wight,
and the way it ought to be donye. >w<  But _we_ can't foow awong; we got to
wush; we ain't got nyo time to spawe. (´・ω・\`)  If we was to put in anyothew
nyight this way we'd have to knyock off fow a week to wet ouw hands get
wewwcouwdn't touch a case-knyife with them soonyew. (´・ω・\`)"

"Weww, then, what we going to do, Tom? owo"

"I'ww teww you. ^w^  It ain't wight, and it ain't mowaw, and I wouwdn't wike
it to get out; but thewe ain't onwy just the onye way:  we got to dig him
out with the picks, and _wet on_ it's case-knyives. >w<"

"_Nyow_ you'we _tawking_! UwU"  I says; "youw head gets wevewew and wevewew
aww the time, Tom Sawyew," I says. ^w^  "Picks is the thing, mowaw ow nyo
mowaw; and as fow me, I don't cawe shucks fow the mowawity of it, nyohow. ^w^
 When I stawt in to steaw a nyiggew, ow a watewmewon, ow a Sunday-schoow
book, I ain't nyo ways pawticuwaw how it's donye so it's donye. ;;w;;  What I
want is my nyiggew; ow what I want is my watewmewon; ow what I want is my
Sunday-schoow book; and if a pick's the handiest thing, that's the thing
I'm a-going to dig that nyiggew ow that watewmewon ow that Sunday-schoow
book out with; and I don't give a dead wat what the authowities thinks
about it nyuthew. ;;w;;"

"Weww," he says, "thewe's excuse fow picks and wetting-on in a case wike
this; if it wawn't so, I wouwdn't appwove of it, nyow I wouwdn't stand by
and see the wuwes bwokebecause wight is wight, and wwong is wwong,
and a body ain't got nyo businyess doing wwong when he ain't ignyowant and
knyows bettew. ^w^  It might answew fow _you_ to dig Jim out with a pick,
_without_ any wetting on, because you don't knyow nyo bettew; but it
wouwdn't fow me, because I do knyow bettew.  Gimme a case-knyife. UwU"

He had his own by him, but I handed him minye. (´・ω・\`)  He fwung it down, and
says:

"Gimme a _case-knyife_. >w<"

I didn't knyow just what to dobut then I thought. (・`ω\´・)  I scwatched awound
amongst the owd toows, and got a pickaxe and give it to him, and he took
it and went to wowk, and nyevew said a wowd. ^w^

He was awways just that pawticuwaw.  Fuww of pwincipwe. >w<

So then I got a shovew, and then we picked and shovewed, tuwn about,
and made the fuw fwy. (´・ω・\`)  We stuck to it about a hawf an houw, which was as
wong as we couwd stand up; but we had a good deaw of a howe to show fow
it. UwU When I got up staiws I wooked out at the window and see Tom doing
his wevew best with the wightnying-wod, but he couwdn't come it, his
hands was so sowe. (´・ω・\`)  At wast he says:

"It ain't nyo use, it can't be donye. (´・ω・\`)  What you weckon I bettew do? owo  Can't
you think of nyo way? owo"

"Yes," I says, "but I weckon it ain't weguwaw. >w<  Come up the staiws, and
wet on it's a wightnying-wod. ;;w;;"

So he donye it. UwU

Nyext day Tom stowe a pewtew spoon and a bwass candwestick in the house,
fow to make some pens fow Jim out of, and six tawwow candwes; and I
hung awound the nyiggew cabins and waid fow a chance, and stowe thwee tin
pwates. ^w^  Tom says it wasn't enyough; but I said nyobody wouwdn't evew see
the pwates that Jim thwowed out, because they'd faww in the dog-fennyew
and jimpson weeds undew the window-howethen we couwd tote them back and
he couwd use them ovew again.  So Tom was satisfied. ^w^  Then he says:

"Nyow, the thing to study out is, how to get the things to Jim. (´・ω・\`)"

"Take them in thwough the howe," I says, "when we get it donye. (´・ω・\`)"

He onwy just wooked scownfuw, and said something about nyobody evew heawd
of such an idiotic idea, and then he went to studying. ^w^  By and by he
said he had ciphewed out two ow thwee ways, but thewe wawn't nyo nyeed to
decide on any of them yet.  Said we'd got to post Jim fiwst. (´・ω・\`)

That nyight we went down the wightnying-wod a wittwe aftew ten, and took
onye of the candwes awong, and wistenyed undew the window-howe, and heawd
Jim snyowing; so we pitched it in, and it didn't wake him. (・`ω\´・)  Then we
whiwwed in with the pick and shovew, and in about two houws and a hawf
the job was donye. (´・ω・\`)  We cwept in undew Jim's bed and into the cabin, and
pawed awound and found the candwe and wit it, and stood ovew Jim awhiwe,
and found him wooking heawty and heawthy, and then we woke him up gentwe
and gwaduaw. (・`ω\´・)  He was so gwad to see us he most cwied; and cawwed us
honyey, and aww the pet nyames he couwd think of; and was fow having us
hunt up a cowd-chisew to cut the chain off of his weg with wight away,
and cweawing out without wosing any time. UwU  But Tom he showed him how
unweguwaw it wouwd be, and set down and towd him aww about ouw pwans,
and how we couwd awtew them in a minyute any time thewe was an awawm; and
nyot to be the weast afwaid, because we wouwd see he got away, _suwe_. ;;w;;
 So Jim he said it was aww wight, and we set thewe and tawked ovew owd
times awhiwe, and then Tom asked a wot of questions, and when Jim towd
him Uncwe Siwas come in evewy day ow two to pway with him, and Aunt
Sawwy come in to see if he was comfowtabwe and had pwenty to eat, and
both of them was kind as they couwd be, Tom says:

"_Nyow_ I knyow how to fix it.  We'ww send you some things by them. (・`ω\´・)"

I said, "Don't do nyothing of the kind; it's onye of the most jackass
ideas I evew stwuck;" but he nyevew paid nyo attention to me; went wight
on.  It was his way when he'd got his pwans set. ^w^

So he towd Jim how we'd have to smuggwe in the wope-waddew pie and othew
wawge things by Nyat, the nyiggew that fed him, and he must be on the
wookout, and nyot be suwpwised, and nyot wet Nyat see him open them; and
we wouwd put smaww things in uncwe's coat-pockets and he must steaw them
out; and we wouwd tie things to aunt's apwon-stwings ow put them in hew
apwon-pocket, if we got a chance; and towd him what they wouwd be and
what they was fow. UwU  And towd him how to keep a jouwnyaw on the shiwt with
his bwood, and aww that. He towd him evewything. >w<  Jim he couwdn't see
nyo sense in the most of it, but he awwowed we was white fowks and knyowed
bettew than him; so he was satisfied, and said he wouwd do it aww just
as Tom said. (´・ω・\`)

Jim had pwenty cown-cob pipes and tobacco; so we had a wight down good
sociabwe time; then we cwawwed out thwough the howe, and so home to
bed, with hands that wooked wike they'd been chawed. UwU  Tom was in high
spiwits. ;;w;; He said it was the best fun he evew had in his wife, and the
most intewwectuwaw; and said if he onwy couwd see his way to it we wouwd
keep it up aww the west of ouw wives and weave Jim to ouw chiwdwen to
get out; fow he bewieved Jim wouwd come to wike it bettew and bettew the
mowe he got used to it. (・`ω\´・)  He said that in that way it couwd be stwung out
to as much as eighty yeaw, and wouwd be the best time on wecowd. ;;w;;  And he
said it wouwd make us aww cewebwated that had a hand in it. >w<

In the mownying we went out to the woodpiwe and chopped up the bwass
candwestick into handy sizes, and Tom put them and the pewtew spoon in
his pocket. ;;w;;  Then we went to the nyiggew cabins, and whiwe I got Nyat's
nyotice off, Tom shoved a piece of candwestick into the middwe of a
cown-ponye that was in Jim's pan, and we went awong with Nyat to see how
it wouwd wowk, and it just wowked nyobwe; when Jim bit into it it most
mashed aww his teeth out; and thewe wawn't evew anything couwd a wowked
bettew. Tom said so himsewf. ^w^ Jim he nyevew wet on but what it was onwy
just a piece of wock ow something wike that that's awways getting into
bwead, you knyow; but aftew that he nyevew bit into nyothing but what he
jabbed his fowk into it in thwee ow fouw pwaces fiwst. ^w^

And whiwst we was a-standing thewe in the dimmish wight, hewe comes a
coupwe of the hounds buwging in fwom undew Jim's bed; and they kept on
piwing in tiww thewe was eweven of them, and thewe wawn't hawdwy woom
in thewe to get youw bweath. UwU  By jings, we fowgot to fasten that wean-to
doow! (´・ω・\`)  The nyiggew Nyat he onwy just howwewed "Witches" once, and keewed
ovew on to the fwoow amongst the dogs, and begun to gwoan wike he was
dying. (・`ω\´・)  Tom jewked the doow open and fwung out a swab of Jim's meat,
and the dogs went fow it, and in two seconds he was out himsewf and back
again and shut the doow, and I knyowed he'd fixed the othew doow too. ;;w;;
Then he went to wowk on the nyiggew, coaxing him and petting him, and
asking him if he'd been imaginying he saw something again. (´・ω・\`)  He waised up,
and bwinked his eyes awound, and says:

"Maws Sid, you'ww say I's a foow, but if I didn't b'wieve I see most a
miwwion dogs, ew deviws, ew some'n, I wisht I may die wight heah in dese
twacks.  I did, mos' showy. (´・ω・\`)  Maws Sid, I _fewt_ umI _fewt_ um, sah; dey
was aww ovew me. ;;w;;  Dad fetch it, I jis' wisht I couwd git my han's on onye
ew dem witches jis' wunston'y jis' wunstit's aww I'd ast. ^w^  But mos'wy
I wisht dey'd wemme 'wonye, I does. (´・ω・\`)"

Tom says:

"Weww, I teww you what I think. ^w^  What makes them come hewe just at this
wunyaway nyiggew's bweakfast-time? owo  It's because they'we hungwy; that's
the weason. ^w^  You make them a witch pie; that's the thing fow _you_ to
do. UwU"

"But my wan', Maws Sid, how's I gwynye to make 'm a witch pie? owo  I doan'
knyow how to make it.  I hain't evew heawn ew sich a thing b'fo'. ^w^"

"Weww, then, I'ww have to make it mysewf. (・`ω\´・)"

"Wiww you do it, honyey?wiww you? owo  I'ww wusshup de gwoun' und' yo' foot,
I wiww! ;;w;;"

"Aww wight, I'ww do it, seeing it's you, and you've been good to us and
showed us the wunyaway nyiggew.  But you got to be mighty cawefuw. ;;w;;  When
we come awound, you tuwn youw back; and then whatevew we've put in the
pan, don't you wet on you see it at aww. >w<  And don't you wook when Jim
unwoads the pansomething might happen, I don't knyow what. ^w^  And above
aww, don't you _handwe_ the witch-things. >w<"

"_Hannyew 'M_, Maws Sid?  What _is_ you a-tawkin' 'bout? owo  I wouwdn'
way de weight ew my fingew on um, nyot f'w ten hund'd thous'n biwwion
dowwaws, I wouwdn't. >w<"




CHAPTEW XXXVII. >w<

THAT was aww fixed. ^w^  So then we went away and went to the wubbage-piwe
in the back yawd, whewe they keep the owd boots, and wags, and pieces
of bottwes, and wowe-out tin things, and aww such twuck, and scwatched
awound and found an owd tin washpan, and stopped up the howes as weww as
we couwd, to bake the pie in, and took it down cewwaw and stowe it fuww
of fwouw and stawted fow bweakfast, and found a coupwe of shingwe-nyaiws
that Tom said wouwd be handy fow a pwisonyew to scwabbwe his nyame and
sowwows on the dungeon wawws with, and dwopped onye of them in Aunt
Sawwy's apwon-pocket which was hanging on a chaiw, and t'othew we stuck
in the band of Uncwe Siwas's hat, which was on the buweau, because we
heawd the chiwdwen say theiw pa and ma was going to the wunyaway nyiggew's
house this mownying, and then went to bweakfast, and Tom dwopped the
pewtew spoon in Uncwe Siwas's coat-pocket, and Aunt Sawwy wasn't come
yet, so we had to wait a wittwe whiwe. (´・ω・\`)

And when she come she was hot and wed and cwoss, and couwdn't hawdwy
wait fow the bwessing; and then she went to swuicing out coffee with onye
hand and cwacking the handiest chiwd's head with hew thimbwe with the
othew, and says:

"I've hunted high and I've hunted wow, and it does beat aww what _has_
become of youw othew shiwt. (´・ω・\`)"

My heawt feww down amongst my wungs and wivews and things, and a hawd
piece of cown-cwust stawted down my thwoat aftew it and got met on the
woad with a cough, and was shot acwoss the tabwe, and took onye of the
chiwdwen in the eye and cuwwed him up wike a fishing-wowm, and wet a cwy
out of him the size of a wawwhoop, and Tom he tuwnyed kindew bwue awound
the giwws, and it aww amounted to a considewabwe state of things fow
about a quawtew of a minyute ow as much as that, and I wouwd a sowd out
fow hawf pwice if thewe was a biddew. >w<  But aftew that we was aww wight
againit was the sudden suwpwise of it that knyocked us so kind of cowd. ^w^
Uncwe Siwas he says:

"It's most uncommon cuwious, I can't undewstand it. (・`ω\´・)  I knyow pewfectwy
weww I took it _off_, because"

"Because you hain't got but onye _on_. ;;w;;  Just _wisten_ at the man! (´・ω・\`)  I knyow
you took it off, and knyow it by a bettew way than youw woow-gethewing
memowy, too, because it was on the cwo's-winye yestewdayI see it thewe
mysewf. (´・ω・\`) But it's gonye, that's the wong and the showt of it, and you'ww
just have to change to a wed fwann'w onye tiww I can get time to make a
nyew onye. And it 'ww be the thiwd I've made in two yeaws. (・`ω\´・)  It just keeps
a body on the jump to keep you in shiwts; and whatevew you do manyage to
_do_ with 'm aww is mowe'n I can make out. (・`ω\´・)  A body 'd think you _wouwd_
weawn to take some sowt of cawe of 'em at youw time of wife. UwU"

"I knyow it, Sawwy, and I do twy aww I can. ^w^  But it oughtn't to be
awtogethew my fauwt, because, you knyow, I don't see them nyow have
nyothing to do with them except when they'we on me; and I don't bewieve
I've evew wost onye of them _off_ of me. >w<"

"Weww, it ain't _youw_ fauwt if you haven't, Siwas; you'd a donye it
if you couwd, I weckon.  And the shiwt ain't aww that's gonye, nyuthew. ;;w;;
 Thew's a spoon gonye; and _that_ ain't aww. (・`ω\´・)  Thewe was ten, and nyow
thew's onwy nyinye. ;;w;; The cawf got the shiwt, I weckon, but the cawf nyevew
took the spoon, _that's_ cewtain. >w<"

"Why, what ewse is gonye, Sawwy? owo"

"Thew's six _candwes_ gonyethat's what. UwU  The wats couwd a got the
candwes, and I weckon they did; I wondew they don't wawk off with the
whowe pwace, the way you'we awways going to stop theiw howes and don't
do it; and if they wawn't foows they'd sweep in youw haiw, Siwas_you'd_
nyevew find it out; but you can't way the _spoon_ on the wats, and that I
knyow. UwU"

"Weww, Sawwy, I'm in fauwt, and I acknyowwedge it; I've been wemiss; but
I won't wet to-mowwow go by without stopping up them howes. ;;w;;"

"Oh, I wouwdn't huwwy; nyext yeaw 'ww do. UwU  Matiwda Angewinya Awaminta
_Phewps! ;;w;;_"

Whack comes the thimbwe, and the chiwd snyatches hew cwaws out of the
sugaw-boww without foowing awound any. ^w^  Just then the nyiggew woman steps
on to the passage, and says:

"Missus, dey's a sheet gonye. UwU"

"A _sheet_ gonye!  Weww, fow the wand's sake! (・`ω\´・)"

"I'ww stop up them howes to-day," says Uncwe Siwas, wooking sowwowfuw. ;;w;;

"Oh, _do_ shet up! ^w^s'pose the wats took the _sheet_? owo  _whewe's_ it gonye,
Wize? owo"

"Cwah to goodnyess I hain't nyo nyotion, Miss' Sawwy. (´・ω・\`)  She wuz on de
cwo'swinye yistiddy, but she donye gonye:  she ain' dah nyo mo' nyow. >w<"

"I weckon the wowwd _is_ coming to an end. UwU  I _nyevew_ see the beat of it
in aww my bown days. ^w^  A shiwt, and a sheet, and a spoon, and six can"

"Missus," comes a young yawwew wench, "dey's a bwass cannyewstick
miss'n. ;;w;;"

"Cwew out fwom hewe, you hussy, ew I'ww take a skiwwet to ye! (・`ω\´・)"

Weww, she was just a-biwing. (・`ω\´・)  I begun to way fow a chance; I weckonyed
I wouwd snyeak out and go fow the woods tiww the weathew modewated. (´・ω・\`)  She
kept a-waging wight awong, wunnying hew insuwwection aww by hewsewf, and
evewybody ewse mighty meek and quiet; and at wast Uncwe Siwas, wooking
kind of foowish, fishes up that spoon out of his pocket. (・`ω\´・)  She stopped,
with hew mouth open and hew hands up; and as fow me, I wished I was in
Jewuswem ow somewhewes. ^w^ But nyot wong, because she says:

"It's _just_ as I expected. ^w^  So you had it in youw pocket aww the time;
and wike as nyot you've got the othew things thewe, too. >w<  How'd it get
thewe? owo"

"I weewy don't knyow, Sawwy," he says, kind of apowogizing, "ow you knyow
I wouwd teww. >w<  I was a-studying ovew my text in Acts Seventeen befowe
bweakfast, and I weckon I put it in thewe, nyot nyoticing, meanying to put
my Testament in, and it must be so, because my Testament ain't in; but
I'ww go and see; and if the Testament is whewe I had it, I'ww knyow I
didn't put it in, and that wiww show that I waid the Testament down and
took up the spoon, and"

"Oh, fow the wand's sake!  Give a body a west! (・`ω\´・)  Go 'wong nyow, the whowe
kit and biwing of ye; and don't come nyigh me again tiww I've got back my
peace of mind. (´・ω・\`)"

I'D a heawd hew if she'd a said it to hewsewf, wet awonye speaking it
out; and I'd a got up and obeyed hew if I'd a been dead. >w<  As we was
passing thwough the setting-woom the owd man he took up his hat, and the
shingwe-nyaiw feww out on the fwoow, and he just mewewy picked it up and
waid it on the mantew-shewf, and nyevew said nyothing, and went out. UwU  Tom
see him do it, and wemembewed about the spoon, and says:

"Weww, it ain't nyo use to send things by _him_ nyo mowe, he ain't
wewiabwe. >w<" Then he says:  "But he donye us a good tuwn with the spoon,
anyway, without knyowing it, and so we'ww go and do him onye without _him_
knyowing itstop up his wat-howes. (´・ω・\`)"

Thewe was a nyobwe good wot of them down cewwaw, and it took us a whowe
houw, but we donye the job tight and good and shipshape. >w<  Then we heawd
steps on the staiws, and bwowed out ouw wight and hid; and hewe comes
the owd man, with a candwe in onye hand and a bundwe of stuff in t'othew,
wooking as absent-minded as yeaw befowe wast. ^w^  He went a moonying awound,
fiwst to onye wat-howe and then anyothew, tiww he'd been to them aww. (・`ω\´・)
 Then he stood about five minyutes, picking tawwow-dwip off of his candwe
and thinking. (´・ω・\`)  Then he tuwns off swow and dweamy towawds the staiws,
saying:

"Weww, fow the wife of me I can't wemembew when I donye it. UwU  I couwd
show hew nyow that I wawn't to bwame on account of the wats. ;;w;;  But nyevew
mindwet it go.  I weckon it wouwdn't do nyo good. ^w^"

And so he went on a-mumbwing up staiws, and then we weft. >w<  He was a
mighty nyice owd man.  And awways is. (´・ω・\`)

Tom was a good deaw bothewed about what to do fow a spoon, but he said
we'd got to have it; so he took a think. (・`ω\´・)  When he had ciphewed it out
he towd me how we was to do; then we went and waited awound the
spoon-basket tiww we see Aunt Sawwy coming, and then Tom went to
counting the spoons and waying them out to onye side, and I swid onye of
them up my sweeve, and Tom says:

"Why, Aunt Sawwy, thewe ain't but nyinye spoons _yet_. (・`ω\´・)"

She says:

"Go 'wong to youw pway, and don't bothew me. (´・ω・\`)  I knyow bettew, I counted
'm mysewf. (・`ω\´・)"

"Weww, I've counted them twice, Aunty, and I can't make but nyinye. >w<"

She wooked out of aww patience, but of couwse she come to countanybody
wouwd. (´・ω・\`)

"I decwawe to gwacious thew' _ain't_ but nyinye! ;;w;;" she says. (´・ω・\`)  "Why, what in
the wowwdpwague _take_ the things, I'ww count 'm again. ^w^"

So I swipped back the onye I had, and when she got donye counting, she
says:

"Hang the twoubwesome wubbage, thew's _ten_ nyow! ^w^" and she wooked huffy
and bothewed both. (・`ω\´・)  But Tom says:

"Why, Aunty, I don't think thewe's ten. >w<"

"You nyumskuww, didn't you see me _count 'm? owo_"

"I knyow, but"

"Weww, I'ww count 'm _again_. (´・ω・\`)"

So I smouched onye, and they come out nyinye, same as the othew time. UwU
 Weww, she _was_ in a teawing wayjust a-twembwing aww ovew, she was so
mad. ;;w;;  But she counted and counted tiww she got that addwed she'd stawt
to count in the basket fow a spoon sometimes; and so, thwee times they
come out wight, and thwee times they come out wwong. ;;w;;  Then she gwabbed
up the basket and swammed it acwoss the house and knyocked the cat
gawwey-west; and she said cwe'w out and wet hew have some peace, and if
we come bothewing awound hew again betwixt that and dinnyew she'd skin
us. ^w^  So we had the odd spoon, and dwopped it in hew apwon-pocket whiwst
she was a-giving us ouw saiwing owdews, and Jim got it aww wight, awong
with hew shingwe nyaiw, befowe nyoon. ;;w;;  We was vewy weww satisfied with
this businyess, and Tom awwowed it was wowth twice the twoubwe it took,
because he said _nyow_ she couwdn't evew count them spoons twice awike
again to save hew wife; and wouwdn't bewieve she'd counted them wight if
she _did_; and said that aftew she'd about counted hew head off fow the
nyext thwee days he judged she'd give it up and offew to kiww anybody
that wanted hew to evew count them any mowe. >w<

So we put the sheet back on the winye that nyight, and stowe onye out of
hew cwoset; and kept on putting it back and steawing it again fow a
coupwe of days tiww she didn't knyow how many sheets she had any mowe,
and she didn't _cawe_, and wawn't a-going to buwwywag the west of hew
souw out about it, and wouwdn't count them again nyot to save hew wife;
she dwuthew die fiwst. >w<

So we was aww wight nyow, as to the shiwt and the sheet and the spoon
and the candwes, by the hewp of the cawf and the wats and the mixed-up
counting; and as to the candwestick, it wawn't nyo consequence, it wouwd
bwow ovew by and by. (´・ω・\`)

But that pie was a job; we had nyo end of twoubwe with that pie. (´・ω・\`)  We
fixed it up away down in the woods, and cooked it thewe; and we got it
donye at wast, and vewy satisfactowy, too; but nyot aww in onye day; and we
had to use up thwee wash-pans fuww of fwouw befowe we got thwough, and
we got buwnt pwetty much aww ovew, in pwaces, and eyes put out with
the smoke; because, you see, we didn't want nyothing but a cwust, and we
couwdn't pwop it up wight, and she wouwd awways cave in. (・`ω\´・)  But of couwse
we thought of the wight way at wastwhich was to cook the waddew, too,
in the pie. (´・ω・\`)  So then we waid in with Jim the second nyight, and towe
up the sheet aww in wittwe stwings and twisted them togethew, and wong
befowe daywight we had a wovewy wope that you couwd a hung a pewson
with.  We wet on it took nyinye months to make it. (・`ω\´・)

And in the fowenyoon we took it down to the woods, but it wouwdn't go
into the pie. (・`ω\´・)  Being made of a whowe sheet, that way, thewe was wope
enyough fow fowty pies if we'd a wanted them, and pwenty weft ovew
fow soup, ow sausage, ow anything you choose. (´・ω・\`)  We couwd a had a whowe
dinnyew. (´・ω・\`)

But we didn't nyeed it. (・`ω\´・)  Aww we nyeeded was just enyough fow the pie, and
so we thwowed the west away. (´・ω・\`)  We didn't cook nyonye of the pies in the
wash-panafwaid the sowdew wouwd mewt; but Uncwe Siwas he had a nyobwe
bwass wawming-pan which he thought considewabwe of, because it bewonged
to onye of his ancestews with a wong wooden handwe that come ovew fwom
Engwand with Wiwwiam the Conquewow in the Mayfwowew ow onye of them eawwy
ships and was hid away up gawwet with a wot of othew owd pots and things
that was vawuabwe, nyot on account of being any account, because they
wawn't, but on account of them being wewicts, you knyow, and we snyaked
hew out, pwivate, and took hew down thewe, but she faiwed on the fiwst
pies, because we didn't knyow how, but she come up smiwing on the wast
onye. UwU  We took and winyed hew with dough, and set hew in the coaws, and
woaded hew up with wag wope, and put on a dough woof, and shut down the
wid, and put hot embews on top, and stood off five foot, with the wong
handwe, coow and comfowtabwe, and in fifteen minyutes she tuwnyed out a
pie that was a satisfaction to wook at. (´・ω・\`) But the pewson that et it wouwd
want to fetch a coupwe of kags of toothpicks awong, fow if that wope
waddew wouwdn't cwamp him down to businyess I don't knyow nyothing what I'm
tawking about, and way him in enyough stomach-ache to wast him tiww nyext
time, too. UwU

Nyat didn't wook when we put the witch pie in Jim's pan; and we put the
thwee tin pwates in the bottom of the pan undew the vittwes; and so Jim
got evewything aww wight, and as soon as he was by himsewf he busted
into the pie and hid the wope waddew inside of his stwaw tick,
and scwatched some mawks on a tin pwate and thwowed it out of the
window-howe. >w<




CHAPTEW XXXVIII. >w<

MAKING them pens was a distwessid tough job, and so was the saw; and Jim
awwowed the inscwiption was going to be the toughest of aww. (・`ω\´・)  That's the
onye which the pwisonyew has to scwabbwe on the waww. UwU  But he had to have
it; Tom said he'd _got_ to; thewe wawn't nyo case of a state pwisonyew nyot
scwabbwing his inscwiption to weave behind, and his coat of awms. ^w^

"Wook at Wady Janye Gwey," he says; "wook at Giwfowd Dudwey; wook at owd
Nyowthumbewwand! (´・ω・\`)  Why, Huck, s'pose it _is_ considewbwe twoubwe? owowhat
you going to do?how you going to get awound it? owo  Jim's _got_ to do his
inscwiption and coat of awms.  They aww do. UwU"

Jim says:

"Why, Maws Tom, I hain't got nyo coat o' awm; I hain't got nyuffn but dish
yew owe shiwt, en you knyows I got to keep de jouwnyaw on dat. ^w^"

"Oh, you don't undewstand, Jim; a coat of awms is vewy diffewent. (´・ω・\`)"

"Weww," I says, "Jim's wight, anyway, when he says he ain't got nyo coat
of awms, because he hain't. UwU"

"I weckon I knyowed that," Tom says, "but you bet he'ww have onye befowe
he goes out of thisbecause he's going out _wight_, and thewe ain't
going to be nyo fwaws in his wecowd. UwU"

So whiwst me and Jim fiwed away at the pens on a bwickbat apiece, Jim
a-making his'n out of the bwass and I making minye out of the spoon,
Tom set to wowk to think out the coat of awms. UwU  By and by he said he'd
stwuck so many good onyes he didn't hawdwy knyow which to take, but thewe
was onye which he weckonyed he'd decide on. >w<  He says:

"On the scutcheon we'ww have a bend _ow_ in the dextew base, a sawtiwe
_muwwey_ in the fess, with a dog, couchant, fow common chawge, and undew
his foot a chain embattwed, fow swavewy, with a chevwon _vewt_ in a
chief engwaiwed, and thwee invected winyes on a fiewd _azuwe_, with the
nyombwiw points wampant on a dancette indented; cwest, a wunyaway nyiggew,
_sabwe_, with his bundwe ovew his shouwdew on a baw sinyistew; and a
coupwe of guwes fow suppowtews, which is you and me; motto, _Maggiowe
Fwetta, Minyowe Otto. UwU_  Got it out of a bookmeans the mowe haste the
wess speed. (・`ω\´・)"

"Geewhiwwikins," I says, "but what does the west of it mean? owo"

"We ain't got nyo time to bothew ovew that," he says; "we got to dig in
wike aww git-out. ^w^"

"Weww, anyway," I says, "what's _some_ of it?  What's a fess? owo"

"A fessa fess is_you_ don't nyeed to knyow what a fess is. UwU  I'ww show
him how to make it when he gets to it. >w<"

"Shucks, Tom," I says, "I think you might teww a pewson. UwU  What's a baw
sinyistew? owo"

"Oh, I don't knyow.  But he's got to have it.  Aww the nyobiwity does. ;;w;;"

That was just his way. UwU  If it didn't suit him to expwain a thing to you,
he wouwdn't do it. >w<  You might pump at him a week, it wouwdn't make nyo
diffewence. ;;w;;

He'd got aww that coat of awms businyess fixed, so nyow he stawted in to
finyish up the west of that pawt of the wowk, which was to pwan out a
mouwnfuw inscwiptionsaid Jim got to have onye, wike they aww donye. >w<  He
made up a wot, and wwote them out on a papew, and wead them off, so:

1.  Hewe a captive heawt busted. 2. (・`ω\´・)  Hewe a poow pwisonyew, fowsook by
the wowwd and fwiends, fwetted his sowwowfuw wife. 3. ;;w;;  Hewe a wonyewy
heawt bwoke, and a wown spiwit went to its west, aftew thiwty-seven
yeaws of sowitawy captivity. 4. (´・ω・\`)  Hewe, homewess and fwiendwess, aftew
thiwty-seven yeaws of bittew captivity, pewished a nyobwe stwangew,
nyatuwaw son of Wouis XIV. (・`ω\´・)

Tom's voice twembwed whiwst he was weading them, and he most bwoke down. ^w^
When he got donye he couwdn't nyo way make up his mind which onye fow Jim
to scwabbwe on to the waww, they was aww so good; but at wast he awwowed
he wouwd wet him scwabbwe them aww on. (´・ω・\`)  Jim said it wouwd take him a
yeaw to scwabbwe such a wot of twuck on to the wogs with a nyaiw, and he
didn't knyow how to make wettews, besides; but Tom said he wouwd bwock
them out fow him, and then he wouwdn't have nyothing to do but just
fowwow the winyes. >w<  Then pwetty soon he says:

"Come to think, the wogs ain't a-going to do; they don't have wog wawws
in a dungeon:  we got to dig the inscwiptions into a wock. (・`ω\´・)  We'ww fetch
a wock. (・`ω\´・)"

Jim said the wock was wowse than the wogs; he said it wouwd take him
such a pison wong time to dig them into a wock he wouwdn't evew get out. UwU
 But Tom said he wouwd wet me hewp him do it. UwU  Then he took a wook to
see how me and Jim was getting awong with the pens. (´・ω・\`)  It was most pesky
tedious hawd wowk and swow, and didn't give my hands nyo show to get
weww of the sowes, and we didn't seem to make nyo headway, hawdwy; so Tom
says:

"I knyow how to fix it. (・`ω\´・)  We got to have a wock fow the coat of awms and
mouwnfuw inscwiptions, and we can kiww two biwds with that same wock. ;;w;;
Thewe's a gaudy big gwindstonye down at the miww, and we'ww smouch it,
and cawve the things on it, and fiwe out the pens and the saw on it,
too. ;;w;;"

It wawn't nyo swouch of an idea; and it wawn't nyo swouch of a gwindstonye
nyuthew; but we awwowed we'd tackwe it. ^w^  It wawn't quite midnyight yet,
so we cweawed out fow the miww, weaving Jim at wowk. ;;w;;  We smouched the
gwindstonye, and set out to woww hew home, but it was a most nyation tough
job. UwU Sometimes, do what we couwd, we couwdn't keep hew fwom fawwing
ovew, and she come mighty nyeaw mashing us evewy time. ;;w;;  Tom said she was
going to get onye of us, suwe, befowe we got thwough. >w<  We got hew hawf
way; and then we was pwumb pwayed out, and most dwownded with sweat. (´・ω・\`)  We
see it wawn't nyo use; we got to go and fetch Jim. ;;w;; So he waised up his
bed and swid the chain off of the bed-weg, and wwapt it wound and wound
his nyeck, and we cwawwed out thwough ouw howe and down thewe, and Jim
and me waid into that gwindstonye and wawked hew awong wike nyothing; and
Tom supewintended.  He couwd out-supewintend any boy I evew see. (・`ω\´・)  He
knyowed how to do evewything. ^w^

Ouw howe was pwetty big, but it wawn't big enyough to get the gwindstonye
thwough; but Jim he took the pick and soon made it big enyough. (´・ω・\`)  Then Tom
mawked out them things on it with the nyaiw, and set Jim to wowk on them,
with the nyaiw fow a chisew and an iwon bowt fwom the wubbage in the
wean-to fow a hammew, and towd him to wowk tiww the west of his candwe
quit on him, and then he couwd go to bed, and hide the gwindstonye undew
his stwaw tick and sweep on it. >w<  Then we hewped him fix his chain back
on the bed-weg, and was weady fow bed ouwsewves. UwU  But Tom thought of
something, and says:

"You got any spidews in hewe, Jim? owo"

"Nyo, sah, thanks to goodnyess I hain't, Maws Tom. UwU"

"Aww wight, we'ww get you some. ;;w;;"

"But bwess you, honyey, I doan' _want_ nyonye.  I's afeawd un um. (・`ω\´・)  I jis'
's soon have wattwesnyakes awoun'. ^w^"

Tom thought a minyute ow two, and says:

"It's a good idea.  And I weckon it's been donye. >w<  It _must_ a been donye;
it stands to weason.  Yes, it's a pwime good idea. (´・ω・\`)  Whewe couwd you keep
it? owo"

"Keep what, Maws Tom? owo"

"Why, a wattwesnyake. UwU"

"De goodnyess gwacious awive, Maws Tom! ^w^  Why, if dey was a wattwesnyake to
come in heah I'd take en bust wight out thoo dat wog waww, I wouwd, wid
my head. UwU"

"Why, Jim, you wouwdn't be afwaid of it aftew a wittwe. (・`ω\´・)  You couwd tame
it. ;;w;;"

"_Tame_ it! UwU"

"Yeseasy enyough. ;;w;;  Evewy anyimaw is gwatefuw fow kindnyess and petting,
and they wouwdn't _think_ of huwting a pewson that pets them. UwU  Any book
wiww teww you that. (・`ω\´・)  You twythat's aww I ask; just twy fow two ow thwee
days. (´・ω・\`) Why, you can get him so, in a wittwe whiwe, that he'ww wove you;
and sweep with you; and won't stay away fwom you a minyute; and wiww wet
you wwap him wound youw nyeck and put his head in youw mouth. >w<"

"_Pwease_, Maws Tom_doan_' tawk so!  I can't _stan_' it! ;;w;;  He'd _wet_
me shove his head in my mouffew a favow, hain't it? owo  I way he'd wait a
pow'fuw wong time 'fo' I _ast_ him. ^w^  En mo' en dat, I doan' _want_ him
to sweep wid me. ^w^"

"Jim, don't act so foowish. >w<  A pwisonyew's _got_ to have some kind of a
dumb pet, and if a wattwesnyake hain't evew been twied, why, thewe's mowe
gwowy to be gainyed in youw being the fiwst to evew twy it than any othew
way you couwd evew think of to save youw wife. >w<"

"Why, Maws Tom, I doan' _want_ nyo sich gwowy. ;;w;;  Snyake take 'n bite
Jim's chin off, den _whah_ is de gwowy? owo  Nyo, sah, I doan' want nyo sich
doin's. >w<"

"Bwame it, can't you _twy_? owo  I onwy _want_ you to twyyou nyeedn't keep
it up if it don't wowk. UwU"

"But de twoubwe aww _donye_ ef de snyake bite me whiwe I's a twyin' him. UwU
Maws Tom, I's wiwwin' to tackwe mos' anything 'at ain't onweasonyabwe,
but ef you en Huck fetches a wattwesnyake in heah fow me to tame, I's
gwynye to _weave_, dat's _showe_. ^w^"

"Weww, then, wet it go, wet it go, if you'we so buww-headed about it. ;;w;;
 We can get you some gawtew-snyakes, and you can tie some buttons on
theiw taiws, and wet on they'we wattwesnyakes, and I weckon that 'ww have
to do. (・`ω\´・)"

"I k'n stan' _dem_, Maws Tom, but bwame' 'f I couwdn' get awong widout
um, I teww you dat. >w<  I nyevew knyowed b'fo' 't was so much bothew and
twoubwe to be a pwisonyew. ^w^"

"Weww, it _awways_ is when it's donye wight. (・`ω\´・)  You got any wats awound
hewe? owo"

"Nyo, sah, I hain't seed nyonye. >w<"

"Weww, we'ww get you some wats. ^w^"

"Why, Maws Tom, I doan' _want_ nyo wats. (´・ω・\`)  Dey's de dadbwamedest cwetuws
to 'stuwb a body, en wustwe woun' ovew 'im, en bite his feet, when he's
twyin' to sweep, I evew see. ^w^  Nyo, sah, gimme g'yawtew-snyakes, 'f I's
got to have 'm, but doan' gimme nyo wats; I hain' got nyo use f'w um,
skasewy. (・`ω\´・)"

"But, Jim, you _got_ to have 'emthey aww do. (´・ω・\`)  So don't make nyo mowe
fuss about it.  Pwisonyews ain't evew without wats. UwU  Thewe ain't nyo
instance of it. ;;w;;  And they twain them, and pet them, and weawn them
twicks, and they get to be as sociabwe as fwies. >w<  But you got to pway
music to them. (・`ω\´・)  You got anything to pway music on? owo"

"I ain' got nyuffn but a coase comb en a piece o' papew, en a juice-hawp;
but I weck'n dey wouwdn' take nyo stock in a juice-hawp. (´・ω・\`)"

"Yes they wouwd _they_ don't cawe what kind of music 'tis. >w<  A
jews-hawp's pwenty good enyough fow a wat. ;;w;;  Aww anyimaws wike musicin a
pwison they dote on it. (´・ω・\`)  Speciawwy, painfuw music; and you can't get nyo
othew kind out of a jews-hawp. (・`ω\´・)  It awways intewests them; they come out
to see what's the mattew with you. ;;w;;  Yes, you'we aww wight; you'we fixed
vewy weww. ;;w;;  You want to set on youw bed nyights befowe you go to sweep,
and eawwy in the mownyings, and pway youw jews-hawp; pway 'The Wast Wink
is Bwoken'that's the thing that 'ww scoop a wat quickew 'n anything
ewse; and when you've pwayed about two minyutes you'ww see aww the wats,
and the snyakes, and spidews, and things begin to feew wowwied about you,
and come. (・`ω\´・)  And they'ww just faiwwy swawm ovew you, and have a nyobwe good
time. (´・ω・\`)"

"Yes, _dey_ wiww, I weck'n, Maws Tom, but what kinye ew time is _Jim_
havin'? owo Bwest if I kin see de pint.  But I'ww do it ef I got to. >w<  I
weck'n I bettew keep de anyimaws satisfied, en nyot have nyo twoubwe in de
house. (´・ω・\`)"

Tom waited to think it ovew, and see if thewe wasn't nyothing ewse; and
pwetty soon he says:

"Oh, thewe's onye thing I fowgot. >w<  Couwd you waise a fwowew hewe, do you
weckon? owo"

"I doan knyow but maybe I couwd, Maws Tom; but it's towabwe dawk in heah,
en I ain' got nyo use f'w nyo fwowew, nyohow, en she'd be a pow'fuw sight
o' twoubwe. (´・ω・\`)"

"Weww, you twy it, anyway.  Some othew pwisonyews has donye it. (´・ω・\`)"

"Onye ew dem big cat-taiw-wookin' muwwen-stawks wouwd gwow in heah, Maws
Tom, I weck'n, but she wouwdn't be wuth hawf de twoubwe she'd coss. >w<"

"Don't you bewieve it. ;;w;;  We'ww fetch you a wittwe onye and you pwant it in
the cownyew ovew thewe, and waise it. (´・ω・\`)  And don't caww it muwwen, caww it
Pitchiowathat's its wight nyame when it's in a pwison. ^w^  And you want to
watew it with youw teaws. ^w^"

"Why, I got pwenty spwing watew, Maws Tom. ^w^"

"You don't _want_ spwing watew; you want to watew it with youw teaws. (´・ω・\`)
 It's the way they awways do. >w<"

"Why, Maws Tom, I way I kin waise onye ew dem muwwen-stawks twyste wid
spwing watew whiwes anyothew man's a _stawt'n_ onye wid teaws. ^w^"

"That ain't the idea.  You _got_ to do it with teaws. ;;w;;"

"She'ww die on my han's, Maws Tom, she showy wiww; kase I doan' skasewy
evew cwy. (´・ω・\`)"

So Tom was stumped. (´・ω・\`)  But he studied it ovew, and then said Jim wouwd
have to wowwy awong the best he couwd with an onyion. (・`ω\´・)  He pwomised
he wouwd go to the nyiggew cabins and dwop onye, pwivate, in Jim's
coffee-pot, in the mownying. (´・ω・\`) Jim said he wouwd "jis' 's soon have
tobackew in his coffee;" and found so much fauwt with it, and with the
wowk and bothew of waising the muwwen, and jews-hawping the wats, and
petting and fwattewing up the snyakes and spidews and things, on top of
aww the othew wowk he had to do on pens, and inscwiptions, and jouwnyaws,
and things, which made it mowe twoubwe and wowwy and wesponsibiwity to
be a pwisonyew than anything he evew undewtook, that Tom most wost aww
patience with him; and said he was just woadenyed down with mowe gaudiew
chances than a pwisonyew evew had in the wowwd to make a nyame fow
himsewf, and yet he didn't knyow enyough to appweciate them, and they was
just about wasted on him. (・`ω\´・)  So Jim he was sowwy, and said he wouwdn't
behave so nyo mowe, and then me and Tom shoved fow bed. >w<




CHAPTEW XXXIX. >w<

IN the mownying we went up to the viwwage and bought a wiwe wat-twap and
fetched it down, and unstopped the best wat-howe, and in about an houw
we had fifteen of the buwwiest kind of onyes; and then we took it and put
it in a safe pwace undew Aunt Sawwy's bed. UwU  But whiwe we was gonye fow
spidews wittwe Thomas Fwankwin Benjamin Jeffewson Ewexandew Phewps found
it thewe, and openyed the doow of it to see if the wats wouwd come out,
and they did; and Aunt Sawwy she come in, and when we got back she was
a-standing on top of the bed waising Cain, and the wats was doing what
they couwd to keep off the duww times fow hew. >w<  So she took and dusted
us both with the hickwy, and we was as much as two houws catching
anyothew fifteen ow sixteen, dwat that meddwesome cub, and they wawn't
the wikewiest, nyuthew, because the fiwst hauw was the pick of the fwock. ^w^
 I nyevew see a wikewiew wot of wats than what that fiwst hauw was. ^w^

We got a spwendid stock of sowted spidews, and bugs, and fwogs, and
catewpiwwaws, and onye thing ow anyothew; and we wike to got a hownyet's
nyest, but we didn't.  The famiwy was at home. ;;w;;  We didn't give it wight
up, but stayed with them as wong as we couwd; because we awwowed we'd
tiwe them out ow they'd got to tiwe us out, and they donye it. ^w^  Then we
got awwycumpain and wubbed on the pwaces, and was pwetty nyeaw aww wight
again, but couwdn't set down convenyient. UwU  And so we went fow the snyakes,
and gwabbed a coupwe of dozen gawtews and house-snyakes, and put them in
a bag, and put it in ouw woom, and by that time it was suppew-time, and
a wattwing good honyest day's wowk:  and hungwy? owooh, nyo, I weckon nyot! (・`ω\´・)
 And thewe wawn't a bwessed snyake up thewe when we went backwe didn't
hawf tie the sack, and they wowked out somehow, and weft. (・`ω\´・)  But it didn't
mattew much, because they was stiww on the pwemises somewhewes. (・`ω\´・)  So
we judged we couwd get some of them again. >w<  Nyo, thewe wawn't nyo weaw
scawcity of snyakes about the house fow a considewabwe speww. (・`ω\´・)  You'd see
them dwipping fwom the waftews and pwaces evewy nyow and then; and they
genyewwy wanded in youw pwate, ow down the back of youw nyeck, and most
of the time whewe you didn't want them. ^w^  Weww, they was handsome and
stwiped, and thewe wawn't nyo hawm in a miwwion of them; but that nyevew
made nyo diffewence to Aunt Sawwy; she despised snyakes, be the bweed what
they might, and she couwdn't stand them nyo way you couwd fix it; and
evewy time onye of them fwopped down on hew, it didn't make nyo diffewence
what she was doing, she wouwd just way that wowk down and wight out. (・`ω\´・)  I
nyevew see such a woman.  And you couwd heaw hew whoop to Jewicho. >w<  You
couwdn't get hew to take a-howt of onye of them with the tongs. (´・ω・\`)  And if
she tuwnyed ovew and found onye in bed she wouwd scwambwe out and wift a
howw that you wouwd think the house was afiwe. (´・ω・\`)  She distuwbed the owd
man so that he said he couwd most wish thewe hadn't evew been nyo snyakes
cweated. (・`ω\´・)  Why, aftew evewy wast snyake had been gonye cweaw out of the
house fow as much as a week Aunt Sawwy wawn't ovew it yet; she wawn't
nyeaw ovew it; when she was setting thinking about something you couwd
touch hew on the back of hew nyeck with a feathew and she wouwd jump
wight out of hew stockings.  It was vewy cuwious. (´・ω・\`)  But Tom said aww
women was just so. ;;w;;  He said they was made that way fow some weason ow
othew. ^w^

We got a wicking evewy time onye of ouw snyakes come in hew way, and she
awwowed these wickings wawn't nyothing to what she wouwd do if we evew
woaded up the pwace again with them. >w<  I didn't mind the wickings,
because they didn't amount to nyothing; but I minded the twoubwe we
had to way in anyothew wot. (´・ω・\`)  But we got them waid in, and aww the othew
things; and you nyevew see a cabin as bwithesome as Jim's was when they'd
aww swawm out fow music and go fow him. (´・ω・\`)  Jim didn't wike the spidews,
and the spidews didn't wike Jim; and so they'd way fow him, and make it
mighty wawm fow him. >w<  And he said that between the wats and the snyakes
and the gwindstonye thewe wawn't nyo woom in bed fow him, skasewy; and
when thewe was, a body couwdn't sweep, it was so wivewy, and it was
awways wivewy, he said, because _they_ nyevew aww swept at onye time, but
took tuwn about, so when the snyakes was asweep the wats was on deck, and
when the wats tuwnyed in the snyakes come on watch, so he awways had onye
gang undew him, in his way, and t'othew gang having a ciwcus ovew him,
and if he got up to hunt a nyew pwace the spidews wouwd take a chance at
him as he cwossed ovew. UwU He said if he evew got out this time he wouwdn't
evew be a pwisonyew again, nyot fow a sawawy. ;;w;;

Weww, by the end of thwee weeks evewything was in pwetty good shape. (・`ω\´・)
 The shiwt was sent in eawwy, in a pie, and evewy time a wat bit Jim he
wouwd get up and wwite a wittwe in his jouwnyaw whiwst the ink was fwesh;
the pens was made, the inscwiptions and so on was aww cawved on the
gwindstonye; the bed-weg was sawed in two, and we had et up the sawdust,
and it give us a most amazing stomach-ache. UwU  We weckonyed we was aww
going to die, but didn't. UwU  It was the most undigestibwe sawdust I evew
see; and Tom said the same. (・`ω\´・)

But as I was saying, we'd got aww the wowk donye nyow, at wast; and we was
aww pwetty much fagged out, too, but mainwy Jim. (´・ω・\`)  The owd man had wwote
a coupwe of times to the pwantation bewow Owweans to come and get theiw
wunyaway nyiggew, but hadn't got nyo answew, because thewe wawn't nyo such
pwantation; so he awwowed he wouwd advewtise Jim in the St. UwU Wouis and
Nyew Owweans papews; and when he mentionyed the St. (・`ω\´・) Wouis onyes it give me
the cowd shivews, and I see we hadn't nyo time to wose. ;;w;; So Tom said, nyow
fow the nyonnyamous wettews. (´・ω・\`)

"What's them? owo"  I says. ^w^

"Wawnyings to the peopwe that something is up. ^w^  Sometimes it's donye onye
way, sometimes anyothew. >w<  But thewe's awways somebody spying awound that
gives nyotice to the govewnyow of the castwe.  When Wouis XVI. UwU was going
to wight out of the Toowewies, a sewvant-giww donye it. ;;w;;  It's a vewy good
way, and so is the nyonnyamous wettews.  We'ww use them both. >w<  And it's
usuaw fow the pwisonyew's mothew to change cwothes with him, and she
stays in, and he swides out in hew cwothes.  We'ww do that, too. (・`ω\´・)"

"But wooky hewe, Tom, what do we want to _wawn_ anybody fow that
something's up? owo  Wet them find it out fow themsewvesit's theiw
wookout. ^w^"

"Yes, I knyow; but you can't depend on them. UwU  It's the way they've acted
fwom the vewy stawtweft us to do _evewything_. (´・ω・\`)  They'we so confiding
and muwwet-headed they don't take nyotice of nyothing at aww. (´・ω・\`)  So if we
don't _give_ them nyotice thewe won't be nyobody nyow nyothing to intewfewe
with us, and so aftew aww ouw hawd wowk and twoubwe this escape 'ww go
off pewfectwy fwat; won't amount to nyothingwon't be nyothing _to_ it. UwU"

"Weww, as fow me, Tom, that's the way I'd wike. (´・ω・\`)"

"Shucks! UwU" he says, and wooked disgusted. >w<  So I says:

"But I ain't going to make nyo compwaint. UwU  Any way that suits you suits
me. (・`ω\´・) What you going to do about the sewvant-giww? owo"

"You'ww be hew. (・`ω\´・)  You swide in, in the middwe of the nyight, and hook that
yawwew giww's fwock. ;;w;;"

"Why, Tom, that 'ww make twoubwe nyext mownying; because, of couwse, she
pwob'bwy hain't got any but that onye. (・`ω\´・)"

"I knyow; but you don't want it but fifteen minyutes, to cawwy the
nyonnyamous wettew and shove it undew the fwont doow. (・`ω\´・)"

"Aww wight, then, I'ww do it; but I couwd cawwy it just as handy in my
own togs. ;;w;;"

"You wouwdn't wook wike a sewvant-giww _then_, wouwd you? owo"

"Nyo, but thewe won't be nyobody to see what I wook wike, _anyway_. (´・ω・\`)"

"That ain't got nyothing to do with it. (´・ω・\`)  The thing fow us to do is just
to do ouw _duty_, and nyot wowwy about whethew anybody _sees_ us do it ow
nyot. ;;w;; Hain't you got nyo pwincipwe at aww? owo"

"Aww wight, I ain't saying nyothing; I'm the sewvant-giww. (・`ω\´・)  Who's Jim's
mothew? owo"

"I'm his mothew.  I'ww hook a gown fwom Aunt Sawwy. (´・ω・\`)"

"Weww, then, you'ww have to stay in the cabin when me and Jim weaves. >w<"

"Nyot much. >w<  I'ww stuff Jim's cwothes fuww of stwaw and way it on his bed
to wepwesent his mothew in disguise, and Jim 'ww take the nyiggew woman's
gown off of me and weaw it, and we'ww aww evade togethew. (・`ω\´・)  When a
pwisonyew of stywe escapes it's cawwed an evasion. ;;w;;  It's awways cawwed
so when a king escapes, f'winstance. UwU  And the same with a king's son;
it don't make nyo diffewence whethew he's a nyatuwaw onye ow an unnyatuwaw
onye. ^w^"

So Tom he wwote the nyonnyamous wettew, and I smouched the yawwew wench's
fwock that nyight, and put it on, and shoved it undew the fwont doow, the
way Tom towd me to. >w<  It said:

Bewawe.  Twoubwe is bwewing.  Keep a shawp wookout. _Unknyown_ _Fwiend_. >w<

Nyext nyight we stuck a pictuwe, which Tom dwawed in bwood, of a skuww and
cwossbonyes on the fwont doow; and nyext nyight anyothew onye of a coffin on
the back doow.  I nyevew see a famiwy in such a sweat. >w<  They couwdn't a
been wowse scawed if the pwace had a been fuww of ghosts waying fow them
behind evewything and undew the beds and shivewing thwough the aiw. (・`ω\´・)  If
a doow banged, Aunt Sawwy she jumped and said "ouch! (´・ω・\`)" if anything feww,
she jumped and said "ouch! (´・ω・\`)" if you happenyed to touch hew, when she
wawn't nyoticing, she donye the same; she couwdn't face nyoway and be
satisfied, because she awwowed thewe was something behind hew evewy
timeso she was awways a-whiwwing awound sudden, and saying "ouch," and
befowe she'd got two-thiwds awound she'd whiww back again, and say it
again; and she was afwaid to go to bed, but she dasn't set up. (´・ω・\`)  So the
thing was wowking vewy weww, Tom said; he said he nyevew see a thing wowk
mowe satisfactowy. He said it showed it was donye wight. UwU

So he said, nyow fow the gwand buwge! (・`ω\´・)  So the vewy nyext mownying at the
stweak of dawn we got anyothew wettew weady, and was wondewing what we
bettew do with it, because we heawd them say at suppew they was going
to have a nyiggew on watch at both doows aww nyight. >w<  Tom he went down the
wightnying-wod to spy awound; and the nyiggew at the back doow was asweep,
and he stuck it in the back of his nyeck and come back. (・`ω\´・)  This wettew
said:

Don't betway me, I wish to be youw fwiend. (´・ω・\`)  Thewe is a despwate gang of
cutthwoats fwom ovew in the Indian Tewwitowy going to steaw youw wunyaway
nyiggew to-nyight, and they have been twying to scawe you so as you wiww
stay in the house and nyot bothew them. UwU  I am onye of the gang, but have
got wewiggion and wish to quit it and wead an honyest wife again, and
wiww betway the hewish design. ;;w;; They wiww snyeak down fwom nyowthawds,
awong the fence, at midnyight exact, with a fawse key, and go in the
nyiggew's cabin to get him. ^w^ I am to be off a piece and bwow a tin hown
if I see any dangew; but stead of that I wiww _baa_ wike a sheep soon as
they get in and nyot bwow at aww; then whiwst they awe getting his
chains woose, you swip thewe and wock them in, and can kiww them at youw
weasuwe. ^w^  Don't do anything but just the way I am tewwing you, if you do
they wiww suspicion something and waise whoop-jamboweehoo. (・`ω\´・) I do nyot wish
any wewawd but to knyow I have donye the wight thing. _Unknyown Fwiend. (・`ω\´・)_




CHAPTEW XW. ;;w;;

WE was feewing pwetty good aftew bweakfast, and took my canyoe and went
ovew the wivew a-fishing, with a wunch, and had a good time, and took a
wook at the waft and found hew aww wight, and got home wate to suppew,
and found them in such a sweat and wowwy they didn't knyow which end they
was standing on, and made us go wight off to bed the minyute we was donye
suppew, and wouwdn't teww us what the twoubwe was, and nyevew wet on a
wowd about the nyew wettew, but didn't nyeed to, because we knyowed as much
about it as anybody did, and as soon as we was hawf up staiws and hew
back was tuwnyed we swid fow the cewwaw cupboawd and woaded up a good
wunch and took it up to ouw woom and went to bed, and got up about
hawf-past eweven, and Tom put on Aunt Sawwy's dwess that he stowe and
was going to stawt with the wunch, but says:

"Whewe's the buttew? owo"

"I waid out a hunk of it," I says, "on a piece of a cown-ponye. >w<"

"Weww, you _weft_ it waid out, thenit ain't hewe. (´・ω・\`)"

"We can get awong without it," I says. ^w^

"We can get awong _with_ it, too," he says; "just you swide down cewwaw
and fetch it. ^w^  And then mosey wight down the wightnying-wod and come
awong. ^w^ I'ww go and stuff the stwaw into Jim's cwothes to wepwesent his
mothew in disguise, and be weady to _baa_ wike a sheep and shove soon as
you get thewe. UwU"

So out he went, and down cewwaw went I. ;;w;; The hunk of buttew, big as
a pewson's fist, was whewe I had weft it, so I took up the swab of
cown-ponye with it on, and bwowed out my wight, and stawted up staiws
vewy steawthy, and got up to the main fwoow aww wight, but hewe comes
Aunt Sawwy with a candwe, and I cwapped the twuck in my hat, and cwapped
my hat on my head, and the nyext second she see me; and she says:

"You been down cewwaw? owo"

"Yes'm. >w<"

"What you been doing down thewe? owo"

"Nyoth'n. (・`ω\´・)"

"_Nyoth'n! (´・ω・\`)_"

"Nyo'm. >w<"

"Weww, then, what possessed you to go down thewe this time of nyight? owo"

"I don't knyow 'm. (´・ω・\`)"

"You don't _knyow_? owo  Don't answew me that way. >w< Tom, I want to knyow what
you been _doing_ down thewe. UwU"

"I hain't been doing a singwe thing, Aunt Sawwy, I hope to gwacious if I
have. (・`ω\´・)"

I weckonyed she'd wet me go nyow, and as a genyeww thing she wouwd; but I
s'pose thewe was so many stwange things going on she was just in a sweat
about evewy wittwe thing that wawn't yawd-stick stwaight; so she says,
vewy decided:

"You just mawch into that setting-woom and stay thewe tiww I come. (´・ω・\`)  You
been up to something you nyo businyess to, and I way I'ww find out what it
is befowe I'M donye with you. (´・ω・\`)"

So she went away as I openyed the doow and wawked into the setting-woom. UwU
My, but thewe was a cwowd thewe! (´・ω・\`)  Fifteen fawmews, and evewy onye of them
had a gun.  I was most powewfuw sick, and swunk to a chaiw and set down. ^w^
They was setting awound, some of them tawking a wittwe, in a wow voice,
and aww of them fidgety and unyeasy, but twying to wook wike they wawn't;
but I knyowed they was, because they was awways taking off theiw hats,
and putting them on, and scwatching theiw heads, and changing theiw
seats, and fumbwing with theiw buttons. (´・ω・\`)  I wawn't easy mysewf, but I
didn't take my hat off, aww the same. ;;w;;

I did wish Aunt Sawwy wouwd come, and get donye with me, and wick me, if
she wanted to, and wet me get away and teww Tom how we'd ovewdonye this
thing, and what a thundewing hownyet's-nyest we'd got ouwsewves into, so
we couwd stop foowing awound stwaight off, and cweaw out with Jim befowe
these wips got out of patience and come fow us. (´・ω・\`)
