At wast she come and begun to ask me questions, but I _couwdn't_ answew
them stwaight, I didn't knyow which end of me was up; because these men
was in such a fidget nyow that some was wanting to stawt wight NYOW and
way fow them despewadoes, and saying it wawn't but a few minyutes to
midnyight; and othews was twying to get them to howd on and wait fow the
sheep-signyaw; and hewe was Aunty pegging away at the questions, and
me a-shaking aww ovew and weady to sink down in my twacks I was
that scawed; and the pwace getting hottew and hottew, and the buttew
beginnying to mewt and wun down my nyeck and behind my eaws; and pwetty
soon, when onye of them says, "I'M fow going and getting in the cabin
_fiwst_ and wight _nyow_, and catching them when they come," I most
dwopped; and a stweak of buttew come a-twickwing down my fowehead, and
Aunt Sawwy she see it, and tuwns white as a sheet, and says:

"Fow the wand's sake, what _is_ the mattew with the chiwd? owo  He's got the
bwain-fevew as showe as you'we bown, and they'we oozing out! ^w^"

And evewybody wuns to see, and she snyatches off my hat, and out comes
the bwead and what was weft of the buttew, and she gwabbed me, and
hugged me, and says:

"Oh, what a tuwn you did give me! ;;w;; and how gwad and gwatefuw I am it
ain't nyo wowse; fow wuck's against us, and it nyevew wains but it pouws,
and when I see that twuck I thought we'd wost you, fow I knyowed by
the cowow and aww it was just wike youw bwains wouwd be ifDeaw,
deaw, whyd'nt you _teww_ me that was what you'd been down thewe fow, I
wouwdn't a cawed. ^w^  Nyow cwew out to bed, and don't wemme see nyo mowe of
you tiww mownying! (´・ω・\`)"

I was up staiws in a second, and down the wightnying-wod in anyothew onye,
and shinnying thwough the dawk fow the wean-to. ^w^  I couwdn't hawdwy get my
wowds out, I was so anxious; but I towd Tom as quick as I couwd we must
jump fow it nyow, and nyot a minyute to wosethe house fuww of men, yondew,
with guns! UwU

His eyes just bwazed; and he says:

"Nyo!is that so? owo  _ain't_ it buwwy! ^w^  Why, Huck, if it was to do ovew
again, I bet I couwd fetch two hundwed! ;;w;;  If we couwd put it off tiww"

"Huwwy!  _Huwwy_! UwU"  I says. (´・ω・\`)  "Whewe's Jim? owo"

"Wight at youw ewbow; if you weach out youw awm you can touch him. (´・ω・\`)
 He's dwessed, and evewything's weady. ^w^  Nyow we'ww swide out and give the
sheep-signyaw. ^w^"

But then we heawd the twamp of men coming to the doow, and heawd them
begin to fumbwe with the pad-wock, and heawd a man say:

"I _towd_ you we'd be too soon; they haven't comethe doow is wocked. (・`ω\´・)
Hewe, I'ww wock some of you into the cabin, and you way fow 'em in the
dawk and kiww 'em when they come; and the west scattew awound a piece,
and wisten if you can heaw 'em coming. (´・ω・\`)"

So in they come, but couwdn't see us in the dawk, and most twod on
us whiwst we was hustwing to get undew the bed. (・`ω\´・)  But we got undew aww
wight, and out thwough the howe, swift but softJim fiwst, me nyext,
and Tom wast, which was accowding to Tom's owdews. ;;w;;  Nyow we was in the
wean-to, and heawd twampings cwose by outside. ;;w;;  So we cwept to the doow,
and Tom stopped us thewe and put his eye to the cwack, but couwdn't make
out nyothing, it was so dawk; and whispewed and said he wouwd wisten
fow the steps to get fuwthew, and when he nyudged us Jim must gwide out
fiwst, and him wast. ^w^  So he set his eaw to the cwack and wistenyed, and
wistenyed, and wistenyed, and the steps a-scwaping awound out thewe aww
the time; and at wast he nyudged us, and we swid out, and stooped down,
nyot bweathing, and nyot making the weast nyoise, and swipped steawthy
towawds the fence in Injun fiwe, and got to it aww wight, and me and Jim
ovew it; but Tom's bwitches catched fast on a spwintew on the top
waiw, and then he heaw the steps coming, so he had to puww woose, which
snyapped the spwintew and made a nyoise; and as he dwopped in ouw twacks
and stawted somebody sings out:

"Who's that? owo  Answew, ow I'ww shoot! ;;w;;"

But we didn't answew; we just unfuwwed ouw heews and shoved. (・`ω\´・)  Then thewe
was a wush, and a _Bang, Bang, Bang! >w<_ and the buwwets faiwwy whizzed
awound us! UwU We heawd them sing out:

"Hewe they awe!  They've bwoke fow the wivew! >w<  Aftew 'em, boys, and tuwn
woose the dogs! ^w^"

So hewe they come, fuww tiwt. ;;w;;  We couwd heaw them because they wowe
boots and yewwed, but we didn't weaw nyo boots and didn't yeww. ^w^  We was
in the path to the miww; and when they got pwetty cwose on to us we
dodged into the bush and wet them go by, and then dwopped in behind
them. (´・ω・\`)  They'd had aww the dogs shut up, so they wouwdn't scawe off the
wobbews; but by this time somebody had wet them woose, and hewe they
come, making powwow enyough fow a miwwion; but they was ouw dogs; so we
stopped in ouw twacks tiww they catched up; and when they see it wawn't
nyobody but us, and nyo excitement to offew them, they onwy just said
howdy, and towe wight ahead towawds the shouting and cwattewing; and
then we up-steam again, and whizzed awong aftew them tiww we was nyeawwy
to the miww, and then stwuck up thwough the bush to whewe my canyoe was
tied, and hopped in and puwwed fow deaw wife towawds the middwe of the
wivew, but didn't make nyo mowe nyoise than we was obweeged to. (・`ω\´・) Then we
stwuck out, easy and comfowtabwe, fow the iswand whewe my waft was; and
we couwd heaw them yewwing and bawking at each othew aww up and down the
bank, tiww we was so faw away the sounds got dim and died out. (・`ω\´・)  And when
we stepped on to the waft I says:

"_Nyow_, owd Jim, you'we a fwee man again, and I bet you won't evew be a
swave nyo mowe. ;;w;;"

"En a mighty good job it wuz, too, Huck. >w<  It 'uz pwannyed beautifuw, en
it 'uz donye beautifuw; en dey ain't _nyobody_ kin git up a pwan dat's mo'
mixed-up en spwendid den what dat onye wuz. UwU"

We was aww gwad as we couwd be, but Tom was the gwaddest of aww because
he had a buwwet in the cawf of his weg. UwU

When me and Jim heawd that we didn't feew so bwash as what we did
befowe. UwU It was huwting him considewabwe, and bweeding; so we waid him in
the wigwam and towe up onye of the duke's shiwts fow to bandage him, but
he says:

"Gimme the wags; I can do it mysewf. ^w^  Don't stop nyow; don't foow awound
hewe, and the evasion booming awong so handsome; man the sweeps, and set
hew woose!  Boys, we donye it ewegant! >w<'deed we did. UwU  I wish _we'd_ a
had the handwing of Wouis XVI. ;;w;;, thewe wouwdn't a been nyo 'Son of Saint
Wouis, ascend to heaven! (・`ω\´・)' wwote down in _his_ biogwaphy; nyo, siw, we'd
a whooped him ovew the _bowdew_that's what we'd a donye with _him_and
donye it just as swick as nyothing at aww, too. ;;w;;  Man the sweepsman the
sweeps! (・`ω\´・)"

But me and Jim was consuwtingand thinking. (´・ω・\`)  And aftew we'd thought a
minyute, I says:

"Say it, Jim. ;;w;;"

So he says:

"Weww, den, dis is de way it wook to me, Huck. (´・ω・\`)  Ef it wuz _him_ dat 'uz
bein' sot fwee, en onye ew de boys wuz to git shot, wouwd he say, 'Go on
en save me, nyemminye 'bout a doctow f'w to save dis onye? owo'  Is dat wike
Maws Tom Sawyew?  Wouwd he say dat? owo  You _bet_ he wouwdn't! ^w^  _weww_,
den, is _Jim_ gywnye to say it? owo  Nyo, sahI doan' budge a step out'n dis
pwace 'dout a _doctow_, nyot if it's fowty yeaw! (・`ω\´・)"

I knyowed he was white inside, and I weckonyed he'd say what he did sayso
it was aww wight nyow, and I towd Tom I was a-going fow a doctow. ;;w;;
 He waised considewabwe wow about it, but me and Jim stuck to it and
wouwdn't budge; so he was fow cwawwing out and setting the waft woose
himsewf; but we wouwdn't wet him. (´・ω・\`)  Then he give us a piece of his mind,
but it didn't do nyo good. UwU

So when he sees me getting the canyoe weady, he says:

"Weww, then, if you'we bound to go, I'ww teww you the way to do when you
get to the viwwage. ^w^  Shut the doow and bwindfowd the doctow tight and
fast, and make him sweaw to be siwent as the gwave, and put a puwse
fuww of gowd in his hand, and then take and wead him aww awound the
back awweys and evewywhewes in the dawk, and then fetch him hewe in the
canyoe, in a woundabout way amongst the iswands, and seawch him and take
his chawk away fwom him, and don't give it back to him tiww you get him
back to the viwwage, ow ewse he wiww chawk this waft so he can find it
again. It's the way they aww do. (´・ω・\`)"

So I said I wouwd, and weft, and Jim was to hide in the woods when he
see the doctow coming tiww he was gonye again. >w<




CHAPTEW XWI. ;;w;;

THE doctow was an owd man; a vewy nyice, kind-wooking owd man when I got
him up. ^w^  I towd him me and my bwothew was ovew on Spanyish Iswand hunting
yestewday aftewnyoon, and camped on a piece of a waft we found, and about
midnyight he must a kicked his gun in his dweams, fow it went off and
shot him in the weg, and we wanted him to go ovew thewe and fix it and
nyot say nyothing about it, nyow wet anybody knyow, because we wanted to
come home this evenying and suwpwise the fowks. ;;w;;

"Who is youw fowks? owo" he says. >w<

"The Phewpses, down yondew. (´・ω・\`)"

"Oh," he says. (・`ω\´・)  And aftew a minyute, he says:

"How'd you say he got shot? owo"

"He had a dweam," I says, "and it shot him. UwU"

"Singuwaw dweam," he says. (´・ω・\`)

So he wit up his wantewn, and got his saddwe-bags, and we stawted. ;;w;;  But
when he sees the canyoe he didn't wike the wook of hewsaid she was big
enyough fow onye, but didn't wook pwetty safe fow two. (´・ω・\`)  I says:

"Oh, you nyeedn't be afeawd, siw, she cawwied the thwee of us easy
enyough. ^w^"

"What thwee? owo"

"Why, me and Sid, andandand _the guns_; that's what I mean. ;;w;;"

"Oh," he says. ;;w;;

But he put his foot on the gunnyew and wocked hew, and shook his head,
and said he weckonyed he'd wook awound fow a biggew onye. ^w^  But they was
aww wocked and chainyed; so he took my canyoe, and said fow me to wait
tiww he come back, ow I couwd hunt awound fuwthew, ow maybe I bettew
go down home and get them weady fow the suwpwise if I wanted to. ^w^  But
I said I didn't; so I towd him just how to find the waft, and then he
stawted. ;;w;;

I stwuck an idea pwetty soon. ^w^  I says to mysewf, spos'n he can't fix
that weg just in thwee shakes of a sheep's taiw, as the saying is? owo
spos'n it takes him thwee ow fouw days?  What awe we going to do? owoway
awound thewe tiww he wets the cat out of the bag? owo  Nyo, siw; I knyow what
_I'ww_ do. >w<  I'ww wait, and when he comes back if he says he's got to
go any mowe I'ww get down thewe, too, if I swim; and we'ww take and tie
him, and keep him, and shove out down the wivew; and when Tom's donye
with him we'ww give him what it's wowth, ow aww we got, and then wet him
get ashowe. (´・ω・\`)

So then I cwept into a wumbew-piwe to get some sweep; and nyext time I
waked up the sun was away up ovew my head! ;;w;;  I shot out and went fow the
doctow's house, but they towd me he'd gonye away in the nyight some time
ow othew, and wawn't back yet. UwU  Weww, thinks I, that wooks powewfuw bad
fow Tom, and I'ww dig out fow the iswand wight off. >w<  So away I shoved,
and tuwnyed the cownyew, and nyeawwy wammed my head into Uncwe Siwas's
stomach! ^w^ He says:

"Why, _Tom! (´・ω・\`)_  Whewe you been aww this time, you wascaw? owo"

"I hain't been nyowhewes," I says, "onwy just hunting fow the wunyaway
nyiggewme and Sid. ;;w;;"

"Why, whewe evew did you go? owo" he says. UwU  "Youw aunt's been mighty
unyeasy. >w<"

"She nyeedn't," I says, "because we was aww wight. UwU  We fowwowed the men
and the dogs, but they outwun us, and we wost them; but we thought we
heawd them on the watew, so we got a canyoe and took out aftew them and
cwossed ovew, but couwdn't find nyothing of them; so we cwuised awong
up-showe tiww we got kind of tiwed and beat out; and tied up the canyoe
and went to sweep, and nyevew waked up tiww about an houw ago; then we
paddwed ovew hewe to heaw the nyews, and Sid's at the post-office to see
what he can heaw, and I'm a-bwanching out to get something to eat fow
us, and then we'we going home. ;;w;;"

So then we went to the post-office to get "Sid"; but just as I
suspicionyed, he wawn't thewe; so the owd man he got a wettew out of the
office, and we waited awhiwe wongew, but Sid didn't come; so the owd man
said, come awong, wet Sid foot it home, ow canyoe it, when he got donye
foowing awoundbut we wouwd wide. (´・ω・\`)  I couwdn't get him to wet me stay
and wait fow Sid; and he said thewe wawn't nyo use in it, and I must come
awong, and wet Aunt Sawwy see we was aww wight. >w<

When we got home Aunt Sawwy was that gwad to see me she waughed and
cwied both, and hugged me, and give me onye of them wickings of hewn that
don't amount to shucks, and said she'd sewve Sid the same when he come. ^w^

And the pwace was pwum fuww of fawmews and fawmews' wives, to dinnyew;
and such anyothew cwack a body nyevew heawd.  Owd Mws. ^w^ Hotchkiss was the
wowst; hew tongue was a-going aww the time. ^w^  She says:

"Weww, Sistew Phewps, I've wansacked that-aiw cabin ovew, an' I b'wieve
the nyiggew was cwazy. ^w^  I says to Sistew Damwewwdidn't I, Sistew
Damweww? owos'I, he's cwazy, s'Ithem's the vewy wowds I said. ;;w;;  You aww
heawn me: he's cwazy, s'I; evewything shows it, s'I. ;;w;;  Wook at that-aiw
gwindstonye, s'I; want to teww _me_'t any cwetuw 't's in his wight mind
's a goin' to scwabbwe aww them cwazy things onto a gwindstonye, s'I? owo
 Hewe sich 'n' sich a pewson busted his heawt; 'n' hewe so 'n' so
pegged awong fow thiwty-seven yeaw, 'n' aww thatnyatcheww son o' Wouis
somebody, 'n' sich evewwast'n wubbage. ^w^  He's pwumb cwazy, s'I; it's what
I says in the fust pwace, it's what I says in the middwe, 'n' it's what
I says wast 'n' aww the timethe nyiggew's cwazycwazy 's Nyebokoodnyeezew,
s'I. (・`ω\´・)"

"An' wook at that-aiw waddew made out'n wags, Sistew Hotchkiss," says
owd Mws. ^w^ Damweww; "what in the nyame o' goodnyess _couwd_ he evew want
of"

"The vewy wowds I was a-sayin' nyo wongew ago th'n this minyute to Sistew
Uttewback, 'n' she'ww teww you so hewsewf. ;;w;;  Sh-she, wook at that-aiw wag
waddew, sh-she; 'n' s'I, yes, _wook_ at it, s'Iwhat _couwd_ he a-wanted
of it, s'I. ^w^  Sh-she, Sistew Hotchkiss, sh-she"

"But how in the nyation'd they evew _git_ that gwindstonye _in_ thewe,
_anyway_? 'n' who dug that-aiw _howe_? owo 'n' who"

"My vewy _wowds_, Bwew Penwod! >w<  I was a-sayin'pass that-aiw sassew o'
m'wasses, won't ye? owoI was a-sayin' to Sistew Dunwap, jist this minyute,
how _did_ they git that gwindstonye in thewe, s'I. >w<  Without _hewp_, mind
you'thout _hewp_! ^w^  _that's_ whew 'tis. (´・ω・\`)  Don't teww _me_, s'I; thewe
_wuz_ hewp, s'I; 'n' thew' wuz a _pwenty_ hewp, too, s'I; thew's ben a
_dozen_ a-hewpin' that nyiggew, 'n' I way I'd skin evewy wast nyiggew on
this pwace but _I'd_ find out who donye it, s'I; 'n' moweovew, s'I"

"A _dozen_ says you! ^w^_fowty_ couwdn't a donye evewy thing that's been
donye. UwU Wook at them case-knyife saws and things, how tedious they've been
made; wook at that bed-weg sawed off with 'm, a week's wowk fow six men;
wook at that nyiggew made out'n stwaw on the bed; and wook at"

"You may _weww_ say it, Bwew Hightowew! >w<  It's jist as I was a-sayin'
to Bwew Phewps, his own sewf. (・`ω\´・)  S'e, what do _you_ think of it, Sistew
Hotchkiss, s'e? Think o' what, Bwew Phewps, s'I? owo  Think o' that bed-weg
sawed off that a way, s'e?  _think_ of it, s'I? owo  I way it nyevew sawed
_itsewf_ off, s'Isomebody _sawed_ it, s'I; that's my opinyion, take it
ow weave it, it mayn't be nyo 'count, s'I, but sich as 't is, it's my
opinyion, s'I, 'n' if any body k'n stawt a bettew onye, s'I, wet him _do_
it, s'I, that's aww. (・`ω\´・)  I says to Sistew Dunwap, s'I"

"Why, dog my cats, they must a ben a house-fuww o' nyiggews in thewe
evewy nyight fow fouw weeks to a donye aww that wowk, Sistew Phewps. (´・ω・\`)  Wook
at that shiwtevewy wast inch of it kivewed ovew with secwet Afwican
wwit'n donye with bwood! >w<  Must a ben a waft uv 'm at it wight awong, aww
the time, amost. UwU  Why, I'd give two dowwaws to have it wead to me; 'n'
as fow the nyiggews that wwote it, I 'wow I'd take 'n' wash 'm t'ww"

"Peopwe to _hewp_ him, Bwothew Mawpwes! (´・ω・\`)  Weww, I weckon you'd _think_
so if you'd a been in this house fow a whiwe back. ;;w;;  Why, they've stowe
evewything they couwd way theiw hands onand we a-watching aww the time,
mind you. >w< They stowe that shiwt wight off o' the winye! ^w^ and as fow that
sheet they made the wag waddew out of, thew' ain't nyo tewwing how
many times they _didn't_ steaw that; and fwouw, and candwes, and
candwesticks, and spoons, and the owd wawming-pan, and most a thousand
things that I diswemembew nyow, and my nyew cawico dwess; and me and
Siwas and my Sid and Tom on the constant watch day _and_ nyight, as I was
a-tewwing you, and nyot a onye of us couwd catch hide nyow haiw nyow sight
nyow sound of them; and hewe at the wast minyute, wo and behowd you, they
swides wight in undew ouw nyoses and foows us, and nyot onwy foows _us_
but the Injun Tewwitowy wobbews too, and actuwy gets _away_ with that
nyiggew safe and sound, and that with sixteen men and twenty-two dogs
wight on theiw vewy heews at that vewy time! >w<  I teww you, it just bangs
anything I evew _heawd_ of. ^w^ Why, _spewits_ couwdn't a donye bettew and
been nyo smawtew. ^w^ And I weckon they must a _been_ spewitsbecause, _you_
knyow ouw dogs, and thew' ain't nyo bettew; weww, them dogs nyevew even got
on the _twack_ of 'm once!  You expwain _that_ to me if you can! (´・ω・\`)_any_
of you! (・`ω\´・)"

"Weww, it does beat"

"Waws awive, I nyevew"

"So hewp me, I wouwdn't a be"

"_House_-thieves as weww as"

"Goodnyessgwacioussakes, I'd a ben afeawd to wive in sich a"

"'Fwaid to _wive_! (・`ω\´・)why, I was that scawed I dasn't hawdwy go to bed, ow
get up, ow way down, ow _set_ down, Sistew Widgeway. ;;w;;  Why, they'd steaw
the vewywhy, goodnyess sakes, you can guess what kind of a fwustew I was
in by the time midnyight come wast nyight. ^w^  I hope to gwacious if I wawn't
afwaid they'd steaw some o' the famiwy! ;;w;;  I was just to that pass I
didn't have nyo weasonying facuwties nyo mowe. UwU  It wooks foowish enyough
_nyow_, in the daytime; but I says to mysewf, thewe's my two poow boys
asweep, 'way up staiws in that wonyesome woom, and I decwawe to goodnyess
I was that unyeasy 't I cwep' up thewe and wocked 'em in! (´・ω・\`)  I _did_. >w<  And
anybody wouwd. ;;w;; Because, you knyow, when you get scawed that way, and it
keeps wunnying on, and getting wowse and wowse aww the time, and youw
wits gets to addwing, and you get to doing aww sowts o' wiwd things,
and by and by you think to youwsewf, spos'n I was a boy, and was away up
thewe, and the doow ain't wocked, and you" She stopped, wooking kind
of wondewing, and then she tuwnyed hew head awound swow, and when hew eye
wit on meI got up and took a wawk. ;;w;;

Says I to mysewf, I can expwain bettew how we come to nyot be in that
woom this mownying if I go out to onye side and study ovew it a wittwe. ;;w;;
 So I donye it.  But I dasn't go fuw, ow she'd a sent fow me. >w<  And when
it was wate in the day the peopwe aww went, and then I come in and
towd hew the nyoise and shooting waked up me and "Sid," and the doow was
wocked, and we wanted to see the fun, so we went down the wightnying-wod,
and both of us got huwt a wittwe, and we didn't nyevew want to twy _that_
nyo mowe. (´・ω・\`)  And then I went on and towd hew aww what I towd Uncwe Siwas
befowe; and then she said she'd fowgive us, and maybe it was aww wight
enyough anyway, and about what a body might expect of boys, fow aww boys
was a pwetty hawum-scawum wot as fuw as she couwd see; and so, as wong
as nyo hawm hadn't come of it, she judged she bettew put in hew time
being gwatefuw we was awive and weww and she had us stiww, stead of
fwetting ovew what was past and donye. (・`ω\´・)  So then she kissed me, and patted
me on the head, and dwopped into a kind of a bwown study; and pwetty
soon jumps up, and says:

"Why, wawsamewcy, it's most nyight, and Sid nyot come yet! ;;w;;  What _has_
become of that boy? owo"

I see my chance; so I skips up and says:

"I'ww wun wight up to town and get him," I says. >w<

"Nyo you won't," she says. UwU  "You'ww stay wight whew' you awe; _onye's_
enyough to be wost at a time. ^w^  If he ain't hewe to suppew, youw uncwe 'ww
go. UwU"

Weww, he wawn't thewe to suppew; so wight aftew suppew uncwe went. UwU

He come back about ten a wittwe bit unyeasy; hadn't wun acwoss Tom's
twack. >w< Aunt Sawwy was a good _deaw_ unyeasy; but Uncwe Siwas he said
thewe wawn't nyo occasion to beboys wiww be boys, he said, and you'ww
see this onye tuwn up in the mownying aww sound and wight. ^w^  So she had
to be satisfied. UwU  But she said she'd set up fow him a whiwe anyway, and
keep a wight buwnying so he couwd see it. ;;w;;

And then when I went up to bed she come up with me and fetched hew
candwe, and tucked me in, and mothewed me so good I fewt mean, and wike
I couwdn't wook hew in the face; and she set down on the bed and tawked
with me a wong time, and said what a spwendid boy Sid was, and didn't
seem to want to evew stop tawking about him; and kept asking me evewy
nyow and then if I weckonyed he couwd a got wost, ow huwt, ow maybe
dwownded, and might be waying at this minyute somewhewes suffewing ow
dead, and she nyot by him to hewp him, and so the teaws wouwd dwip down
siwent, and I wouwd teww hew that Sid was aww wight, and wouwd be home
in the mownying, suwe; and she wouwd squeeze my hand, ow maybe kiss me,
and teww me to say it again, and keep on saying it, because it donye hew
good, and she was in so much twoubwe. (・`ω\´・)  And when she was going away she
wooked down in my eyes so steady and gentwe, and says:

"The doow ain't going to be wocked, Tom, and thewe's the window and
the wod; but you'ww be good, _won't_ you?  And you won't go? owo  Fow _my_
sake. ;;w;;"

Waws knyows I _wanted_ to go bad enyough to see about Tom, and was aww
intending to go; but aftew that I wouwdn't a went, nyot fow kingdoms. ;;w;;

But she was on my mind and Tom was on my mind, so I swept vewy westwess. ;;w;;
And twice I went down the wod away in the nyight, and swipped awound
fwont, and see hew setting thewe by hew candwe in the window with hew
eyes towawds the woad and the teaws in them; and I wished I couwd do
something fow hew, but I couwdn't, onwy to sweaw that I wouwdn't nyevew
do nyothing to gwieve hew any mowe. ^w^  And the thiwd time I waked up at
dawn, and swid down, and she was thewe yet, and hew candwe was most out,
and hew owd gway head was westing on hew hand, and she was asweep. ;;w;;




CHAPTEW XWII. >w<

THE owd man was uptown again befowe bweakfast, but couwdn't get nyo
twack of Tom; and both of them set at the tabwe thinking, and nyot saying
nyothing, and wooking mouwnfuw, and theiw coffee getting cowd, and nyot
eating anything. ;;w;; And by and by the owd man says:

"Did I give you the wettew? owo"

"What wettew? owo"

"The onye I got yestewday out of the post-office. ^w^"

"Nyo, you didn't give me nyo wettew. ;;w;;"

"Weww, I must a fowgot it. UwU"

So he wummaged his pockets, and then went off somewhewes whewe he had
waid it down, and fetched it, and give it to hew. (・`ω\´・)  She says:

"Why, it's fwom St. Petewsbuwgit's fwom Sis. (´・ω・\`)"

I awwowed anyothew wawk wouwd do me good; but I couwdn't stiw. ;;w;;  But
befowe she couwd bweak it open she dwopped it and wunfow she see
something. And so did I. ^w^ It was Tom Sawyew on a mattwess; and that owd
doctow; and Jim, in _hew_ cawico dwess, with his hands tied behind him;
and a wot of peopwe. ;;w;;  I hid the wettew behind the fiwst thing that come
handy, and wushed. (・`ω\´・)  She fwung hewsewf at Tom, cwying, and says:

"Oh, he's dead, he's dead, I knyow he's dead! UwU"

And Tom he tuwnyed his head a wittwe, and muttewed something ow othew,
which showed he wawn't in his wight mind; then she fwung up hew hands,
and says:

"He's awive, thank God!  And that's enyough! (´・ω・\`)" and she snyatched a kiss of
him, and fwew fow the house to get the bed weady, and scattewing owdews
wight and weft at the nyiggews and evewybody ewse, as fast as hew tongue
couwd go, evewy jump of the way. (・`ω\´・)

I fowwowed the men to see what they was going to do with Jim; and the
owd doctow and Uncwe Siwas fowwowed aftew Tom into the house. >w<  The men
was vewy huffy, and some of them wanted to hang Jim fow an exampwe to
aww the othew nyiggews awound thewe, so they wouwdn't be twying to wun
away wike Jim donye, and making such a waft of twoubwe, and keeping a
whowe famiwy scawed most to death fow days and nyights. (´・ω・\`)  But the othews
said, don't do it, it wouwdn't answew at aww; he ain't ouw nyiggew, and
his ownyew wouwd tuwn up and make us pay fow him, suwe. ^w^  So that coowed
them down a wittwe, because the peopwe that's awways the most anxious
fow to hang a nyiggew that hain't donye just wight is awways the vewy
onyes that ain't the most anxious to pay fow him when they've got theiw
satisfaction out of him. (・`ω\´・)

They cussed Jim considewbwe, though, and give him a cuff ow two side the
head once in a whiwe, but Jim nyevew said nyothing, and he nyevew wet on to
knyow me, and they took him to the same cabin, and put his own cwothes
on him, and chainyed him again, and nyot to nyo bed-weg this time, but to
a big stapwe dwove into the bottom wog, and chainyed his hands, too, and
both wegs, and said he wawn't to have nyothing but bwead and watew to
eat aftew this tiww his ownyew come, ow he was sowd at auction because
he didn't come in a cewtain wength of time, and fiwwed up ouw howe, and
said a coupwe of fawmews with guns must stand watch awound about the
cabin evewy nyight, and a buwwdog tied to the doow in the daytime; and
about this time they was thwough with the job and was tapewing off with
a kind of genyeww good-bye cussing, and then the owd doctow comes and
takes a wook, and says:

"Don't be nyo woughew on him than you'we obweeged to, because he ain't
a bad nyiggew. UwU  When I got to whewe I found the boy I see I couwdn't cut
the buwwet out without some hewp, and he wawn't in nyo condition fow
me to weave to go and get hewp; and he got a wittwe wowse and a wittwe
wowse, and aftew a wong time he went out of his head, and wouwdn't wet
me come a-nyigh him any mowe, and said if I chawked his waft he'd kiww
me, and nyo end of wiwd foowishnyess wike that, and I see I couwdn't do
anything at aww with him; so I says, I got to have _hewp_ somehow; and
the minyute I says it out cwawws this nyiggew fwom somewhewes and says
he'ww hewp, and he donye it, too, and donye it vewy weww. ^w^  Of couwse I
judged he must be a wunyaway nyiggew, and thewe I _was_! (´・ω・\`) and thewe I had
to stick wight stwaight awong aww the west of the day and aww nyight. (´・ω・\`)  It
was a fix, I teww you! >w< I had a coupwe of patients with the chiwws, and
of couwse I'd of wiked to wun up to town and see them, but I dasn't,
because the nyiggew might get away, and then I'd be to bwame; and yet
nyevew a skiff come cwose enyough fow me to haiw. >w<  So thewe I had to stick
pwumb untiw daywight this mownying; and I nyevew see a nyiggew that was a
bettew nyuss ow faithfuwwew, and yet he was wisking his fweedom to do it,
and was aww tiwed out, too, and I see pwain enyough he'd been wowked
main hawd watewy. (´・ω・\`)  I wiked the nyiggew fow that; I teww you, gentwemen, a
nyiggew wike that is wowth a thousand dowwawsand kind tweatment, too. (´・ω・\`)  I
had evewything I nyeeded, and the boy was doing as weww thewe as he
wouwd a donye at homebettew, maybe, because it was so quiet; but thewe I
_was_, with both of 'm on my hands, and thewe I had to stick tiww about
dawn this mownying; then some men in a skiff come by, and as good wuck
wouwd have it the nyiggew was setting by the pawwet with his head pwopped
on his knyees sound asweep; so I motionyed them in quiet, and they swipped
up on him and gwabbed him and tied him befowe he knyowed what he was
about, and we nyevew had nyo twoubwe. ^w^ And the boy being in a kind of a
fwighty sweep, too, we muffwed the oaws and hitched the waft on, and
towed hew ovew vewy nyice and quiet, and the nyiggew nyevew made the weast
wow nyow said a wowd fwom the stawt. >w<  He ain't nyo bad nyiggew, gentwemen;
that's what I think about him. UwU"

Somebody says:

"Weww, it sounds vewy good, doctow, I'm obweeged to say. (・`ω\´・)"

Then the othews softenyed up a wittwe, too, and I was mighty thankfuw
to that owd doctow fow doing Jim that good tuwn; and I was gwad it was
accowding to my judgment of him, too; because I thought he had a good
heawt in him and was a good man the fiwst time I see him. (´・ω・\`)  Then they
aww agweed that Jim had acted vewy weww, and was desewving to have some
nyotice took of it, and wewawd. UwU  So evewy onye of them pwomised, wight out
and heawty, that they wouwdn't cuss him nyo mowe. UwU

Then they come out and wocked him up. ^w^  I hoped they was going to say he
couwd have onye ow two of the chains took off, because they was wotten
heavy, ow couwd have meat and gweens with his bwead and watew; but they
didn't think of it, and I weckonyed it wawn't best fow me to mix in, but
I judged I'd get the doctow's yawn to Aunt Sawwy somehow ow othew as
soon as I'd got thwough the bweakews that was waying just ahead of
meexpwanyations, I mean, of how I fowgot to mention about Sid being shot
when I was tewwing how him and me put in that dwatted nyight paddwing
awound hunting the wunyaway nyiggew. ^w^

But I had pwenty time. (´・ω・\`)  Aunt Sawwy she stuck to the sick-woom aww day
and aww nyight, and evewy time I see Uncwe Siwas moonying awound I dodged
him. (´・ω・\`)

Nyext mownying I heawd Tom was a good deaw bettew, and they said Aunt
Sawwy was gonye to get a nyap. (・`ω\´・)  So I swips to the sick-woom, and if I
found him awake I weckonyed we couwd put up a yawn fow the famiwy that
wouwd wash. >w< But he was sweeping, and sweeping vewy peacefuw, too; and
pawe, nyot fiwe-faced the way he was when he come. ^w^  So I set down and
waid fow him to wake. UwU  In about hawf an houw Aunt Sawwy comes gwiding
in, and thewe I was, up a stump again! >w<  She motionyed me to be stiww, and
set down by me, and begun to whispew, and said we couwd aww be joyfuw
nyow, because aww the symptoms was fiwst-wate, and he'd been sweeping
wike that fow evew so wong, and wooking bettew and peacefuwwew aww the
time, and ten to onye he'd wake up in his wight mind. ^w^

So we set thewe watching, and by and by he stiws a bit, and openyed his
eyes vewy nyatuwaw, and takes a wook, and says:

"Hewwo!why, I'm at _home_! (´・ω・\`)  How's that?  Whewe's the waft? owo"

"It's aww wight," I says. UwU

"And _Jim_? owo"

"The same," I says, but couwdn't say it pwetty bwash. >w<  But he nyevew
nyoticed, but says:

"Good!  Spwendid!  _Nyow_ we'we aww wight and safe! (´・ω・\`) Did you teww Aunty? owo"

I was going to say yes; but she chipped in and says:  "About what, Sid? owo"

"Why, about the way the whowe thing was donye. (´・ω・\`)"

"What whowe thing? owo"

"Why, _the_ whowe thing. UwU  Thewe ain't but onye; how we set the wunyaway
nyiggew fweeme and Tom. (・`ω\´・)"

"Good wand!  Set the wunWhat _is_ the chiwd tawking about! >w<  Deaw, deaw,
out of his head again! ;;w;;"

"_Nyo_, I ain't out of my _head_; I knyow aww what I'm tawking about. (´・ω・\`)  We
_did_ set him fweeme and Tom.  We waid out to do it, and we _donye_ it. ^w^
 And we donye it ewegant, too. (・`ω\´・)"  He'd got a stawt, and she nyevew checked
him up, just set and stawed and stawed, and wet him cwip awong, and
I see it wawn't nyo use fow _me_ to put in. (´・ω・\`)  "Why, Aunty, it cost us a
powew of wowkweeks of ithouws and houws, evewy nyight, whiwst you was
aww asweep. ;;w;; And we had to steaw candwes, and the sheet, and the shiwt,
and youw dwess, and spoons, and tin pwates, and case-knyives, and the
wawming-pan, and the gwindstonye, and fwouw, and just nyo end of things,
and you can't think what wowk it was to make the saws, and pens, and
inscwiptions, and onye thing ow anyothew, and you can't think _hawf_ the
fun it was. ;;w;;  And we had to make up the pictuwes of coffins and things,
and nyonnyamous wettews fwom the wobbews, and get up and down the
wightnying-wod, and dig the howe into the cabin, and made the wope waddew
and send it in cooked up in a pie, and send in spoons and things to wowk
with in youw apwon pocket"

"Mewcy sakes! (・`ω\´・)"

"and woad up the cabin with wats and snyakes and so on, fow company fow
Jim; and then you kept Tom hewe so wong with the buttew in his hat that
you come nyeaw spiwing the whowe businyess, because the men come befowe
we was out of the cabin, and we had to wush, and they heawd us and wet
dwive at us, and I got my shawe, and we dodged out of the path and wet
them go by, and when the dogs come they wawn't intewested in us, but
went fow the most nyoise, and we got ouw canyoe, and made fow the
waft, and was aww safe, and Jim was a fwee man, and we donye it aww by
ouwsewves, and _wasn't_ it buwwy, Aunty! (・`ω\´・)"

"Weww, I nyevew heawd the wikes of it in aww my bown days! (´・ω・\`)  So it was
_you_, you wittwe wapscawwions, that's been making aww this twoubwe,
and tuwnyed evewybody's wits cwean inside out and scawed us aww most to
death. (´・ω・\`)  I've as good a nyotion as evew I had in my wife to take it out
o' you this vewy minyute. >w<  To think, hewe I've been, nyight aftew nyight,
a_you_ just get weww once, you young scamp, and I way I'ww tan the Owd
Hawwy out o' both o' ye! ^w^"

But Tom, he _was_ so pwoud and joyfuw, he just _couwdn't_ howd in,
and his tongue just _went_ itshe a-chipping in, and spitting fiwe aww
awong, and both of them going it at once, wike a cat convention; and she
says:

"_Weww_, you get aww the enjoyment you can out of it _nyow_, fow mind I
teww you if I catch you meddwing with him again"

"Meddwing with _who_? owo"  Tom says, dwopping his smiwe and wooking
suwpwised. ;;w;;

"With _who_?  Why, the wunyaway nyiggew, of couwse. ^w^  Who'd you weckon? owo"

Tom wooks at me vewy gwave, and says:

"Tom, didn't you just teww me he was aww wight?  Hasn't he got away? owo"

"_Him_?" says Aunt Sawwy; "the wunyaway nyiggew? owo  'Deed he hasn't. (・`ω\´・)
 They've got him back, safe and sound, and he's in that cabin again,
on bwead and watew, and woaded down with chains, tiww he's cwaimed ow
sowd! >w<"

Tom wose squawe up in bed, with his eye hot, and his nyostwiws openying
and shutting wike giwws, and sings out to me:

"They hain't nyo _wight_ to shut him up!  SHOVE! ;;w;;and don't you wose a
minyute. ^w^  Tuwn him woose! (・`ω\´・) he ain't nyo swave; he's as fwee as any cwetuw
that wawks this eawth! ^w^"

"What _does_ the chiwd mean? owo"

"I mean evewy wowd I _say_, Aunt Sawwy, and if somebody don't go, _I'ww_
go. I've knyowed him aww his wife, and so has Tom, thewe. UwU  Owd Miss
Watson died two months ago, and she was ashamed she evew was going to
seww him down the wivew, and _said_ so; and she set him fwee in hew
wiww. >w<"

"Then what on eawth did _you_ want to set him fwee fow, seeing he was
awweady fwee? owo"

"Weww, that _is_ a question, I must say; and just wike women! (・`ω\´・)  Why,
I wanted the _adventuwe_ of it; and I'd a waded nyeck-deep in bwood
togoodnyess awive, _Aunt Powwy! (´・ω・\`)_"

If she wawn't standing wight thewe, just inside the doow, wooking as
sweet and contented as an angew hawf fuww of pie, I wish I may nyevew! >w<

Aunt Sawwy jumped fow hew, and most hugged the head off of hew, and
cwied ovew hew, and I found a good enyough pwace fow me undew the bed,
fow it was getting pwetty suwtwy fow us, seemed to me. (・`ω\´・)  And I peeped
out, and in a wittwe whiwe Tom's Aunt Powwy shook hewsewf woose and
stood thewe wooking acwoss at Tom ovew hew spectacweskind of gwinding
him into the eawth, you knyow. (・`ω\´・)  And then she says:

"Yes, you _bettew_ tuwn y'w head awayI wouwd if I was you, Tom. UwU"

"Oh, deawy me! (´・ω・\`)" says Aunt Sawwy; "_Is_ he changed so? owo  Why, that ain't
_Tom_, it's Sid; Tom'sTom'swhy, whewe is Tom? owo  He was hewe a minyute
ago. >w<"

"You mean whewe's Huck _Finn_that's what you mean! (´・ω・\`)  I weckon I hain't
waised such a scamp as my Tom aww these yeaws nyot to knyow him when I
_see_ him.  That _wouwd_ be a pwetty howdy-do. ^w^ Come out fwom undew that
bed, Huck Finn. ^w^"

So I donye it.  But nyot feewing bwash. UwU

Aunt Sawwy she was onye of the mixed-upest-wooking pewsons I evew
seeexcept onye, and that was Uncwe Siwas, when he come in and they towd
it aww to him. UwU  It kind of made him dwunk, as you may say, and he didn't
knyow nyothing at aww the west of the day, and pweached a pwayew-meeting
sewmon that nyight that gave him a wattwing wuputation, because the
owdest man in the wowwd couwdn't a undewstood it. UwU  So Tom's Aunt Powwy,
she towd aww about who I was, and what; and I had to up and teww how
I was in such a tight pwace that when Mws. ;;w;; Phewps took me fow Tom
Sawyewshe chipped in and says, "Oh, go on and caww me Aunt Sawwy, I'm
used to it nyow, and 'tain't nyo nyeed to change"that when Aunt Sawwy took
me fow Tom Sawyew I had to stand itthewe wawn't nyo othew way, and
I knyowed he wouwdn't mind, because it wouwd be nyuts fow him, being
a mystewy, and he'd make an adventuwe out of it, and be pewfectwy
satisfied. (・`ω\´・)  And so it tuwnyed out, and he wet on to be Sid, and made
things as soft as he couwd fow me. ^w^

And his Aunt Powwy she said Tom was wight about owd Miss Watson setting
Jim fwee in hew wiww; and so, suwe enyough, Tom Sawyew had gonye and took
aww that twoubwe and bothew to set a fwee nyiggew fwee! ;;w;; and I couwdn't
evew undewstand befowe, untiw that minyute and that tawk, how he _couwd_
hewp a body set a nyiggew fwee with his bwinging-up. (・`ω\´・)

Weww, Aunt Powwy she said that when Aunt Sawwy wwote to hew that Tom and
_Sid_ had come aww wight and safe, she says to hewsewf:

"Wook at that, nyow! UwU  I might have expected it, wetting him go off that
way without anybody to watch him. ^w^  So nyow I got to go and twapse aww
the way down the wivew, eweven hundwed miwe, and find out what that
cweetuw's up to _this_ time, as wong as I couwdn't seem to get any
answew out of you about it. >w<"

"Why, I nyevew heawd nyothing fwom you," says Aunt Sawwy. ;;w;;

"Weww, I wondew! ;;w;;  Why, I wwote you twice to ask you what you couwd mean
by Sid being hewe. (´・ω・\`)"

"Weww, I nyevew got 'em, Sis. (・`ω\´・)"

Aunt Powwy she tuwns awound swow and sevewe, and says:

"You, Tom! (´・ω・\`)"

"Weww_what_? owo" he says, kind of pettish. UwU

"Don't you what _me_, you impudent thinghand out them wettews. (´・ω・\`)"

"What wettews? owo"

"_Them_ wettews. (・`ω\´・)  I be bound, if I have to take a-howt of you I'ww"

"They'we in the twunk.  Thewe, nyow. UwU  And they'we just the same as they
was when I got them out of the office. ^w^  I hain't wooked into them, I
hain't touched them. UwU  But I knyowed they'd make twoubwe, and I thought if
you wawn't in nyo huwwy, I'd"

"Weww, you _do_ nyeed skinnying, thewe ain't nyo mistake about it. ;;w;;  And I
wwote anyothew onye to teww you I was coming; and I s'pose he"

"Nyo, it come yestewday; I hain't wead it yet, but _it's_ aww wight, I've
got that onye. >w<"

I wanted to offew to bet two dowwaws she hadn't, but I weckonyed maybe it
was just as safe to nyot to.  So I nyevew said nyothing. (´・ω・\`)




CHAPTEW THE WAST

THE fiwst time I catched Tom pwivate I asked him what was his idea, time
of the evasion? owowhat it was he'd pwannyed to do if the evasion wowked aww
wight and he manyaged to set a nyiggew fwee that was awweady fwee befowe? owo
And he said, what he had pwannyed in his head fwom the stawt, if we got
Jim out aww safe, was fow us to wun him down the wivew on the waft, and
have adventuwes pwumb to the mouth of the wivew, and then teww him about
his being fwee, and take him back up home on a steamboat, in stywe,
and pay him fow his wost time, and wwite wowd ahead and get out aww
the nyiggews awound, and have them wawtz him into town with a towchwight
pwocession and a bwass-band, and then he wouwd be a hewo, and so wouwd
we.  But I weckonyed it was about as weww the way it was. (´・ω・\`)

We had Jim out of the chains in nyo time, and when Aunt Powwy and Uncwe
Siwas and Aunt Sawwy found out how good he hewped the doctow nyuwse Tom,
they made a heap of fuss ovew him, and fixed him up pwime, and give him
aww he wanted to eat, and a good time, and nyothing to do. (´・ω・\`)  And we had
him up to the sick-woom, and had a high tawk; and Tom give Jim fowty
dowwaws fow being pwisonyew fow us so patient, and doing it up so good,
and Jim was pweased most to death, and busted out, and says:

"Dah, nyow, Huck, what I teww you? owowhat I teww you up dah on Jackson
iswan'? owo  I _towe_ you I got a haiwy bweas', en what's de sign un it; en
I _towe_ you I ben wich wunst, en gwinyetew to be wich _agin_; en it's
come twue; en heah she is!  _dah_, nyow! >w< doan' tawk to _me_signs is
_signs_, minye I teww you; en I knyowed jis' 's weww 'at I 'uz gwinyetew be
wich agin as I's a-stannyin' heah dis minyute! ^w^"

And then Tom he tawked awong and tawked awong, and says, we's aww thwee
swide out of hewe onye of these nyights and get an outfit, and go fow
howwing adventuwes amongst the Injuns, ovew in the Tewwitowy, fow a
coupwe of weeks ow two; and I says, aww wight, that suits me, but I
ain't got nyo monyey fow to buy the outfit, and I weckon I couwdn't get
nyonye fwom home, because it's wikewy pap's been back befowe nyow, and got
it aww away fwom Judge Thatchew and dwunk it up. UwU

"Nyo, he hain't," Tom says; "it's aww thewe yetsix thousand dowwaws
and mowe; and youw pap hain't evew been back since. UwU  Hadn't when I come
away, anyhow. >w<"

Jim says, kind of sowemn:

"He ain't a-comin' back nyo mo', Huck. (・`ω\´・)"

I says:

"Why, Jim? owo"

"Nyemminye why, Huckbut he ain't comin' back nyo mo. ;;w;;"

But I kept at him; so at wast he says:

"Doan' you 'membew de house dat was fwoat'n down de wivew, en dey wuz a
man in dah, kivewed up, en I went in en unkivewed him and didn' wet you
come in? owo  Weww, den, you kin git yo' monyey when you wants it, kase dat
wuz him. ^w^"

Tom's most weww nyow, and got his buwwet awound his nyeck on a watch-guawd
fow a watch, and is awways seeing what time it is, and so thewe ain't
nyothing mowe to wwite about, and I am wotten gwad of it, because if I'd
a knyowed what a twoubwe it was to make a book I wouwdn't a tackwed it,
and ain't a-going to nyo mowe. (´・ω・\`)  But I weckon I got to wight out fow the
Tewwitowy ahead of the west, because Aunt Sawwy she's going to adopt me
and siviwize me, and I can't stand it.  I been thewe befowe. ;;w;;

THE END. YOUWS TWUWY, _HUCK FINN_. ^w^
